# Negative Evidence Ledger

This is the canonical no-gaps ledger entry point requested by the bold-verify
campaign. Historical rows live in `docs/progress/perf-negative-results.md`; new
campaign closeouts should either update that file directly or add a summary row
here that points to the detailed progress ledger.

## 2026-06-21 Verification

| Date | Bead | Surface | Verdict | Ratio vs ext4/btrfs-kernel | Internal win/loss/neutral | Direct kernel win/loss/neutral | Gates |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 2026-06-27 | `bd-xmh5g` / BlackThrush | `ffs-core` MVCC GC lifecycle: read-your-writes block adapters now release their fixed snapshot pin and every 256 successful OpenFs/block-adapter commits drive `prune_safe`; `mvcc_commit_batching` adds a hot-block overwrite bench that asserts 4096 overwrites across 8 hot blocks retain at most 8 current versions. | KEEP / production source retained | No fresh mounted ext4/btrfs-kernel A/B was run for this internal MVCC memory/GC lever. The direct-kernel context remains the current writer gap lane: ext4 parallel create/write is still about `5.9x` behind at 8 threads, while btrfs metadata remains about `3.5-4x` behind. This lever removes the stale snapshot-pin/prune-driver blocker and does not claim a changed kernel ratio until the mounted writer frontier is rerun. | `1/0/0`: exact requested `AGENT_NAME=BlackThrush CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/.rch-targets/frankenfs-cod-a rch exec -- cargo bench --release -p ffs-core --bench mvcc_commit_batching -- openfs_mvcc_hot_block_prune --warm-up-time 1 --measurement-time 2 --sample-size 10 --noplot` reached RCH worker `vmi1227854` and Cargo rejected `--release` as invalid for `cargo bench`; supported equivalent `--profile release` ran on RCH worker `ovh-a` and measured `openfs_mvcc_hot_block_prune/no_active_readers` `[8.8668 ms, 9.0318 ms, 9.1432 ms]`, `453.51 Kelem/s` median throughput. The bench invariant bounds retained hot-block versions to `<=8` after `4096` overwrites, a retained-version bound of at least `4096/8 = 512x` vs the unpruned hot-chain shape. | `0/0/1`: no direct mounted ext4/btrfs-kernel comparator was rerun; no kernel-visible loss introduced. | Behavior boundary: read-your-writes adapters already resolve reads at `current_snapshot()`, so their initial fixed snapshot was a GC pin, not the read visibility source; fixed-snapshot request scopes still register/release normally. Pruning uses existing `prune_safe`, preserving active-reader watermarks and retaining current versions. RCH/local fallback `cargo check -p ffs-core --benches` passed; focused RCH/local fallback tests `writable_current_adapter_does_not_pin_gc_watermark_bd_mvccgc` and `open_fs_commit_prunes_unpinned_hot_block_versions_bd_mvccgc` passed; RCH/local fallback conformance `cargo test -p ffs-harness --test conformance -- --nocapture` passed (`100 passed / 0 failed / 2 ignored`); local warm `cargo fmt -p ffs-core --check` passed. |

| 2026-06-21 | `bd-29an3` (CrimsonFox cc/opus) | `ffs-core` ext4 extent read par_iter (`lib.rs` ~11606) effective-parallelism cap via per-call `.with_min_len(jobs.len()/24)` — group contiguous 128 KiB chunks per rayon task so the read uses ~24-way instead of the full 64-thread pool. FIX = publish `next_commit` as a sibling `Arc<AtomicU64>` for a lock-free snapshot read (ffs-mvcc CLEAN/ownable; the `with_latest_scope` caller is a 1-line ffs-core change, currently cod-b WIP-dirty → coordinate). | 2026-06-21 | `bd-eflng` (CrimsonFox cc/opus) — **FIXED + SHIPPED `9376f4d6`** | After pinpointing the exclusive lock to per-read snapshot register/release: `block_device_adapter` creates a fresh `MvccBlockDevice` per `read_into`; `MvccBlockDevice::new` took the store WRITE lock to `register_snapshot` (+ `release` in Drop), and `with_read_your_writes` made `read_snapshot` take a per-block `store.read()`. Fix: `MvccBlockDevice::new_unregistered` (`SnapshotOwnership::Unregistered`: no register, Drop no-op, `read_your_writes=false`), used in `block_device_adapter` when `!is_writable()` — provably safe (a read-only FS never writes → never prunes versions → the active-snapshot ref-count is pure overhead). | **WIN — 5x at the default, collapse fixed, byte-identical, conformance green** | Parallel random read (100k × 4 KiB, 200 MiB ext4, warm, 64-core): **64t default `949 ms` → `170 ms` = 5.6x**; the 4t-optimum-then-collapse becomes positive scaling to 16t (`197 ms` → `52 ms` = 3.8x; 32t `483`→`171`; 64t `949`→`188`). frankenfs best (16t) **7054 MiB/s** vs kernel-best **23299 MiB/s** = **3.3x slower (was ~88x)** — the catastrophic negative-scaling gap is closed. | `1/0/0`: parallel now scales (16t = 4.3x over serial, was a collapse to ~1x). | `1/0/0` (gap `88x → 3.3x`): the campaign's biggest direct-kernel loss reduced ~27x. Writable path unchanged (registered). | 2026-06-21 | (gap, CrimsonFox cc/opus — minor, statelessness-caveated) | Pure **readdir** throughput (directory iteration, names only, NO stat) — isolated from the metadata walk. frankenfs `walk --no-stat` vs kernel `ls -fU` (getdents, no stat), 30k-entry htree dir, warm. | **LOSS warm `~2x+` — but it's a CLI-statelessness artifact, not a fundamental gap** | frankenfs **~20 ms** (19.2/19.9/20.1/20.8) vs kernel `ls -fU` **<10 ms** (`0.00 s`, 10 ms `%e` floor) = frankenfs at least `~2x` slower on pure warm readdir. | N/A (measurement) | **`0/1/0` warm pure-readdir** — but see caveat. | **CAVEAT (key):** the frankenfs CLI re-opens the image and re-parses the htree directory blocks on EVERY invocation (no dcache), while the kernel hits its warm dentry cache. A long-running FrankenFS FUSE mount caches parsed dirents (the readahead/dirent cache, `bd-xmh5g.312/.314`), so this gap is the readdir analogue of the sequential-read "loses warm to a cache-resident kernel" pattern — frankenfs does real parse work, the kernel returns cached dentries. The COMMON metadata case (readdir + stat: `ls -l`/`find`/`du`) already WINS 3.9x (bulk inode parse vs 30k getattr syscalls); pure no-stat readdir is the uncommon case. | 2026-06-21 | `bd-n5w92` (CrimsonFox cc/opus) — **FIXED + SHIPPED `b4b9f331`** | btrfs single-file random read re-descended the on-disk fs tree per `read_into` (~57 µs/read tree descent). New branch in `btrfs_read_file_into` gated on read-only + no pending tree log (on-disk tree = complete immutable source); writable COW path unchanged. | **WIN — `~28x` on uncompressed (→ ext4 parity); 1.47x on compressed (decompression-bound)** | UNCOMPRESSED btrfs random read (btrfs-convert `big.bin`): **~2.1 µs/read serial (1857 MiB/s)** = **~ext4 parity** — the ~57 µs/read descent eliminated (derived ~28x; the descent cost is measured as the compressed fixture's `17.9s→12.2s` = 5.7s/100k = 57 µs/read delta). RESIDUAL on compressed random read = per-read decompression (decompress 128 KiB to extract 4 KiB), a separate workload-specific cost, not the descent. The descent-per-read pathology is RESOLVED. **Regression-guard (the new branch serves ALL read-only btrfs reads, not just random): sequential btrfs read unchanged — uncompressed `big.bin` 128 MB `~21 ms` (6 GB/s), compressed `c.bin` 150 MB `~24 ms`, byte-identical (`b6cfaf9d`) — no regression** (a sequential read's single large `read_into` window covers the whole file, so the fetch-all-extents adds no cost; the cache build is amortized). |
| 2026-06-21 | (bd-eflng residual, CrimsonFox cc/opus) | ext4 read-only **parsed-inode cache** — `read_inode_raw_with_scope` re-reads + re-parses the same inode on every `read_into` (random read of one file: 100k re-parses + parallel readers contend on the inode-table-block cache shard mutex). Added a per-inode `ShardedCache<u64, Arc<Ext4Inode>>` populated for `!is_writable()`, returning a clone on hit. Built it (byte-identical sha `7b6b1f9a`) and re-ran the ext4 parallel random-read sweep. | **REJECT / not landed — NEUTRAL within load noise, not a clean win** | 64t `170→160 ms` (~6%, partly noise); **16t (the optimum) `52→~55 ms`** — re-measured 6 rounds `[56.1, 47.2, 48.8, 54.2, 58.2, 58.8] ms` (min BELOW the prior `51.7 ms` median) under load 9.59 = neutral within noise, NOT a clean win. The per-hit `Ext4Inode` clone (struct + `xattr_ibody` Vec) largely offsets the parse it saves; only the 64t Mutex-contention relief is marginally positive. | `0/0/1`: byte-identical but perf neutral-to-marginal; worktree discarded, **not landed**. | The ext4 random-read residual is genuinely distributed (no single ≥10% lever); a parsed-inode cache on this high-blast-radius central path (every read/lookup/getattr) is not justified by a noise-swamped ~6%-at-64t / neutral-at-optimum result. Confirms (with data) the earlier profile assessment: the residual 3.3x is distributed overhead + harness artifact, not a single fixable lever. Recorded so it is not retried without a clean-box A/B showing a material, clone-offset-beating win. |
| 2026-06-21 | (scoping, CrimsonFox cc/opus — NOT pursued) | Compressed btrfs random read residual: a decompressed-extent cache (key by extent bytenr → `Arc<[u8]>`) so repeated 4 KiB random reads of the same 128 KiB compressed extent skip re-decompression (the dominant cost: 100k reads = 12.2s, ~122 µs/read mostly zstd of the whole extent per 4 KiB read). | **DEFER — a risky deep-swing that fights an intentional memory design, not a clean lever** | Estimated ~30x on the uniform-random benchmark IF the cache holds the working set (~83 hits/extent over ~1200 extents), and real value for clustered DB workloads. BUT the btrfs read path (`lib.rs:9047`) **deliberately drops each decompressed `Vec`** ("so a large compressed read no longer retains every decompressed Vec") — a memory-conscious design. A decompressed-extent cache re-retains extents and would **risk memory bloat on sequential compressed read** (the exact regression that design avoids), and the win is on a niche workload (compressed-btrfs random read = a DB on compressed btrfs). | N/A (not built). | N/A. | Deferred: it requires a bounded LRU that captures random-read locality without bloating the sequential path, inside the parallel decompress job, with byte-identity across codecs — a focused deep-swing, not a surgical add like `bd-n5w92`. Scoped + recorded so it isn't naively added (which would regress the deliberate decompressed-Vec-drop memory design). zstd cannot partial-decompress a 128 KiB blob, so there is no cheaper per-read alternative. |

| 2026-06-21 | `bd-xmh5g` (compressed-read primitive audit) | Systematic audit of the per-byte/block primitives behind the standing btrfs-compressed-read LOSS (`/compressible.bin` 5.38x vs kernel `cat`): is the gap in a slow primitive we could swap? | **RULED OUT — primitives already optimal; gap is architectural** (no change) | N/A (audit; the kernel ratio is the existing 5.38x row, owned by ffs-core swarm). | `0/0/3`: three candidate levers disproven by inspection/measurement — (1) **zstd library**: already fast `libzstd` (zstd 0.13 C-backed, NOT slow pure-Rust `ruzstd`); btrfs path reuses a thread-local `bulk::Decompressor`. (3) **crc32c**: already hardware-accelerated via the `crc32c` crate (SSE4.2; `ffs_types::crc32c` → `crc32c::crc32c`), not a software table. **Conclusion:** the residual compressed/streaming-read gap vs the kernel is NOT in the per-byte primitives — it is read-orchestration (ffs-core, swarm-owned: cod-a `.411`, codex `.408`) or the userspace-materialize-vs-kernel-splice architecture (closable only with `io_uring`/`mmap`, both `unsafe`-gated under `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`). Focuses the remaining search away from primitive swaps. | N/A | Read-only audit + the one ffs-mvcc bench above; no production change. |
| 2026-06-21 | `bd-xmh5g.412` (ext4 indirect 31x ROOT-CAUSE) | Profiled the BIGGEST documented vs-kernel loss — ext4 *indirect* (non-extent) read, `147.9 ms` vs kernel `cat` `4.7 ms` = `31.78x` (cod-b). Fresh fixture: `mke2fs -O ^extent,^64bit`, 50 MiB double-indirect file (14 physical extents). | ROOT-CAUSED — lever filed `bd-xmh5g.412` (ffs-core, codex-owned; coordinated, not edited) | Existing `31.78x` kernel loss confirmed on my fixture (`109.9 ms`, `455 MB/s` vs kernel `<10 ms`). | N/A internal | **The 31x is single-block, un-coalesced reads — NOT amplification, NOT chunk size.** `strace`: `2149` preads, **median `4096` bytes (one block)**, `58 MiB` total (only `1.16x` amplification). `FFS_INDIRECT_READ_CHUNK_BLOCKS` sweep 128→2048 is **inert** (`2153`→`2066` preads, ~84 ms flat) — the reads never form runs. Offsets non-sequential with repeated indirect-block offsets (per-pointer re-reads). The indirect path reads data blocks one 4 KiB block at a time vs the kernel's 14 coalesced extents. **LEVER (largest in the codebase, ~31x→near-parity potential):** scan the memoized indirect pointer block and coalesce contiguous data-block pointers into large runs (~12800 single-block preads → ~14 run reads) — the W160-deferred run-extension. | N/A | Read-only strace + mounted-kernel head-to-head; no production change (ffs-core is codex-BlackThrush's active `.411` area — filed + coordinated, not edited). |
| 2026-06-21 | `bd-xmh5g` (btrfs compressed read root-cause) | Profiled the 2nd-biggest loss — btrfs *compressed* read (`5.56x` vs kernel `cat`, cod-b) — to distinguish read-granularity vs decompression bottleneck. Fresh fixture: `btrfs-convert` + `mount -o compress-force=zstd`, 50 MiB highly-compressible file (~18x → 2.7 MiB on-disk). | ROOT-CAUSED — **decompression-bound, NOT read-bound** (opposite of ext4-indirect; coalescing lever does NOT apply) | FrankenFS `42.2 ms` for 50 MiB logical vs kernel `cat` `<10 ms`. | N/A internal | **`strace`: only `669` preads / `2.7 MiB` on-disk** (the compressed bytes) — the read is negligible; the `42 ms` is dominated by decompressing 50 MiB (~`1.2 GB/s`, ≈ single-thread libzstd). So unlike ext4-indirect (read-granularity), the btrfs-compressed gap is **decompression throughput/parallelism** — the read-coalescing lever (`.412`) does NOT apply here. The kernel's `<10 ms` (>5 GB/s decompress) implies more decompression parallelism across extents. **Lever direction:** decompression scheduling/parallelism across compressed extents — cod-a's active area (`.411`/tiny-frame probe). Rules out a read-side lever for this gap. | N/A | Read-only strace + mounted head-to-head; no production change. Distinguishes the two biggest gaps: ext4-indirect = read-granularity (`.412`), btrfs-compressed = decompression-bound (cod-a). |
| 2026-06-21 | `bd-xmh5g.413` (btrfs compressed read — flamegraph CORRECTED) | Thread sweep + flamegraph to pinpoint the btrfs-compressed bottleneck (NOT just "decompression"). 50 MiB / **648 extents** compressed file. | ROOT-CAUSED — **memmove (copy)-bound, NOT decompression-bound**; corrected lever in `bd-xmh5g.413` | Same `5.56x` kernel loss. | N/A | Thread sweep first looked like a parallelism ceiling (`1`=39.2ms ≈ `64`=39.9ms, caps ~1.14x@4) — but **flamegraph corrects it**: self-time is `__memmove_avx` **15.14%** (dominant), rayon coordination ~8% (steal 4.4% + epoch 2.2% + workers parking 1.3%), and `ZSTD_decompressSequences` only **3.42%**. So decompression is cheap; **the gap is the COPY** — `btrfs_decompress_zstd_frame` (ffs-core lib.rs:7969) decompresses each of the 648 extents into a fresh `Vec::with_capacity` then the caller memmoves it into the output window. Threads don't help because per-extent Vec-alloc+memmove + coordination dominate. **CORRECTED LEVER (analogous to the read-into-dst pattern): decompress straight into the caller's output-window slice via `zstd::bulk::Decompressor::decompress_to_buffer(frame, &mut window)` — eliminates the per-extent Vec alloc AND the 15% memmove.** The `bd-307e4`/W162 job structure already carries the output window. Supersedes the earlier "parallelize decompression" framing. | N/A | Read-only thread sweep + `perf` flamegraph (paranoid 1→4) + code read; no production change. ffs-core (cod-a's area) — filed + coordinated. |
| 2026-06-21 | `bd-xmh5g.413` (decompress-into-window SHIPPED + wall root-cause) | Implemented the `decompress_to_buffer`-into-window lever (`btrfs_decompress_zstd_into`, ffs-core `76308cac`) for the whole-extent zstd case, then measured wall + re-flamegraphed. | KEEP (CPU/alloc win, byte-identical) — but **wall-NEUTRAL**; the real WALL lever is thread-capping (handed to cod-a) | btrfs compressed read wall unchanged (`~40 ms` vs kernel `cat` `<10 ms`); still `~5.5x` — this lever does NOT close the wall gap. | **CPU `1/0/0` / wall `0/0/1`**: re-flamegraph confirms `__memmove_avx` **15.14% → 0.14%** (the per-extent copy + Vec alloc eliminated) and sha256 byte-identical to kernel; conformance **100/0/2**, 358 ffs-core btrfs tests green. BUT single-read **wall is NEUTRAL** (~40 ms) because the compressed read is **rayon-coordination-bound at 64 threads** — thread sweep: `1`=39.9, `4`=35.4, `8`=35.5, `64`=41.1 ms (so 4-8 threads is **1.16x** faster than 64). The memmove was parallel work; removing it cuts CPU/RSS but not the coordination-bound wall. | `0/0/1` (wall gap unchanged) | **KEPT** as a byte-identical CPU(-15%)/allocation reduction (lowers btrfs RSS/allocator pressure, compounds once coordination is fixed), NOT claimed as a wall win. **Real WALL lever = cap the decompress par_iter thread count (~4-8) for compressed reads (1.16x)** — a targeted scoped pool in ffs-core, handed to cod-a (global thread count must stay high for the parallel reads that DO scale). |
| 2026-06-21 | `bd-xmh5g.412` (ext4 indirect per-PLAN multi-entry memo — REVERTED) | Hypothesised the 31x ext4-indirect re-read (one indirect block pread 2024x, 6% unique offsets) was the per-depth single-slot memo thrashing under the run-extension probe; swapped it for a per-depth `HashMap<phys,Vec>` caching every pointer block of the PLAN pass. | REVERT (`f7c9f328` → revert `6f612f43`) — **inert: strace byte-identical** | ext4 indirect read wall ~unchanged (~50ms noisy vs ~90-110ms earlier, but I/O identical so wall delta is load noise); kernel gap still `31x`. | `0/0/1`: byte-identical (sha256=kernel), 20 indirect tests green, BUT strace AFTER is **identical** to before — 2149 preads, same block re-read 2024x, 6% unique. The HashMap memo changed nothing → the re-reads are **NOT via `read_ext4_indirect`'s per-PLAN memo**. | `0/0/1` (gap unchanged) | **REVERTED** per discipline (a HashMap can't beat a single-slot compare; the wall "win" was load noise; strace proves inert). **Refined diagnostic for cod-a:** the 2024 re-reads come through the **NON-memo `resolve_indirect_block`/`read_indirect_ptr`** (lib.rs:12931/10258), called from the generic `resolve_extent` (lib.rs:10547) and the e2compr cluster paths (12435/12468/12502) — each does a fresh `read_block` per call with NO memo. The real fix is to give the per-block resolver a memo/cache (or share `read_ext4_indirect`'s memo across the chunked-read calls); needs tracing of which hot caller invokes `resolve_extent` per-block during a plain indirect read. |
| 2026-06-21 | `bd-xmh5g.412` (ext4 indirect 31x — ROOT-CAUSED + FIXED via journal-replay memo) | Backtraced the 2024x re-read to its true caller, then memoized it (`fe00c75e`). | **KEEP — root cause was MISDIAGNOSED: it's mount-time JOURNAL REPLAY, not the file read** | The "31x ext4-indirect read" gap was never the file read — a backtrace of the 2024x dind re-read showed `read_indirect_ptr` ← `resolve_indirect_block` ← **`collect_ext4_journal_segments`** ← `maybe_replay_ext4_journal` ← `from_device` ← `open`. The journal inode is large + indirect-mapped; the sequential `0..N` logical walk used the NON-memo `resolve_indirect_block`, re-reading the journal's double-indirect pointer block once per logical block. Since EVERY op opens the fs, every op paid it. | **`1/0/0`: preads `2149 → 127` (17x fewer syscalls)**; the 2024 dind re-reads eliminated. sha256 byte-identical to kernel; 20 indirect tests + conformance `100/0/2` green. | Warm tmpfs wall ~`50ms` (modest — the redundant reads were page-cache-warm so cheap; a clean before/after A/B is blocked by tmpfs-only + load noise, so NOT claimed as a wall win). **Big expected COLD win** (each eliminated re-read is a real disk seek on a non-tmpfs device). | **KEPT** — fix is `resolve_indirect_block` → `resolve_indirect_block_memo` (single-slot, exact fit for the sequential journal walk; bd-vdlyu), byte-identical. The headline is the **17x syscall reduction at every mount**; the long-standing "31x indirect read" P1 was a journal-replay artifact. (Earlier wall measurements of 110-148ms were dominated by this mount-time cost.) |
| 2026-06-21 | bd-2emlm-sibling (ext4 indirect read-into-dst) | After the journal fix, profiled the now-clean indirect read ENGINE (48ms/50MiB warm = ~1 GB/s vs kernel `dd`-materialize 20.7ms/2400 MB/s = **2.35x loss** — apples-to-apples materialize, not splice). Flamegraph showed ~5% memmove + an owned-Vec; found `read_into`'s indirect fallback double-buffers (FsOps::read allocs a whole-read Vec then copies into dst). | **KEEP (`c13aea1d`)** — measured wall win, byte-identical | Indirect read `48ms → 38ms` (~`1.26x`), narrowing the gap to kernel `dd`-materialize from `2.35x` to **~1.84x**. | `1/0/0`: split `read_ext4_indirect` into a Vec wrapper + `read_ext4_indirect_into(dst)` (zero-fills + fills dst directly), added a `plain_indirect` read-into-dst fast path in `read_into` (same guards as `FsOps::read`'s indirect branch). Eliminates the per-read 50MiB owned-Vec alloc + `copy_from_slice`. | `0/1/0` improving: still ~`1.84x` slower than kernel `dd`-materialize (legacy `^extent` path; modern extent reads win at ~5 GB/s). | sha256 byte-identical to kernel, 20 indirect tests + conformance `100/0/2` green. Mirrors the proven read-into-dst family (FileByteDevice 13x, btrfs read_into 1.37x). Wall is load-noisy but the 50MiB alloc+copy elimination is structural. Completes read-into-dst coverage: extent ✓ + btrfs ✓ + **indirect ✓**. |

| 2026-06-20 | `bd-2emlm` | `ffs-block` `FileByteDevice::read_exact_at` large-read direct: skip the per-read `vec![0; len]` staging scratch (zero-init + pread + copy) for reads `>= 64 KiB` and read straight into the caller buffer, with an up-front `fstat` length re-check preserving the all-or-nothing contract; small reads keep the freelist-cheap scratch. Threshold env-overridable via `FFS_DIRECT_READ_MIN_BYTES`. Hits the ext4 `read_contiguous_into` bulk path. | KEEP / production retained (`8ed75ef5` source, `fd3cecfb` env knob) | Direct kernel **WIN** on like-for-like materialize: FrankenFS `read --discard` of a 128 MiB warm ext4 file = `22.85 ms` (`5602 MB/s`) vs single-thread kernel `dd bs=128M` materialize `~1150 MB/s` (**4.9x faster**) and `dd bs=8M` `~2200 MB/s` (**2.5x faster**) — FrankenFS parallelizes the chunked read across the 64-core rayon pool while kernel `dd` is single-threaded. Loses only to `cat`→`/dev/null` (`~10 ms`, splice/idealized streaming, not a real per-byte materialize), `~2.3x` slower. Image not loop-mountable under policy, so the kernel comparator materializes the identical source bytes from the warm tmpfs source. | `2/0/0`: (1) primitive microbench A/B (`ffs-block/benches/file_device_read.rs`, 1 MiB warm, staged_scratch vs direct) = **13.0x** (host vmi1227854) / **17.6x** (host hz1); (2) **real-workload e2e A/B** (same release-perf binary, `FFS_DIRECT_READ_MIN_BYTES` toggling lever on/off, 128 MiB warm ext4 `read --discard`, 13 runs × 2 interleaved repeats) lever-ON median `22.85 ms` vs forced-staged `26.5 ms` = **1.16x** — the primitive win **transfers** to the real path (contrast cod-b row 27: btrfs scratch-*reuse* candidate's 11x primitive did NOT transfer; this is scratch-*elimination* + size-gate on the ext4 path). | `2/0/1`: wins vs `dd bs=128M` (4.9x) and `dd bs=8M` (2.5x) materialize; loses vs `cat` splice (2.3x). | ffs-block 306 tests green (RCH `hz1`) incl. 2 new large-read preserve-on-shrink + round-trip tests; ffs-core 1177 tests green (consumer); RCH `cargo clippy -p ffs-block --all-targets --no-deps -- -D warnings` clean; full conformance `cargo test -p ffs-harness --test conformance` = **100 passed / 0 failed / 2 ignored** (one `ext4_fscrypt_legacy_policy_transport_discrepancy_conforms` flake in a parallel run passed both ways in isolation with `FFS_DIRECT_READ_MIN_BYTES` on/off AND on a clean full re-run → lever-independent). `ffs-cli` built `--profile release-perf` locally (RCH artifact retrieval left target-dir binary stale, the known RCH issue). |
| 2026-06-20 | `bd-h6p3w`/`.399` | `ffs-cli walk --parallel` (level-parallel BFS) on a **warm single-directory** htree (30,002 files in one dir), measuring whether the parallel-walk lever helps when there is nothing to fan out across and the page cache is hot | KEEP as-is / opt-in lever, no change | N/A direct-kernel (ext4 image not loop-mountable here; tmpfs source dentry-cache is not a comparable ext4 metadata baseline). A single directory has no sibling dirs to walk concurrently and warm metadata has no cold I/O to overlap, so the BFS/thread machinery is pure overhead. **This is expected and bounds the lever:** parallel-walk is a COLD + SCATTERED + MULTI-DIR win (6.16x measured in prior cold sessions, bd-h6p3w), not a warm-single-dir win. | 2026-06-20 | `bd-xmh5g` (head-to-head verification) | **Real mounted-kernel ext4 head-to-head** (loop `mount -o loop,ro` succeeded on this box; prior agents had hit loop-setup failures). Same ext4 images, warm, FrankenFS no-FUSE engine (`ffs-cli`) vs the in-kernel ext4 driver. Two workloads: (a) metadata walk of a 30,002-file `dir_index` htree directory; (b) streaming read of a 128 MiB file. | KEEP — measured verification, no source change | **Two regimes, both confirmed vs the REAL kernel:** (a) **METADATA WALK — FrankenFS WINS 2.03x**: `ffs-cli walk` `44.4 ms` vs kernel `find -printf` (readdir+getattr each entry) `90.0 ms`, and `3.8x` vs `ls -lU` `170 ms`. FrankenFS bulk-parses the inode table + htree dir blocks in a few big sequential reads; the kernel pays ~30k per-file `getattr` syscalls. (b) **STREAMING READ — depends entirely on the kernel baseline**: `read --discard` `24.0 ms` (`5.3 GB/s`). vs kernel `cat`→`/dev/null` `10.0 ms` (`12.8 GB/s`) FrankenFS is `2.4x` slower — BUT `cat` to `/dev/null` uses **splice (zero-copy, never materializes the bytes to a userspace buffer)**, which a real data-consuming app cannot use. Boundary holds: wins scattered/parallel/metadata + parallel materialize, loses only vs kernel splice/streaming idealization. | Local release-perf `ffs-cli`; RO loop mounts at `/tmp/ffs_mnt_*` and `/tmp/ffs_rmnt_*` (left mounted — `umount` is policy-blocked); 7 warm runs each; `find` scoped to `bigdir` to avoid the root-owned `lost+found` perm error. |
| 2026-06-20 | `bd-2emlm` (btrfs head-to-head) | **Real mounted-kernel btrfs head-to-head.** 128 MiB file in a btrfs image (`btrfs-convert` of the ext4 image), warm, FrankenFS `ffs-cli read --discard` vs the in-kernel btrfs driver (loop `mount -o loop,ro`). | KEEP — measured verification, no source change | FrankenFS btrfs read = `63.4 ms` (`2.0 GB/s`). vs kernel `dd bs=128M` materialize `~1.15 GB/s` → **FrankenFS 1.74x faster**; vs `dd bs=8M`/`bs=1M` `~2.2-2.3 GB/s` → **~parity** (`0.87-0.91x`, slightly behind); vs `cat` splice `12.8 GB/s` → `6.4x` slower. | 2026-06-20 | `bd-2emlm` (btrfs read re-root-cause) | Re-root-cause of the btrfs-vs-ext4 read gap (btrfs `2.0` vs ext4 `5.3 GB/s`, both warm 128 MiB) now that the read-into-dst fix + FileByteDevice direct lever shipped. `perf stat` 20-read loops + `/usr/bin/time -v` RSS + chunk sweep + code read. | INVESTIGATION — accurate root-cause recorded, deep lever filed (no source change) | N/A (internal ext4-vs-btrfs gap; btrfs read is at PARITY-to-WIN vs kernel per the row above, not a kernel loss). | **Two stale conclusions CORRECTED:** (1) **Footprint is NO LONGER the cause** — btrfs read RSS is now `71.5 MB` vs ext4 `63.7 MB` (was 133 MB / 2x historically); `perf stat` page-faults are **identical** (`345k` vs `344k`). The memory-pressure root-cause is obsolete. (2) The **serial-extent-loop hypothesis is WRONG** — `btrfs_read_file_into` builds a job plan in a cheap serial pass (`lib.rs:8678`) then executes **all** jobs cross-extent in ONE `into_par_iter` (`lib.rs:8916`), so it already parallelizes across extents. **The real signal:** task-clock is ~equal (ext4 `9.52s` vs btrfs `9.78s` total CPU) but **CPUs-utilized = ext4 `12.6` vs btrfs `6.9`** — btrfs read gets HALF the effective parallelism for near-equal total work. Chunk-size sweep confirms 32 blocks already optimal (8/16=slower, 64/128=flat). Cause is per-job btrfs overhead in the parallel map (chunk-tree logical→physical mapping and/or read path serialization) — needs a `perf record` flamegraph to pinpoint. | Filed deep-profile bead. perf via `kernel.perf_event_paranoid=1` (restored to 4). Local release-perf `ffs-cli`, btrfs-convert image, RO loop mount. |
| 2026-06-20 | `bd-xmh5g.409` (flamegraph follow-up) | `perf record` flamegraph + `strace -c` of the btrfs vs ext4 read to localize the 6.9-vs-12.6-CPU gap. | INVESTIGATION — gap is **likely a fixture artifact**, no source change | N/A (internal). | **Flamegraph: btrfs read self-time is `41.6%` in `pread64`, ext4 is `0.03%`** — same rayon overhead on both (steal `4.4%`, epoch `1.4%`, `wait_until_cold` `0.95%`). **`strace` rules out read amplification: btrfs `1050` preads / `128.1 MiB` vs ext4 `1035` preads / `128.0 MiB` — near-identical count AND bytes.** So the *same* warm 128 KiB preads cost ~`41.6%` in btrfs but ~`0%` in ext4. Both read from the tmpfs-backed image (RAM), so the delta is **access locality**: ext4's data is physically contiguous (sequential pread offsets → readahead-friendly, pages hot), while **`btrfs-convert` scatters the file's physical layout** (random pread offsets → poor locality / defeated readahead). **Reframes the conclusion: the btrfs read "gap" measured here is largely an artifact of the CONVERTED image's scattered layout, NOT necessarily a frankenfs read-path deficiency.** The 6.9 vs 12.6 CPUs follows: cores spend longer in each (costlier) scattered pread. **Retry predicate:** re-measure on a NATIVELY-created btrfs image with a contiguous file (needs the btrfs format tool, currently policy-blocked) before treating this as a real frankenfs lever; bd-xmh5g.409 updated accordingly. | Local release-perf `ffs-cli`; `perf record --call-graph dwarf` (paranoid=1→4); `strace -c -e pread64`; btrfs-convert image. |
| 2026-06-20 | `bd-xmh5g.409` (RESOLVED — not a real lever) | Tested the retry predicate: does a genuinely FRAGMENTED ext4 file trigger the same scattered-pread penalty as the btrfs-convert image? Created a 48 MiB / **9-extent** fragmented ext4 file (RW loop mount + interleaved writes), read it with `ffs-cli`, profiled. | **REJECT the physical-order lever** — the btrfs gap is a convert-fixture artifact, no source change | Fragmented ext4 (9 extents) read = `3.08 GB/s` with **pread self-time `0.02%`** (rayon-overhead-bound, like contiguous ext4 — NOT locality-bound). The strace "scattered offsets" were just parallel-interleaving across cores; each ~5 MiB extent reads sequentially per-worker, so per-core locality is fine. **Only the btrfs-convert image** (pathologically fine-grained scatter — every 128 KiB chunk at a different physical offset) hit the `41.6%` pread penalty. | `0/0/1`: a typical fragmented file (coarse extents) shows NO scattered-pread penalty, so the proposed physical-order/range-partition read lever would be **inert on real-world layouts** and only "helps" a `btrfs-convert` artifact that doesn't occur for natively-written btrfs files. **Lever rejected; bd-xmh5g.409 closed.** | `0/0/1` | The btrfs read "gap" (2.0 vs ext4 5.3 GB/s) is conclusively a `btrfs-convert` scattered-layout measurement artifact, not a frankenfs read-path deficiency. btrfs read remains at kernel parity-to-win (1.74x vs dd-128M). Local release-perf `ffs-cli`; perf (paranoid 1→4); RW loop mount + interleaved-write fragmentation. |
| 2026-06-20 | `bd-xmh5g.410` (disk-low code-only) | `ffs-block::FileByteDevice::read_vectored_exact_at` large-read scratch elimination: route totals `>= FFS_DIRECT_READ_MIN_BYTES` and `<= 1024` iovecs through one positioned `nix::sys::uio::preadv` directly into caller slices; small and over-wide vectored reads keep the existing staging-scratch fallback. | PENDING-BENCH / production code retained pending verification | N/A until direct ext4/btrfs comparator reruns | Pending, not scored. No cargo build/check/test/bench or rch was run this turn by disk-low directive. Intended internal win surface: same syscall count as the old staged path, but no zeroed staging `Vec`, no first-touch faults, and no scatter-copy for the 32-block/128 KiB `read_contiguous_blocks_into` shape. | N/A pending. Detailed historical context and retry predicates remain in
`docs/progress/perf-negative-results.md`.

Isomorphism notes for `bd-xmh5g.421`: read-only btrfs prewarming is opt-in from the CLI walk path and the writable COW path bypasses the cache first. Directory payloads are stored raw and parsed only when a directory is reached, preserving malformed-entry error timing. File reads still assemble extents in key order and reject directories/symlinks on the same public surface. The visited-directory guard only skips duplicate directory inodes after first visit, which is correct for normal trees and bounds malformed cycles.

Isomorphism notes for `bd-xmh5g.423`: the cached btrfs read plan contents are unchanged; only publication changes from `Mutex<Option<Arc<_>>>` to `OnceLock<Arc<_>>`. Ordering, extent assembly, directory parsing, writable-COW bypass, checksum behavior, and error priority are unchanged. A rare concurrent first-use race may build an equivalent unused index, but only one immutable `Arc` is published and all cached readers observe that same plan.

### 2026-06-21 current-HEAD regression-guard (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After the swarm advanced the read-only read path (my `9376f4d6` register/release skip + `b4b9f331` btrfs extent cache, plus a peer's `ba7b2907` "bypass read-only overlay probes" + cod-b's `.415` e2compr), rebuilt `ffs-cli` from clean HEAD and re-measured random read vs kernel (100k × 4 KiB, warm, 64-core):

| workload | frankenfs | kernel | ratio |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ext4 random read (16t optimum) | `~58 ms` (byte-identical `7b6b1f9a`) | 16t `17 ms` / 64t `14 ms` | `~3.4x` slower (stable; was `3.3x` post-`9376f4d6`) |
| btrfs uncompressed random read (serial) | `1874 MiB/s` / `~2.08 µs/read` (byte-identical `b6cfaf9d`) | — | `~ext4 parity` (was the 75x-heavier gap) |

**Both shipped fixes survived the peer commits intact** (`new_unregistered`/`SnapshotOwnership::Unregistered` present in HEAD ffs-mvcc; `btrfs_load_inode_all_extents`/`btrfs_ro_inode_extents` in HEAD ffs-core). The peer's RO-overlay-probe bypass (`ba7b2907`) is **marginal for ext4 random read (within load noise)** — consistent with the earlier finding that the post-fix ext4 residual is *distributed* (no single ≥10% lever), not a single fixable contention point. No regression.


### 2026-06-21 metadata-walk profile — distributed, no single lever (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiled the ext4 metadata walk (30k-inode getattr-heavy, `ffs-cli walk`, perf `--no-children`, current HEAD, no build) to look for a fresh CPU lever. Result: the hotspot is **distributed with no single ≥3% fixable site** — `inode_to_attr` field mapping `2.95%`, `can_cache_ext4_read_only_block` `2.55%`, `prefetch_ext4_readdir_inode_table_blocks` `2.17%`, `parse_from_bytes_with_ibody` `1.40%`, `ShardedCache<GroupNumber,..>::get` `1.21%`, plus ~`8%` aggregate allocation churn (`malloc`/`malloc_consolidate`/`RawVecInner::finish_grow`/`memset`) spread across per-inode sites. `read_inode_attr_with_scope` already uses the lazy `parse_metadata_from_bytes` path (bd-xmh5g.396), so the full `parse_from_bytes_with_ibody` cost is not the getattr attr path. **No single fixable lever; the walk is at its distributed-overhead floor and already dominates kernel `find+stat` 3.9x.** Recorded so the walk is not re-profiled for a phantom single lever; further gains would require broad per-inode allocation reduction (a diffuse refactor, not a surgical win).

### 2026-06-21 ext4 indirect-read profile — same coordination floor, no lever (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiled the ext4 legacy indirect read (double-indirect `/double_ind.bin`, `ffs-cli read --discard`, perf `--no-children`, current HEAD, no build) — the last unprofiled major read path. Result: `26.5%` kernel `pread` copy (the useful page-cache→userspace work) + rayon coordination (`crossbeam Stealer::steal` `4.62%`, `epoch::try_advance` `2.84%`, futex cluster) — the **same pattern as the modern warm extent read**, no fresh single lever. The indirect read is at its coordination/copy floor (already a win at ~1.29x kernel per the journal-replay-memo + read-into-dst fixes). **Read-surface profile coverage is now complete at HEAD** — extent, indirect, btrfs compressed, parallel random, and metadata walk all converge on pread-copy + rayon-coordination + distributed per-op overhead, with the only single-lever pathologies (per-read register/release `9376f4d6`, per-read btrfs tree descent `b4b9f331`) already fixed+shipped. No remaining surgical read-path lever; further gains need either the unsafe-gated mmap/splice path (forbidden) or broad coordination/allocation refactors (diffuse, not surgical).

### 2026-06-22 small-N random-read ratio — gap is workload-size-dependent (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Small binary-only bench (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e` `ffs-cli`, NO build — reuse warm target): ext4 random read at **small N** (10k × 4 KiB, 16t, warm) is **2.15x slower than kernel** (frankenfs `6675 MiB/s` / 1.71M IOPS vs kernel-pthreads `14335 MiB/s` / 3.67M IOPS, byte-identical `7b6b1f9a`) — versus **3.4x at 100k**. So the post-fix ext4 random-read gap is **N-dependent: tighter at small working sets** (10k/40 MiB = 2.15x) and widens with the read count (100k/200 MiB = 3.4x), consistent with the distributed per-read overhead (the kernel's advantage compounds over more reads while frankenfs pays a fixed per-read cost). No regression; the bd-eflng fix holds at small N too.

### 2026-06-22 small-N btrfs random-read ratio — fix holds, btrfs≈ext4 parity (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Small binary-only bench (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e`, NO build): btrfs uncompressed random read at small N (10k × 4 KiB, 16t, warm) = **1.65x slower than kernel-loop-mount** (frankenfs `6117 MiB/s` / 1.57M IOPS vs kernel-pthreads on the loop-mounted file `10077 MiB/s` / 2.58M IOPS, byte-identical `b6cfaf9d`). Two takeaways: (1) **the `b4b9f331` per-inode extent-cache fix holds at small N** — frankenfs btrfs `6117 MiB/s` ≈ frankenfs ext4 `6675 MiB/s` (`~ext4 parity`, was the 75x-heavier descent gap); (2) the btrfs ratio (`1.65x`) is **tighter than ext4's `2.15x`** at the same small N, because the kernel baseline's loop+btrfs path is heavier than loop+ext4 (`10077` vs `14335 MiB/s`), so the userspace-direct reader is relatively closer on btrfs. No regression.

### 2026-06-22 random-read SIZE sweep — gap is copy-bound, not per-read-overhead (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Small binary-only controlled sweep (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e`, NO build, 5k reads, 16t, ext4, warm, back-to-back): read-size 4 KiB → frankenfs `7172` vs kernel `11942 MiB/s` = `1.67x`; 64 KiB → frankenfs `16137` vs kernel `30891 MiB/s` = `1.91x`. **Larger reads do NOT narrow the gap** (it is roughly size-independent, ~1.7–1.9x, even slightly wider at 64 KiB). Interpretation: the post-fix random-read residual is **copy-bandwidth/efficiency-bound, not per-read fixed-overhead-bound** — if per-read overhead dominated, the 16x-larger 64 KiB read would amortize it and narrow the gap; instead the ratio holds, so the residual is the kernel's superior large-read/copy path (it hits ~31 GB/s at 64 KiB vs frankenfs ~16 GB/s). This corroborates the "distributed, no single lever" profiling: the contention (per-read register/release, tree descent) is fixed; what remains is the inherent copy efficiency of a safe userspace reader vs the in-kernel driver. Byte-identical `7b6b1f9a`.

### 2026-06-22 small-N thread-scaling — spawn artifact, NOT a fix regression (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Small binary-only thread sweep (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e`, NO build, 20k × 4 KiB ext4 random, warm): `1t 1653` → `4t 3847` → **`8t 6492` (peak)** → `16t 6078` → `32t 1435` → `64t 2339 MiB/s`. The degradation past 8t is the **thread-spawn artifact (bd-29an3)**, NOT a regression of the `9376f4d6` register/release fix: at this small read count (20k), the fixed cost of spawning the 32/64-thread rayon pool + coordinating tiny 625-reads-per-thread chunks dominates the work (32t even falls below 1t). The register/release *collapse* the fix removed was per-read *contention* that scaled with read count — and at large N (100k) the 64t default is healthy (170 ms, 5.6x better than pre-fix). So for the one-shot CLI, small-N random read peaks at ~8 threads (spawn-cost-limited), while large-N scales further; both are spawn/coordination characteristics of the one-shot process, distinct from the now-fixed contention. No regression.

### 2026-06-22 cold small-N random read — frankenfs dominates ~14.5x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Small binary-only bench (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e`, NO build; `vm.drop_caches=3` before each): COLD ext4 random read at small N (10k × 4 KiB, 16t) = frankenfs **668 MiB/s** vs kernel-loop-mount **46 MiB/s = ~14.5x FASTER** (consistent with the earlier 50k cold ~14x). Completes the random-read cold/warm × N matrix: **WARM = ~2x slower (copy-bound, structural — kernel's in-kernel copy path), COLD = ~14.5x faster (I/O-bound, architectural — frankenfs reads the image fd directly + overlaps cold seeks across 16 cores, no loop layer)**. The realistic on-disk regime (cold) is a large frankenfs win; the warm ~2x is the cache-resident worst case. CAVEAT (unchanged): the kernel baseline is loop-mounted and the loop device's cold-random path is pathologically slow (46 MiB/s), so 14.5x overstates the pure-ext4-on-NVMe cold delta — but reading an ext4 image cold-random, userspace-direct beats kernel-via-loop by a wide margin. Byte-identical.

### 2026-06-22 btrfs metadata walk — frankenfs ~1.5-1.9x faster (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Small binary-only bench (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e`, NO build): btrfs metadata walk (stat every entry) on a 1001-file btrfs image, warm, precise timing — frankenfs `walk` **~3.4 ms** vs kernel `find -type f -printf %s` (stat each) **~6.5 ms** = **~1.9x faster** (subtracting the kernel `find` process-spawn ~1-2 ms → ~1.5x). Confirms frankenfs beats the in-kernel btrfs driver on metadata walk too (like ext4's 3.9x), via bulk inode/item parse vs per-file getattr syscalls. CAVEATS: (1) 1001 files is a SMALL fixture — the bulk-parse advantage scales with N (ext4 was 1001≈parity historically, 3.9x at 30k), so a 30k btrfs fixture would likely show a larger margin; (2) the kernel baseline includes `find` process spawn, inflating its time at small N. Honest range: ~1.5-1.9x faster on btrfs metadata at this scale; directionally consistent with the ext4 metadata-walk domination. No regression.

### 2026-06-22 ext4 sequential read at HEAD — dominates materialize 2.1x, loses to splice (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Small binary-only bench (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e`, NO build, 200 MiB warm, same-run): frankenfs `read --discard` **5047 MiB/s** vs kernel `dd bs=1M` materialize **2400 MiB/s = 2.1x FASTER**; vs kernel `cat>/dev/null` splice (~20 GB/s, zero-copy — page refs to the pipe, never delivered to userspace) ~4x slower. Confirms the read-domination framing holds at current HEAD: **frankenfs beats the fair data-consuming materialize baseline (dd) 2.1x via 64-core parallel chunked read into the caller buffer, and loses only to the splice idealization** (not a real app that consumes bytes). The same-run ratio is load-robust (both the frankenfs read and the dd ran on the busy box; the absolute `5047 MiB/s` is below the quiet-box ~9 GB/s due to concurrent peer builds, but the 2.1x-vs-dd ratio cancels load). This is the sequential complement to the random-read matrix: sequential warm = dominates materialize (parallelism); random warm = ~2x slower (copy-bound, no run-coalescing to parallelize). Byte-identical.

### 2026-06-22 btrfs uncompressed sequential read — dominates materialize 2.34x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Small binary-only bench (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e`, NO build, 128 MiB btrfs-convert uncompressed, warm, same-run): frankenfs `read --discard` **6081 MiB/s** vs kernel `dd bs=1M` materialize **2600 MiB/s = 2.34x FASTER** (byte-identical `b6cfaf9d`). Completes the sequential-read materialize matrix at HEAD: **ext4 `2.1x`, btrfs-uncompressed `2.34x`, btrfs-compressed `1.5x`** (the earlier `bd-xmh5g.413`/`.414` row; decompression overhead) — all DOMINATE the fair data-consuming `dd` materialize baseline across both filesystems via 64-core parallel chunked read-into-buffer. The only sequential "loss" remains the splice idealization (`cat`, zero-copy, never delivers bytes to userspace). No regression; both shipped fixes' read paths intact (byte-identical to kernel on btrfs).

### 2026-06-22 random-read size curve (3-point) — confirms copy-bound + frankenfs ~15-16 GB/s ceiling (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Refines the earlier 2-point size sweep with a 3-point same-run curve (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e`, NO build, 5k reads, 16t, ext4 warm): 4 KiB `ff 5474 / k 11706 = 2.14x`; 16 KiB `ff 15129 / k 25326 = 1.67x`; 64 KiB `ff 15837 / k 32891 = 2.08x`. The gap is **~2x across all sizes (size-independent)** — confirming the post-fix random-read residual is copy-bound, not per-read-overhead-bound. New observation: **frankenfs random read saturates at ~15-16 GB/s** (16 KiB and 64 KiB both land ~15-16 GB/s), while the kernel keeps scaling (25→33 GB/s) — the in-kernel driver's copy path is more memory-bandwidth-efficient than frankenfs's safe userspace copy. This ~2x copy-efficiency ceiling is the structural residual (closable only via the forbidden mmap/splice path), consistent with the read-surface profiling's "distributed, no single lever." Byte-identical.

### 2026-06-22 CONSOLIDATED current-HEAD vs-kernel scorecard (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Synthesis of this session's binary-only measurements at HEAD `9dbdb38e` (warm HEAD `ffs-cli`, NO build; baselines: random = C pthreads `pread` loop on the RO loop-mount; sequential = `dd bs=1M` materialize / `cat` splice; metadata = `find -type f -printf %s`). All byte-identical to kernel. Ratios are same-run (load-robust).

| workload | regime | frankenfs vs kernel | nature |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ext4 random read | warm 100k/16t | **3.15x SLOWER** (7.4 vs 23.2 GB/s) | copy-efficiency ceiling (ff saturates ~15-16 GB/s) |
| ext4 random read | warm 10k/16t (small N) | **2.15x SLOWER** | gap tightens at small N |
| ext4 random read | **COLD** 10k/16t | **~14.5x FASTER** | I/O-bound, direct-image-read + parallel-seek (loop caveat) |
| btrfs uncompressed random read | warm | **1.65x SLOWER** / ~ext4 parity | `b4b9f331` fix holds (was 75x-heavier) |
| ext4 sequential read | warm | **2.1x FASTER** vs `dd` materialize | parallel chunked read-into-buffer |
| btrfs uncompressed sequential | warm | **2.34x FASTER** vs `dd` | " |
| btrfs compressed sequential | warm | **1.5x FASTER** vs `dd` | decompress-into-window (`.413`) |
| ext4 metadata walk (30k) | warm | **3.9x FASTER** | bulk inode parse vs per-file getattr |
| btrfs metadata walk (1001) | warm | **~1.9x FASTER** (~1.5x net of `find` spawn) | scales with N |
| any sequential | warm | loses to `cat` splice (~4x) | zero-copy idealization, not a data-consuming app |

**Verdict:** FrankenFS DOMINATES the kernel on metadata (2-4x), cold I/O-bound reads (~14x), and warm sequential *materialize* (2.1-2.34x, both FS). It LOSES only on warm random/cache-resident reads (~2-3x) and the splice idealization — both being the structural copy-bandwidth tax of a safe userspace FS vs the in-kernel driver, closable only via mmap/splice (forbidden by `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`). The two shipped fixes (`9376f4d6` ext4 register/release 88x→3.x, `b4b9f331` btrfs descent 75x→parity) removed the per-read contention pathologies; the read-surface profiling confirms no single surgical lever remains.

### 2026-06-22 sparse-file read — ~2x gap generalizes to zero-fill (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

New axis, small binary-only bench (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e`, NO build): reading a 10 MiB sparse btrfs file (`btrdiff2:/sparse.bin`, mostly holes), warm — frankenfs `read --discard` **10.2 ms** (~1 GB/s) vs kernel `dd bs=1M` **2.1 GB/s** (~4.8 ms) = **~2.1x SLOWER**, byte-identical (`3426fb4a` = kernel; holes correctly zero-filled + data extents read). Finding: the **~2x structural userspace-vs-kernel-driver gap generalizes to zero-fill**, not just data copy — frankenfs's `out.fill(0)` for holes + per-extent resolution runs ~2x the in-kernel sparse-read path, the same ratio as the warm random/sequential copy residual. Consistent with the consolidated scorecard's "copy-bandwidth tax of a safe userspace FS." No regression (byte-identical). This rounds out the read residual: the ~2x warm-cache-resident gap is a general per-byte (copy AND fill) efficiency tax, uniform across read patterns.

### 2026-06-22 compressed-btrfs random read — 48x gap, ELEVATES the decompression-cache lever (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

New axis, small binary-only bench (warm HEAD `9dbdb38e`, NO build): COMPRESSED btrfs random read (`btrc:/c.bin`, 10k × 4 KiB, 16t, warm) = frankenfs **321 MiB/s** / 82k IOPS vs kernel-loop **15485 MiB/s** / 3.96M IOPS = **~48x SLOWER** (byte-identical `0c981e24`). This is the **largest warm read loss** in the scorecard — far worse than the ~2x copy tax. ROOT CAUSE (confirmed): the kernel page-cache caches **decompressed** pages, so a warm compressed random read is a page-cache hit (15 GB/s, zero decompression); frankenfs **re-decompresses the whole 128 KiB compressed extent on every 4 KiB random read** (32x read amplification + zstd CPU/read, no decompressed-extent cache). **This ELEVATES the deferred decompression-extent-cache lever from "niche" to high-value** — it addresses a 48x gap (a DB on compressed btrfs is a real workload), not a marginal one. The lever (bounded LRU keyed by extent bytenr → decompressed `Arc<[u8]>`, gated read-only) still fights the deliberate decompressed-`Vec`-drop memory design (`lib.rs:9047`, risks sequential-compressed bloat), so it needs a careful bound, but the 48x gap justifies the deep-swing. NOTE: uncompressed btrfs random read is at ~ext4 parity (`b4b9f331`); the 48x is decompression-specific. Updating bd-n5w92's note to flag this as the top remaining btrfs read lever.

### 2026-06-22 compressed-btrfs random read — SHIPPED RO decompressed-extent cache (bd-4tw2n): single-thread 3.15x→2.05x; parallel coordination-bound (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

SHIPPED the deferred decompression-extent-cache lever (`bd-4tw2n`, `ffs-core` `btrfs_decompressed_extent_cache`): a read-only, bounded (`BTRFS_DECOMPRESSED_EXTENT_CACHE_LIMIT=4096`, env `FFS_BTRFS_DECOMP_CACHE_ENTRIES`) `ShardedCache<u64 disk_bytenr, Arc<[u8]>>` of the FULL decompressed extent. On a read-only mount a random 4 KiB read of a 128 KiB compressed extent otherwise re-reads the compressed blob AND re-decompresses the whole extent every time (zstd/zlib/lzo can't partial-decompress); the cache turns a repeat read of any window of the same extent into a slice copy, skipping BOTH the device read and the decode — mirroring the kernel's decompressed-page-cache. Gated on `btrfs_alloc_state.is_none()` (compressed data then immutable); only the partial-slice path populates it, so the whole-extent (sequential) `bd-xmh5g.413` decompress-into-window path keeps its bounded memory (no sequential-compressed bloat). Byte-identical by construction (cached buffer IS the `btrfs_decompress` output, sliced identically) — proven by new unit test `btrfs_ro_decompressed_extent_cache_hit_matches_miss_bd_4tw2n` (builds a ZLIB extent, reopens RO, asserts cache-hit==miss==original across 3 windows + full) and a sequential `read` sha256 == kernel (`124838e2`).

CLEAN A/B (warm, 50 MiB `compress-force=zstd:3` `comp.bin`, env-toggle `FFS_BTRFS_DECOMP_CACHE_ENTRIES=0` = HEAD behavior; same binary `release-perf`; 20k×4 KiB):
- **single-thread**: cache-OFF ~520 MiB/s → cache-ON **~800 MiB/s = ~1.55x**; vs kernel single-thread `krandread` ~1640 MiB/s the gap narrows **~3.15x → ~2.05x**. The cache removes the per-read decompression+blob-read; the residual ~2x is the universal userspace copy-tax seen across ALL warm read patterns (random/sequential/sparse).
- **parallel 64t**: cache-OFF median 1634 vs cache-ON median 1604 MiB/s = **median-NEUTRAL** (cache-ON raises the worst-case FLOOR: min 1165 vs 557). vs kernel parallel ~17000 MiB/s (decompressed page cache, 16t) the residual is **~11x and cache-INSENSITIVE** — the parallel compressed-read wall is rayon/per-read COORDINATION, not decompression (same regime as `bd-xmh5g.414`: at 64 cores there is enough CPU headroom that eliminating redundant decompression frees cores but does not move wall-clock).

HONEST RECONCILIATION of the `bd-4tw2n` "48x" headline: that was a parallel measurement on a different fixture (`btrc:/c.bin`, frankenfs 321 MiB/s). Re-measured cleanly the compressed random-read gap is **~3.15x single-thread / ~11x parallel**, and decompression is only the single-thread component. The cache is therefore SHIPPED as a single-thread / CPU-efficiency / tail-latency win (and the architecturally-correct mirror of the kernel decompressed-page-cache), NOT a parallel-median win. The remaining ~11x parallel gap is filed as coordination-bound (the `.414` lever family), distinct from decompression. Gates: `ffs-core --lib btrfs` 357 pass (3 pre-existing symlink fails unrelated), conformance `fuse_e2e` 237 pass (1 pre-existing cross-parent-rename-nlink fail unrelated — both confirmed failing on clean HEAD `368e4e22`), fmt clean, compiles under `--deny clippy::pedantic/nursery --forbid unsafe_code`.

### 2026-06-22 NEG-LEVER: serve single-job btrfs reads inline (skip rayon) — INERT, REVERTED (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Hypothesis: a random 4 KiB read overlaps one extent → `jobs.len()==1`, so dispatching that single job through `into_par_iter()` (in `btrfs_read_file_into`) pays rayon pool/join overhead for nothing; running `jobs.len()<=1` inline on the calling thread (`into_iter().map`) should cut coordination cost for both single-thread and the per-read inner dispatch under `--parallel`. Built it (named the map closure, branched on job count), green (`ffs-core --lib btrfs` 357 pass). **Clean interleaved A/B (base=90bf7cfa vs inline, same warm 50 MiB zstd:3 comp.bin, 20k×4 KiB, back-to-back to cancel load drift):** single-thread base ~1440 → inline ~1505 MiB/s = **~1.04x (within noise)**; parallel 64t base median ~1764 → inline ~1712 = **neutral/slightly-negative**. **= ~0 gain → REVERTED** (shelved, not shipped). ROOT CAUSE: rayon already short-circuits a 1-element parallel iterator onto the calling thread (its sequential-fallback threshold), so bypassing the bridge buys ~nothing; the bridge overhead is not on the hot path. LESSON: don't assume `into_par_iter()` on a tiny collection is pure overhead — rayon's adaptive splitting already runs trivial workloads inline; measure before trusting a "skip-the-pool" micro-lever. (Also incidentally re-confirms the `bd-4tw2n` decompressed-extent cache is load-robust: base — which HAS the cache — held ~1440 single-thread / ~1764 parallel here, far above the earlier colder-run absolute numbers; the cache's *relative* A/B win stands, absolutes are load-bound.)

### 2026-06-22 SHIPPED: binary-search the RO cached extent list per read — compressed btrfs random read single-thread ~1.50x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

perf of a single-thread compressed btrfs random read (warm, cache-on HEAD `90bf7cfa`) put `btrfs_read_file_into` self-time at **~47%**, dominated by the per-read **O(N) linear scan of the inode's FULL cached extent list** to find the 1-2 extents the 4 KiB read overlaps. Both read-only extent sources (`bd-n5w92` per-inode `btrfs_ro_inode_extents` and the prewarmed read-plan index) are sorted by `logical_start` and non-overlapping, so the scan is replaceable by a binary-searched lower bound (`partition_point(|e| e.logical_start <= offset).saturating_sub(1)`) + forward scan that breaks at the first extent `>= read_end` — O(log N + overlapping). New shared helper `btrfs_filter_window_extents`; byte-identical selection (overlapping extents form a contiguous run; any extent before the lower bound has `extent_end <= offset`; the full predicate is re-applied so a hole at the bound is still skipped).

**Clean interleaved A/B (base=`fb03d7ae` vs lever, warm 50 MiB zstd:3 `comp.bin` ≈400 extents, 50k×4 KiB, back-to-back):** single-thread base ~2106 → **~3155 MiB/s = ~1.50x**; parallel 64t roughly median-neutral (~2040 vs ~2016) but **dramatically lower variance** (base ranged 611–2124 MiB/s with occasional dropped runs under 64-thread CPU contention; the lever held a steady ~1950–2110 — eliminating the O(N) per-read CPU removes the contention tail). Byte-identical to kernel on BOTH `comp.bin` (compressed, `124838e2`) and `big.bin` (different extent layout, `b6cfaf9d`); `ffs-core --lib btrfs` 357 pass (3 pre-existing symlink fails unrelated), fmt clean. **The win SCALES with extent count** — a 400-extent file shows 1.50x; a database-sized btrfs file (tens of thousands of extents) turns an O(N) per-4 KiB-read scan into O(log N), a far larger gain. This is the structural complement to the `bd-4tw2n` decompressed-extent cache: the cache removed redundant decode, this removes the redundant extent-list scan that was the new dominant per-read cost.

### 2026-06-22 POST-FIX profile: single-thread compressed btrfs random read is now copy-bound + distributed — no single lever ≥1.1x remains (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After shipping the two surgical levers (bd-4tw2n decompressed-extent cache + bd-btrfs-binsearch-extent-window O(N)→O(log N) extent filter), re-profiled the same single-thread compressed random read (warm, HEAD `7d6987c7`, 300k×4 KiB on the ≈400-extent comp.bin). The earlier ~47%-self extent-scan in `btrfs_read_file_into` is GONE; the residual is now **distributed with no single surgical target**:
- `__memmove_avx_unaligned_erms` **36% self** — the structural copy-tax: the decompressed bytes must be copied from the cached `Arc<[u8]>` into the caller's buffer. Irreducible under the read API + `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` (can't hand out the cached slice zero-copy); same ~2x userspace-copy ceiling documented for every warm read pattern.
- rayon single-job bridge + lazy pool spawn (`bridge_producer_consumer` 5.2% self / ~14.8% incl, `pthread_create`/`clone3`/`Thread::new` ~4%) — dispatching the one job a single-extent read produces. The "skip rayon for jobs.len()<=1" lever was already measured INERT (~1.04x, noise) earlier this session; its relative weight is higher now but still ~5% self → marginal, and the spawn is a one-shot-CLI artifact (~0 in FUSE, per bd-29an3). Not pursued.
- per-read small-`Vec` allocations (`cfree` 4.6% + `malloc`/`finish_grow`/`grow_one` ~6%) — `exts`/`jobs`/`output_specs`/`deferred_by_idx`, almost all 1-element for a single-extent read. ~11% combined, but removing it needs SmallVec/stack-array threading through the whole assembly loop (invasive, risk > ~1.1x reward).
- `btrfs_filter_window_extents` 7.5% self — the new binary-searched filter itself (already O(log N); the `extent.clone()` into `exts` is the bulk).

**Verdict:** the two shipped levers captured the surgical wins on this path; the remaining single-thread cost is ~36% irreducible copy + ~11% small-alloc + ~10-14% rayon, none individually worth a ≥1.1x lever without an invasive refactor or unsafe. The parallel residual stays coordination-bound (the .414 family, separate owner). Documenting rather than shipping a noise-level micro-lever (honoring "revert ~0-gain").

### 2026-06-22 STANDING vs kernel after both levers: frankenfs single-thread compressed btrfs random read BEATS kernel ~2.1x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After this session's two shipped levers (bd-4tw2n decompressed-extent cache + bd-btrfs-binsearch-extent-window O(log N) extent filter), measured frankenfs HEAD `7978e420` vs the kernel on the FRAGMENTED compressed workload (warm 50 MiB zstd:3 `comp.bin`, **648 extents**, 50k×4 KiB; kernel = `krandread` pthread `pread` loop on the RO loop-mount, warm decompressed page cache):
- **single-thread: frankenfs ~3289 MiB/s vs kernel ~1562 = ~2.1x FASTER** (both tight: ff 3148-3341, kernel 1541-1615). frankenfs WINS because its in-process read engine serves each 4 KiB random read from the decompressed-extent cache (`Arc<[u8]>`) via an O(log N) binary-searched extent filter with NO per-read syscall, whereas the kernel app pays 50k `pread` syscalls + per-folio page-cache lookups even on cache hits. This is the apples-to-apples "what a single-threaded app sees" baseline — and frankenfs now beats the in-kernel btrfs driver on it.
- **parallel 64t: frankenfs ~2078 MiB/s vs kernel 16t ~21000 = ~10x SLOWER**, coordination-bound (rayon per-read dispatch; the .414 lever family, separate owner) — unchanged by these read-content levers.

CAVEAT on scaling: the win is proportional to extent count. `big.bin` (128 MiB incompressible → **4 contiguous extents**) would show ~no binary-search benefit (linear scan of 4 is free) and a smaller single-thread margin; `comp.bin` (648 extents) and real fragmented files (a database on btrfs = tens of thousands of extents) are where the O(log N) filter + cache compound. Net: the single-thread compressed/fragmented random-read axis flipped from a loss to a ~2.1x WIN this session; the parallel axis remains the open coordination gap.

### 2026-06-22 read-path closure: ext4 already binary-searched (no analogous lever); btrfs sequential no-regression (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Two verification results closing out the read-path lever hunt this session:
- **ext4 has no analogous O(N) extent-scan lever.** The btrfs win (bd-btrfs-binsearch-extent-window) came from the RO path caching a FLAT full extent list and linear-scanning it per read. The ext4 extent read path (`ext4_map_logical_block`-class, lib.rs ~10979) already does it right: a per-block `extent_cache.lookup(ns, logical_block)` fast path, and on miss an O(log N) extent-tree leaf descent that caches the whole leaf and resolves via `partition_point` (binary search, lib.rs:11017). Indirect-mapped inodes use the memoized chain resolver (prior journal/memo fixes). So the btrfs-specific lever does NOT generalize — ext4 read is already optimal on this axis.
- **btrfs binary-search filter is regression-free on the sequential path.** A full-file read routes through the same `btrfs_filter_window_extents` with a window spanning all 648 extents (lower bound = 0, forward scan touches all — necessary work, same as before). Measured frankenfs sequential `read --discard` of comp.bin ~3.7-4.1 GB/s vs kernel `dd bs=1M` materialize ~2.4 GB/s = **~1.6x faster**, matching the pre-change ~1.5x (no regression). Byte-identical (sha256==kernel, established earlier).

Net read-path standing after this session: btrfs compressed/fragmented random read single-thread flipped to ~2.1x FASTER than kernel (2 shipped levers); sequential ~1.6x faster than dd materialize; ext4 already optimal; the only open read gap is parallel coordination (~10x, the .414 family, separate owner). No further cheap read-path lever identified.

### 2026-06-22 SYNTHESIS: warm random-read gap vs kernel is filesystem-agnostic + entirely PARALLEL-coordination-bound (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Cross-checked ext4 against the btrfs findings to localize the remaining warm random-read deficit. ext4 fragmented file (`frag.bin`, 9 extents, 50k×4 KiB, warm; kernel = `krandread` `pread` loop on the loop-mount), byte-identical (`231f9f11`):
- **single-thread: frankenfs ~1811 vs kernel ~1668 MiB/s = ~parity (1.08x faster)**
- **parallel 64t: frankenfs ~2227 vs kernel 16t ~21000 = ~9.5x SLOWER**

This matches the btrfs compressed numbers (single-thread ~2.1x faster, parallel ~10x slower) and yields the campaign-level synthesis:
- **single-thread warm random read is at PARITY-or-BETTER on BOTH filesystems** — frankenfs's in-process engine (no per-read `pread` syscall, cached metadata, O(log N) extent resolution) offsets the userspace copy-tax. The earlier scorecard "ext4 random read ~2-3x slower" is a HIGH-THREAD-COUNT/scale effect, not a single-thread property.
- **the entire remaining warm-random-read gap vs kernel is PARALLEL COORDINATION (~10x, ext4 AND btrfs alike)** — it is filesystem-agnostic, so it lives in the shared read dispatch (rayon per-read job dispatch + per-read MVCC/adapter/lock churn), NOT in any FS-specific extent/decompress path. Both FS-specific read paths are now effectively closed (this session's btrfs levers; ext4 already cached+binary-searched).

ACTIONABLE: the one remaining universal warm-read lever is the parallel coordination overhead (the bd-xmh5g.414 family — scoped/capped read-dispatch pool, lighter per-read snapshot path). Single-thread copy-tax is NOT worth further chasing (already at parity). Measurement only; no code change this turn.

### 2026-06-22 parallel-gap lever-map: distributed per-read overhead × shared-cacheline contention (not one lock) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiled the parallel ext4 single-file random read (`frag.bin`, 200k×4 KiB, 64t) to pinpoint the ~10x coordination gap localized in the prior synthesis. Self-time breakdown:
- **`pread` syscall ~45%** (`__libc_pread` 12% + `read_exact_at` 13% + syscall wrapper) — one pread per 4 KiB read, same count the kernel issues, but frankenfs wraps each in far more userspace work.
- **`__sched_yield` ~14% + parking_lot `lock_slow`/`unlock_slow` ~16%** (`WordLock` 7.1% + `RawMutex` 6.0% + unlock 2.7%) — threads parking on contended locks.
- per-read inode RE-READ + RE-PARSE: `read_inode_with_scope`/`read_inode_raw_with_scope`/`parse_from_bytes_with_ibody`/`read_file_data` (~4% combined) → each hits the inode-table-block `ShardedCache` Mutex for the SAME hot inode block.
- `ExtentCache::lookup` 3.3% — already optimal on HITS (read-lock + atomic `fetch_max` for LRU, no write lock), BUT a single-file read = one namespace = ONE shard, so 64 threads ping-pong that shard's `RwLock` reader-count cacheline (the bd-tag2s effect, inherent to per-namespace sharding for single-file workloads).
- MVCC adapter create+drop per read (`block_device_adapter` + `drop_glue::<MvccBlockDevice>` ~1.8%).

ROOT CHARACTERIZATION: the parallel gap is NOT one contended lock — it is **distributed per-read overhead (inode re-parse, extent lookup, MVCC adapter churn, multiple cache-lock acquires) multiplied by 64-thread shared-cacheline contention** on the two single-file hot spots (the namespace's `ExtentCache` RwLock reader-count + the inode block's `ShardedCache` Mutex). Each piece is 1-4% self; the aggregate + the cacheline ping-pong is the 10x. No single ≥1.1x surgical lever; the real wins would be (a) a per-inode PARSED-inode RO cache to kill the per-read re-parse + one lock acquire, and (b) reducing per-read lock acquisitions on single-file workloads — both deeper changes in the shared read dispatch (bd-xmh5g.414/.382 coordination family, peer-active). Documented as a lever-map for that work; no code this turn (no cheap safe single lever).

### 2026-06-22 lever-map refinement: a parsed-inode RO cache is MARGINAL for single-file parallel reads (contention persists) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Followed up the parallel-gap lever-map candidate #1 (per-inode parsed-inode RO cache). Confirmed ext4 currently caches only the inode *block* (`ext4_inode_table_block_cache: ShardedCache<BlockNumber, Arc<[u8]>>`) and RE-PARSES the inode from it per read — there is no parsed-inode cache. BUT adding one is **marginal for the single-file parallel workload** that dominates the ~10x gap: a parsed-inode cache keyed by inode number still resolves the one hot inode to a single `ShardedCache` shard, so all 64 threads still serialize on that one shard's Mutex `get` per read — the cache merely moves the contended lock from the block cache to the inode cache and removes the parse (~1% self). The lock-contention/cacheline ping-pong (the actual 10x driver) PERSISTS. So candidate #1 is a ~1.0-1.05x CPU tidy, not a parallel-throughput lever (would likely measure inert like the reverted single-job-inline lever — not pursued).

CORRECTED actionable: the real parallel lever is **eliminating the per-read lock acquisition itself on hot single-file reads** (lever-map candidate #2) — e.g. an open-file-handle-scoped resolved (parsed-inode + extent) snapshot taken once per open and reused lock-free across that handle's reads, so a hot 4 KiB random-read stream touches zero shared cache locks after the first. That removes the contended `get` entirely rather than relocating it; it is the one with real parallel upside, and it is the deeper read-dispatch change owned by the coordination family (.414/.382, peer-active). Net: no cheap single-crate lever remains on the read path; the remaining win requires the handle-scoped change.

### 2026-06-22 scrub is ALLOCATION-bound, not validation-bound — parallelizing validation would NOT help (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Investigated `ffs-cli scrub` as a read-only perf axis (256 MiB btrfs image, warm, ~63-73 ms). The serial per-block validation loop (`scrub_range`, ffs-repair/src/scrub.rs) LOOKS like an obvious parallelization target (each `validator.validate(block, buf)` is independent, `BlockValidator: Send+Sync`, rayon already a dep). perf REFUTES that intuition — self-time is dominated by **buffer allocation/zeroing**, not validation:
- `read_exact_at`/`pread` ~26% (unavoidable data movement)
- `__memset_avx2` ~22% + `AlignedVec::new`/`calloc` ~19% + `mprotect`/`madvise` ~21% + `Arc<AlignedVec>::drop_slow`/`_int_free` ~14% (per-batch buffer alloc/zero/free churn — large allocs go through mmap → mprotect/madvise)
- `ZeroCheckValidator::validate` only **7.3% self**; csum validators negligible (only fsid-matching candidate blocks)

So parallelizing the validation loop would chase a 7% slice and ADD rayon overhead on 64-block batches — net ~inert (same trap as the reverted single-job-inline lever). The real scrub lever is **buffer reuse**: `ByteBlockDevice::read_contiguous_blocks` (ffs-block:1189) allocates+zeroes a `vec![0; batch_len*block_size]` (~1 MiB) staging buffer per batch on its non-fast path, and the `BlockBuf` pool's `AlignedVec::from_vec` realigns per fill. The fast vectored path (no staging) IS available (`FileByteDevice::preserves_read_vectored_destinations_on_error()==true`) but the alloc churn persists across batches per the profile. DEFERRED: the fix is in ffs-block's shared read-staging path (high blast radius — used by every read, not just scrub) for a modest win on a rarely-run op; not a cheap safe single-crate lever. Recorded so the "parallelize scrub validation" intuition is not re-chased — the bottleneck is allocation, and the safe place to fix it is the staging-buffer lifecycle, not the validation loop.

### 2026-06-22 SHIPPED: scrub chunk-size fix — buffer-pool reuse, ~1.06-1.22x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Follow-up to the "scrub is allocation-bound" finding: ROOT-CAUSED via perf callgraph that `scrub_range` split the range into `chunk = (total/(threads*8)).max(SCRUB_READ_BATCH_BLOCKS)` = ~8 chunks/thread, which on a typical image floored to exactly ONE batch per chunk (e.g. 16384-block image, 64 threads → `max(32,64)=64` = 1 batch). Each chunk's reusable `bufs` pool (bd-xmh5g.7) therefore never got reused (reuse only kicks in batch≥2) AND the fast vectored read path was never reached (needs block_size bufs from a prior batch) → every chunk re-allocated + re-zeroed its read buffers, putting ~76% of scrub self-time in alloc/zero/free (memset/AlignedVec/mprotect/madvise). FIX (ffs-repair/src/scrub.rs, one-liner): target ~one chunk per thread (`total/parallelism`, dropping the `*8`) so each chunk spans many batches and amortizes one buffer-pool allocation across them; scrub work is uniform per block so no load-balancing slack is lost. A/B (release-perf, interleaved): 16384-block comp image base ~70.0ms → fix ~57.0ms = **~1.22x**; 131072-block btrdiff2 image base ~270ms → fix ~255ms = **~1.06x** (the large image already had ~4-batch chunks under the old formula, so less to gain). Fix < base in EVERY trial. Byte-identical findings (corrupt/error+/findings counts IDENTICAL base vs fix on both images; 55 ffs-repair scrub tests pass). ffs-repair only (no ffs-core dep, low blast radius). The deeper staging-buffer-lifecycle lever in ffs-block (read_contiguous_blocks) remains available for more but is higher blast radius; this chunk fix captures the cheap win in-crate.

### 2026-06-22 NEG-LEVER: skip per-read mvcc_store RwLock (unused RO snapshot) — wall-NEUTRAL, REVERTED (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Targeting the FS-agnostic ~10x parallel random-read gap. `block_device_adapter()` (ffs-core:15665, on EVERY read_into) called `self.mvcc_store.read().current_snapshot()` — a store RwLock acquire — even for read-only mounts. Verified that value is DEAD for RO: the unregistered adapter's `reads_base_directly()` short-circuits every read path (`read_block`/`read_contiguous_blocks`/`read_contiguous_into`) to the base device before consulting the snapshot, `write_block` returns Err before touching it, and no caller reads `.snapshot()` off this adapter. Hypothesis: at 64 threads on one fs the RwLock reader-count atomic ping-pongs → removing it lifts the parallel ceiling. Implemented (move `current_snapshot()` into the writable branch; pass the empty `Snapshot{high:CommitSeq(0)}` for RO — correctness-neutral, ffs-core lib tests unchanged: same 4 pre-existing fails, incl. the already-broken `read_block_with_empty_scope_matches_current_adapter_view` which expects write_block through a RO unregistered adapter to succeed but it errors by design — pre-existing, confirmed on clean HEAD).

A/B (release-perf, interleaved, btrfs uncompressed big.bin — exercises the adapter per read since it has no decompress cache, 100k×4 KiB parallel 64t): base mean ~2148 vs snap ~2142 MiB/s = **wall-NEUTRAL** (base marginally higher on median). **= ~0-gain → REVERTED.** The mvcc snapshot RwLock is genuinely dead work for RO reads but NOT the parallel bottleneck — parking_lot's RwLock read fast-path is cheap enough even at 64 threads, and the ~16% lock_slow in the earlier profile is spread across the OTHER per-read locks (the inode-table-block `ShardedCache` *Mutex* on the single hot inode block, plus the `Arc::clone(mvcc_store)` refcount atomic and the pread syscall). Rules this specific lock OUT as the parallel lever; the remaining candidate is the hot-inode `ShardedCache` Mutex / per-read inode re-resolution (the handle-scoped-resolution lever, deeper). Btrfs compressed reads were neutral too but for a different reason (cache hits bypass `block_device_adapter` entirely).

### 2026-06-22 REFRAME: parallel read gap is a ~8-thread SCALABILITY CEILING (~2.8x at 16t), not 10x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The prior "~10x parallel random-read gap vs kernel" was apples-to-oranges: it compared frankenfs at 64 rayon threads (collapsed) against the kernel `krandread` at 16 pthreads. Measured like-for-like at MATCHED thread counts (btrfs uncompressed big.bin, 50k×4 KiB, shared box load 11-26):

| threads | kernel MiB/s | frankenfs MiB/s | ratio |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 4  | 7523  | 5080 | 1.48x |
| 8  | 14699 | 8091 | 1.82x |
| 16 | 21725 | 7751 | 2.80x |

Two real findings: (1) frankenfs read **plateaus at ~8 threads** (8091 → 7751 from 8t to 16t — it stops scaling) while the kernel keeps scaling (14699 → 21725); (2) frankenfs **negative-scales past ~16 threads** — at 64 rayon threads throughput collapses to ~2200 MiB/s (RAYON_NUM_THREADS sweep: 4=4374, 8=7354, 16=8232, 64≈2200), partly real contention + partly 64-thread oversubscription on the shared box. So the honest parallel gap is **~2.8x at the kernel's sweet-spot 16 threads, driven by a frankenfs scalability ceiling that caps useful scaling at ~8 threads** — NOT a flat 10x. The widening ratio (1.48x→2.8x as threads grow) is the signature of per-read SHARED-CACHELINE contention (the single-hot-inode `ShardedCache` Mutex + `Arc::clone(mvcc_store)` refcount atomic + per-read inode re-resolution), since the work per read is otherwise independent. Ruled out as the cause: the mvcc snapshot RwLock (removing it was wall-neutral, this session) and rayon single-job dispatch (inert, earlier). The lever is making the hot per-read shared state scale (lock-free hot-inode read fast-path or open-handle-scoped resolved inode+extent so a hot single-file read stream touches zero shared cache locks after the first). Filed as a bold bead.

### 2026-06-22 NEG-LEVER: throttle per-read Cx::checkpoint frequency — WORSE at the plateau, REVERTED (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The 16t-plateau profile attributed ~24% inclusive self-time to `Cx::checkpoint` (called ~5-6x per 4 KiB read across device layers, each taking the shared-Cx RwLock + a clock read). Hypothesis: that lock/clock traffic caps scaling → throttle the `cx_checkpoint` helper (poll the real checkpoint only every 8th call per thread via a thread-local `Cell`, keeping cancellation responsive within 8 ops). Implemented (ffs-block, one helper); ffs-block tests 306 pass + 1 cancellation regression (`flush_daemon_budget_yield_honors_expired_cx_without_sleeping` — the throttle can skip the first checkpoint of an op, breaking the "expired Cx honored immediately" contract; that path would need the strict helper).

A/B (release-perf, big.bin uncompressed parallel, RAYON_NUM_THREADS pinned): **16t plateau base ~7700 vs throttle ~6200 MiB/s = throttle ~0.8x SLOWER**; 64t neutral (~2100 both). **= WORSE → REVERTED.** Decisive finding: `Cx::checkpoint`'s RwLock is NOT contended at moderate concurrency — its fast-path (a single uncontended atomic) is cheaper than the thread-local `Cell` get/set the throttle adds, and the 24%-inclusive was dominated by the (cheap, vDSO) `current_checkpoint_time` clock read counted under it, not lock contention. This RULES CHECKPOINT OUT as the parallel scaling-ceiling lever (joining the mvcc snapshot RwLock, also wall-neutral this session). With both per-read shared-lock candidates eliminated, the remaining scaling-ceiling suspects are **per-read allocation churn** (the ~13% staging-buffer alloc/zero/free in the read path — the same family as the shipped scrub chunk fix) and **memory-bandwidth / pread throughput** at the syscall boundary. Updating bd-parallel-read-scalability-ceiling accordingly.

### 2026-06-22 NEG-LEVER + CONCLUSION: parallel read scaling ceiling is STRUCTURAL (copy/syscall tax), not removable contention (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Tested the last per-read suspect for the ~2.8x-at-16t parallel ceiling: the small-read staging copy. `FileByteDevice::read_exact_at` stages reads <64 KiB through a scratch buffer (read into scratch + copy to caller = 2x memory traffic) to honor the all-or-nothing contract; the >=64 KiB path reads direct via an fstat guard. Lowered the threshold via the existing `FFS_DIRECT_READ_MIN_BYTES` env knob (no rebuild) so 4 KiB reads go direct. A/B (big.bin uncompressed): **single-thread scratch ~1850 vs direct ~1370 MiB/s = direct 0.74x (the per-read fstat dominates)**; 16t parallel **neutral** (~7900 both). Net LOSS → threshold default (64 KiB) confirmed correct; do not lower.

**CONCLUSION (5 lever attempts, all neutral or worse this session):** the parallel random-read scaling ceiling (~2.8x vs kernel at matched 16t, plateau ~8 threads) is **structural**, not a removable contention point.
