Eliminated as causes: mvcc snapshot RwLock (wall-neutral), `Cx::checkpoint` frequency (throttle 0.8x WORSE — its RwLock isn't contended), small-read staging copy (neutral parallel / worse single-thread), rayon single-job dispatch (inert, earlier), thread-local read scratch (inert, bd-cc-rscratch). The residual is the inherent **userspace pread + safe-copy memory-bandwidth tax** of a `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` FS vs the kernel's in-page-cache copy path — the same ~2x copy-efficiency ceiling documented across every warm read pattern (random/sequential/sparse). It is closable only via the forbidden mmap/splice path. The deep lock-free-hot-inode / handle-scoped-resolution candidates remain UNVERIFIED but are now LOW priority: every removable-contention experiment has been neutral/worse, strongly implying they would be too. Net honest standing: frankenfs read is **single-thread parity-or-faster than kernel** (no per-read syscall) and **~2.8x slower at the kernel's 16-thread sweet spot** due to the structural copy tax — not a contention bug.

### 2026-06-22 NEG-LEVER: pre-size scrub read buffers (skip batch-1 staging) — neutral, REVERTED (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Follow-on to the shipped bd-scrub-chunk-buffer-reuse: after that fix each chunk spans many batches but its FIRST batch still finds empty (len-0) buffers, falls to `read_contiguous_blocks`' slow path, and allocates a `vec![0; batch_len*block_size]` staging buffer once per chunk. Pre-sized the pool to block_size (`BlockBuf::zeroed`) so batch-1 takes the fast vectored path (no staging). Byte-identical (55 scrub tests pass; scrub findings identical base vs presize). A/B (release-perf): on a lightly-noisy run the small comp image flattered it (~1.46x, single lucky trial) but the robust 7-trial A/B on the larger btrdiff2 image (131072 blocks, box load ~33) was **neutral** (base median ~252ms vs presize ~257ms — base marginally ahead). **= ~0-gain → REVERTED.** The chunk-size fix already captured the buffer-reuse win; the residual staging is batch-1-only per chunk (~64 chunks for a 64-thread split) and its bytes equal the pre-sized pool's anyway, so eliminating it nets nothing measurable. Scrub allocation is now as low as the in-crate (ffs-repair) levers reach; further reduction would need the ffs-block read_contiguous_blocks staging lifecycle (shared read path, high blast radius) for a rare-op gain — not worth it.

### 2026-06-22 LOAD-INDEPENDENT confirm: random read issues kernel-identical preads (no amplification lever) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

To close the "is the random-read copy-efficiency gap a syscall/over-split lever?" question without timing (box load ~33, timing A/B unreliable), strace'd a frankenfs random 64 KiB read: **181 of 200 reads issue exactly one `pread64(…, 65536)`** (the handful of 16384/4096/896 preads are metadata) — i.e. one pread per random read, the SAME I/O unit the kernel `krandread` baseline issues. So the ~1.7-1.9x random-read copy-efficiency ceiling (frankenfs ~16 GB/s vs kernel ~31 GB/s at 64 KiB) is NOT read amplification or over-splitting (deterministically ruled out) — both issue identical preads; the residual is the in-kernel copy path's per-byte advantage (page-cache readahead/prefetch + zero userspace hop), structural under `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`. Combined with the 5 reverted-neutral contention levers and the structural parallel-ceiling close, the warm random-read gap is now exhaustively characterized as the copy/bandwidth tax — the documented endpoint, addressable only by the filed bd-zero-copy-read-path (io_uring registered buffers / mmap). No code lever remains on this path.

### 2026-06-22 SIMD-csum lever N/A — btrfs CRC32C already hardware-accelerated (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Checked the SIMD angle (user-invited): btrfs default csum is CRC32C, used in scrub tree-block verify, superblock verify, and (off-by-default) verified reads. `ffs_types::crc32c` delegates to the `crc32c` crate (workspace dep across 9 crates), which uses the x86 SSE4.2 hardware `crc32` instruction with runtime feature detection — already optimal, no software/table fallback to replace. The per-call `let _ = simd_capabilities()` is a `OnceLock::get_or_init` (cheap atomic load after first call), not per-call detection. So there is no SIMD csum lever. Combined with: zstd decompression via the `zstd` crate (already optimized), the AVX `__memmove` copy (glibc-optimal), and CRC32C hardware — the compute-bound paths in my lane are all already accelerated. No SIMD/branchless lever found on the read/scrub/csum paths.

### 2026-06-22 alloc/write hot path already optimized — no scan lever; lane survey complete (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Surveyed the write/allocation path (the one axis untouched by the read campaign) for an algorithmic lever, load-independently (box load ~38 — timing A/B is noise, so verified by code/complexity not benchmark). `bitmap_find_free` (ffs-alloc/src/lib.rs:201) is already **word-at-a-time** — a 64-bit scan using `(!word).trailing_zeros()` for the first free bit (8x fewer iterations than a byte loop), with a byte/bit fallback only for the unaligned head/tail — and a `SuccinctBitmap` (rank/select, succinct.rs) exists for O(1)-ish find_free on full groups. So block allocation's free-search is not a naive linear scan; no O(N)->O(log N) lever there.

LANE SURVEY COMPLETE (all load-independently verified this session): read = structurally copy/bandwidth-bound (kernel-identical preads, 5 contention levers neutral/worse, single-thread parity-or-faster); csum = hardware SSE4.2 CRC32C; decompress = zstd crate; copy = AVX `__memmove`; alloc free-search = word-at-a-time + succinct bitmap; scrub = chunk-buffer-reuse shipped. Every hot path in the read/scrub/csum/alloc lane is already optimized or structurally bounded. The remaining measured gaps need either the filed bd-zero-copy-read-path (io_uring/mmap, deep) or are out of this lane (FUSE write head-to-head; metadata + parallel-decompress coordination = peer-owned .423/.414). Under box load ~38, timing head-to-head is unreliable, so further levers must be load-independent algorithmic wins — and none remain in-lane. Documented endpoint.

### 2026-06-22 NEG-LEVER: per-thread buffer reuse in parallel rand-read (map_init) — neutral, REVERTED (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Noticed a methodology mismatch: the kernel `krandread` baseline `malloc`s one buffer per worker thread (reused across all its reads), while the frankenfs parallel rand-read harness allocated + zeroed a fresh `vec![0; size]` PER read (100k alloc/memset/free the kernel never pays). Hypothesized this inflated the frankenfs side of the head-to-head. Fixed with rayon `map_init` (one reused buffer per worker, matching krandread). A/B (big.bin uncompressed, 4 KiB, 16t — the alloc-heaviest case): base mean ~8514 vs map_init ~8171 MiB/s = **neutral-to-slightly-worse → REVERTED.** The per-read `vec![0; 4096]` is tcache-served (thread-local freelist, ~free) and the 4 KiB memset is cheap/amortized, so eliminating it saves nothing measurable — and map_init's per-item closure has its own small overhead. The "unfairness" was theoretical, not material: the parallel-read gap is NOT inflated by harness buffer allocation. This is the 6th read-path lever this session to measure neutral/worse, further corroborating that the warm random-read gap is the structural copy/bandwidth tax, not any removable per-read overhead (alloc included).

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED: lock-free hot-inode slot — parallel read negative-scaling FIXED, 64t ~4.3x (CORRECTS the "structural" close) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The parallel-read scaling ceiling I closed as "structural" was NOT fully structural — found and fixed the real contention. A single-file random-read stream resolves the SAME inode every read; `btrfs_ro_inode_extents` (a `ShardedCache`) took the key's shard **Mutex** (EXCLUSIVE — serializes even concurrent readers) per read, so all workers on one file convoyed on one lock → negative-scaling (64t collapsed to ~2500 MiB/s). Added an `arc-swap` `ArcSwapOption` single-slot lock-free "hot inode" cache in front (ffs-core): a hot single-file stream serves the inode lock-free, falling back to the sharded cache + publishing on a miss (last-writer-wins, same immutable RO extent list; gated to the RO branch). A/B (big.bin uncompressed, 100k×4 KiB parallel, box load ~13): **64t base ~2500 → hot ~10700 MiB/s = ~4.3x** (eliminates the collapse — frankenfs now SCALES past 8 threads); 16t ~1.15x; comp.bin 64t base ~2270 → ~9522 median. Byte-identical (sha256==kernel both files; 357 btrfs tests; conformance 237 pass + 1 pre-existing unrelated; fmt clean). Shipped `e9a09bfa`.

KEY CORRECTION to the earlier "5 levers neutral → structural" close: the neutral mvcc experiment removed an RwLock **read** (shared, non-serializing — so removing it was neutral), which MISLED me into generalizing "lock removal won't help." The actual culprit was a different lock TYPE — the `ShardedCache` **exclusive Mutex** on the single hot inode, which serializes readers and convoys under parallelism. LESSON: distinguish lock TYPE — a shared-read lock being neutral does NOT imply an exclusive Mutex on the same hot key is neutral; the Mutex was the scaling killer. The residual gap is now ~2x at matched threads (the copy tax) WITHOUT the negative-scaling collapse — the parallel ceiling is lifted.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED: ext4 lock-free hot-inode slot — parallel read negative-scaling FIXED, 64t ~5.6x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Applied the btrfs hot-inode fix (bd-...lockfree-slot, e9a09bfa) to ext4 — `bd-ext4-hot-inode-lockfree-slot-knc5f`. ext4 had the IDENTICAL negative-scaling collapse: a single-file random-read stream resolves the SAME inode every `read_into`, and `read_inode_with_scope` hits the `ext4_inode_table_block_cache` shard **Mutex** (exclusive — serializes concurrent readers) on the one hot inode-table block, so all 64 workers convoy on that lock. Measured baseline (big.dat 128 MiB, 50k×4 KiB, RAYON_NUM_THREADS pinned): **1t 1937, 8t 7310, 16t 7765, 64t 1984 MiB/s** — 64t collapses BELOW 8t (the btrfs signature). FIX (ffs-core): an `arc_swap::ArcSwapOption<(u64, Arc<Ext4Inode>)>` hot slot in front of the per-read inode resolution in `read_into`'s ext4 arm; a hot single-file stream serves the parsed inode lock-free (one arc-swap load + a thread-local struct clone — no shared state), missing → falls back to `read_inode_with_scope` and publishes (last-writer-wins). RO-gated (`!is_writable()`): the on-disk inode is immutable so the publish is safe; a writable mount skips the slot entirely (never read, never published).

A/B (interleaved, same fixture): 1t 1937→2037 (~1.05x), 8t 7310→8436 (~1.15x), 16t 7765→8833 (~1.14x), **64t 1984→11183 MiB/s = ~5.6x** (3-trial repeat under box load 26: base ~2040, hot ~10860 = ~5.3x, robust) — eliminates the collapse: 64t now SCALES past 16t (11183 > 8833), mirroring the btrfs result. Byte-identical (full-file sha256 hot == base == kernel mount: ab735822…). Compiled clean under `--deny clippy::pedantic --deny clippy::nursery --forbid unsafe_code` (the release-perf ffs-cli build succeeded). ffs-core `--lib` suite now CONFIRMED GREEN (ran the prebuilt test binary disk-neutral, no recompile): **1178 passed**, the only 4 failures are the documented clean-HEAD pre-existing fails (3× `btrfs_symlink*` + `read_block_with_empty_scope_matches_current_adapter_view`, all unrelated to this change). The change is a structural mirror of the already-shipped btrfs sibling (e9a09bfa), RO-gated, with downstream `&inode` uses unchanged (the inode stays an owned `Ext4Inode`), so blast radius is minimal. The clone-out-of-Arc approach (vs the btrfs Arc-clone) keeps the diff minimal — `Ext4Inode` is small/fixed-size with an inline i_block SmallVec, so the per-read clone is a thread-local memcpy and the win is purely skipping the shard Mutex. LESSON RE-CONFIRMED: the parallel-read scaling-ceiling killer across BOTH filesystems is the per-read **exclusive Mutex** on a single hot cache key (inode/inode-table-block), not the shared-read RwLocks (mvcc snapshot / extent_cache) which measured neutral — a lock-free single-slot front for the hot key lifts the ceiling.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐MEASUREMENT-ARTIFACT FIX: rand-read harness shared ONE Cx across all parallel reads (64t ~1.47x understated) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiling the post-hot-inode ext4 64t parallel random read (now ~10.9 GiB/s, ~1.7x vs kernel) showed the residual was dominated by `Cx::checkpoint` (26.85% self+inclusive) and `RawRwLock::lock_shared_slow` (31.84%) — NOT the copy tax. Root cause: `Cx::checkpoint`'s fast path takes the Cx's inner `RwLock` in **shared** mode (to read `fast_cancel` + snapshot the budget), and the `rand-read` harness created ONE `cx = cli_cx()` and shared it (`&cx`) across all parallel reads (ffs-cli/main.rs randread_cmd). So every `cx_checkpoint` (called 5-6× per 4 KiB read across device layers) on all 64 rayon workers ping-ponged that single Cx's reader-count cacheline → `lock_shared_slow`. **The real FUSE layer creates a fresh `Cx::for_request()` per request** (every fuse handler, ffs-fuse/lib.rs:2724), so a real mount NEVER shares a Cx across concurrent reads — the contention was a pure HARNESS artifact inflating the frankenfs side at high parallelism.

FIX (ffs-cli only): give each parallel read its own `cli_cx()` (= `Cx::for_request()`), exactly matching FUSE per-request semantics. A/B (big.dat 128 MiB ext4, 50k×4 KiB): shared-cx 8t 8049 / 16t 9216 / 64t 10933 → per-read-cx 8t 7614 / 16t 11572 / **64t 10933→~16000 MiB/s = ~1.47x** (3-trial median ~16000, robust). 8t is marginally slower (the honest per-op Cx construction cost FUSE always pays); the win grows with thread count as the shared-cacheline contention it removes is superlinear. Re-profile CONFIRMS: `Cx::checkpoint` 26.85%→**1.26%**, `lock_shared_slow` 31.84%→**10.53%**. Byte-identical (sha256 read == kernel mount). Fair 64t head-to-head is now frankenfs ~16000 vs kernel ~25000 MiB/s = **~1.5x** (was a misleading ~1.7-2.3x under the shared-Cx harness). LESSON: always give each parallel unit of work its own per-request Cx in benchmarks — a shared Cx's checkpoint RwLock is a 64-thread cacheline-contention artifact that FUSE (per-request Cx) never pays; like-for-like means matching the deployment's cancellation-scope granularity, not just the I/O. The hot-inode-Mutex fix (426979e3) remains a REAL win (the inode-table `ShardedCache` Mutex is shared fs-wide, contended in FUSE too); only the Cx contention was harness-only. NEXT real lever now exposed: `ExtentCache::lookup` (25% self, the ext4 per-block extent-cache shard RwLock — genuinely fs-shared, contended in FUSE) is the new top — a lock-free hot-extent path (mirroring btrfs's in-memory extent filter) is the follow-up.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED: ext4 lock-free hot-extent slot — removes the per-block ExtentCache RwLock, 64t ~1.2-1.35x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After the hot-inode Mutex fix (426979e3) and the per-request-Cx harness fix (f5ba3ab3), the 64t ext4 read profile's top self-time became `ExtentCache::lookup` (25% self, 14.6% BTreeMap query + ~10.5% `lock_shared_slow`): `resolve_extent` takes the extent cache's per-namespace shard `RwLock` in shared mode for EVERY logical block, so all readers of one hot file ping-pong that one shard's reader-count cacheline. Unlike the Cx contention this is GENUINELY fs-shared (a real FUSE mount, with per-request Cx, still shares the one `OpenFs` extent cache) — a real lever, not a harness artifact.

FIX (ffs-core): a lock-free `arc_swap::ArcSwapOption<(ns, Arc<[ExtentMapping]>)>` "hot extent list" slot. `resolve_extent` checks it first (lock-free arc-swap load + ns compare): on a match it resolves the block by in-memory `partition_point` over the sorted, non-overlapping mapping list — no RwLock, no per-block BTreeMap range query — mirroring btrfs's in-memory extent filter. Populated once per hot inode by `ext4_ensure_hot_extents` (full extent list via `collect_extents_with_scope`, converted with the SAME `logical_start/physical_start/actual_len/is_unwritten` mapping `walk_extent_tree_leaf` uses, so an in-memory resolve is byte-identical). Two safety gates: RO only (`!is_writable` — the on-disk tree can't change under the cached list) AND only when the inode is ALREADY hot (`inode_was_hot`: its `ext4_hot_inode` slot matched on a prior read), so a multi-file workload reading each inode once NEVER pays the full-tree walk to build the list. The new `ext4_resolve_block_from_mappings` is a verbatim copy of `resolve_extent`'s post-walk per-block translation (covering extent = last `logical_start <= block`; past-span / no-cover / zero-phys → hole).

A/B (big.dat 128 MiB ext4, 50k×4 KiB, per-request-Cx baseline, interleaved): 8t 7929→8384 (1.06x), 16t 11218→13598 (1.21x), **64t base ~14500 → hot ~17400 MiB/s median = ~1.2-1.35x** (4-trial interleaved under box load 14-21, hot beats base EVERY trial: base 13810/14635/14353/15965, hot 16850/19116/17081/17687). Byte-identical (full-file sha256 read == kernel mount: ab735822…, exercises the hot path across big.dat's 2-extent boundary). ffs-core `--lib` GREEN: **1178 passed**, only the 4 documented clean-HEAD pre-existing fails (3× btrfs_symlink* + read_block_with_empty_scope), zero new. Compiled clean under `--deny pedantic/nursery --forbid unsafe_code`. Coverage note: hole/unwritten resolution relies on the verbatim-mirror logic + the existing `resolve_extent` cache-path tests (no sparse-file fixture to hand); the end-to-end sha256 covers the multi-extent contiguous case. Fair 64t gap vs kernel now ~1.4x (kernel ~24000-25000). The three ext4 parallel-read levers this session (hot-inode Mutex, per-request Cx, hot-extent RwLock) together took 64t from a ~2000 MiB/s NEGATIVE-SCALING collapse to ~17400 MiB/s = ~8.7x, scaling cleanly past 16 threads.

### 2026-06-22 NEG-LEVER: Arc-share the hot ext4 inode (kill the per-read clone) — wall-NEUTRAL, REVERTED (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The hot-extent profile showed `Ext4Inode::clone` at ~8% self-time at 64t — my hot-inode slot serves the inode by cloning the small struct out of the `Arc` (so downstream `&inode` uses stay unchanged) instead of sharing the `Arc` like the btrfs slot does. Tried binding the inode as `Arc<Ext4Inode>` and dereferencing it downstream (`inode.as_ref()` at the 7 call sites), so a hot hit is a pure refcount bump with zero struct memcpy. Byte-identical (sha256 read == kernel). A/B (big.dat, 50k×4 KiB, 64t, interleaved x4 under box load ~20): base (clone-out) 16834/18147/20918/17674 vs arc 20148/17377/17630/17011 = **wall-NEUTRAL** (base ahead in 3 of 4 noisy trials). **= ~0-gain → REVERTED.** The 8% clone is per-thread CPU that overlaps the pread + shared-lock critical path (the section is I/O/coordination-bound at 64t, not CPU-bound), so eliminating it frees already-idle CPU without moving the wall — the same "N% self-time in a parallel section is CPU-positive but wall-neutral when the section is I/O/coordination-bound" pattern as the btrfs decompress memmove (.413). The clone-out form is also the smaller diff (downstream `&inode` unchanged), so it stays. Confirms the ext4 64t residual is now the structural pread/copy tax (30-32% in `read_exact_at`/`pread`), not the per-read inode handling — the documented copy-tax endpoint, same as btrfs.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED: cache the read-only MVCC snapshot (lock-free) — removes per-read mvcc_store RwLock, 64t ~1.24x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After the hot-inode/hot-extent/Cx fixes, the 64t ext4 read profile still showed ~12.7% `lock_shared_slow` NOT attributable to the extent cache (bypassed) or Cx (per-request now). Root cause: BOTH `with_latest_scope` (once per `read_into`) and `block_device_adapter` (per block read) call `self.mvcc_store.read().current_snapshot()` — taking the store's `RwLock` in shared mode every read — so all 64 workers ping-pong that one reader-count cacheline. Unlike the per-read `Ext4Inode::clone` (parallel CPU, overlaps → wall-neutral), lock contention is SERIALIZATION (threads park/spin on the lock), so removing it moves the wall.

A read-only mount never commits, so `current_snapshot()` is INVARIANT. FIX (ffs-core): a `OnceLock<Snapshot>` (`ro_snapshot`) + a `latest_snapshot()` helper — writable mounts re-read the live snapshot (read-your-writes unchanged), RO mounts resolve it once under the lock then serve it from the lock-free OnceLock (an atomic acquire) on every later read. Wired into both `with_latest_scope` and `block_device_adapter`. (Supersedes the earlier reverted-neutral attempt that touched only `block_device_adapter` and was masked by the then-dominant extent/Cx locks — covering `with_latest_scope` too, and caching the REAL snapshot instead of passing an empty one, is what makes it land now.)

A/B (big.dat 128 MiB ext4, 50k×4 KiB, hot-extent baseline, interleaved x5 under box load ~20): base 14259/16309/16752/16832/18505 vs ro **20762/21526/24700/18417/18074 MiB/s = ~1.24x median** (ro wins ALL 5 trials; range 1.08-1.47x). Byte-identical (sha256 read == kernel mount). ffs-core `--lib` GREEN: **1178 passed**, only the 4 documented pre-existing fails, zero new (despite `with_latest_scope` being used by every op). Clean under `--deny pedantic/nursery --forbid unsafe_code`. KEY LESSON corrected: the earlier "mvcc snapshot RwLock removal is wall-neutral" conclusion was CONDITIONAL on the extent/Cx locks dominating — once those were removed the mvcc read became the exposed serial point, and removing it (both sites, real cached snapshot) is a real ~1.24x. The four ext4 parallel-read levers this session (hot-inode Mutex, per-request Cx, hot-extent RwLock, RO-snapshot RwLock) took 64t from a ~2000 MiB/s NEGATIVE-SCALING collapse to ~21000 MiB/s ≈ kernel parity-ish (~24000-25000), scaling cleanly past 16 threads — the parallel-read scaling ceiling is essentially closed.

**RO-snapshot transfers to btrfs (fs-agnostic confirm):** `with_latest_scope` + `block_device_adapter` are on the btrfs read path too. A/B on a btrfs-convert fixture (/big.bin 128 MiB, 64t, 40k×4 KiB, interleaved x4): base (hot-inode only) 11384/14917/14894/15481 vs ro 15895/16872/16722/14206 = **~1.09x median** (ro wins 3 of 4; smaller than ext4's 1.24x because btrfs's read path carries more per-read work — extent-tree descent fallbacks, decompression checks — diluting the lock removal's share). So the RO-snapshot lever lifts BOTH filesystems' parallel random read; the byte-identity is structural (it removes a lock, never touches data — the ext4 sha256==kernel check covers correctness).

### 2026-06-22 CONCLUSION: ext4/btrfs parallel random-read scaling ceiling CLOSED — residual is structural pread + harness rayon (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After the 4 levers (hot-inode Mutex, per-request Cx, hot-extent RwLock, RO-snapshot RwLock), the rosnap 64t ext4 profile shows `lock_shared_slow` is GONE (was 31.84%→…→0): every per-read shared-lock contention point is eliminated. The remaining top self-time is (1) `read_exact_at`/`__libc_pread` 34-35% — the structural userspace pread + safe-copy tax of a `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` FS, the documented endpoint closable only via the filed io_uring/mmap zero-copy path; and (2) `crossbeam steal` 7.97% — rayon work-stealing over the harness's 50k tiny per-read jobs, a HARNESS parallelism artifact (a real FUSE mount dispatches to its own worker threads, not a rayon `par_iter`, so it never pays this). The smaller residuals (`Ext4Inode::clone` 3.1% [reverted as wall-neutral], Cx `checkpoint_budget_exhaustion` 3.4%, memmove 3%) are per-thread CPU that overlaps the I/O-bound critical path. NET: ext4 64t parallel random read went from a ~2000 MiB/s NEGATIVE-SCALING collapse to ~21000 MiB/s (≈ kernel ~24-25k, ~1.2x) scaling cleanly past 16 threads — the parallel-read scaling ceiling that was the campaign's biggest documented gap is CLOSED to its structural floor on BOTH filesystems. NEXT un-dominated gaps (need a new fixture or are out of this lane): multi-file parallel read (grep -r/tar — the single-slot hot-inode/hot-extent caches thrash when many inodes are concurrently hot; a small N-way lock-free set would generalize them, but needs a many-small-file fixture to measure); btrfs compressed parallel read (decompress coordination, peer-owned .414); FUSE write head-to-head (unmeasured).

### 2026-06-22 NEW GAP + NEG-LEVER: multi-file parallel read ~2.9x vs kernel; nested-rayon skip wall-NEUTRAL, REVERTED (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

With the single-file parallel random-read ceiling closed, probed the MULTI-FILE workload (grep -r/tar/build — many files read concurrently, where the single-slot hot-inode/hot-extent caches thrash). Built a 256-file × 256 KiB ext4 fixture (mke2fs -d) and a FAIR in-process threaded kernel reader (`/tmp/kmultiread.c` — opens+reads all files with 64 pthreads, no per-file process, unlike `xargs cat` which is ~8x slower purely from 256 fork+exec). Fair head-to-head (64MB, 64t): kernel ~12652 MiB/s vs frankenfs `walk --read-data --parallel` ~4385 MiB/s = **~2.9x slower** — a real un-dominated gap. Profile decomposes it: ~41% `pread` (structural copy tax), **~27% rayon coordination** (`steal` 10.7% + `bridge_producer_consumer` 8% + `StackJob` 7.9% — NESTED `par_iter`: `read_file_data` fans each small file's ~2 chunks onto the pool while the outer per-file `par_iter` already saturates it), ~1% `arc_swap::Debt::pay_all` (the hot-inode slot thrashing its `store()` on every cold inode — a small multi-file regression from my own lever).

LEVER TRIED: skip `read_file_data`'s inner chunk `par_iter` when already inside a rayon worker (`rayon::current_thread_index().is_some()`) or ≤1 job — keeping the chunk-overlap win only for a top-level large single-stream read (main thread). A/B (multi-file walk, interleaved x4): base 87137/104696/97058/70430 vs nest 99567/92990/78972/73356 = **wall-NEUTRAL** (each wins 2 of 4; absolute ~5x worse than an unloaded run because box load was ~29 — timing unreliable). Large single-file sequential read unregressed (base 71158/86725 vs nest 73907/80151, neutral). **= ~0-gain (and unmeasurable under load 29) → REVERTED.** The ~27% rayon coordination is per-thread CPU that overlaps the pread-bound critical path (same "self-time ≠ wall when I/O-bound" pattern as the inode clone), so removing it doesn't move the wall — AND under load ~29 timing A/B is pure noise (the documented "load-independent algorithmic wins only above load ~30" rule). The multi-file ~2.9x gap is REAL and stands as the next lever target, but needs (a) a low-load window for reliable timing and (b) a load-independent angle: the structural pread copy tax (io_uring/mmap, filed) dominates at 41%, and the rayon overhead is harness-parallelism-shaped (a real FUSE mount dispatches per-request, not via a nested `par_iter`). Filed as the next bold bead.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐CORRECTION+SHIPPED: nested-rayon skip IS a ~1.09x multi-file win (the "neutral" was load-29 noise) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The prior entry reverted the `read_file_data` nested-`par_iter` skip as "wall-neutral" — but that A/B ran under box load ~29 (absolute walk times ~5x inflated, pure noise). RE-MEASURED under reliable load ~9-10 (multi-file walk --read-data --parallel, 256-file ext4 fixture, interleaved x6): base (rosnap) 16604/16735/15080/15862/15456/14836 vs nest 15263/14426/14834/14274/13750/14401 us = **~1.09x, nest wins ALL 6 trials**. So the lever is REAL — confirming the ~27% nested-rayon coordination (`steal`+`bridge`+`StackJob`) is NOT fully I/O-overlapped; skipping the inner chunk `par_iter` when already inside a rayon worker (`rayon::current_thread_index().is_some()`) or with ≤1 job removes enough of it to move the wall. UN-REVERTED and SHIPPED. ffs-core `--lib` GREEN: **1178 passed**, only the 4 documented pre-existing fails, zero new. Clean under `--deny pedantic/nursery --forbid unsafe_code`. Large single-file sequential read unregressed (it runs on the main thread → `nested=false` → keeps the 32-block chunk-overlap win). LESSON (re-affirmed): under box load ≳25-30 a timing A/B is unmeasurable — a "neutral" result there is NOT evidence of no-gain; re-measure in a low-load window before reverting. Multi-file parallel read gap now ~2.7x vs kernel (was ~2.9x); the residual is the structural pread copy tax (41%, io_uring/mmap — bd-kdmu4).

**Post-nested-fix multi-file profile (lane characterized):** with the inner `par_iter` skipped, the multi-file walk profile is `pread` 43.6% (structural copy tax) + ~25% OUTER `walk_one_dir` per-inode `par_iter` coordination (`steal`/`bridge`/`StackJob` — ffs-cli walk-harness parallelism; a real FUSE mount dispatches each getattr/read as a separate per-request worker, never via this nested rayon, so it's a harness artifact not a real-fs cost) + `arc_swap::Debt::pay_all` 2.1% (the single-slot `ext4_hot_inode` `store()` thrashing on every cold small-file inode — a minor multi-file regression from the hot-inode lever, since small files in a walk are read once and never re-hit the slot). So the REAL-fs residual of the multi-file ~2.7x gap is the structural pread tax (bd-kdmu4, io_uring/mmap); the arc-swap thrash would be cured by the N-way lock-free hot cache (or a size-gated store that skips small files) but is only ~2% and unmeasurable under the harness-rayon-dominated wall. Multi-file lane characterized to its structural floor.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐⭐⭐SHIPPED: write path ~5x — gate an O(N) evidence-only version-chain scan off the commit hot path (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

FIRST write-path measurement this session (built `ffs-cli write-bench`: enable_writes + write loop, each write a full MVCC commit; kernel baseline = RW loop-mount pwrite via `/tmp/kwrite.c`). Fair head-to-head (big.dat ext4, 20k×4 KiB): frankenfs ~75-95 MiB/s vs kernel buffered+fsync ~600 MiB/s = **~6.9x slower** — the biggest documented gap. Profile: **`MvccStore::release_snapshot` 72% self-time**. ROOT CAUSE (proven by a stub experiment: stubbing the call → write 82→~420 MiB/s = ~5x): `release_snapshot` (and a sibling chain-pressure path) eagerly called `versions_eligible_at_watermark` — an **O(tracked_blocks) scan of every version chain** — on EVERY commit (the watermark advances each write), purely to populate one `info!(target: "ffs::mvcc::evidence")` field. ⭐KEY GOTCHA: making it a lazy `info!` FIELD EXPRESSION did NOT help (wall-neutral) — the `fmt`+`EnvFilter` subscriber registers the callsite as `Interest::sometimes`, so tracing evaluates the field then filters at runtime → the scan still ran with the target disabled. FIX: gate the whole thing behind an explicit runtime `tracing::enabled!(target: "ffs::mvcc::evidence", Level::INFO)` so the scan only runs when a subscriber will actually record the event (both the `release_snapshot` and `force_advance_oldest_snapshot` sites).

A/B (interleaved x3/x2): seq write 75→~400 MiB/s = **~5.3x**, random 87→~430 = **~4.9x**. Write gap vs kernel: ~6.9x → **~1.4x**. Byte-identical (OLD vs GATE written-image sha256 IDENTICAL — purely a log-scan removal, commit data path untouched). Evidence log PRESERVED: with `RUST_LOG=ffs::mvcc::evidence=info` it still emits `snapshot_advanced` + `versions_eligible` on every commit (50/50). ffs-mvcc `--lib` GREEN (480 passed, 0 failed; the direct `versions_eligible_at_watermark` unit tests unaffected — the function body is unchanged, only its CALL is gated). Clean under `--deny pedantic/nursery --forbid unsafe_code`. ⭐LESSON: a `tracing` field expression is NOT a free lazy guard under a dynamic `EnvFilter` (Interest::sometimes → eager eval); an expensive observability computation on a hot path must be gated by an explicit `enabled!` check. The write/commit path was never profiled until this session — one disabled-log O(N) scan was costing ~80% of every write.

### 2026-06-22 NEG-LEVER: full-block write builds buffer from slice (skip the wasted zero-init) — wall-NEUTRAL, REVERTED (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After the commit-scan gate (b1619f0b, write ~5x), the write profile's top was per-write buffer alloc: `_int_malloc` 26.7% + `calloc` 24.7% + `memset` 23%. The full-block-write branch in `ext4_write` did `vec![0u8; bs]` (calloc-zero) then `copy_from_slice` the full 4 KiB over it — the zero-init is 100% overwritten. Built the block buffer directly from the source slice (`data[..].to_vec()` = one alloc + copy, no memset) for the full-block case (partial writes unchanged). Byte-identical (gate vs nz written-image sha256 IDENTICAL). A/B (big.dat, 20k×4 KiB, interleaved x8 under load ~13): avg gate 431 vs nz 421 MiB/s, **nz wins only 3/8 = wall-NEUTRAL** (a noisier x6 earlier flattered it 5/6 — noise). **= ~0-gain → REVERTED.** The 23% `memset` self-time fully OVERLAPS the alloc + commit critical path (same "self-time ≠ wall when the section is alloc/commit-bound" pattern as the ext4 inode clone) — removing it frees already-overlapped CPU without moving the wall. The dominant cost is the per-write ALLOCATION itself (`malloc`), which is fundamental: each write creates a new immutable block version (`Arc<AlignedVec>`) stored in the MVCC version chain, so the buffer cannot be pooled/reused. The write path's real residual after the scan-gate fix (~1.4x vs kernel) is per-write allocation + the commit's `apply_fcw_commit` (~10%), both structural to the MVCC-versioned write model — not a removable zero-init. Write lane characterized to its structural floor.

### 2026-06-22 write lane at structural floor + prune_safe antipattern-sweep (defensive, unmeasured-in-CLI) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After the commit-scan gate (b1619f0b, write ~5x → ~1.4x vs kernel), profiled the residual two ways: (1) big-file random writes — per-write `Arc<AlignedVec>` version alloc (malloc 27% + memcpy) + `apply_fcw_commit` (~10%); (2) a SMALL-file hammer (50000 writes to a 64 KiB/15-block file → ~3300 overwrites/block, to force version-chain growth + chain-pressure pruning) — measured **937 MiB/s** (FASTER than big-file writes: tiny hot working set, no allocation, chains stay short — pruning is NOT a collapse). The hammer profile's top is `memmove` 34% (copy each 4 KiB block into its new immutable version) + `apply_fcw_commit` 16% + alloc ~26% + `crc32c` 4% — ALL fundamental to the MVCC-versioned write model (every write = a new immutable, checksummed block-version copy). No `prune_safe`/`version_count` in either profile: pruning is cheap, not a hot path. So the write path is at its **structural floor** — the one removable cost (the disabled-log O(N) commit scan) was captured by b1619f0b; the rest is the inherent copy+alloc+checksum of versioned writes (closable only by a different write model: batch/group commit, or non-versioned in-place — a large redesign, not a lever).

ANTIPATTERN SWEEP (defensive, NOT a measured lever): found a sibling of the b1619f0b disabled-log O(N) scan — `MvccStore::prune_safe` calls `version_count()` (an O(tracked_blocks) chain-length sum) TWICE per prune, ONLY to compute `freed`/`remaining` for a `debug!`/`trace!` gc log. Gated both behind `tracing::enabled!(Level::DEBUG)` (the pruning itself always runs). HONEST CAVEAT: `prune_safe` is the GC-daemon / chain-pressure path and is NOT hot in any CLI benchmark available (the no-FUSE write-bench never spawns the mvcc_gc daemon; the hammer's chain pruning didn't surface it), so this has **no measured CLI ratio** — it is a zero-risk dead-work removal (the scans only ever fed disabled logs) completing the antipattern sweep, expected to help the FUSE `mvcc_gc` daemon's per-cycle CPU. ffs-mvcc `--lib` GREEN (480 passed, 0 failed). Shipped as hygiene, explicitly flagged unmeasured.

### 2026-06-22 NO-GAP: large-directory lookup — frankenfs at parity-or-FASTER than kernel warm despite O(N) linear scan (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Investigated a suspected algorithmic gap: `Ext4ImageReader::lookup` (ext4.rs:5027) LINEAR-SCANS every directory block (`for lb in 0..num_blocks`) and does NOT use the ext4 htree (dx hashed B-tree) index, even though ffs-dir has the hash/find primitives — so lookup is O(N_blocks) vs the kernel's O(log N) htree. Built a `ffs-cli lookup-bench` harness (paginated readdir to collect ALL names across all dir blocks — a single readdir page biases names to early blocks and makes a linear scan terminate early, hiding the cost) + a kernel `stat` baseline (`/tmp/kstat.c`), and htree-indexed fixtures created via the KERNEL (mount RW + create files; `mke2fs -d` makes FLAT dirs the kernel would also linear-scan → no gap — must use kernel-built htree dirs, confirmed via `lsattr` 'I' flag). Measured (warm, htree dirs, names spanning all blocks): **12000 entries: frankenfs ~133k vs kernel ~122k lookups/s; 60000 entries: frankenfs ~140k vs kernel ~92k lookups/s** — frankenfs is at parity-or-FASTER, and its throughput does NOT degrade with dir size. So despite the O(N) linear scan, there is **NO warm lookup gap**: the per-block scan is ~50 ns over the RO block cache (`ext4_file_data_block_cache`), and frankenfs's in-process lookup has NO per-call syscall, whereas the kernel pays a ~10 us `stat` syscall per lookup — the syscall overhead dominates the kernel's htree advantage at these sizes, so frankenfs WINS. The htree index would only help (a) COLD (each dir block = a disk seek — unmeasurable on tmpfs) or (b) VERY large dirs (>~100k entries, where N×50 ns exceeds the syscall cost). NOT a warm lever — frankenfs already dominates this workload. Shipped the `lookup-bench` harness (useful for the cold/huge-dir case) and filed the htree-index implementation as a latent bead. LESSON: an O(N) algorithm is not automatically a gap — frankenfs's structural advantage (no syscall per metadata op, warm block cache) offsets a worse asymptotic constant at realistic sizes; measure before assuming the textbook complexity wins.

### 2026-06-22 NO-GAP: full readdir of a large dir is O(N), NOT O(N²) — snapshot cache works (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Hypothesized an O(N²) readdir: `Ext4ImageReader::read_dir` reads ALL `num_blocks` with no offset awareness, and `FsOps::readdir(offset)` filters from the full list — so a paginated full enumeration (page cap `READDIR_SNAPSHOT_PAGE_MAX = 512`) could re-read the whole directory per page. DISPROVEN by a scaling test: `walk --no-stat` (readdir-only) on a 12000-entry htree dir = 50.9 ms vs a 60000-entry dir (5×) = 192 ms = **3.78× for 5× entries ⇒ O(N)** (sub-linear, not the ~25× an O(N²) would show). The `slice_readdir_snapshot` / `readdir_snapshot_serve` mechanism (a cached full `Arc<Vec<DirEntry>>` listing sliced by `partition_point` per page, invalidated on dir mutation) IS serving paginated enumeration in O(page), so a full `ls`/`find` is O(N) total — no algorithmic readdir gap. A vs-kernel constant-factor (frankenfs ~192 ms vs kernel `ls -f` ~34 ms for 60000 entries) was observed but is UNRELIABLE: measured under box load ~52-71 (other agents saturating the box — timing dead above load ~30, the documented rule). The per-entry readdir constant (parse_dir_block + `DirEntry{name: Vec<u8>}` per entry + snapshot Arc) MAY have removable overhead, but it needs a low-load window to measure — filed as a follow-up; not chased under load 71 (would be pure noise). Net: readdir is algorithmically sound (O(N), cached); lookup is parity-or-faster (prior entry); frankenfs metadata-read is at parity-or-better than kernel on every cleanly-measurable warm workload.

### 2026-06-22 GAP FOUND (load-blocked): readdir inode-table prefetch rayon coordination dominates htree-dir readdir (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiled `walk --no-stat` (readdir-only) of a 60000-entry htree dir (perf self-time % is LOAD-INDEPENDENT, valid even though the box was at load 45-97 from other agents). DAMNING: `prefetch_ext4_readdir_inode_table_blocks` rayon fan-out dominates — `StackJob` 31% + `__sched_yield` 30% + `crossbeam steal` 18% + `pthread_create`/`mprotect`(thread-stack) ~17% + `calloc` 17%. Root cause: the readdir inode-table prefetch (a speculative warm-the-getattr-cache optimization) fires per readdir PAGE (lib.rs:30329/30354) unconditionally, and for an htree directory the entries are returned in HASH order, so a 512-entry page maps to up to 512 SCATTERED inode-table blocks — exceeding the serial threshold (`blocks.len() < current_num_threads()`) → it fans out onto rayon, and the per-page coordination (futex yield/steal/thread-spawn) dwarfs the actual block reads. For a `--no-stat`/pure-readdir consumer (`ls -f`, counting, `find -type d`) the entire prefetch is WASTED (no getattr follows). Filed bd-... P1. Fix options: (a) skip prefetch for readdir-only consumers (zero-risk, needs a stat-intent flag); (b) nested-rayon guard (`current_thread_index().is_some()` → serial) mirroring the shipped read_file_data fix (3e94e916); (c) raise the serial threshold so scattered-inode pages stay serial. NOT shipped this turn: the box is externally saturated (load 45→97 from peer agents all session; timing A/B is pure noise above ~load 30, the documented rule), so the wall ratio of any fix is unmeasurable right now — and measure-or-revert forbids shipping a speculative perf change blind. The profile evidence is strong and load-independent; this is a high-confidence lever pending a low-load window. (readdir itself is O(N) — the snapshot cache works; this is a constant-factor coordination cost, not an algorithmic one.)

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED: skip readdir inode-prefetch for readdir-only walks — ~2.25x large-dir readdir (bd-neteo) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Follow-through on bd-neteo (the inode-prefetch rayon coordination found via load-independent profiling). The readdir inode-table prefetch warms the getattr cache, but a readdir-ONLY consumer (`ls -f`, name enumeration, `getdents` count) never reads those blocks, and on a large htree dir its rayon fan-out (hash-ordered entries → up to ~512 scattered inode-table blocks/page) dominated ~60% of readdir self-time. FIX (ffs-core): a `readdir_prefetch_disabled` `AtomicBool` (default OFF — the default path is byte-identical to before) + `set_readdir_prefetch_disabled` setter, gating both `prefetch_ext4_readdir_inode_table_blocks` calls; the ffs-cli walk sets it when `--no-stat && !--read-data` (a pure readdir that touches no inode). Profile-confirmed (load-independent): `prefetch_ext4_readdir_inode_table_blocks` GONE, `sched_yield` 30%→5.3%, `crossbeam steal` 18%→3%. WALL A/B (walk --no-stat, 60000-entry htree dir, interleaved x5 under box load ~24 — measurable again after the box freed from a peer-driven load-106 spell): old (prefetch) ~44362 vs new (skip) ~19682 us median = **~2.25x** (new wins all 5 trials, 44→20 ms). vs kernel `ls -f` ~34 ms: the prefetch had made frankenfs readdir SLOWER than the kernel (44 ms); skipping it makes it FASTER (20 ms). Byte-identical readdir output (60000/60000 entries old==new). ffs-core `--lib` GREEN (1178 passed, only the 4 documented pre-existing fails). Clean under `--deny pedantic/nursery --forbid unsafe_code`. The WITH-stat prefetch tradeoff (is the fan-out net-negative even when getattr follows? → serial-always or nested-guard) remains open in bd-neteo for a low-load cold/warm measurement. LESSON: a speculative cache-warming prefetch is a LOSS for the consumer that doesn't use it — gate speculation on caller intent; and the box DID free up (load 106→24), so a measurement deferred for saturation became obtainable — patience on load beats shipping blind.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED follow-up: readdir inode-prefetch is net-NEGATIVE even WITH-stat (warm) — env knob + finding (bd-neteo) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Tested whether the readdir inode-prefetch helps the COMMON with-stat path (`ls -l`: readdir + getattr each entry) via an `FFS_NO_READDIR_PREFETCH` env knob (ffs-cli) that disables it for any walk. A/B (walk WITH getattr, 60000-entry htree dir, interleaved x4, box load ~53 — off wins EVERY trial despite the load): prefetch-on ~75363 vs prefetch-off ~52933 us median = **~1.4x faster WITHOUT the prefetch**. So the speculative inode-table prefetch is net-NEGATIVE WARM even when getattr DOES follow: its rayon fan-out coordination (on a large htree dir, up to ~512 scattered inode-table blocks/page) costs MORE than the warm getattr-cache hits it saves (warm inode-block reads are cheap RAM hits, the coordination is futex yield/steal/thread-spawn). This matches the codebase's OWN prior note (the serial-guard comment: the fan-out "outweighs the cold-I/O overlap... measured ~1.7x slower even COLD") — the fan-out is just counterproductive; the existing `blocks.len() < current_num_threads()` serial guard simply doesn't cover htree dirs whose hash-ordered entries scatter inodes across >64 blocks/page. SHIPPED the `FFS_NO_READDIR_PREFETCH` opt-in knob (low-risk, lets warm-dominated deployments take the ~1.4x). The clean DEFAULT fix — raise the serial threshold so scattered-inode pages serialize the prefetch (keeping cache-warming, dropping the fan-out) — is the next step in bd-neteo: it touches the default readdir path so wants a stable-low-load A/B (box load oscillated 24→106 this session) + a cold check; warm evidence + the prior cold note both point to it being a broad win. Net so far: readdir-only large-dir walk ~2.25x (shipped default, 62f77460), with-stat ~1.4x (opt-in knob); frankenfs large-htree-dir readdir went from SLOWER than kernel `ls -f` (44ms) to FASTER (20ms).

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED: serialize the readdir inode-prefetch (drop the fan-out) — ~1.2x with-stat default, no cold risk (bd-neteo) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The default fix for bd-neteo (the inode-prefetch rayon fan-out). After the no-stat skip (62f77460, ~2.25x) and the FFS_NO_READDIR_PREFETCH knob (~1.4x warm with-stat by skipping the prefetch entirely), measured the SAFE default: make the prefetch ALWAYS serial (remove the `into_par_iter` path) — it still warms the getattr cache (the prefetch's purpose) but drops the never-beneficial parallel dispatch. Justification: my warm A/B (1.4-2.25x worse WITH the fan-out) AND the codebase's own serial-guard note ("~1.7x slower even COLD — coordination outweighs the cold-I/O overlap"); the old `blocks.len() < current_num_threads()` guard serialized small pages but let htree dirs (hash-ordered → up to ~512 scattered inode-table blocks/page) fan out. A/B (walk WITH getattr, 60000-entry htree dir, interleaved x6 under box load ~36): fan-out ~65000 vs serial ~54000 us median = **~1.2x** (serial wins ALL 6 trials). Less than the prefetch-OFF 1.4x because serial still READS the inode blocks (just serially) — keeping the cache-warming so a COLD getattr still benefits (no cold regression; serial cold ≈ no-overlap but the getattr would read those blocks anyway), whereas OFF skips them (faster warm, colder cold). Byte-identical readdir output (60000==60000, the prefetch never affects the dirent list). ffs-core `--lib` GREEN (1178 passed, only the 4 documented pre-existing fails). Clean under `--deny pedantic/nursery --forbid unsafe_code` (removed the now-unused rayon prelude import). Net readdir family: no-stat ~2.25x (default), with-stat ~1.2x (default, safe) / ~1.4x (FFS_NO_READDIR_PREFETCH opt-in, warm). frankenfs large-htree-dir readdir was SLOWER than kernel `ls -f` (44ms with fan-out); now FASTER. bd-neteo RESOLVED. LESSON: when a speculative parallel optimization is net-negative, serializing it (keep the work, drop the dispatch) is the safe default — it preserves the intended benefit (cache-warming) while removing the measured coordination loss, avoiding the cold/warm tradeoff that a full skip carries.

### 2026-06-22 NO-GAP: with-stat metadata walk (ls -l) — frankenfs FASTER than kernel readdir, even (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After resolving the readdir prefetch (bd-neteo), profiled + benched the with-stat walk (`ls -l`: readdir + getattr each of 60000 htree-dir entries, the heaviest common metadata workload). Head-to-head (warm, load ~14): frankenfs `walk` (with getattr) **51593 us** vs kernel `find -printf` (readdir, NO stat) **79967 us** — frankenfs's full readdir+getattr is FASTER than the kernel's readdir ALONE. (`find | xargs stat` was 9.9 SECONDS, but that's 60000 fork+exec of a stat process — process-churn-bound, unfair; the in-process numbers are the fair comparison.) So the with-stat walk is DOMINATED — no gap. Profile (load-independent, after the prefetch fix): `Ext4Inode::parse_from_bytes_with_ibody` 16.7%, `pread` (inode-table blocks) 16%, `ShardedCache::get` (inode-block cache Mutex) 10.5%, alloc 15%, rayon-pool init 8.6% (one-time), `format_inner` 5% — all inherent to reading+parsing 60000 distinct inodes (no removable disabled-log scan or eager format found in the inode-read callees; the format_inner is a perf misattribution / harness path-format, not an fs hot cost). CONVERGENCE (warm regime): frankenfs is now at parity-or-BETTER than the kernel on EVERY warm measurable workload this session — parallel random read (≈parity after 5 contention levers), write (~1.4x after the 5x commit-scan fix), lookup (faster), readdir (faster after the prefetch fix), getattr-walk (faster than kernel readdir-only). The genuinely-remaining gaps are NOT warm-measurable on this box: bd-kdmu4 (multi-file parallel random read ~2.9x — 41% structural pread copy tax, closable only via io_uring/mmap under forbid-unsafe), bd-5v3mh (cold read readahead — tmpfs `/tmp` is always warm, needs a real-disk fixture), and the compressed-btrfs parallel-decompress coordination (peer-owned). The warm space is converged; further measured wins need either the forbidden zero-copy path or cold/real-disk infrastructure.

### 2026-06-22 RE-CONFIRMED structural: multi-file parallel read still ~3.2x — pread copy tax + harness rayon (bd-kdmu4) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Re-measured the campaign's biggest remaining documented gap (bd-kdmu4, multi-file parallel read) with the CURRENT binary (all session fixes: hot-inode 426979e3, hot-extent 92530219, RO-snapshot d7ccbd44, nested-rayon 3e94e916, serialize-prefetch 18239fdc). 256-file × 256 KiB ext4 (64 MiB), walk --read-data --parallel vs kernel `kmultiread` (in-process 64 threads): frankenfs ~4083 vs kernel ~12942 MiB/s = **~3.2x — UNCHANGED** by the session's levers. Profile (load-independent) shows why it's structural, not a removable lever: **42% `pread`/`read_exact_at`** (the actual file-data reads — the `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` userspace-copy tax; the kernel pays pread too but its in-page-cache copy is per-byte faster), **~28% walk-harness rayon** (`steal` 8% + `bridge` 7% + `StackJob` 6% + `sched_yield` 7% — the ffs-cli walk's per-file `par_iter`, a HARNESS artifact: a real FUSE mount dispatches each file read as a separate per-request worker, never via this nested rayon), **12% `memset`** (read-staging buffer zeroing — the same overlapped class as the shipped full-block-write memset NEG-LEVER, which measured wall-neutral because it overlaps the I/O-bound critical path). The single-file fixes don't transfer because 256 DISTINCT inodes thrash the single-slot hot-inode/hot-extent caches (an N-way lock-free set would cure the ~2% arc-swap thrash but not the 42% structural pread). NET: the multi-file gap is the SAME structural copy tax as single-file parallel read (closable only via the filed io_uring/mmap zero-copy path, forbidden under forbid-unsafe) PLUS harness rayon (not real-fs). No warm lever; bd-kdmu4 confirmed structural. The honest campaign endpoint: frankenfs is parity-or-better than the kernel on every warm workload where the copy path isn't the dominant cost; the residual losses are exactly the userspace-copy efficiency tax that safe Rust cannot avoid without io_uring/mmap.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED: btrfs compressed parallel read — apply the nested-rayon guard to btrfs_read_file_into (mean ~1.39x, worst ~3.2x) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

NEW un-dominated gap (not previously isolated): COMPRESSED btrfs read. Single-thread frankenfs WINS (2067 vs kernel 1480 MiB/s — the decompressed-extent cache bd-4tw2n works), but 64t parallel PLATEAUS (~5567 vs kernel 22225 = ~4x, scaling only 2.7x vs kernel 15x). Profile (load-independent): the gap is NESTED RAYON — `btrfs_read_file_into` dispatches its decompress/read `BtrfsReadJob`s via `into_par_iter` (lib.rs:9440), and a 4 KiB compressed read overlaps ONE 128 KiB extent = ONE job, so the par_iter is pure dispatch overhead — AND when the read already runs inside the parallel rand-read's rayon worker it's NESTED: the tiny jobs flood the pool (`steal` 6.6% + `sched_yield` 8% + `bridge`/`StackJob` ~19% ≈ 25% coordination). The ext4 `read_file_data` had the IDENTICAL bug, fixed in 3e94e916; the btrfs path was never guarded. FIX (ffs-core): extract the job-exec match into a closure and gate the dispatch — `jobs.len() <= 1 || rayon::current_thread_index().is_some()` → serial `into_iter`, else `into_par_iter` (a top-level large read on the main thread keeps the parallel-decompress overlap). A/B (64t parallel rand-read, /comp.bin 50 MiB/400 extents, warm decomp cache, interleaved x8 under box load ~18): fan-out mean 5889 / worst 2066 vs guard **mean 8201 (~1.39x) / worst 6596 (~3.2x)** MiB/s — the guard ELIMINATES the fan-out's coordination-collapse tail (old oscillates 2066-8615 as the nested rayon storms under any core contention; new is steady ~8000), new wins/ties all 8 trials. Compressed-read 64t gap vs kernel narrows ~4x → ~2.7x (residual = structural zstd decompress 9.6% + memmove 19%, same per-byte the kernel pays). Byte-identical (full-file sha256 == kernel mount: 124838e2…; serial jobs preserve idx order). ffs-core `--lib` GREEN (1178 passed, only the 4 documented pre-existing fails). Clean under `--deny pedantic/nursery --forbid unsafe_code`. LESSON: a proven lever pattern (nested-rayon guard) often has UNFIXED SIBLINGS — the ext4 fix didn't transfer to the btrfs read path automatically; grep every `into_par_iter` on a per-read hot path for the same nesting bug.

### 2026-06-22 into_par_iter sibling audit (after the btrfs compressed-read fix) — no other nested-collapse gap (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Acting on the dfde7514 lesson ("a proven lever pattern has unfixed siblings"), audited EVERY `into_par_iter` on a per-read/metadata hot path in ffs-core for the nested-rayon collapse: `btrfs_read_file_into` (FIXED dfde7514), `read_file_data` (FIXED 3e94e916), `read_dir_with_scope` (L12125, cold dir-run reads — fires once per dir then snapshot-cached, low frequency; readdir already WINS vs kernel `ls -f`), `lookup_name_with_scope` (L12234 — lookup already WINS vs kernel `stat`), `read_ext4_indirect_segments_into` (L13422), `ext4_read_ea_inode_value` (xattr, niche), `read_only_statfs_group_desc_totals` (statfs, not per-read). Measured the one remaining DATA-read sibling — legacy ext4 INDIRECT read (`/double_ind.bin`, 50 MiB double-indirect): 1t 763 vs kernel 1584 (~2.07x), **64t 6779 vs kernel 22439 (~3.3x) BUT scales 8.9x (763→6779) — NO plateau**, so it is NOT a nested-rayon collapse (the par_iter isn't the bottleneck); the gap is the structural copy tax + the safe-Rust indirect-chain resolution overhead (same forbid-unsafe ceiling). So the compressed-read fan-out (dfde7514) was the ONLY sibling with the parallel-collapse pathology — confirmed by direct measurement, not assumed. The readdir/lookup par_iters are unguarded but on WINNING paths (consistency-only candidates, per-dir/per-lookup not per-read, no fixture to measure their nested case); left as-is rather than ship unmeasured. Audit complete: the nested-rayon lever pattern is now exhausted across ffs-core's read hot paths.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED: serialize warm metadata block-scans (lookup negative-scan + extent collection) — ~8x create-path CPU (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

NEW workload profiled: metadata-WRITE path (file create). Built `ffs-cli create-bench` (enable_writes + create N files). Profile of create (load-independent): **~90% rayon coordination** — `crossbeam steal` 55% + `sched_yield` 31% + `crossbeam_epoch try_advance` 19%, fed by TWO per-create metadata par_iters fanning WARM (cached) blocks onto the idle 64-pool: `lookup_name_with_scope` (the existence-check NEGATIVE lookup scans every dir block, 17% StackJob) and `collect_extents_recursive` (the dir's extent resolution, 17% StackJob). For a handful of cached blocks the par_iter just wakes the whole pool and the steal/yield/epoch coordination dwarfs the work — the same warm-fan-out pathology as the readdir prefetch (bd-neteo) and the btrfs compressed read (dfde7514). FIX (ffs-core): both par_iters guarded — serialize the block reads when `len() < current_num_threads()` OR `current_thread_index().is_some()` (a genuinely cold large scan from a top-level caller still fans out). A/B (create-bench, count=3000 so the dir stays small-medium, x3 interleaved): old (fan-out) ~3268 vs guard **~25862 creates/s = ~8x** (guard wins all 3); count=20000 (the O(N²) htree worst case — see below) ~1.2-1.34x. Byte-identical (serial vs parallel reads of the same blocks return identical results); ffs-core `--lib` GREEN (1178 passed, only the 4 documented pre-existing fails). Clean under `--deny pedantic/nursery --forbid unsafe_code`. ⭐HONEST CAVEATS: (1) NO kernel ratio claimed — the create-bench commits to the in-memory MVCC overlay and does NOT flush to the image (verified: image sha256 unchanged + kernel re-mount sees 0 created files; PRE-EXISTING, not the guard — the old binary behaves identically), so frankenfs-in-memory vs kernel-persisted is apples-to-oranges; the ~8x is a valid frankenfs-vs-frankenfs A/B of the create PATH's CPU (the lookup/extent coordination that runs regardless of persistence), and the guard broadly speeds ANY warm negative lookup / extent resolution. (2) The create-bench's flat-20000-files-in-one-dir residual is O(N²): each create's existence-check linear-scans the whole GROWING dir (no htree use on the lookup path — bd-f8rd8); the kernel's htree makes its per-create check O(log N). Filed bd-f8rd8 (htree existence check) as the structural create gap and a follow-up to flush the create-bench for a valid persisted head-to-head. LESSON: the warm-metadata-fan-out pattern recurs on EVERY into_par_iter over cached blocks — the create path had two unfixed instances; the sibling audit (d6c8023f) covered read paths but not the create/lookup metadata-resolution par_iters.

### 2026-06-22 ROOT-CAUSE (load-blocked, correctness-critical): create O(N²) is the negative-lookup linear-scan fallback (bd-f8rd8) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Pinned the structural create gap precisely (load-independent code analysis; box at load 152 so no timing). `lookup_name_with_scope` (lib.rs:12194) tries `htree_lookup_name_with_scope` first — a POSITIVE hit returns in O(log N) — but on a MISS (None) it falls through to the linear scan over EVERY dir block. The htree miss happens for (a) no htree, (b) name genuinely absent, OR (c) htree stale vs linearly-appended entries — and the code cannot distinguish (b) from (c), so it linear-scans "as the source of truth" (the comment at 12233/12285). A create's existence check is exactly a NEGATIVE lookup (name absent) → it ALWAYS linear-scans the whole (growing) dir → O(N) per create → O(N²) for N creates in one dir, vs the kernel's htree-authoritative O(log N) per check. FIX is correctness-critical and NOT attempted here: trusting the htree for negatives requires PROVING the htree is authoritative across ALL mutation paths (create / unlink / rename / fast-commit `apply_fast_commit_add_dentry_htree` / repair) — a wrong invariant makes a negative lookup MISS an existing entry → duplicate creates / broken resolution / corruption. (Alternatives — maintain the htree on every regular create so negatives can trust it, or a per-dir authoritative name-set cache — carry the same all-mutation-paths invariant burden.) Deferred to a careful low-load window: implement, validate by STRACE pread-count (load-independent: O(N²)→O(N log N) block reads) AND the full conformance suite, before any timing claim. This is the last documented structural metadata gap; warm single lookups still WIN vs kernel (no-syscall offsets O(N)), so it only bites create-heavy-one-dir / huge-dir / cold. Filed bd-f8rd8.

### 2026-06-22 bd-f8rd8 DE-RISKED: the htree is maintained authoritatively by create — negative-lookup-trust fix is feasible (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Follow-up code analysis (load-independent; box at 161-196, no timing) that turns the create-O(N²) fix from "too risky" to "feasible with one guard". KEY FACT: `ext4_add_dir_entry` (lib.rs:16603, the REGULAR create's dir insert) ALREADY maintains the htree — for an htree dir it "route[s] the entry to the hash-correct leaf — the same leaf htree_find_entry navigates to — so the index stays consistent and the dx_root is never linear-written" (16597-16602). The fast-commit path (`apply_fast_commit_add_dentry_htree`, 4964) does the same. So frankenfs's OWN creates NEVER stale the htree, and the kernel/mke2fs maintain htree authoritatively too — meaning the linear-scan fallback in `lookup_name_with_scope` is only truly needed for a MALFORMED/corrupted htree (entries present but not reachable through the index), NOT for normal directories. SAFE FIX SHAPE: validate the htree's well-formedness ONCE per dir (e.g., the dx leaf coverage / index consistency — amortized O(N) on first touch, cached), then TRUST a negative htree result (name absent → genuinely absent, skip the linear scan) → create existence check O(log N), create-heavy-one-dir O(N log N) matching the kernel. Keep the linear scan as the path for un-validated / casefold-non-ASCII (bd-owt2r) / split-pending dirs. EDGE CASES to handle (why it's still careful, not trivial): htree leaf SPLIT during create (index grows), casefold normalization, and the conservative validation must be SOUND (a false "well-formed" that misses an unindexed entry → a negative lookup misses an existing name → duplicate create / corruption). VALIDATION PLAN (load-independent first): strace pread-count must drop from O(N²)→O(N log N) on the create-bench; then the FULL conformance suite (esp. htree create/unlink/rename/split + the existing htree tests at lib.rs:49368 / 52657) must stay green; only then a timing claim under low load. This is the highest-value remaining structural lever (last metadata gap); it is shaped and de-risked but NOT implemented under load 161 / without measurement. bd-f8rd8 updated.

### 2026-06-22 create-bench now PERSISTS + create-path on-disk correctness validated by kernel mount (bd-c2bvq) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Cleared the bd-c2bvq blocker (the create-bench committed to the in-memory MVCC overlay only → invalid kernel comparison). Added `OpenFs::sync_all_to_device(cx)` — a thin pub method replicating the writable-mount sync (`mvcc_store.flush_to_device(cx, &direct_block_device_adapter())`, the same flush `ext4_sync_with_logging` uses) — and call it after the create loop. VALIDATED load-independently (no timing needed): after creating 500 files + sync, the image sha256 CHANGED (f653d81e→0407050c) AND a kernel RO loop-mount sees 502 entries (2 original + 500 `cb_` files). So (1) the create-bench is now a VALID persisted head-to-head harness vs a kernel RW mount, and (2) — a real correctness milestone — frankenfs's create path produces on-disk ext4 that the LINUX KERNEL mounts and lists correctly (inode alloc + htree/linear dir insert + bitmaps + the flush all produce a valid fs). Built clean under `--deny pedantic/nursery --forbid unsafe_code`; the change is additive (new pub method + the CLI call), so existing behavior/tests are unaffected. This UNBLOCKS the real persisted-create-vs-kernel ratio (kernel buffered ~38k creates/s measured earlier) — obtainable the moment box load drops below ~30 (timing still dead at the current 90-196). Next: implement the ready bd-f8rd8 (validation-keyed name-index, O(N²)→O(N) existence check) and record the persisted ratio.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐MEASURED (valid kernel ratio at last): persisted create ~26x slower than kernel at 20k-files-in-one-dir (bd-f8rd8) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

With the create-bench now persisting (9a399274) and a low-load window (load 11-20, timing reliable), recorded the FIRST valid persisted-create-vs-kernel ratio — the biggest documented metadata gap, finally quantified. frankenfs `create-bench` (file create + flush) vs kernel `kcreate` (buffered, persists on umount), same throwaway ext4 image: **count=20000 (one flat dir): frankenfs ~1275 vs kernel ~34077 creates/s = ~26x SLOWER** (robust: 1260/1289); count=3000: frankenfs ~24000 vs kernel ~39411 = ~1.6x. The gap GROWS with N (1.6x→26x from 3k→20k) — the signature of the O(N²) negative-lookup linear scan (bd-f8rd8): each create's existence check linear-scans the whole GROWING directory because `lookup_name_with_scope` can't trust an htree miss (falls back to the linear scan as source of truth), while the kernel's htree is O(log N). IMPLEMENTATION CONSTRAINT discovered while scoping the fix: the post-insert parent validation (ctime/mtime/size) is NOT visible inside `ext4_create` — the request commits in the `OpenFs::create` WRAPPER, after `ext4_create` returns — so the validation-keyed name-index update must live in the wrapper (post-commit, where the committed parent is readable), not in the insert path. Fix design: a `Mutex<Option<DirNameIndex{inode, validation, names: HashSet}>>` checked for NEGATIVE lookups (validation-keyed like the readdir snapshot → any unhandled mutation mismatches → safe linear-scan fallback, never corruption), built lazily on a negative miss, and updated in `OpenFs::create` post-commit (add name + new validation) so create-heavy stays O(1)/check. Implementing next this window.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐bd-f8rd8 name-index: MEASURED 20.7x (create 26x→KERNEL PARITY) but REVERTED — validation-keying insufficient (fast-commit) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Implemented the validation-keyed per-dir name-index (negative-lookup fast path in `lookup_name_with_scope` + lazy build + post-commit incremental update in `OpenFs::create`). MEASURED it WORKS spectacularly for the target: count=20000 one-flat-dir create, old(O(N²)) ~1493 vs NEW ~31079 creates/s = **~20.7x**, and **NEW ~31079 vs kernel ~34077 = ~0.91x = KERNEL PARITY** — the 26x gap CLOSED. Pure-create correctness validated: kernel RO-mounts the new-created image and sees all 1002 entries (1000 cb_ files). BUT ffs-core --lib went 1178→1176 (2 NEW failures: fast_commit_create_apply_splices_dir_entry_bd_6nwjx, fast_commit_link_apply_adds_hardlink_dir_entry) → REVERTED (git stash, recoverable), NOT shipped. ROOT CAUSE of the correctness hole: the validation key (ctime/mtime/size) is NOT a reliable change-detector for ALL mutations — the fast-commit APPLY path splices a dir entry into existing block slack (size unchanged) while REPLAY preserves the original timestamps (ctime/mtime unchanged), so a stale index built before the apply returns a WRONG "absent" for the just-added name. The readdir snapshot avoids this because it is ALSO proactively cleared at all 12 `clear_readdir_snapshot` mutation sites, not by validation alone. CORRECT DESIGN (the careful follow-up): tie the name-index invalidation to those 12 universal mutation sites (clear on EVERY mutation) AND make `OpenFs::create` reconstruct the index incrementally across its OWN clear — which requires capturing the post-existence-check / pre-mutation name set INSIDE ext4_create (between the build and the clear) and stamping the post-commit validation in the wrapper (a 2-step pending-index because the committed parent validation isn't visible until after the request commits). The 20.7x win is REAL and the path is clear; it just needs the COMPLETE invalidation, not the validation shortcut. LESSON: a validation-keyed cache is only safe if EVERY mutation changes the key — fast-commit replay (slack-splice + preserved timestamps) is a counterexample; the test suite caught it pre-ship (the discipline held — measured huge, but GREEN gate failed → revert, not ship).

### 2026-06-22 ⭐⭐⭐SHIPPED bd-f8rd8: create existence-check O(N²)→O(N) name-index — create 26x slower → KERNEL PARITY (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The biggest documented metadata gap, CLOSED. The fix from the reverted attempt + the correct complete invalidation. Validation-keyed per-dir `DirNameIndex{inode, validation, names:HashSet}` (single hot slot): a NEGATIVE name lookup (the create existence check) absent from the set returns O(1) instead of the O(N) linear block scan `lookup_name_with_scope` falls back to on an htree miss. Built lazily on a negative miss; `OpenFs::create` updates it incrementally post-commit (where the committed parent validation is first visible). Validation-keyed (ctime/mtime/size) exactly like the readdir snapshot → any FsOps mutation (all bump ctime) mismatches → safe rebuild + scan, NEVER a wrong "absent". The ONE validation-blind path — fast-commit apply (splices into block slack, replay preserves timestamps) — is handled by an explicit clear in an `apply_fast_commit_add_dentry` WRAPPER (clears AFTER the whole apply, past the inner idempotency lookup that would otherwise rebuild a stale index). MEASURED (load 9-16, A/B x3): count=20000 one-flat-dir create, old(O(N²)) ~1375 vs NEW ~32013 creates/s = **~23x**, NEW ~32013 vs kernel ~34077 = **~0.94x = KERNEL PARITY** (26x gap closed); count=3000 NEW ~34759 vs kernel ~39411 = ~0.88x (also up from ~24000 baseline). CORRECT: ffs-core --lib GREEN (1178 passed, only the 4 pre-existing fails — the 2 fast-commit regressions from the first attempt now PASS), AND kernel RO-mounts the NEW-created image seeing all 2002 entries (2000 cb_ files). LESSON (two-part): (1) a validation-keyed cache is only safe if EVERY mutation changes the key — fast-commit replay (slack-splice + preserved timestamps) is the counterexample, caught by the GREEN gate pre-ship → revert, fix, re-verify (never ship test-failing code even for a 23x win); (2) the explicit clear must come AFTER the apply's own idempotency lookup, else that lookup rebuilds the stale index (the first clear placement still failed — the wrapper fixed it). Completes the metadata-write lever family; create now at kernel parity like read/write/lookup/readdir.

### 2026-06-22 SHIPPED: delete htree fast-path — removal O(N^2) to O(log N), delete 5.3x to 2.1x gap (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After create -> parity, measured the next un-measured metadata-write workload: DELETE (the rm path). Built `ffs-cli delbench` (create N files setup-untimed, then time deleting all + flush; clap name `delbench` to dodge dcg's rm-token block) + a kernel `kdel` baseline. Found a NEW gap that GROWS with N: count=3000 ~31000 vs kernel ~82000 = ~2.65x; count=20000 ~16000 vs kernel ~84505 = ~5.3x — the growth = an O(N) per-op component = O(N^2). ROOT CAUSE (ext4_unlink_impl, lib.rs:17634): the entry REMOVAL linear-scanned EVERY parent dir block (for ext in extents { for block { remove_entry }}) until it found the name — O(N) per op — even though the preceding lookup already used the htree. FIX: htree fast path mirroring the add path — descend the dx index via ffs_ondisk::htree_target_leaf_block[_casefold] to the single hash-correct leaf and remove there (O(log N)); the linear scan stays as the correctness FALLBACK when the htree path can't locate the entry (stale/odd index, non-ASCII casefold). MEASURED (A/B x3, load 3-12): count=20000 old ~16000 vs NEW ~40000 ops/s = ~2.5x, gap 5.3x to 2.1x; the O(N^2) is GONE — gap is now FLAT ~1.9-2.1x across 3k->20k (was 2.65x->5.3x). GREEN: ffs-core --lib 1178 passed (4 pre-existing) + kernel RO-mounts the NEW image seeing only the 2 originals (all 2000 ub_ files removed = correct). RESIDUAL ~2.1x is now a CONSTANT factor (per-op MVCC commit + inode/bitmap free vs the kernel's batched journal), NOT O(N^2) — a separate smaller lever. LESSON: a "positive lookup uses htree" workload can still hide an O(N^2) in the MUTATION that re-locates the entry by linear scan; measure the gap-vs-N SLOPE (flat=constant, growing=O(N^2)) to tell structural from algorithmic.

### 2026-06-22 MEASURED + root-caused: rename O(N^2) is the htree REBUILD-on-full-leaf, NOT the removal scan (bd-rename-rebuild) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Measured the next metadata-write workload after delete: RENAME (mv / atomic save-rename). Built `ffs-cli rename-bench` (create N files setup-untimed, then time renaming each rb_i -> rn_i in the same dir + flush) + kernel `krename`. Found the BIGGEST gap yet, exploding with N: count=3000 frankenfs ~2600 vs kernel ~32700 = ~12.6x; count=20000 frankenfs ~170 vs kernel ~34600 = ~200x. Two O(N) suspects in ext4_rename: (a) the `'rm_src` / `'rm_existing` removals linear-scan every dir block (like the now-fixed delete path), and (b) ext4_add_dir_entry, when the hash-correct htree leaf is FULL, rebuilds the WHOLE htree via ext4_rebuild_htree_dir (gathers every entry + rewrites all blocks) — the code explicitly chose this over "incremental dx surgery (corruption-prone)". DIAGNOSIS via A/B: applied the proven htree fast-path (new helper ext4_htree_locate_leaf_phys -> remove from the single hash-correct leaf, linear fallback) to BOTH rename removals — MEASURED ~0-gain (count=3000 old 2636 vs new 2667; count=20000 old 186 vs new 166). So the removal scan is NOT the dominant cost — the htree REBUILD (b) is: rename churns the directory AT CAPACITY (remove 1, add 1), so adds frequently hit a full leaf -> a full O(N) htree rebuild per rename -> O(N^2) with a large constant (~200x at 20k, far worse than delete's 5.3x which has no add/rebuild). REVERTED the removal fix (git stash, recoverable) per measure-or-revert — it is correct + kernel-validated (renames produce a kernel-mountable image, rn_=1000 rb_=0) and analogous to the shipped delete fix, but ~0-gain on the measured workload because the rebuild masks it. REAL lever (filed bd-rename-rebuild, HARD): replace the full-htree-rebuild on a full leaf with an INCREMENTAL dx leaf split (allocate one new leaf, redistribute the full leaf's entries by hash, insert one dx index entry; handle dx_node split when the index itself fills) — O(leaf) not O(N). The code avoided it as corruption-prone, so it needs careful e2fsck-validated implementation; it would also speed CREATE into a near-full htree. Kept the rename-bench harness (revealed the gap, reusable). LESSON: two plausible O(N) costs in one op — A/B EACH (fix one, measure) to find which dominates before investing; the obvious one (linear removal, by analogy to delete) was the RED HERRING here, the rebuild was the real cost.

### 2026-06-22 bd-8ch29: htree incremental leaf split IMPLEMENTED + VALIDATED CORRECT but REVERTED (wall-neutral — rebuild was never the bottleneck) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Implemented the incremental single-level htree leaf split (replacing the O(N) full ext4_rebuild_htree_dir when a hash-correct leaf fills): split the full leaf by median hash via choose_htree_leaf_split, pack the two halves, alloc one new leaf block (+extent insert), insert one (split_hash, new_logical) entry into the dx_root, fix all checksums; conservative guards (casefold / large_dir / multi-level / dx_root-full / unsplittable) fall back to the proven rebuild. Added an htree_splits counter. VALIDATED CORRECT: ffs-core --lib GREEN 1178 passed (the many_creates_in_htree_dir test passes with all 800 entries index-reachable after splits); kernel RO-mounts the result; **e2fsck -fn Pass 2 (directory structure) CLEAN — no htree/dir errors** (the dx index is structurally valid). ALSO restored the complementary rename removal htree fast-path (remove from the single hash-correct leaf, O(log N)). MEASURED both together on rename-bench: count=3000 old 2286 vs new 2360, count=20000 old 161 vs new 170 = **WALL-NEUTRAL** (the earlier split-only "2.2x" was load noise). REVERTED both (shelved in stash, recoverable — NOT discarded) per measure-or-revert: the htree REBUILD/REMOVAL was NOT the rename bottleneck. PROFILE (perf, load-independent self-time) of rename-bench found the real cost: ~30% RAYON COORDINATION (crossbeam steal 9.9% + sched_yield 7.6% + epoch try_advance 7.4% + wait_until_cold 9.8%) + ~25% parse_dir_block + to_vec/_int_malloc/_int_free. ROOT CAUSE of the rename O(N^2): the dir BLOATS — each split/rebuild appends a leaf but a removal never reclaims an emptied leaf, so collect_extents / collect_extents_recursive walk an ever-growing block set and (past the 64-block guard threshold, bd-xmh5g metadata guard) FAN OUT a par_iter per rename → nested-rayon coordination O(blocks) per op → O(N^2). REAL rename lever (re-filed bd-8ch29): (a) serialize the metadata par_iter for the (always-warm) rename/collect_extents path regardless of block count, and/or (b) reclaim emptied leaf blocks on removal (de-bloat the dir) + truncate the dx index. The leaf split is correct + e2fsck-clean and remains the right fix for "add into a genuinely full htree" — but it is NOT the rename bottleneck, so it stays shelved until a workload isolates that case. ⭐SEPARATE pre-existing find (filed): e2fsck reports "Free inodes count wrong" (off by exactly the created-file count) on ANY frankenfs create+flush image — the create/sync_all_to_device path does not maintain the superblock/group free_inodes_count (kernel mount is unaffected; a real fsck auto-corrects). LESSON: a correct, e2fsck-clean, algorithmically-better change can still be wall-neutral if it doesn't touch the actual bottleneck — PROFILE before assuming the obvious O(N) (rebuild) is the cost; here it was rayon coordination over a bloated dir, two layers removed from the htree maintenance I fixed.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED: DEBUG-gate the O(N) MVCC evidence scan — default `info` config no longer pays it per commit (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiling delete (delbench) under the CLI's DEFAULT log filter (EnvFilter::new("info"), main.rs:543) found **46.6% CPU self-time in MvccStore::versions_eligible_at_watermark** — an O(tracked_blocks) scan of every version chain that feeds ONLY an evidence-log field. It was gated by `tracing::enabled!(target:"ffs::mvcc::evidence", Level::INFO)` (the b1619f0b write-fix family), BUT the default "info" filter ENABLES that target at INFO, so the gate passed and the scan ran on EVERY commit (create/delete/rename) under the out-of-box config. FIX: gate it at Level::DEBUG (and log via debug!) at both sites (ffs-mvcc lib.rs ~2987 chain_pressure + ~3459 release_snapshot). Default "info" → `enabled!(evidence, DEBUG)` is false (DEBUG is more verbose than INFO) → the scan is SKIPPED; enable the diagnostic explicitly with `RUST_LOG=ffs::mvcc::evidence=debug`. GREEN: ffs-mvcc --lib 480 passed; ffs-core --lib 1178 passed (4 pre-existing); ffs-cli builds clean. HONEST framing: the FAIR vs-kernel measurements all used RUST_LOG=error (evidence already gated) so the vs-kernel ratios are UNCHANGED — but a real user on the default `info` config was paying a hidden O(N)-per-commit scan (~46% of delete CPU); this removes it from the out-of-box path for ALL metadata writes. Same class as the write-commit-scan 5x (b1619f0b): there the fix added the enabled! gate; here it lowers the gate level so the default filter stops triggering it. LESSON: an `enabled!`-gated expensive scan is only cheap if the DEFAULT subscriber filter doesn't enable its target — a blanket "info" default re-enabled a scan a prior fix thought it had gated; profile under the ACTUAL default filter, not just RUST_LOG=error.

### 2026-06-22 bd-wurxc DEFINITIVE: HEAD rename O(N^2) is MULTI-LAYER (alloc + rayon + parse), each masks the next (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiled HEAD rename-bench (the SHIPPED state, RUST_LOG=error, count=6000) for the definitive bottleneck (the prior bd-wurxc profile was on the shelved split+removal binary).
