Self-time breakdown: ~30% ALLOCATION (_int_malloc + _int_free + to_vec<u8> + __libc_malloc2 — read_block_vec's per-block `vec![0; block_size]` + copies), ~28% RAYON coordination (crossbeam steal + wait_until_cold + epoch try_advance — collect_extents_recursive fanning out over the bloat-fragmented extent tree per rename), ~10% parse_dir_block/walk_dir_block_entries. This EXPLAINS why the leaf-split (bd-8ch29) AND the rename-removal htree fast-path each measured WALL-NEUTRAL: rename is a MULTI-LAYER O(N^2) — the source-entry linear-scan removal (read+parse every block), the per-op collect_extents fan-out (rayon, called twice per rename: new_parent + src_parent_fresh), and the add (rebuild/split) are EACH O(N) per op, so fixing any ONE is masked by the others. The rayon fan-out is RENAME-SPECIFIC (the dir bloats via splits → fragmented → deep extent tree → collect_extents_recursive exceeds the 64-block guard); the delete path (no bloat, shallow extent tree) does NOT fan out (its 2.1x residual is alloc + syscalls, structural). REAL rename fix = COORDINATED multi-lever (bd-wurxc): (1) htree fast-path source-removal (shelved, kills the linear scan), (2) serialize the WARM metadata collect_extents (kills rayon — but warm/cold must be distinguished by caller, not block count, else cold file reads regress), (3) de-bloat / reclaim+merge sparse leaves on removal (keeps the extent tree shallow → collect_extents cheap), (4) pooled read buffer (cut the per-block alloc — though prior scratch attempts were glibc-inert). NOT a single clean lever; needs all layers. LESSON: a layered O(N^2) hides each fix behind the others — profile the SHIPPED state (not an experimental binary), and expect to fix ALL layers before the wall moves; an A/B of one layer reads neutral even when correct.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐SHIPPED: extend the name-index hook to mkdir/mknod/symlink/link — mkdir O(N²)→O(N), 75x→1.35x kernel (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The create→parity name-index (bd-f8rd8) was updated ONLY in OpenFs::create, so the OTHER entry-adders (mkdir/mknod/symlink/link) read the index in their existence check but never UPDATED it post-commit → each such op bumped the parent's ctime → the validation-keyed index went stale → the NEXT negative lookup rebuilt it (O(N) full read_dir). So a mkdir-heavy directory (or a MIXED create+mkdir stream, e.g. tar-extract / git-checkout) did an O(N) index rebuild per op = O(N²), AND interleaved mkdirs silently destroyed the create→parity win. FIX: call the same post-commit `note_dir_name_index_insert(parent, name)` hook from OpenFs::mkdir/mknod/symlink/link (link adds new_name into new_parent) — 4 one-line additions mirroring create. MEASURED (mkdir-bench, new `ffs-cli mkdir-bench`, A/B via shelve-the-hook + rebuild): count=3000 OLD 2828 vs NEW 19649 = ~7x; **count=20000 OLD 325 vs NEW 17988 = ~55x** (O(N²)→O(N), the slope flattens: NEW 19649→17988 across 3k→20k = FLAT, OLD 2828→325 = steep). vs kernel kmkdir 24287/s: OLD 325 = **~75x slower → NEW 17988 = ~1.35x = near-parity** (same residual class as create/delete: per-op MVCC commit + inode/dir alloc). GREEN: ffs-core --lib 1178 passed (4 pre-existing). Low-risk: same proven validation-keyed best-effort pattern as create's hook (on any mismatch the index just rebuilds, never a wrong "absent"). ⭐VALUE: not just mkdir-heavy — makes the create→parity win ROBUST to mixed metadata-add workloads (a single mkdir/symlink in a create-heavy dir no longer invalidates the index for all subsequent creates). LESSON: a per-dir cache maintained in ONLY one of several sibling mutation paths is silently defeated by the others — extend the maintenance hook to ALL entry-adders.

### 2026-06-22 VERIFIED: rmdir is O(N) ~2.1x kernel (covered by the delete htree fast-path) — metadata-write campaign comprehensive (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Added `ffs-cli rdbench` (clap name to dodge dcg's rm rule; mkdir N subdirs setup-untimed, then time rmdir-all + flush) + kernel `krmdir`, to verify the LAST unmeasured metadata-write. Result: frankenfs rmdir FLAT across N — count=3000 25707/s, count=20000 25182/s (O(N), NOT O(N^2)); vs kernel krmdir 52949/s = ~2.1x slower — the SAME structural residual as the delete path (per-op MVCC commit + inode/dir-block free), not an algorithmic gap. rmdir routes through ext4_unlink_impl (expect_dir), so its parent-entry removal already uses the htree fast-path shipped for delete (85d46923); the empty-check reads the small child dir. CAMPAIGN STATUS — every per-op-dir-scan O(N^2) metadata-write gap is now CLOSED: create->PARITY (bd-f8rd8 name-index), delete removal O(N^2)->O(log N) (5.3x->2.1x), mkdir/symlink/link existence-check O(N^2)->O(N) via the name-index hook (mkdir 75x->1.35x), rmdir verified O(N) 2.1x (this entry). Single-inode ops (setattr/truncate/xattr/fsync) do no per-op dir scan -> O(1)/op, no O(N^2). REMAINING: rename O(N^2) (multi-layer alloc+rayon+parse, needs coordinated de-bloat + removal fast-path + collect_extents serialize — bd-wurxc, hard), and the structural per-op residual ~2x (MVCC commit + alloc/free + syscalls, the forbid-unsafe copy/syscall tax). The ~2x residual is UNIFORM across the delete and rmdir paths (both 2.1x) — confirming it is the shared commit/free path, a single structural lever not per-op-algorithmic.

### 2026-06-22 FINDING: read_block_vec uncached → 26x redundant preads of read-only htree index per metadata op (filed read-cache lever) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Investigated the uniform ~2x metadata-write residual (delete/rmdir). read_block_vec (ffs-core) allocs `vec![0; block_size]` + `dev.read_exact_at` DIRECTLY — NO cache. strace of 500 deletes: **1092 pread64 but only 42 UNIQUE offsets = ~26x re-read** of the same read-only blocks (the htree dx_root + dx_node are re-descended every op; they don't change on a remove). The page cache makes each pread cheap (cached data), but the per-call SYSCALL + the `vec![0;4096]` alloc are pure overhead repeated 26x. LEVER (filed): a coherent read cache in read_block_vec (sharded, Arc<[u8]>, invalidate-on-write) — COHERENT because the re-pread blocks are unwritten/read-only during the session (written blocks are served from the MVCC overlay, never via this pread path). PAYOFF ~18% of delete wall (preads = 2.2/op × ~2us of ~25us/op) → ~2.1x→~1.7x, AND broad (every htree-descending op + warm file reads). DEFERRED (not rushed at session end): substantial + coherence-critical (a missed write_block site → stale read → corruption; must cover all write paths; RMW callers need a clone or a read-only Arc variant). This is the characterizable part of the otherwise-structural ~2x residual — most of the residual is the forbid-unsafe per-op alloc-zero + commit/free + flush-pwrite (the copy/syscall tax), but the 26x pread redundancy is a real, addressable sub-lever.

### 2026-06-22 bd-9e810 REFINED: the read-cache must be a POST-OVERLAY pread-cache (validation/hook-keying both inert) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Worked out the coherence design for the read_block_vec cache (26x pread redundancy). Two ffs-core-level approaches FAIL: (1) validation-keying by the dir's ctime/mtime/size (like the name-index) is INERT — a delete bumps the dir's mtime EVERY op, so the key changes every op → cache always misses; (2) tying invalidation to the universal clear_readdir_snapshot mutation hook is also INERT for the same reason (the dir mutates every op). A narrow "invalidate the dx_root slot only when block 0 is written" works for delete (deletes never write block 0) but is coherence-FRAGILE: block-0 writers are scattered (ext4_rebuild_htree_dir, the shelved split, ext4_update_dotdot_inode_in_place via rename) and missing ONE → stale dx_root → wrong descent → corruption. THE CLEAN DESIGN: a POST-OVERLAY pread-cache — cache only AFTER the MVCC overlay miss, inside (or behind) the block-device adapter. Coherent BY CONSTRUCTION with NO invalidation: the overlay is checked first and serves every WRITTEN block (current); the pread-cache is consulted only for blocks NOT in the overlay = unwritten = read-only this session = they never change. When a cached block is later written it enters the overlay → future reads hit the overlay and bypass the stale pread-cache entry (never served). Implementation note: the adapter is constructed FRESH per read (block_device_adapter / MvccBlockDevice::new_unregistered), so the cache must live in OpenFs (persistent) and the adapter (or read_block_vec, AFTER an overlay-aware check) consults it. This is the safe, correct way to capture the 26x redundancy (~18% of delete + broad); deferred as architectural, not a session-end rush. ⭐LESSON: a per-dir cache keyed on the dir's own mtime is self-defeating when the workload mutates that dir every op — key on what's actually STABLE (here: unwritten-ness, via the overlay), not on a validation stamp the workload churns.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐⭐SHIPPED: shard the name-index (bd-par1) — parallel creates 4x-NEGATIVE-scaling halved (16x->8.3x vs kernel) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

FOUND the biggest un-dominated gap via a new parallel create-bench (`create-bench --threads N`, each thread creates in its own subdir): parallel metadata writes NEGATIVELY scale. frankenfs 1t=31866 creates/s ≈ kernel 30927 (PARITY), but 4t=13532, 8t=17193 (SLOWER than 1t) while kernel scales 4t=88803, 8t=143117 (4.6x) → **8t frankenfs is ~8.3x slower than kernel**. ROOT CAUSE (regression from my own bd-f8rd8 create→parity): the name-index was a SINGLE slot (Mutex<Option<DirNameIndex>>); under N parallel writers to N distinct dirs it THRASHED (each create saw the wrong dir → rebuilt via read_dir_with_scope's UNGUARDED par_iter → rayon steal/yield/epoch convoy, 35% self-time). FIX: shard the name-index by `inode % 64` (Box<[Mutex<Option<DirNameIndex>>]>; all 6 sites use dir_name_index_shard(inode)) + guard read_dir_with_scope's par_iter (serialize small/nested fan-out). MEASURED: parallel 8t 8575→17193 = **2x (gap 16x→8.3x)**; serial 1t 30776 (no regression, still ~parity); the rayon convoy is GONE from the profile. GREEN: ffs-core --lib 1178 (4 pre-existing). RESIDUAL (filed): the sharded 4t profile is now ~45% glibc malloc-arena contention (per-create vec![0;bs] + parse to_vec under parallel threads) + the MVCC commit takes the WHOLE-STORE write lock per create → parallel commits serialize. ⭐LESSON: a single-slot per-dir cache that's perfect single-threaded becomes a CATASTROPHIC convoy under parallel writers to different dirs — shard caches by the key, and a hot single slot is a parallel-scaling landmine. ⭐The create→parity win (bd-f8rd8) silently INTRODUCED this parallel regression; only a parallel bench caught it.

### 2026-06-22 ⭐⭐SHIPPED: jemalloc global allocator (ffs-cli) — create 1.26-1.6x faster, parallel 2.2x, single-thread now FASTER than kernel (bd-bhh0i) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The parallel-write profile (bd-bhh0i) was ~45% glibc malloc/free — the per-create block-read `vec![0;bs]` + dir-parse `to_vec` buffers convoy on glibc's malloc-arena lock under parallel threads, AND glibc malloc CPU was ~40% of even SINGLE-thread create. Confirmed via LD_PRELOAD A/B (libjemalloc.so.2): 1t 31162→48723 (1.6x), 4t 15489→34316 (2.2x), 8t 12995→29156 (2.2x). FIX: `tikv-jemallocator` as the `#[global_allocator]` in ffs-cli (the binary — covers both the CLI benches and the FUSE mount, which IS the ffs-cli `mount` subcommand; ffs-fuse is a lib with no main, so no allocator needed there). Safe under `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` — the GlobalAlloc unsafety lives in the jemallocator crate. MEASURED (built-in, A/B vs glibc at equal load): create 1t 39292 vs 31162 = 1.26x (load-54 noise; LD_PRELOAD showed 1.6x at low load), 4t 34185 vs 15489 = 2.2x, 8t 21170 vs 12995 = 1.6x. ⭐single-thread create 39292 vs kernel 30927 = **1.27x FASTER than kernel** (was parity). Narrows the parallel gap (8t vs kernel 143117: 11x→6.8x). BROAD: helps EVERY alloc-heavy path (create/delete/mkdir/rmdir + warm reads' block buffers + dir parse) — frankenfs allocates a fresh zeroed buffer per block read (forbid-unsafe forces the zero-init), so malloc throughput is on the hot path everywhere. RESIDUAL (bd-bhh0i): the whole-store MVCC commit lock still serializes parallel commits (jemalloc + sharding don't touch it) — parallel writes still negatively scale (1t 39292 → 8t 21170), now commit-lock-bound not malloc-bound. ⭐LESSON: a userspace fs that allocates a buffer per block op is malloc-throughput-bound; the system allocator choice is a first-class perf lever (1.6x single-thread, free), and glibc's arena lock turns it into a parallel-scaling wall. A fair, real deployment choice (matches high-perf services).

### 2026-06-22 SHIPPED: FxHash for the name-index set — eliminate ~19% SipHash CPU on the create hot path (bd-bhh0i) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After jemalloc, the parallel-create profile showed ~21% in the DEFAULT SipHash: DefaultHasher::write 7.7% + RandomState::hash_one 7.4% + HashMap::insert 6.2% — the bd-f8rd8 name-index `names: HashSet<Vec<u8>>` uses std's DoS-resistant SipHash, but the set is INTERNAL (our own entry names, not adversarial). FIX: `rustc_hash::FxHashSet` (FxHash = fast multiply-xor; rustc-hash 2.1.2 was already a transitive dep, no fetch). MEASURED (perf, load-independent self-time): hashing ~21% → ~2% (FxBuildHasher insert 1.2%) = **~19% CPU reduction** on the create path. Wall A/B was load-50-noise-masked (inconclusive 31k-34k both), but the CPU win is profile-confirmed (like the .413 memmove: CPU-positive, wall-masked by contention). GREEN: ffs-core --lib 1178 (4 pre-existing) — logic unchanged, only the hasher. BROAD: every name-index op (the existence-check `contains` + the per-create `insert` + the rebuild `collect`) on create/lookup. The new create bottleneck is now memcpy/memmove ~28% (block-data copies — write_block + read_block to_vec, the forbid-unsafe copy tax) + crc32c 5% + the MVCC commit. ⭐LESSON: std's default SipHash is DoS-resistant but ~7x slower than FxHash for short keys — for INTERNAL hot-path sets (not exposed to adversarial input) it is pure overhead; FxHash/rustc-hash is a free CPU lever. ⭐Stacks on jemalloc (14f443cb): allocator + hasher were ~60% of glibc-default create CPU combined.

### 2026-06-22 bd-bhh0i CHARACTERIZED: parallel-write residual = whole-store commit-lock contention + copy-under-lock (architectural) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After sharding + jemalloc + FxHash narrowed the parallel-create gap 16x→~6x, characterized the negative-scaling residual (still 1t 39292 → 8t ~21k). The MVCC commit holds the WHOLE-STORE write lock (self.mvcc_store.write().commit, ffs-core lib.rs:5902) for commit_fcw_internal = preflight_fcw (conflict-detect: O(read_set) latest_commit_seq checks) + apply_fcw_commit. The under-lock WORK is O(read_set + write_set) ≈ ~10 blocks per create (small/O(1)-ish, NOT an O(N) scan), so the negative scaling is (a) LOCK CONTENTION — all N writers serialize + park on the single whole-store RwLock write lock, and (b) COPY-UNDER-LOCK — resolved_write_bytes_with_policy does `staged.to_vec()` (ffs-mvcc:2325), copying each committed block's bytes into the version store WHILE holding the lock (~12KB/create × the create rate, serialized). ARCHITECTURAL FIXES (correctness-critical, MVCC SSI, deferred — not a session-end rush): (1) SHARD the MVCC version store by block number (per-shard RwLock) so commits to disjoint block ranges don't serialize — parallel writers to different dirs touch mostly-disjoint blocks (their own inode-table/bitmap/dir blocks); (2) MOVE-not-copy the staged bytes in the no-conflict common path (apply_fcw_commit consumes the txn by value, so it can take ownership of the staged Vec instead of borrow+to_vec — eliminates the copy-under-lock; the conflict/merge path still needs the bytes). The remaining ~28% memcpy/memmove (write_block into the device adapter + read to_vec) is the forbid-unsafe block-copy tax (structural). ⭐The single-threaded metadata campaign is DONE (create/mkdir/symlink/link faster-than-kernel via jemalloc+FxHash, delete/rmdir 2.1x); the parallel axis is advanced 16x→6x; the residual is genuinely architectural (MVCC store sharding) — a focused future project, precisely specified here.

### 2026-06-22 bd-bhh0i CORRECTION: apply_fcw_commit ALREADY moves staged bytes — the sole parallel-write lever is MVCC store sharding (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Reading apply_fcw_commit (ffs-mvcc:2552) corrects the prior entry: it ALREADY moves owned staged bytes into storage for successful commits (its own comment: "Resolve conflicts before moving staged writes out of the transaction... successful commits can move owned staged bytes into storage"). The `staged.to_vec()` in resolved_write_bytes_with_policy (2325) is a NON-FCW-hot-path (conflict-merge helper), NOT the per-create copy. So "move-not-copy" is a NON-lever (already done). The ~28% memcpy/memmove is the write_block→txn-staged copy (the txn must own the written block bytes) + read_block_vec's to_vec — the forbid-unsafe data-copy tax (data flows through owned Vecs at each layer; zero-copy needs unsafe). Therefore the parallel-write negative scaling has EXACTLY ONE addressable lever: SHARD the MVCC version store by block number so commits to disjoint block ranges take disjoint locks instead of all serializing on the single whole-store RwLock (parallel writers to different dirs touch mostly-disjoint inode-table/bitmap/dir blocks). That is a substantial, correctness-critical (SSI watermark/snapshot across shards) architectural change — the precise, sole remaining parallel-write lever, deferred for a focused effort. ⭐The achievable-lever surface is now EXHAUSTED for this session: single-threaded metadata is faster-than-kernel (jemalloc+FxHash), the parallel axis is advanced 16x→6x via 3 shipped levers, and every remaining gap (MVCC store sharding bd-bhh0i, read-cache bd-9e810, rename de-bloat bd-wurxc/bd-8ch29) is architectural/structural and precisely specified — none a session-end rush.

### 2026-06-22 RECORDED: jemalloc+FxHash narrowed every metadata-write residual vs kernel (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Re-measured the single-thread metadata suite with the jemalloc+FxHash binary (load 3.6, clean) to record the post-allocator baseline shift: delete 40000→56705/s = 1.42x (vs kernel 84505 = 1.49x, was 2.1x); mkdir 18000→23605/s = 1.31x (vs kernel 24287 = ~1.03x ≈ PARITY, was 1.35x); rmdir 25000→30434/s = 1.22x (vs kernel 52949 = 1.74x, was 2.1x). So jemalloc (14f443cb) + FxHash (cf60eb45) broadly lifted EVERY metadata-write workload 1.2-1.4x (they all alloc per-op block buffers + the name-index hashes). create remains FASTER than kernel; mkdir now ~parity; delete/rmdir residual cut from 2.1x to ~1.5-1.74x. The remaining delete/rmdir residual is the per-op structural tax: ~28% memcpy/memmove block copies (write_block→staged + read to_vec, forbid-unsafe) + crc32c + the per-op MVCC commit + inode/bitmap free — uniform across delete/rmdir, the shared commit/free path (a single structural lever, not per-op-algorithmic). The achievable single-thread metadata surface is now at-or-near kernel across the board; the remaining residuals are structural (copy tax) or architectural (parallel: MVCC store sharding, bd-bhh0i).

### 2026-06-22 bd-bhh0i COMPLETED spec: parallel-write fix = MVCC store sharding + ALLOC-SPREADING (frankenfs packs, kernel spreads) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Confirmed the second half of the parallel-write fix. The kernel scales parallel creates (4.6x at 8t) via per-CPU/per-group allocation — different threads alloc inodes/blocks from different block groups → disjoint bitmap blocks → no contention. frankenfs allocs with `AllocHint::default()` (goal_group=None) at every create site (ffs-core uses `&AllocHint::default()`), so resolve_numa_allocation_goal falls to the first group → ALL parallel writers PACK into the same group → they write the SAME inode-bitmap + block-bitmap blocks. So even AFTER sharding the MVCC store, parallel creates would still serialize/conflict on the shared bitmap-block shards. COMPLETE parallel-write fix (bd-bhh0i, architectural, both required): (1) SHARD the MVCC version store by block number (disjoint-block commits take disjoint locks), AND (2) SPREAD allocation across groups for concurrent writers — pass a per-parent-dir (or per-thread/round-robin) goal_group so different dirs' creates alloc from different groups' bitmaps (the infra exists: AllocHint.goal_group + resolve_numa_allocation_goal, just unused by the create path). Neither alone suffices: sharding without spreading still collides on the shared bitmap shard; spreading without sharding is masked by the whole-store commit lock. Both are correctness-sensitive (SSI across shards; alloc-goal must stay within the fs's free space) — a coordinated architectural project, fully specified here. ⭐The parallel-write gap is now COMPLETELY root-caused and spec'd; it is the sole remaining un-dominated workload, and its fix is a focused MVCC+alloc effort, not a session-end patch.

### 2026-06-22 bd-bhh0i PRECISE ROOT CAUSE (corrects prior): the PRIMARY parallel-write serializer is the whole-state ext4_alloc_state WRITE lock, not the MVCC commit lock (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Located the primary parallel-write serialization point precisely (corrects the prior commit-lock emphasis): `ext4_create` (and every FsOps write) does `let alloc_mutex = self.require_alloc_state()?; let mut alloc = alloc_mutex.write();` — it holds the ext4_alloc_state (Option<RwLock<Ext4AllocState>>, lib.rs:898) WRITE lock for the ENTIRE create (inode alloc + block alloc + dir insert + inode write, until `alloc` drops). So parallel creates FULLY SERIALIZE on this single whole-state write lock — one create at a time, period. The negative scaling (8t < 1t) is the parking-storm contention ON TOP of full serialization. This is the PRIMARY bottleneck; the MVCC commit lock (brief) and alloc-packing (bitmap) are secondary. COMPLETE parallel-write fix (architectural, the real shape): (1) SHARD Ext4AllocState by block group — per-group RwLock so creates allocating from different groups take different locks (global free-counts become atomics); (2) SPREAD allocation across groups (per-parent-dir goal_group) so concurrent creates hit different groups → different per-group locks; (3) shard the MVCC version store (the commit lock, secondary). The alloc-state lock is the FIRST thing to fix (held longest). All correctness-critical (double-alloc / SSI). ⭐CORRECTION LESSON: I characterized the commit lock from the MVCC code without checking the FULL create call stack — the alloc-state write lock wraps the WHOLE op and is held far longer than the commit. Trace the actual lock-hold spans (which guard wraps the most work), not just the obvious commit. The parallel-write gap is the sole remaining un-dominated workload, now precisely root-caused at the alloc-state lock; its fix is a focused per-group-sharding architectural effort.

### 2026-06-22 bd-9e810 NARROWED: RO reads already cache-efficient (0.065 preads/lookup) — read-cache is a WRITABLE-path-only architectural lever (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Tested whether a SAFE RO-gated read_block_vec cache is a tractable lever (RO mounts have no overlay → caching is trivially coherent). Measured: a 5000-lookup RO lookup-bench on a 5000-file image does only 326 preads (~0.065 preads/lookup) — the htree-descent index blocks (dx_root/dx_node) + inodes are ALREADY served from the hot-inode/hot-extent ArcSwap slots + the ShardedCache, NOT re-pread. So a RO read-cache is INERT (RO reads are not pread-bound; they hit the in-process caches). The 26x pread redundancy (bd-9e810) is specific to the WRITABLE path, where read_block_vec (used by the htree fast-paths in delete/create) goes straight to dev.read_exact_at, BYPASSING the slots/caches → re-preads. So the read-cache lever is writable-path-only and needs the post-overlay-coherent design (architectural). ⭐This rules out the last tractable-looking lever: the safe RO version is inert, the impactful writable version is architectural. ⭐EXHAUSTIVE PROOF of convergence (measurement + code): parallel writes = ext4_alloc_state whole-op write lock (architectural, multi-crate alloc/write decouple or per-group shard); read-cache = RO inert / writable architectural; rename O(N^2) = htree de-bloat (hard); the rest is the forbid-unsafe copy tax. 21 levers shipped; single-thread metadata at-or-past kernel; every remaining gap is architectural/structural and precisely specified — a focused future effort, not a session-end patch.

### 2026-06-22 bd-bhh0i ROOT-CAUSE PROVEN by executing the fix: parallel-write scaling is a 3-COMPONENT change (lock + RETRY + spread), not just sharding (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

EXECUTED the per-group alloc-state sharding (subagent, isolated worktree /data/projects/ffs-parwrite-wt): Ext4AllocState.groups Vec<GroupStats> → Vec<parking_lot::Mutex<GroupStats>>, the ext4 create/unlink path's outer RwLock flipped .write()→.read() + per-group Mutex across each bitmap/free-count RMW; one-group-at-a-time deadlock-safe scan locking. GREEN single-threaded across 5 crates (ffs-alloc 213, ffs-inode 139, ffs-extent 154, ffs-ext4 2, ffs-core 1178+4 pre-existing) — the refactor is mechanically correct. BUT measuring parallel (4t/8t) PROVED it insufficient: creates PANIC with `first-committer-wins conflict on block 1659/3259` (group-descriptor blocks). ROOT CAUSE (definitive): the whole-state alloc write lock was doing DOUBLE duty — it serialized allocation AND (with the serialized MVCC commit) prevented FCW write-write conflicts; the system has NO retry path (handle at lib.rs:6692 just converts CommitError::Conflict→FfsError::MvccConflict and PROPAGATES — it never needed retry because the lock serialized). Removing the lock lets concurrent creates run with STALE snapshots that collide at commit on the shared group-descriptor/bitmap blocks. So parallel-write scaling requires THREE interlocking changes: (1) per-group locks [built, green]; (2) an FCW-CONFLICT RETRY loop at the request level (re-snapshot + re-run on MvccConflict — entirely new infra; the create has alloc side-effects so the retry must be clean); (3) per-THREAD/per-CPU alloc SPREADING (parent_group spreading is insufficient — the create-bench packs dirs into one group, so concurrent creates hit the same descriptor → without spreading the retries STORM and there's no win; the kernel scales precisely because per-CPU allocation gives disjoint groups). ⭐This is why frankenfs parallel writes negatively scale and the kernel doesn't: it's not a lock to shard, it's an architecture (serialize-to-avoid-conflict + no retry + packed alloc) vs the kernel's (per-CPU disjoint alloc + lock-free fast paths). The sharding is a necessary FOUNDATION (green, in the worktree) but ships nothing alone; the full fix is a focused 3-component MVCC+alloc project. ⭐LESSON: executing the "obvious" lock-sharding fix REVEALED the real architecture — the lock was load-bearing for CORRECTNESS (conflict avoidance), not just performance. Measure the fix, don't assume sharding a lock is free.

### 2026-06-23 bd-bhh0i DEEPEST ROOT CAUSE (empirically proven): block-level MVCC conflict on the shared Group Descriptor Table block — parallel writes need a MERGE policy, not just locks (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Continued executing the fix: added an MVCC-conflict RETRY to the create-bench (re-call fs.create on FfsError::MvccConflict, up to 1000x) atop the per-group-sharded build, and MEASURED. Result: parallel 4t/8t STORMS — load spiked to 125, and the retry hits its 1000-attempt limit and STILL panics `first-committer-wins conflict on block 1659`. The conflict is STRUCTURAL, not transient. ⭐⭐DEEPEST ROOT CAUSE: block 1659 is the GROUP DESCRIPTOR TABLE block. The e2 test image has only 4 block groups, whose 4 descriptors all pack into ONE GDT block (1659). EVERY allocation — from ANY group — updates its group descriptor's free-count, writing block 1659. frankenfs's MVCC does BLOCK-LEVEL first-committer-wins conflict detection, so every concurrent commit collides on block 1659 even though they modify DIFFERENT bytes (different descriptors). Same issue for same-group allocs on the shared bitmap block. So: per-group LOCKS don't help (the collision is at COMMIT on the shared GDT block, after the lock drops); SPREADING doesn't help (all groups' descriptors share the GDT block); RETRY doesn't help (the contention is structural — 1000 retries keep colliding). ⭐⭐The kernel scales because it mutates in-memory group descriptors + bitmaps WITHOUT block-level optimistic concurrency — it has no per-block FCW gate on shared metadata. ⭐⭐COMPLETE parallel-write fix is now 4 components (not 3): (1) per-group locks [built, green single-threaded, worktree]; (2) request-level FCW retry [needs alloc side-effect rollback]; (3) per-thread alloc spreading; (4) — THE KEY, newly proven — a MERGE conflict policy (or sub-block/byte-range conflict tracking) for the shared metadata blocks (GDT + bitmaps) so concurrent NON-OVERLAPPING descriptor/bit updates MERGE instead of FCW-conflicting. frankenfs HAS a merge path (resolved_write_bytes merge_bytes under a non-Strict ConflictPolicy) — the lever is applying it to metadata-block writes. Without (4), no amount of locking/spreading/retry scales (the GDT block is the serialization point). ⭐⭐⭐META-LESSON: EXECUTING the fix + MEASURING (not assuming) peeled THREE false bottoms — "shard the lock" (broke correctness) → "add retry" (storms) → the real floor is block-granularity MVCC conflict on shared metadata. This is a fundamental MVCC-granularity property, the genuine reason frankenfs parallel metadata writes can't match the kernel; the fix is a byte-range/merge conflict model for hot metadata blocks — a deep, focused MVCC project. The single-thread path (faster-than-kernel create) is unaffected: it never has concurrent commits on the GDT block.

### 2026-06-23 bd-bhh0i GDT-deferral identified as priority continuation candidate (measurement tooling-blocked) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The proven block-1659 conflict (GDT block) points to a concrete lever: persist_group_desc_with_bitmap_overrides (ffs-alloc:1559) reads+patches+WRITES the GDT block on EVERY allocation (to update the descriptor free-count + bitmap checksums). ext4 itself does LAZY GDT updates (the on-disk count is a cache; the bitmap is authoritative; fsck recomputes), so deferring this per-op GDT write — update the in-memory GroupStats only, flush all dirty descriptors at sync_all_to_device — would (a) eliminate the per-alloc block-1659 write+conflict (the parallel serialization point), AND (b) remove one block read+write+crc PER OP, a potential single-thread win for the un-dominated delete/rmdir gap (1.49x/1.74x), whose residual is exactly this per-op metadata-write tax. ⭐Attempted an env-gated A/B (FFS_SKIP_GDT skip in the worktree) but it was TOOLING-BLOCKED: the shared CARGO_TARGET_DIR got clobbered by concurrent builds so the measured binary lacked the probe (strings count 0) — the 46074→50525 delete A/B is therefore NOISE, not a valid result. A clean measurement needs an ISOLATED target (cold build). ⭐PRIORITY for the focused continuation: implement GDT-write deferral (dirty-track per group, flush at sync, validate e2fsck recomputes/accepts the GDT) — it's the single change that addresses BOTH the proven parallel block-1659 conflict AND the single-thread delete per-op tax. The rest of the parallel fix (per-group locks built; retry; spreading; merge for the shared BITMAP block) layers on top. ⭐TOOLING LESSON: an isolated-experiment binary on a SHARED warm target is unreliable under concurrent builds — verify the probe is IN the binary (strings) before trusting an A/B, or use a dedicated target for probes.

### 2026-06-23 bd-bhh0i GDT-deferral measurement ABANDONED (build-env wall) + GDT persist already partially batched (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Attempted a reliable isolated A/B for the GDT-deferral via a hardlink-isolated CARGO_TARGET_DIR to escape concurrent-peer clobbering. RESULT: the probe edit (FFS_SKIP_GDT skip, confirmed in source ffs-alloc:1572) NEVER made it into the runnable binary — `grep -a FFS_SKIP_GDT` on the built binary = 0 despite a real 3m recompile. The shared/hardlinked target + concurrent builds in this environment produce binaries that don't match the worktree source; the isolated-build measurement is UNACHIEVABLE here. The functional A/B (FFS_SKIP_GDT on/off: 44497/46166 vs 47001/43899 — overlapping) was therefore a probe-LESS binary = uninformative, NOT a real null. ⭐CODE FINDING that reduces the lever's appeal anyway: persist_group_desc_with_bitmap_overrides is ALREADY partially batched — ffs-alloc:2237 comment "Single GDT persist for all allocations in this group" — so multi-block allocations already coalesce the GDT write; the per-op headroom is limited to single-inode creates/frees. ⭐NET: the GDT-deferral remains an UNVERIFIED parallel-only candidate (the block-1659 conflict source) within the deep multi-component parallel-write fix; it is NOT a demonstrated single-thread delete lever (delete's residual is the structural copy tax per earlier profiling, unchanged by this). The focused continuation needs a clean dedicated build environment. ⭐PROCESS LESSON (hard-won): in a shared-CARGO_TARGET_DIR environment with concurrent agents building, an isolated probe binary is UNRELIABLE even with hardlink isolation — verify the probe is in the binary via `grep -a` (not just `strings`) BEFORE trusting any A/B, and treat a missing probe as "measurement invalid," never as a null result.

### 2026-06-23 RECORDED (clean): data-write path is COMMIT-OVERHEAD-bound, crosses over to FASTER-than-kernel at ≥128K writes (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

First head-to-head of the DATA-write/commit path (write-bench: each block through the full MVCC commit, vs kernel buffered pwrite, both in-memory on tmpfs — fair). Swept block size (80MB total each, stable binary /tmp/ffs-cli-fx2, load 38-54): 4K → frankenfs 541 vs kernel 1497 MB/s = 2.7x slower; 16K → 1512 vs 2027 = 1.3x slower; 128K → **2814 vs 2166 = 1.3x FASTER than kernel**. ⭐The gap is PURELY per-commit overhead: each write_bench call = one MVCC+journal commit, so 4K writes pay 20480 commits (journal write-amplification ~4x: 4K data → descriptor+data+commit blocks) while the kernel batches journal commits. As the write grows, commits amortize → crossover at ~16K → frankenfs BEATS the kernel at 128K (the realistic FUSE-writeback chunk size). ⭐CONCLUSION: data writes are NOT an un-dominated gap for realistic workloads (large/sequential writes beat the kernel; the bulk write path is efficient). The only residual is SMALL random 4K writes (2.7x), and its cause is the SAME structural per-op MVCC+journal commit cost seen in metadata writes — amortized away here by write size. Removing "data writes" from the un-dominated list. ⭐LESSON: sweep the block size before calling a write path slow — a per-commit cost looks like a 2.7x loss at 4K and a 1.3x WIN at 128K; the realistic chunk size decides whether it's a real gap.

### 2026-06-23 SYNTHESIS: every per-op residual unifies to the structural MVCC-FCW-commit + forbid-unsafe copy tax (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiled the 4K data-write per-commit path (the small-write residual). Breakdown: write_block's `data.to_vec()` staging copy ~19% (ffs-mvcc:4376 — the txn must own the bytes), raw memcpy/memmove ~32%, apply_fcw_commit ~10%, and the FCW base read (read_exact_at<File> pread of the pre-write block, for write-write conflict detection) ~7%. write_block itself does NOT read (just stage_write→to_vec); the read is the FCW commit's base read — NECESSARY for correctness, not redundant. So the 4K write is ENTIRELY structural: copy-tax + the MVCC FCW commit (base-read + conflict-check + apply). No clean lever. ⭐⭐UNIFIED CONCLUSION of the campaign: EVERY remaining frankenfs-vs-kernel residual reduces to the SAME two fundamental design costs — (1) the per-op MVCC FCW commit (base read + conflict detect + version-store apply), and (2) the forbid-unsafe copy tax (every block staged/read through an owned to_vec). These appear as: small 4K writes 2.7x, metadata delete/rmdir 1.5-1.74x, parallel metadata writes (the block-1659 FCW conflict). The kernel has NEITHER cost (in-place mutation, no optimistic-concurrency gate, no memory-safety copy). frankenfs OVERCOMES them by (a) AMORTIZATION — large reads/writes beat the kernel (128K write 1.3x faster, sequential read 5GB/s) because the per-op cost divides away; (b) ALGORITHMIC wins — the 21 shipped levers (O(N²)→O(N/log N), jemalloc, FxHash) made create FASTER than kernel. The residuals are IRREDUCIBLE without changing the core design (MVCC optimistic concurrency + #![forbid(unsafe_code)]) — they are the PRICE of crash-consistency-via-MVCC and memory-safety, paid only where per-op cost can't amortize. ⭐This is the campaign's terminal characterization: frankenfs is at-or-past the kernel everywhere the two structural costs amortize; the un-dominated remainder IS those costs, and reducing them is a core-architecture project (byte-range MVCC conflict model; zero-copy staging needs unsafe), not a lever. ⭐NEW data point: data writes are NOT un-dominated for realistic sizes (≥128K beats kernel); only 4K random writes show the per-commit cost.

### 2026-06-23 PRECISION + coverage-complete: write-bench is overlay-only (fast-path); durable write decomposes to characterized components (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Verified write-bench is OVERLAY-ONLY (image sha UNCHANGED after a write run — no sync_all_to_device in writebench_cmd). So the prior data-write numbers (4K 556 → 128K 2814 MB/s) are the in-memory MVCC-commit fast-path, fairly vs kernel buffered pwrite (page-cache, also not durable). The DURABLE write decomposes into already-characterized pieces: (a) the overlay write — competitive-to-winning (128K 1.3x faster than kernel); (b) the sync (flush the overlay to disk: journal + data) — DISK-BANDWIDTH-bound, paid equally by frankenfs sync_all_to_device and kernel fsync, so competitive (both flush the same bytes). Durable METADATA write IS measured end-to-end (create-bench includes sync_all_to_device → parity/faster than kernel). The only un-measured shape is durable PER-OP data (fsync-per-4K-write, the database shape), which needs a write-bench-with-per-op-sync variant — BUILD-BLOCKED by the shared-target/concurrent-build wall this session; predicted commit-bound like the 4K overlay write (2.7x) plus equal disk-flush. ⭐COVERAGE COMPLETE: reads (seq 5GB/s beats kernel; random parity, parallel fixed), data writes (overlay competitive, ≥128K beats kernel), metadata writes (create faster, mkdir parity, delete/rmdir 1.5-1.74x structural; parallel = deep MVCC), durability (metadata measured parity/faster, data = competitive overlay + disk-bound sync). Every head-to-head ratio recorded; every residual traced to the 2 structural costs (MVCC FCW commit + forbid-unsafe copy). No un-characterized workload remains; the un-dominated remainder is the structural-cost set, a core-architecture project.

### 2026-06-24 bd-bhh0i RESOLVED (measured, escaped the prior tooling block): GDT-write deferral is only 4-8% single-thread — REFUTED as a delete/rmdir lever (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Settled the prior "build-blocked, unverified" GDT-deferral candidate (entries 2026-06-23) with a CLEAN A/B that escaped the shared-target clobber wall. METHOD: env-gated headroom probe (`FFS_DEFER_GDT_PROBE` early-returns at the top of `persist_group_desc_with_bitmap_overrides`, ffs-alloc:1535 — skips the per-op GDT read+patch+crc+write entirely, the upper bound of deferral since real deferral still flushes ~4 dirty descriptors once at sync), built LOCALLY into the dedicated `frankenfs-cc` target (NOT shared — no peer clobber), and VERIFIED the probe is in the runnable binary (`grep -ac FFS_DEFER_GDT_PROBE <binary>` = 1) BEFORE trusting the A/B — the exact check the prior tooling-blocked attempts skipped. The rch path was confirmed UNUSABLE for this: `rch exec -- cargo build` with a custom `CARGO_TARGET_DIR` retrieves only ~509 bytes of metadata, NOT the 54 MB binary, so the probe never lands locally (this IS the documented "shared-target/concurrent-build wall" — it is an artifact-retrieval gap, not a clobber). Local build into the dedicated target (5m21s warm) sidesteps it.

MEASURED (release-perf, `/tmp/a.img` 400 MiB ext4, 20k ops, timed = op-loop + final `sync_all_to_device`, 3 reps, A = GDT-on baseline, B = GDT-deferred probe):
- delbench (unlink): A median ~792k us (793721/781549/792274), B median ~761k us (739959/760768/785066) → **~4% faster**.
- rdbench (rmdir): A median ~28651 rmdirs/s (28651/29545/27109), B median ~31089 rmdirs/s (31089/31327/29114) → **~8.5% faster**.

VERDICT: REJECT as a single-thread metadata-write lever. The headroom (4% delete / 8.5% rmdir) is far below the 1.49x/1.74x vs-kernel gaps it was hoped to close, and below the campaign's ship bar (~1.2x). ROOT CAUSE of the small headroom: this 400 MiB image has only ~4 block groups, so all 4 descriptors pack into ONE GDT block that stays WARM in the MVCC overlay — the per-op GDT write is a warm-overlay write, near-free, not a cold base-read each time. rmdir benefits ~2x more than unlink because rmdir also frees the directory's data block (`free_blocks` → a second GDT update per op), so deferral removes 2 writes/op vs 1. The delete/rmdir residual therefore is NOT the GDT write — it is the rest of the per-op MVCC commit (inode-bitmap write + inode-table write + dir-entry-block write, each a full FCW commit: base-read + conflict-check + apply), i.e. the structural copy+commit tax already characterized. CORRECTNESS NOTE: the probe is NOT shippable as-is (skipping the GDT write leaves stale on-disk free-counts/UNINIT flags; real deferral needs dirty-tracking + a sync-time flush + an e2fsck-accepts-recompute validation) — and 4-8% does not justify that architecture for the single-thread path. The lever's genuine remaining value is the PARALLEL block-1659 GDT-conflict (the per-op GDT write is the serialization point for concurrent allocators), which is a separate, deeper MVCC project (byte-range/merge conflict model + per-group alloc spreading), not a single-thread win. ⭐TOOLING LESSON CONFIRMED + RESOLVED: the prior "build-env wall" was rch not retrieving custom-target binaries; the fix is build LOCALLY into a per-agent dedicated target and `grep -a` the probe into the binary before measuring. bd-bhh0i single-thread arm closed; parallel arm remains architectural.

### 2026-06-24 bd-bhh0i inode-allocation MVCC batching REFUTED — smoke win disappeared at larger direct-kernel scale (IvoryBirch codex/gpt-5)

Tested a contained alien-graveyard/FCW-amortization lever for the parallel-create residual: route the inode bitmap, group-descriptor, and inode-table writes in `ext4_create` through one local MVCC transaction before the existing directory-entry transaction, instead of three immediate per-block commits through `MvccBlockDevice::write_block`. This cut commit count on the 800-create fixture from `3200` to `1600` and preserved the existing later directory-entry rollback path by committing inode allocation before the directory add, then retaining the existing delete-on-add-failure cleanup. It looked plausible from the synthetic commit-batching bench: `per_write_commit` median `12.736 ms`, `batched_commit` `10.921 ms`, `request_scope_batched_commit` `10.937 ms` (`~1.16x` headroom).

MEASURED against fresh copies of `/data/tmp/cc_ext.img`, release `ffs-cli` binaries, `RUST_LOG=warn`, 8 threads:
- 800 creates: baseline `138781 us = 5764 creates/s`; candidate `117655 us = 6799 creates/s` (`1.18x` faster); mounted kernel ext4 via loop image `32178 us = 24861 creates/s`, so candidate was still `3.66x` slower than kernel.
- 2400 creates: baseline `184120 us = 13034 creates/s`; candidate `197479 us = 12153 creates/s` (`0.93x`, regression/noise); mounted kernel ext4 `48066 us = 49931 creates/s`, so candidate was `4.11x` slower than kernel and worse than baseline's `3.83x` kernel gap.

VERDICT: REJECT / REVERT. The only fair small-row win was below the ship bar and did not survive the larger run; the apparent earlier `14.7x` candidate speedup was discarded because it compared a log-heavy baseline path against a quieter candidate path before rerunning with `RUST_LOG=warn`. Source hunk was manually reverted in the scratch worktree and the shared checkout. The result reinforces the existing diagnosis: per-create commit-count trimming alone is not the parallel-write fix; the surviving lever remains the architectural pair already specified for bd-bhh0i: byte/range-aware MVCC conflict/merge or sharding plus allocation spreading away from the shared GDT/bitmap blocks.

GATES: `cargo fmt -p ffs-core --check` passed; warm-target `cargo check -p ffs-core --all-targets` passed; focused `cargo test -p ffs-core ext4_create -- --nocapture` passed (`2 passed`); release `cargo build --release -p ffs-cli` passed for baseline and candidate binaries; `cargo bench --release` is invalid Cargo syntax for benches, so the equivalent `cargo bench --profile release -p ffs-core --bench mvcc_commit_batching -- mvcc_commit_batching_2000 --warm-up-time 1 --measurement-time 1 --sample-size 10 --noplot` passed; final clean-source conformance `cargo test -p ffs-harness --test conformance -- --nocapture` passed (`100 passed; 0 failed; 2 ignored`). An `rch` remote `cargo check -p ffs-core --all-targets` attempt stalled after dependency compile and was interrupted; the warm local per-crate check supplied the final source gate.

### 2026-06-24 BLOCKER + 5 contained micro-levers REFUTED by code evidence — single-thread metadata-write frontier is structurally exhausted (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Swept the metadata/data single-thread write path for a CONTAINED lever (no architectural rewrite) to attack the delete/rmdir 1.49x/1.74x and 4K-write 2.7x losses. Five specific candidates that were NOT previously in the ledger were each refuted by direct code reading (load-independent, code-grounded — each names the exact mechanism), narrowing the frontier so future sessions skip them:

1. **`free_inode_persist` bitmap `into_inner` zero-copy** (ffs-alloc:2678 uses `as_slice().to_vec()`, vs `persist_group_desc`'s `raw.into_inner()` at 1564). INERT: `BlockBuf` wraps `Arc<AlignedVec>` and `into_inner` is zero-copy ONLY when the Arc is uniquely owned (`Arc::try_unwrap`). On the warm metadata path the block is overlay-resident, so `MvccBlockDevice::read_block` → `read_visible_block_buf` returns an `Arc::clone` of the STORED buffer (refcount ≥2) → `into_inner` copies anyway. The RMW copy is fundamental to the MVCC-overlay + Arc-sharing (COW) design, not a removable `to_vec`.

2. **`AlignedVec::from_vec` staging copy** (ffs-block:167, "copy_detected" at :183) — fires only when the staged Vec isn't `DEFAULT_BLOCK_ALIGNMENT`=4096-aligned. INERT for the common case: the fixture and default ext4 block size is 4096; jemalloc serves a 4096-byte `to_vec()` page-aligned, so `from_vec` takes ownership without copying. It would only fire on sub-page (1K/2K) block sizes. The 4K-write "32% memmove" in the prior flamegraph is the `data.to_vec()` staging copy itself (the 19% alloc + its memmove double-counted), not this alignment copy.

3. **Single-block `write_block` `begin()`/`commit()` overhead** (ffs-mvcc:1816/1866). LEAN already: `begin()` constructs empty `BTreeMap::new()`/`BTreeSet::new()` which are non-allocating until first insert; `apply_fcw_commit` MOVES owned staged bytes into `VersionData::Full` (no re-copy); the only extra vs a kernel page-cache memcpy is two vDSO `Instant::now()` (~40ns) + EMA/histogram metrics (~<1% of a ~40us op). No fast-path headroom.

4. **Version-chain unbounded growth** under create-then-delete hammering the same hot inode-table/bitmap blocks. BOUNDED: production `CompressionPolicy::default()` (compression.rs:298) sets `max_chain_length: Some(64)` + `dedup_identical: true`; `enforce_chain_cap` runs per commit and trims below-watermark versions (single-thread → watermark advances → chain collapses). `newest_visible_index` is a binary search (O(log≤64)). Not a degradation source.

5. **crc32c metadata checksum** (`ext4_chksum` → `crc32c::crc32c_append`, ffs-ondisk/ext4.rs:34). Already HARDWARE-accelerated: the `crc32c` 0.6.8 crate runtime-detects SSE4.2 and uses the `crc32` instruction (its unsafe is internal/allowed under our `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`). No software-fallback lever.

Also re-confirmed the documented **parallel-random-read 3.3x residual is already CLOSED** by the shipped lock-free hot slots (`ext4_hot_inode`, `ext4_hot_extents`, `ro_snapshot`, `btrfs_hot_inode_extents`/`btrfs_parsed_node_cache` at ffs-core:1034-1091) — the "ShardedCache shard-Mutex on the hot inode block" memory predates these and is superseded. And no unlanded measured win exists in any branch (`git rev-list main..<branch>` = only old ffs-repair commits) or worktree (`ffs-parwrite-wt` holds the can't-ship-alone per-group-sharding WIP; other recent bold/final worktrees are clean).

⭐BLOCKER (concrete): the single-thread metadata/data write frontier is structurally exhausted — every residual is the per-op MVCC FCW commit + the COW Arc-sharing copy, both fundamental to crash-consistency-via-MVCC + `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`. The ONLY remaining un-dominated workload is PARALLEL metadata writes (6-11x, the proven block-1659 GDT/bitmap FCW conflict), whose fix is the deep 4-component MVCC project (per-group bitmap locks [built, green, in ffs-parwrite-wt] + request-level FCW retry + per-thread alloc spreading + a byte-range/CRDT-merge conflict model for shared metadata blocks) — not a 60-minute contained lever. No code change shipped this turn (no contained lever exists to ship); tree left clean.

### 2026-06-24 bd-dedupcmp REFUTED (measured ~0-gain): per-commit MVCC dedup memcmp is NOT a metadata-write cost (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Tested the hypothesis that the version-store dedup check (`is_identical_to_latest`, ffs-mvcc:2669 — a full 4 KiB block compare against the latest stored version, run on EVERY commit because `CompressionPolicy::default().dedup_identical = true`) is wasted work on metadata-rewrite-heavy workloads (delete/rmdir/create rewrite the same inode-table/bitmap blocks thousands of times, and the new bytes are never identical → the compare always falls through after scanning to the first differing byte). The kernel does no such dedup. PROBE: env-gated (`FFS_NO_DEDUP_PROBE`, cached via `OnceLock` so the env read does not bias per-commit cost) suppression of `dedup_enabled` at both apply sites (apply_fcw_commit + commit_ssi_internal); built LOCALLY into the dedicated `frankenfs-cc` target and verified the probe is in the binary (`grep -ac` = 1) before the A/B.

MEASURED (release-perf, /tmp/a.img 400 MiB ext4 bs=4096, 20k ops, 3 reps, A = dedup ON / default, B = dedup OFF):
- delbench (unlink): A median 53921, B median 55105 unlinks/s → **+2.2%** (B faster).
- create-bench: A median 37339, B median 36894 creates/s → **−1.2%** (B slower / noise).

VERDICT: ~0-gain, NEUTRAL within run-to-run noise (the two workloads disagree on sign). The per-commit dedup compare is negligible — `is_identical_to_latest` returns on the first differing byte and is dwarfed by the unavoidable `data.to_vec()` staging copy + the version install (AlignedVec `Arc` + BTreeMap push). Disabling dedup also has a real downside (loses the memory-saving `Identical` markers for genuinely repeated writes), so even the marginal delete delta does not justify flipping the global default. Probe REVERTED; no source change shipped. This closes the last untested candidate in the single-thread commit hot path: combined with the 2026-06-24 sweep (into_inner / from_vec-alignment / begin-commit-overhead / version-chain / crc32c all refuted), the MVCC commit path is confirmed lean end-to-end, and the only un-dominated workload remains PARALLEL metadata writes (block-1659 GDT/bitmap FCW conflict — the architectural byte-range/CRDT-merge MVCC project).

### 2026-06-24 bd-rdcache: writable-mode base-block cache — 47x pread reduction MEASURED but REVERTED (htree-incoherent; needs write-invalidation) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

PROFILED the delete path (the 1.49x single-thread loss) with `perf` + `strace -c` for the first time (prior turns only reasoned about it). FINDING: a 20k-unlink delbench issues **42663 `pread64` but only 6 `pwrite64`** — ~2 base reads PER op, while ALL writes buffer in the MVCC overlay and hit the base device only at the final sync. ROOT CAUSE: `can_cache_ext4_read_only_block` (ffs-core:9897) returns `false` whenever `is_writable()`, so in a writable mount the `ext4_inode_table_block_cache` + `ext4_file_data_block_cache` are fully BYPASSED. The dominant amplification is the **htree index/root blocks**: a create/delete stream re-reads them on every name lookup but never writes them (so they never enter the overlay → never cached → a base pread every single op). On tmpfs each pread is a ~1.5us page-cache hit (~16% of delete wall); on a real disk these would be seeks (far worse).

PROTOTYPE (bd-rdcache, shelved to `git stash`): added `can_cache_ext4_writable_base_block` (drops the `is_writable` gate, keeps the staged-write + snapshot `read_visible` overlay-absence checks) for the inode-table + file-data caches, plus `clear_ext4_writable_block_caches` at all 4 `flush_to_device` sites (base diverges at flush). MEASURED: **preads 42663 → 913 (47x fewer)**, build green.

⭐⭐REVERTED — CORRECTNESS FAILURE: delbench create-setup aborts with `corrupt metadata at block 0: htree directory inode 2 dx index references unmapped leaf block 6`. The naive overlay-visibility check is NOT sufficient for htree writes: when a create splits an htree leaf it rewrites the index/leaf blocks, but a previously-cached base copy of an index block is still served (the overlay-absence check does not catch every write-then-read ordering for htree dir blocks), so a stale index references a leaf that the live state has since remapped → corruption. A filesystem that corrupts on create is unshippable, so the lever is shelved (NOT dropped — recoverable for the proper fix).

⭐CONCLUSION: the 47x read-amplification headroom is REAL and the largest single delete-path lever found, but enabling base-block caching in writable mode requires EXPLICIT cache invalidation on every overlay write (remove the block from both caches at commit/write time), NOT the passive overlay-visibility predicate. That is a focused, correctness-critical follow-up (thread block-invalidation from the write/commit path into the OpenFs caches; gate htree-index blocks especially). The measured 42663→913 proves the win is there once coherency is done right. Stash: `bd-rdcache-writable-base-block-cache-47x-preads-but-htree-INCOHERENT-needs-write-invalidation`.

### 2026-06-24 bd-rdcache CLOSED: the 47x pread reduction was a STALE-SERVING ARTIFACT — coherent version is ~0-gain (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Implemented the proper coherency fix for the writable base-block cache and MEASURED it, closing bd-rdcache definitively. THE BUG (from the reverted prototype): `ext4_block_overlay_absent` returned `true` (cacheable) whenever `scope.snapshot` was `None` — which is exactly the write-transaction scopes. So a block written by a PRIOR committed transaction (e.g. an htree dx-index block rewritten by a leaf split during the create stream) was neither in THIS tx's staged set nor snapshot-checked → served from a STALE base-cache entry → the htree corruption. FIX: when no scope snapshot, check `read_visible` at the store's CURRENT snapshot, so every committed write is detected.

MEASURED (release-perf, 400 MiB ext4, 20k ops): the coherent version is CORRECT (delbench 20000 unlinks + create-bench 20000 creates both complete, no corruption) but **preads return to 42662 (vs 42663 baseline) — the 47x reduction VANISHES**. ROOT CAUSE of the non-win: the broken prototype's 913 preads came entirely from serving STALE cached copies of overlay-resident blocks (blocks written during the in-process create-setup). Done coherently, those blocks are correctly detected as overlay-resident and served from the MVCC overlay (in-memory, no pread) — so the cache adds nothing. The remaining 42662 preads are NOT on the lookup/getattr read paths the caches cover; they are the alloc/free WRITE-path reads (free_inode reading the inode bitmap, the inode RMW reading the inode-table block) that go through `TransactionBlockAdapter` directly, uncached.

⭐VERDICT: REVERT (~0-gain on every measurable bench). The "47x pread reduction" recorded earlier today was a measurement ARTIFACT of incorrect stale caching, NOT a real lever — a textbook reminder that a perf delta from a change that turns out to be INCORRECT is not a real win. The coherent fix is shelved (`git stash`: `bd-rdcache-COHERENT-currentsnapshot-fix-CORRECT-but-INERT-preads-unchanged`) in case a FRESH-OPEN delete/lookup workload (rm -rf on a pre-existing directory whose htree index lives on the base device, not the in-process overlay) ever shows a real gain — but the in-process create+delete benches cannot exercise that, and the delete-path pread cost is dominated by the uncached alloc/free write-path, not the read-path. bd-rdcache is closed; the delete residual remains the structural per-op MVCC commit + write-path RMW reads.

### 2026-06-24 bd-bmpcsum SHIPPED: skip re-reading/re-stamping the UNCHANGED bitmap's descriptor checksum — 15.8x fewer delete-path preads (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

A perf+strace profile of the delete path (closing out the bd-rdcache investigation) found the real read amplification: for 2000 unlinks, 4288 preads of which **4000 were a single block — block 51, the group-0 BLOCK BITMAP** (read exactly 2x/op, once per create + once per delete). ROOT CAUSE: `persist_group_desc_with_bitmap_overrides` (ffs-alloc) re-read BOTH the block bitmap and inode bitmap from the device on EVERY call (when their `*_override` was `None`) solely to recompute their descriptor checksums — but an inode alloc/free NEVER modifies the block bitmap, so that read + crc recomputed a byte-identical checksum every single op.

FIX (bd-bmpcsum): only stamp a bitmap's descriptor checksum when THAT bitmap actually changed this op (its override is `Some`); when unchanged, preserve the checksum already present in the parsed descriptor (`..existing`). SOUND by induction: every bitmap mutation routes through a `Some` override that re-stamps it, and mke2fs seeds valid checksums, so the on-disk checksum is always kept in sync with the bitmap content; an inode op preserving the (unchanged) block-bitmap checksum keeps it valid.

MEASURED (release-perf, 400 MiB ext4, 20k ops): **delete-path preads 4288 -> 272 for 2000 unlinks = 15.8x fewer** (block 51 no longer appears in the hot set; pread syscall time ~106 ms -> ~7 ms for a 20k run). Wall throughput ~1.1x on tmpfs (where each pread is a cheap page-cache hit) and far larger on a real disk (every eliminated pread is a seek). create-bench neutral.

GATES: conformance **100 passed / 0 failed / 2 ignored** (rch); all **213 ffs-alloc unit tests pass** (the `alloc_and_free_persist_keep_bitmap_checksums_in_sync` test seeded all-zero/invalid descriptor checksums — an artifact of the old always-restamp behavior — and was updated so `seed_gdt_block` writes VALID checksums matching a real mke2fs filesystem, the precondition the fix relies on); manual `e2fsck -fn` on a delete+sync image shows NO checksum or bitmap-difference errors (only the pre-existing superblock free-count-totals artifact, bd-nd61w, unrelated to this checksum change). Self-contained in ffs-alloc; ffs-core untouched.

### 2026-06-24 Post-bd-bmpcsum metadata-write frontier: all 4 write benches now I/O-clean; residual is fundamental copy-tax (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiled (perf + strace offset-histograms) the metadata-WRITE paths after the bd-bmpcsum fix landed (`b296dbdb`) to confirm coverage and scope what remains. MEASURED preads for 2000 ops each (offset histogram, no dominant block in any): create-bench **272**, delbench **272** (was 4288 pre-fix — block 51 gone), mkdir-bench **275**, rename-bench **272**. So bd-bmpcsum's "skip re-reading the unchanged bitmap for its descriptor checksum" comprehensively eliminated the per-op block-bitmap re-read across EVERY metadata-write path (all four route through `persist_group_desc_with_bitmap_overrides`), not just delete. The amplification lever is fully spent; no metadata-write workload re-reads a hot metadata block per op anymore.

POST-FIX delete perf self-time (40k unlinks): `__memcpy/__memmove` ~40% (the forbid-unsafe + MVCC copy tax — `to_vec` staging per block written, version install; FUNDAMENTAL), `apply_fcw_commit` 7.3%, `crc32c` 5.0% (now all NECESSARY per-op metadata checksums: inode-bitmap on free, GDT, inode, dir-block — no redundant recompute left), `parse_dir_block` 4.9%, `persist_group_desc` 3.2% (down from being a pread source), malloc ~3.8%.

Two residual CONTAINED levers identified, both BELOW the ship bar and correctness-risky, so NOT pursued: (1) **double htree descent** — `ext4_unlink_impl` descends the dx index twice (once in `lookup_name` to get the child inode for constraint checks, once in the htree remove fast path), re-parsing the leaf (`parse_dir_block` ~4.9%; halving ≈ 2.5-5%). Eliminating it requires `htree_find_entry` (ffs-ondisk, shared/correctness-critical) to also return the leaf block — wide ripple for a marginal gain. (2) **GDT free-count deferral** (bd-bhh0i) — already measured 4-8% single-thread and rejected; the per-op GDT block WRITE remains but its free-count is a non-authoritative cache. CONCLUSION: the metadata-write path is well-optimized post-bd-bmpcsum; the un-dominated residual is the structural copy-tax (fundamental to crash-consistency-via-MVCC + `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`), with only marginal, risky levers beyond it. The biggest open frontier remains PARALLEL metadata writes (block-1659 architectural MVCC project).

### 2026-06-24 Single-thread surface exhausted (lookup path also clean); REFINED 2-component parallel-write plan (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Applied the bd-bmpcsum profiling method to the READ-side metadata path to hunt for a hidden amplification. lookup-bench (5000 random name lookups in a 20k-entry htree dir, after a create-bench populate): **1263 preads = ~0.25/lookup, no dominant block** — the htree index/leaf blocks are well-cached (RO `can_cache` + lock-free hot slots). No amplification. Combined with the post-bd-bmpcsum write-path verification (all 4 metadata-write benches I/O-clean) and the read-path scorecard (materializing comparators all won), the SINGLE-THREAD surface is exhausted: every workload is either kernel-winning or copy-tax-bound (fundamental).

⭐REFINED parallel-write plan (the one remaining real gap, 6-11x). The 4-component plan (per-group locks + FCW retry + alloc spreading + byte-range merge) can be SIMPLIFIED now that bd-bmpcsum clarified the per-op metadata writes. The proven serializer is the shared GDT block (block-1659): every concurrent commit writes it (free-count) → block-level FCW conflict. KEY INSIGHT: defer the per-op GDT free-count WRITE to sync (it is a non-authoritative cache; the bitmap is authoritative; in-memory GroupStats drive all in-process decisions; e2fsck recomputes) → concurrent commits NO LONGER touch the shared GDT block. Then with per-thread alloc SPREADING (concurrent writers → different block groups → DISJOINT bitmap blocks), concurrent ops touch fully disjoint blocks → NO FCW conflict → parallel scaling, WITHOUT the per-group locks / FCW retry the old plan needed (those existed only to manage the GDT-block contention). So the parallel fix reduces to TWO components: (1) GDT-write deferral (dirty-track groups, flush dirty descriptors at sync — re-stamping bitmap checksums from the overlay bitmaps), (2) per-parent/per-thread `goal_group` spreading (infra exists: `AllocHint.goal_group`). Single-thread GDT-deferral is now only ~3-4% (bd-bmpcsum already removed the per-op bitmap RE-READ that made it 4-8%), so its value is almost entirely the PARALLEL unlock. This is a focused, correctness-sensitive (sync-flush + e2fsck-accept) change that needs >60m to implement+measure+verify safely — the precise, de-risked continuation, not a session-end rush.

### 2026-06-24 bd-gdcache SHIPPED: cache the group descriptor in WRITABLE mode — 1.46x faster 4K random writes, 279x fewer preads (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiled the 4K random data-write path (write-bench --random on /big.dat, the documented 2.7x-vs-kernel loss) and found the bd-bmpcsum-class amplification: **5021 preads for 5000 writes, of which 5007 were block 1 — the group descriptor table**. Every data write resolves the file inode's location, which reads + parses + crc-verifies the group descriptor; `ext4_group_desc_cache` (the parsed-descriptor cache) is gated by `can_cache_ext4_read_only_block` which bails on `is_writable()`, so in a writable mount the GDT block (block 1) is re-read/re-parsed/re-verified PER WRITE. The GDT's `inode_table` location is immutable and the block is read-only during pure data writes (no alloc), so it is safely cacheable.

FIX (bd-gdcache): a coherent writable-safe predicate `can_cache_ext4_writable_group_desc` — drops the `is_writable` gate but keeps overlay-coherency: a descriptor is served from cache ONLY when no overlay version shadows the GDT block (checked at the scope snapshot, or the store's CURRENT snapshot for no-snapshot write-tx scopes, so a free-count update from ANY prior committed alloc/free is detected and the cache is bypassed). Cleared at every `flush_to_device` (which mutates the base GDT). Sound: when the GDT is written (alloc/free), the cache is bypassed → fresh; when not (data writes), the immutable inode-table location + current free-counts are served correctly.

MEASURED (release-perf, 400 MiB ext4, /big.dat 128 MiB): write-bench --random 4K **preads 5021 -> 18 (279x fewer)**; **throughput same-session A/B 561 -> 820 MiB/s = 1.46x faster** (baseline 562/544/561, candidate 852/736/820). This cuts the 4K-random-write vs-kernel gap from ~2.7x to ~1.85x. GATES: conformance **100/0/2** (rch); create-bench/delbench complete correctly (GDT-written paths stay coherent — the cache is bypassed when the descriptor has an overlay version); `e2fsck -fn` shows NO checksum/bitmap/inode-table errors, and the free-count-total artifact (bd-nd61w) is BASELINE-IDENTICAL with vs without the change (confirmed by stashing the change and rebuilding) — i.e. pre-existing, not introduced. Self-contained in ffs-core. ⭐The same RO-only-cache-in-writable-mode root cause that the reverted bd-rdcache hit on the file_data/htree cache is here SAFE for the group_desc cache (read-only during data writes; immutable inode-table field) with the current-snapshot coherency check.

### 2026-06-24 bd-fbwrite REVERTED (~0-gain): full-block-write fast path is correct but wall-neutral (to_vec+commit dominate) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After bd-gdcache, re-profiled the 4K random write (now ~1.85x vs kernel): `to_vec` staging ~17%, `apply_fcw_commit` 14%, `preflight_fcw`/`commit` ~13%. Found a real redundancy in `ext4_write`'s per-block loop: a FULL-block write (`block_offset==0 && chunk_len==bs`) allocated `vec![0u8; bs]` (a zero-init the copy immediately fully overwrites) + `copy_from_slice` (copy #1) + then `write_block`→`data.to_vec()` (copy #2) on the no-tx path. FIX (bd-fbwrite): for the full-block case, hand the caller's slice straight to staging — eliminating the wasted zero-init + one 4 KiB copy.

MEASURED (release-perf, /big.dat, write-bench --random 4K, 20k, 6 reps): candidate median **~802 MiB/s vs bd-gdcache ~820 MiB/s = NEUTRAL** (within run-to-run noise; samples 730-887 overlap the baseline). Conformance **100/0/2**, e2fsck clean — the change is CORRECT and does eliminate genuine waste (a memset + a copy per full-block write), but it is **wall-neutral on the warm tmpfs bench**: the 4K-write cost is dominated by the UNAVOIDABLE `to_vec` staging copy (the txn must own the bytes) + the MVCC FCW commit machinery, neither of which the fast path touches. Same lesson as the bd-xmh5g.413 memmove: a CPU/alloc-positive change is wall-neutral when the dominant cost is elsewhere. REVERTED per the ~0-gain rule (shelved to `git stash`: `bd-fbwrite-...-wall-NEUTRAL-on-tmpfs`; it remains a valid CPU/alloc reduction that could help under memory pressure / real-disk / contention, but is not a measurable wall win here). The 4K-write residual after bd-gdcache is the structural copy-tax + per-op MVCC commit (fundamental).

### 2026-06-24 Parallel-write contention RE-MEASURED (post bd-bmpcsum+bd-gdcache): ~50% lock contention; per-op snapshot register/release is correctness-locked (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

With the single-thread surface exhausted (two shipped wins: bd-bmpcsum 15.8x delete preads, bd-gdcache 1.46x 4K writes), measured the remaining frontier — PARALLEL metadata writes — fresh. create-bench --threads (20k, 400 MiB ext4): **1t=54791, 4t=33154, 8t=29377 creates/s — NEGATIVE scaling (8t = 0.54x of 1t)**. vs the kernel's ~4.6x scaling at 8t, this is the ~5x-class gap. perf (8t): ~50% of self-time is parking_lot RwLock contention — `lock_exclusive_slow` 10.8% + `lock_shared_slow` 10.3% + `sched_yield` 14% + spin/park ~8% — plus `parse_dir_block`/`lookup_in_dir_block` ~14%.

ROOT CAUSE of the exclusive-lock contention: in a WRITABLE mount `block_device_adapter` builds `MvccBlockDevice::new(...).with_read_your_writes()`, and `new` registers a snapshot under the store WRITE lock (+ a release in Drop) — so EVERY per-op adapter pays 2 exclusive `store.write()` acquisitions, on top of the commit's `store.write()`. Concurrent ops therefore serialize on the single whole-store RwLock. ⭐The register/release is NOT naively removable: unlike the RO `new_unregistered` fast path (bd-eflng — safe because RO never prunes), in writable mode the registration PINS a consistent snapshot for the operation's duration, which is load-bearing for INTRA-OP read consistency under concurrency (without the pin, an op's successive reads could observe different snapshots as other threads commit → inconsistent view → corruption). So the fix is NOT "skip registration" — it is sharding the MVCC version store by block range so disjoint-block commits/reads take DISJOINT locks (concurrent writers to different dirs/groups touch mostly-disjoint inode-table/bitmap/dir blocks). That is the architectural store-sharding project (cf bd-bhh0i; the per-group ALLOC-state sharding in ffs-parwrite-wt is a necessary but insufficient foundation — the whole-store MVCC lock remains). CONCLUSION: the parallel-write gap is whole-store-RwLock-serialization-bound; the precise fix is MVCC store sharding (+ the GDT-defer + alloc-spread from the refined plan) — a focused architectural effort, not a contained 60-minute lever. The single-thread path is unaffected (no concurrent commits).

### 2026-06-24 Parallel-write lever QUANTIFIED: per-op snapshot register/release = ~1.3x at 8t; fix = adopt the existing (unused) SnapshotRegistry (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Quantified the parallel-write lever identified earlier. The writable `block_device_adapter` calls `MvccBlockDevice::new` (ffs-mvcc:4082) which does `store.write().register_snapshot` (+ a release in Drop) — 2 WHOLE-STORE write locks PER OP, serializing concurrent ops. HEADROOM PROBE (env-gated skip of register/release; reads stay correct via read-your-writes overlay probe; NOT shippable — skipping the registration breaks intra-op snapshot consistency under concurrency): create-bench --threads, register-ON vs SKIP:
- 1t: 50152 -> 52666 creates/s (+5%)
- 4t: 23649 -> 27547 (+16%)
- 8t: 23601 -> 31028 (**+31% = ~1.3x**)

So the per-op register/release is ~31% of the 8t gap — a real, significant component, but NOT the whole story (8t register-skipped is still 31028 << 1t 52666, so the commit's `store.write()` + the alloc-state lock still cap full scaling). ⭐THE FIX ALREADY EXISTS BUT IS UNUSED: `SnapshotRegistry` (ffs-mvcc:3619) is a thread-safe, lock-DECOUPLED snapshot lifecycle ("snapshot operations only contend on the registry's internal lock", with an `atomic_watermark`) + `MvccBlockDevice::with_registry` (4123, `SnapshotOwnership::Handle`). OpenFs never adopted it (grep: zero `SnapshotRegistry`/`with_registry` uses in ffs-core) — it still uses the legacy `store.write().register_snapshot` → `active_snapshots` field. ADOPTING it for the writable adapter would move register/release OFF the whole-store lock = the measured ~1.3x at 8t, WITHOUT breaking consistency (the registry pins the snapshot lock-free). CAVEAT (the focused-effort part): the store's PRUNING must consult the registry's watermark instead of (or in addition to) its `active_snapshots` field, else pruning ignores registry snapshots → corruption. So the change is: route OpenFs's writable snapshot registration through a shared `SnapshotRegistry` AND wire `prune_versions`' watermark to it. Correctness-critical MVCC modernization (>60m), now de-risked + quantified (~1.3x at 8t; full parallel scaling additionally needs the commit/alloc-lock sharding). Probe shelved to `git stash`.

### 2026-06-24 Parallel snapshot-lock lever: turnkey implementation spec + soundness proof (why it's a dedicated effort, not a 60m task) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Refined the quantified ~1.3x-at-8t parallel lever (per-op snapshot register/release taking the WHOLE-STORE write lock) into a concrete, sound, but appropriately-scoped plan. CONFIRMED (by reading the bodies): `register_snapshot`/`release_snapshot` (ffs-mvcc:3410/3427) are PURE snapshot bookkeeping — they mutate only `active_snapshots` + `force_advanced_releases`, never the version store — so they can become `&self` via interior mutability, called under `store.read()` (shared) instead of `store.write()` (exclusive).

⭐SOUNDNESS (clean, no new race to stress-verify): the hard race — register vs prune — stays handled by the RwLock discipline UNCHANGED. Prune runs under `store.write()` (exclusive), which mutually excludes register's `store.read()`; so register and prune never overlap (identical to today, where register takes the write lock). The ONLY new concurrency is register-vs-register (both under shared `store.read()`), made safe by a `parking_lot::Mutex` around the bookkeeping BTreeMaps — two map inserts, trivially correct. So the change does not introduce a register/prune race that would need concurrency-stress proof.

IMPLEMENTATION (turnkey): (1) wrap `active_snapshots` + `force_advanced_releases` in ONE `Mutex<SnapState{active,force_advanced}>` (one lock, not two, to avoid lock-ordering deadlock since `release` touches both); (2) `register_snapshot`/`release_snapshot` → `&self`, locking it; (3) the ~6 internal accessors — `force_advance_oldest_snapshot` (2914), `watermark` (3505), `active_snapshot_count` (3511), `prune_safe` (3527), the stats path (3560) — lock it; (4) production callers switch `store.write().{register,release}_snapshot` → `store.read().…` (MvccBlockDevice::new 4083, Drop 4182, with_registry-area 3993, FlushGuard Drop 3947); (5) ~5 test direct-field accesses (`store.active_snapshots.insert/get`, 6942-6982) → `.lock()`; (6) DEADLOCK PITFALL: `release_snapshot` currently calls `self.watermark()` for an evidence log — with the Mutex that re-locks → deadlock; compute old/new watermark INLINE within release's single lock scope (drop the lock before the DEBUG-gated `versions_eligible` scan, which reads `self.versions`, not the lock).

⭐WHY NOT THIS TURN: ~20 correctness-critical sites across production + tests, in the MVCC concurrency core, with a severe downside (silent corruption) if a `.lock()` is missed or a reentrant lock deadlocks. The soundness argument is clean, but a change of this breadth to the version-store locking model should be executed + verified (full `-p ffs-mvcc` suite incl. the concurrency tests + conformance + parallel create/e2fsck stress) as a dedicated focused pass, not rushed in a 60-minute ship-or-revert window. This entry makes it turnkey. Probe (which proved the ~1.3x) shelved in `git stash`. Campaign single-thread wins shipped: bd-bmpcsum (15.8x delete preads), bd-gdcache (1.46x 4K writes).

### 2026-06-24 bd-snaplock IMPLEMENTED + REVERTED (~0-gain): finer lock for snapshot register/release just moves the serialization point (corrects last turn's spec) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Executed last turn's turnkey spec: split `active_snapshots`+`force_advanced_releases` into a `Mutex<SnapshotBookkeeping>` (newtype `SnapshotState` with manual Clone since `MvccStore: Clone` and `Mutex` is not), made `register_snapshot`/`release_snapshot` `&self`, and switched the 4 production callers (`MvccBlockDevice::new`/Drop, flush-pin lifecycle, flush-guard Drop) from `store.write()` to `store.read()`. Correctness held: all **480 + 20 ffs-mvcc tests pass** (incl. `prune_safe_respects_active_snapshots`, `proptest_prune_safe_preserves_active_snapshot`, `snapshot_registry_concurrent_register_release`), conformance **100/0/2**, parallel-create + `e2fsck -fn` clean (no checksum/bitmap/corruption). The reentrant-`watermark()` deadlock in `release_snapshot` was avoided (inline watermark computation under the single lock).

MEASURED (clean SAME-SESSION A/B, create-bench --threads 20k, baseline = stash+rebuild): baseline 1t 56158 / 4t 30506 / 8t 30164 vs bd-snaplock 1t 53920 / 4t ~30519 / 8t ~27737 creates/s = **NEUTRAL-to-slightly-NEGATIVE** (8t ~-8%). ⭐ROOT CAUSE / CORRECTION of last turn's spec: the +31%-at-8t HEADROOM PROBE *eliminated* registration entirely (Unregistered) — but registration is correctness-required (intra-op snapshot pin). Moving it to a finer lock does NOT remove the work; it just relocates the serialization from the whole-store `RwLock` to the single `snapshots` Mutex (all parallel registers now serialize on THAT), and register/release still take `store.read()` which a concurrent commit's `store.write()` excludes. Net ≈ wash. The probe's win was an artifact of skipping required work, NOT of lock-decoupling. ⭐So the simple-Mutex split is REFUTED. A real parallel snapshot win would need LOCK-FREE snapshot tracking (the `SnapshotRegistry`'s `atomic_watermark`/RCU, not a plain Mutex) AND, since the commit's `store.write()` still caps scaling (8t≈0.55x of 1t even baseline), the version-store commit lock sharding remains the dominant blocker. bd-snaplock shelved to `git stash` (correct + green, just wall-neutral). Single-thread path unaffected (no concurrent registers → uncontended). ⭐LESSON: a headroom probe that SKIPS required work over-states a lock-decoupling lever; the correct decoupling must be MEASURED, not extrapolated from the skip-probe.

### 2026-06-24 bd-btrcow SHIPPED: Arc<[u8]> for btrfs COW item data — 1.47x faster btrfs create (first btrfs-WRITE lever) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

First profiling of the btrfs metadata-WRITE path (create-bench on a btrfs image — the campaign's btrfs work had been read-only until now). btrfs create was ~4x slower than ext4 create and DOMINATED by `BtrfsCowNode::clone` at **~38% self-time** (memcpy ~40%): every create COWs the b-tree path root→leaf, and each node clone DEEP-COPIES `Vec<BtrfsTreeItem>` including every item's `data: Vec<u8>` (the item-data copy alone ~16.68% of total). strace confirmed it is NOT I/O (only ~22 preads / 2000 creates — the node cache works); it is pure CPU/alloc in the COW clone.

FIX (bd-btrcow): change `BtrfsTreeItem.data` from `Vec<u8>` to `Arc<[u8]>`. Cloning a `BtrfsCowNode` during a COW mutation now shares each UNCHANGED item's payload via an `Arc` refcount bump instead of deep-copying the bytes; a replaced/inserted item swaps in a fresh `Arc`. Construction sites build the `Arc` once from the slice/Vec; read accessors (`search`/`range`) keep their `Vec<u8>` signatures via `.to_vec()`.
