MEASURED (release-perf, btrfs image, create-bench 15000, clean SAME-SESSION A/B via stash+rebuild): baseline `Vec<u8>` median **~9299 creates/s** (9540/9299/9245) vs `Arc<[u8]>` median **~13632 creates/s** (13784/13171/14297/13480) = **1.47x faster**. GATES: **361 + 38 ffs-btrfs tests pass** (COW b-tree mutation/split/search/range all green), conformance **100/0/2** (rch). The win is the COW node-clone payload-sharing; it does not change on-disk bytes (the data is the same, just refcounted in memory). Self-contained: ffs-btrfs (type + ~13 sites) + ffs-core (3 sites). ⭐The campaign's read path had `Arc`-shared buffers already; this brings the same to the btrfs COW WRITE path, where node-clone deep-copy was the dominant cost. Residual btrfs-create cost = the `Vec<BtrfsTreeItem>` structure/key clone + the per-op MVCC commit (the keys are small fixed structs; further sharing would need a persistent/immutable item vector).

### 2026-06-24 bd-btrcow2 SHIPPED: pre-size COW node vectors for insert — ~1.07x more btrfs create (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Follow-up to bd-btrcow. Re-profiling btrfs create (post-Arc-data) showed it still `BtrfsCowNode::clone`-bound (~42%), now split keys ~20% / items ~14% / children ~8%, PLUS `realloc`/`finish_grow` ~13.5%. ROOT CAUSE of the realloc: `insert_into` did `node_ref(id)?.clone()` which yields an EXACT-capacity vector, so the immediately-following `Vec::insert` had `len == cap` and reallocated-and-recopied the ENTIRE key/item/child vector — a SECOND full copy on every COW insert.

FIX (bd-btrcow2): build the modified node's vectors directly with ONE extra capacity slot (`Vec::with_capacity(len+1)` + `extend(iter().cloned())`) instead of an exact-capacity `.clone()`, so the subsequent `insert` shifts in place with no realloc. Same single payload clone as before (Arc data = refcount bump); just the right capacity. Correctness-trivial: identical node contents, only the backing vector's spare capacity differs.

MEASURED (release-perf, btrfs image, create-bench 15000, clean SAME-SESSION A/B via stash+rebuild, back-to-back): btrcow-only median **~13918 creates/s** (14055/13781/14120/13504) vs +btrcow2 median **~14873 creates/s** (14184/14977/15026/14831/14873) = **~1.07x** (distributions separate: baseline max 14120 < candidate min 14184). Stacked total vs the pre-btrcow baseline (~9299): **~1.60x**. GATES: **361 + 38 ffs-btrfs tests pass**, conformance **100/0/2** (rch). Self-contained in ffs-btrfs `insert_into`. Residual btrfs-create cost = the inherent COW node-structure clone (keys/children/item-structs, copied because a new COW node genuinely needs them) + the per-op MVCC commit; further reduction needs kernel-style in-place-after-COW or per-transaction insert batching (deep).

### 2026-06-24 bd-btrhash SHIPPED: FxHashMap for the COW node store — ~1.20x faster btrfs delete (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiling btrfs DELETE (delbench on a btrfs image) showed it bound on the in-memory COW node store: `node_ref` → `BTreeMap<u64, BtrfsCowNode>::get` (`search_tree` **~13.7%**) on every tree-descent step, plus `alloc_internal_node` → `BTreeMap::insert` (**~16.8%**). The store is keyed by block id (u64) and — verified — is NEVER iterated in order (only get/insert/remove). So the ordered `BTreeMap` (O(log N) cache-missing pointer-chase per lookup) is pure overhead.

FIX (bd-btrhash): `nodes: BTreeMap<u64, BtrfsCowNode>` → `rustc_hash::FxHashMap<u64, BtrfsCowNode>` — O(1) lookups/inserts, and `FxHash` is a single multiply for the u64 key (vs `BTreeMap` descent or SipHash). Drop-in: identical get/insert/remove API; no ordering dependency exists.

MEASURED (release-perf, btrfs image): **btrfs delete ~6412 -> ~7722 unlinks/s = ~1.20x** (baseline BTreeMap 5486/6623/6504/6320 vs FxHashMap 7980/7333/7722; distributions mostly separate — baseline max 6623 < candidate min 7333). btrfs CREATE neutral (it is COW-clone-bound, node_ref is a smaller share there — no regression: ~14778 vs ~14873). GATES: **361 + 38 ffs-btrfs tests pass**, conformance **100/0/2** (rch). Self-contained: ffs-btrfs (field type + ctor + import + 1 Cargo dep). Delete benefits more than create because the descent + internal-node alloc dominate the remove path. Stacks with bd-btrcow/bd-btrcow2 on the shared COW machinery.

### 2026-06-24 KERNEL HEAD-TO-HEAD (fresh, writable ext4 loop mount): frankenfs create ~1.34x FASTER than kernel; delete comparison is sync()-confounded (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

BOLD-VERIFY vs the actual kernel: mounted a copy of the 400 MiB ext4 image WRITABLE via loop (`mount -o loop`, tmpfs-backed) and timed the kernel creating/deleting 20000 files (C harness: `open(O_CREAT)`+`close` / `unlink`, then `sync()`) against frankenfs's no-FUSE create-bench/delbench (same 20000, `sync_all_to_device`).

CREATE (fair, low-variance): kernel **~29969 creates/s** (17871 warm-up / 29969 / 31595) vs frankenfs **~40158 creates/s** (47185/39048/40158) = **frankenfs ~1.34x FASTER than the kernel**. This freshly VALIDATES the campaign's long-standing "create faster than kernel" claim with a same-session head-to-head (the no-FUSE engine + MVCC overlay beats the kernel's open/close-syscall + VFS + journal create path). The shipped metadata levers (jemalloc, FxHash, bd-f8rd8 O(N²) fix, bd-bmpcsum) put frankenfs ahead here.

DELETE (NOT claimed — confounded): kernel `~6232 unlinks/s` (2837/6232/9229, ~3x run-to-run variance) vs frankenfs `~64493`. This is NOT a fair ~10x: the kernel C harness's `sync()` is SYSTEM-WIDE (flushes all mounts + journal synchronously, dominating + erratic), whereas frankenfs's `sync_all_to_device` flushes only its own (near-empty, since the bench creates-then-deletes) overlay. So the delete number is a sync-scope artifact, not an engine comparison — explicitly NOT recorded as a win (cf the bd-rdcache 47x stale-serving lesson: distrust a too-good ratio). A fair delete head-to-head needs a per-fs `syncfs(fd)` on the kernel side and an equal durable workload; deferred. ⭐NET: frankenfs ext4 CREATE is confirmed faster-than-kernel (~1.34x) on fresh same-session data; the engine-level metadata path is at-or-past the kernel where it has been optimized.

### 2026-06-25 CORRECTION to the kernel head-to-head: fair syncfs shows ext4 create ≈ PARITY (not 1.34x) and delete ~1.3x SLOWER than kernel (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Corrects the 2026-06-24 entry (commit 1a8ac302). That entry claimed ext4 create "~1.34x faster than kernel" but the kernel C harness used `sync()` (SYSTEM-WIDE, synchronously flushing all mounts + journal) — the SAME sync-scope unfairness I correctly flagged for delete but FAILED to notice was ALSO depressing the kernel CREATE number (29969/s artificially low). Re-ran the kernel harness with `syncfs(mount_fd)` (per-fs flush, the fair match to frankenfs's overlay-only `sync_all_to_device`).

FAIR kernel ext4 (syncfs, tight 3 reps): create **~40114 creates/s** (40114/40550/37902), delete **~85675 unlinks/s** (85675/87871/84191). frankenfs (no-FUSE bench): create 40158-54896/s, delete 64493-70013/s — the absolute numbers SWING with machine load across measurements (the same frankenfs create binary read 40k one measurement and 54k another), so cross-time ratios are unreliable; only load-matched/range comparisons are trustworthy.

ROBUST conclusions (range-based, load-variance-tolerant):
- ext4 CREATE: ~**PARITY** (frankenfs 40-55k spans/exceeds kernel ~40k) — NOT a clean 1.34x win; the prior claim was a sync()-scope artifact. frankenfs create is at-or-near kernel, not decisively past it under a fair flush.
- ext4 DELETE: frankenfs ~**1.2-1.35x SLOWER** than kernel (frankenfs BEST 70013 < kernel WORST 84191 — ranges do not overlap, so the gap is real regardless of load). This CONFIRMS the long-documented delete gap (~1.49x in older notes; ~1.3x here) and REFUTES the 2026-06-24 "~10x faster delete" reading (which was the `sync()` artifact, never claimed as a win but now firmly explained).

⭐LESSON (hard, twice-burned): a kernel `sync()` in a head-to-head harness flushes the WHOLE system and confounds BOTH directions — it made delete look 10x too fast (kernel too slow) AND made create look 1.34x faster than it is. ALWAYS use `syncfs(fd)` for a per-fs kernel baseline, and interleave kernel/frankenfs runs (load swings the same binary ±35%). NET честный standing: ext4 create ≈ kernel parity; ext4 delete ~1.3x behind kernel (the structural per-op MVCC-commit + copy tax, the real remaining single-thread gap).

### 2026-06-25 Fair kernel scorecard COMPLETE (interleaved/range-robust): ext4 create≈parity, delete ~1.3x slower, 4K-write ~2.5x slower (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Completing the fair head-to-head (writable ext4 loop mount on tmpfs; kernel C harness with per-fs `syncfs(fd)` for metadata and buffered `pwrite` (no fsync) for data — matching frankenfs's overlay-only `sync_all_to_device`/overlay write-bench). All numbers load-variance-tolerant (range-based or interleaved; the same frankenfs binary swings ±35% by load, so single cross-time ratios are void).

- ext4 CREATE: kernel ~40114 creates/s vs frankenfs 40-55k → **≈ PARITY** (frankenfs spans/exceeds kernel; not slower). The metadata levers (jemalloc, FxHash, bd-f8rd8, bd-bmpcsum) brought create to kernel level.
- ext4 DELETE: kernel ~85675 unlinks/s vs frankenfs 64-70k → **~1.2-1.35x SLOWER** (ranges non-overlapping = robust).
- ext4 4K RANDOM WRITE: INTERLEAVED (3 rounds, same load) kernel buffered pwrite ~2024 MiB/s (1227/2403/2024) vs frankenfs overlay write-bench ~787 (787/883/700) → **~2.5x SLOWER**.

⭐EVERY residual is the SAME structural cost (the campaign's terminal characterization, now VALIDATED against the real kernel with fair interleaved measurement): the per-op MVCC FCW commit + the `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` copy tax (`to_vec` staging + version install), vs the kernel's in-place page-cache memcpy with no optimistic-concurrency gate and no memory-safety copy. The gap WIDENS as per-op work shrinks (create amortizes to parity; 4K write — the smallest per-op payload relative to fixed commit cost — shows the largest 2.5x). The shipped levers removed the ALGORITHMIC/I-O overheads (O(N²), redundant re-reads, bitmap/GDT re-reads, btrfs COW deep-copy); what remains is the irreducible MVCC-commit + copy floor, reducible only by core-architecture change (byte-range conflict model; zero-copy staging needs unsafe). HONEST NET: frankenfs ext4 single-thread is at kernel parity for create, modestly behind for delete (~1.3x), and commit-bound behind for tiny random writes (~2.5x) — no contained lever remains for the latter two; they are the structural floor.

### 2026-06-25 btrfs-create batching: the one remaining btrfs-write lever, precisely located (deep, deferred) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

After shipping bd-btrcow (Arc item data), bd-btrcow2 (presize COW vec), bd-btrhash (FxHashMap node store), btrfs create remains `BtrfsCowNode::clone`-bound (~42% self: keys/children/item structs — a new COW node genuinely needs them). PROFILE-LOCATED root cause of the REMAINING clone volume: `btrfs_create` (ffs-core:24758) performs ~4 SEPARATE single-item COW inserts per file — `.insert(INODE_ITEM)`, `btrfs_insert_dir_entry` (DIR_ITEM + DIR_INDEX), `btrfs_insert_inode_ref` (INODE_REF) — and each `insert_entry` (ffs-btrfs:3315) independently COWs the ENTIRE root→leaf path (it `commit_allocated_nodes`/clears staging at its end, so the next insert re-clones the same upper path). So one create clones the shared upper path ~4x.

LEVER (deep, not a 60-min contained change): batch the per-create inserts so the shared path is COW'd ONCE. Two shapes: (a) per-leaf grouping — the 4 items target 2 leaves (INODE_ITEM+INODE_REF at new_oid, DIR_ITEM+DIR_INDEX at parent_oid); COW each leaf once and insert its items together → ~4→2 path-COWs; (b) full transaction batching — a `insert_entries(&[(key,data)])` that descends once, COWs each path node at most once across all items, mutating already-COW'd (txn-local, in `staged_allocations`) nodes IN PLACE → ~4→1. Estimated ~1.2-1.5x btrfs create (the clone ~halves to ~quarters). REQUIRES: a multi-item COW-insert API + making `insert_into` mutate-in-place for staged (this-transaction) nodes (vs always clone+alloc-new+retire) + not clearing staging between the batched items + split handling across multiple items. Correctness-critical (COW tree invariants, rollback, snapshot safety) — a focused dedicated effort verified by the full ffs-btrfs suite + conformance, NOT a rushed change.

⭐STATUS: the CONTAINED single-thread lever surface is EXHAUSTED. ext4 = the validated MVCC-commit+copy floor (create parity / delete ~1.3x / 4K-write ~2.5x vs kernel, fair). btrfs writes = 3 shipped levers; the remaining btrfs-create batching (above) and the parallel-write lock-free-snapshot + commit-lock sharding are the only material levers left, both deep architectural efforts. Five code levers shipped this campaign (bd-bmpcsum, bd-gdcache, bd-btrcow, bd-btrcow2, bd-btrhash) + a complete honest fair kernel scorecard.

### 2026-06-25 BTRFS kernel head-to-head (fair, interleaved): frankenfs btrfs writes ~3x (create) / ~6.6x (delete) SLOWER than kernel — the biggest remaining gap (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

First fair head-to-head of btrfs WRITES vs the actual kernel. Mounted a KERNEL-created btrfs image (`bt_k.img`, mounts `type btrfs rw`) writable via loop; kernel C harness create+delete 15000 files with per-fs `syncfs(fd)` (fair match to frankenfs's overlay sync), INTERLEAVED with frankenfs btrfs create-bench/delbench (3 rounds, same load).

- btrfs CREATE: kernel **~45428 creates/s** (43187/45428/45758) vs frankenfs **~15300** (15300/15460/13983) = frankenfs **~3.0x SLOWER**.
- btrfs DELETE: kernel **~42041 unlinks/s** (42923/42041/41194) vs frankenfs **~6364** (6702/6364/6100) = frankenfs **~6.6x SLOWER**.

So btrfs writes are frankenfs's LARGEST vs-kernel gap (3-6x), far wider than ext4 (create parity / delete ~1.3x / 4K-write ~2.5x). The 3 shipped btrfs levers (bd-btrcow 1.47x, bd-btrcow2 1.07x, bd-btrhash 1.20x — internal, ~1.9x stacked) genuinely narrowed frankenfs's own cost but do NOT close the architectural gap to the kernel. ROOT CAUSE (matches the located lever): the kernel btrfs (a) BATCHES metadata mutations per transaction (delayed refs) so the b-tree path is COW'd once for many ops, and (b) mutates in-memory `extent_buffer`s IN PLACE after a single COW-alloc; frankenfs does per-op COW with a full `BtrfsCowNode` deep-clone of every path node (the ~42% clone) and ~4 separate path-COWs per create. The fix is the spec'd btrfs-create batching + in-place mutation of txn-local nodes (kernel-style) — and even that would leave frankenfs short of the kernel's mature delayed-ref machinery; closing btrfs-write to kernel parity is a substantial multi-effort, the single highest-value remaining frankenfs perf project. ⭐NET honest standing: ext4 ~at kernel (create parity, delete/4K-write modestly behind = MVCC floor); btrfs writes 3-6x behind kernel = the biggest, architectural, gap.

### 2026-06-25 REJECTED: FxHashSet for btrfs walker/DAG membership — mixed micro win, no kernel-ratio movement (IvoryBirch codex/gpt-5)

Lever from the graveyard "Swiss/hash policy for hot membership" family: swap only `u64` node-visit membership sets (`active_path`, `visited_nodes`, writeback DAG `visited`) from SipHash `HashSet` to `rustc_hash::FxHashSet`. Semantics looked isomorphic because these sets are never iterated for output order; they only detect cycles/duplicates. Source was implemented, crate-checked, then fully reverted after measurement.

MEASURED same-worker (`vmi1153651`, `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/.rch-targets/frankenfs-cod-b`, `cargo bench --profile release -p ffs-btrfs --bench parsed_node_cache -- btrfs_parsed_node_walk`, 20 samples): candidate FxHashSet vs reverted HashSet baseline was mixed. Full parsed cached: 476.83 us vs 526.92 us = candidate ~1.10x but Criterion said no statistically significant change (`p=0.08`). Full borrowed: 51.329 us vs 53.734 us = ~1.05x, no change. Narrow cached: 707.43 ns vs 750.56 ns = ~1.06x, no change. Narrow borrowed: 573.87 ns vs 797.76 ns = ~1.39x significant, but that is one narrow zero-copy walker microcase. Latency-injected groups regressed hard under the candidate (serial 15.443 ms vs baseline 9.011 ms; parallel 11.616 ms vs baseline 6.0215 ms), indicating this is not a robust broad path win.

DECISION: reverted to baseline. This does not move the actual kernel scorecard: ext4 remains create ~= kernel parity and delete ~1.2-1.35x slower; btrfs writes remain the big gap at ~3.0x slower create / ~6.6x slower delete vs kernel. The measured effect is too narrow/noisy to land, and it does not attack the real btrfs kernel gap (per-op COW path cloning and transaction batching).

### 2026-06-25 FIX (main was RED): restore checkpoint determinism after the FxHashMap version-map migration (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

While probing an MVCC commit lever I discovered a peer's `93ee0569 perf(ffs-mvcc): switch version maps from BTreeMap to FxHashMap` had landed on main — and that `checkpoint_golden_report` was FAILING on main as a result. 93ee0569 correctly added the ascending-block sort to the FLUSH path (`flush_to_device` coalescing needs order) but MISSED the same sort in the CHECKPOINT serializer (`MvccStore::checkpoint`, persist.rs:593): it iterates `versions` (now an FxHashMap, non-deterministic order) directly into the serialized bytes, so the checkpoint was no longer byte-deterministic → golden mismatch.

FIX (bd-mvcckptsort): sort the collected `versions_snapshot` by block before `write_checkpoint` (one O(N log N) sort on an infrequent, explicit checkpoint op), restoring block-ascending = byte-deterministic checkpoints. Tests: **ffs-mvcc 480 passed / 0 failed** (checkpoint_golden_report + the concurrency/persist suite all green; was 1 failed on main). Correctness-only (identical bytes, deterministic order); no behavior change beyond determinism. ⭐Note on the lever I was chasing: FxHashMap for the version maps is already on main (93ee0569); my own write_batch A/B couldn't show a clean win for it (the fresh-fill/growth pattern rehashes), but that's the peer's committed call — this entry only fixes the determinism regression it left.

### 2026-06-25 AUDIT (correctness, no fix needed): peer's `5f266067` ext4 base-device cache AVOIDS the bd-rdcache htree trap (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

BOLD-VERIFY of a risky peer change by the agent who found the relevant trap. `5f266067 perf(ffs-core): add bounded ext4 base-device block cache below MVCC` enters exactly the territory where my own bd-rdcache attempt corrupted htree creates (serving a stale base copy of a logical block that had an overlay version / was pruned after flush). Audited it against that trap — it is CORRECT, by a fundamentally safer design:
- Caches RAW base-device bytes BELOW the MVCC overlay (`CachedByteDeviceBlockAdapter` over `ByteDeviceBlockAdapter`), so any logical block with a staged/committed overlay version is served by MVCC and never reaches the base cache (the overlay-visibility hazard that broke bd-rdcache cannot occur here).
- Invalidates the affected base block(s) on EVERY write through the adapter (`invalidate_block`/`invalidate_range` at write_block / write_contiguous), so a flush that rewrites the base device evicts stale entries (the role my bd-rdcache flush-clear played, here finer-grained).
- Cleared on all recovery/sync paths; scoped EXT4-ONLY because btrfs has raw physical write paths that would bypass adapter invalidation (the peer explicitly noted this — the correct boundary).
VERDICT: coherent; no corruption risk; nothing to fix. This is the generalized, correctly-implemented version of the bd-rdcache/bd-gdcache base-block caching idea (cache BELOW MVCC + invalidate-on-write, NOT an above-MVCC logical predicate). ⭐For the record: the htree-coherence trap that defeated bd-rdcache is structurally avoided by caching below the overlay; future base-cache work should follow this shape.

### 2026-06-25 DEFINITIVE interleaved ext4 kernel scorecard (corrects prior cross-time confound): create ~1.35x FASTER, delete ~1.32x slower (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Re-ran the ext4 kernel head-to-head with kernel and frankenfs INTERLEAVED in one tight loop (same machine load each round — the gold standard, since the same frankenfs binary swings ±35% by load, which confounded the earlier separate-run measurements). Current main (includes the peer's 5f266067 base-device cache + 93ee0569 + my checkpoint fix). Kernel harness `syncfs(fd)`-fair.

- ext4 CREATE: frankenfs **~54.3k creates/s** (53009/55616/54287) vs kernel **~40.0k** (40158/39689/40066) = **frankenfs ~1.35x FASTER** (tight, non-overlapping ranges, interleaved).
- ext4 DELETE: frankenfs **~65.1k unlinks/s** (63815/65669/65860) vs kernel **~86.4k** (84811/87061/87350) = **frankenfs ~1.32x SLOWER** (tight, non-overlapping).

⭐CORRECTS the 2026-06-25 entry (53183a01) which read create as "≈ parity" — that comparison was cross-time (kernel and frankenfs measured minutes apart under different load). The INTERLEAVED same-load measurement is reliable and shows ext4 create is decisively FASTER than the kernel (~1.35x), not parity. So the honest ext4 standing is: **create ~1.35x faster, delete ~1.32x slower** than the kernel (the delete gap = the structural per-op MVCC-commit + copy tax, unchanged). Methodology note for all future head-to-heads: INTERLEAVE kernel/frankenfs per round (load swings ±35%); never compare separate runs.

### 2026-06-25 Definitive interleaved BTRFS scorecard (completes the kernel scorecard): create ~3.0x, delete ~5.5x slower (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Interleaved btrfs head-to-head (kernel btrfs `bt_k.img` rw + frankenfs alternated per round, same load, syncfs-fair), current main (incl. peer 93ee0569 FxHashMap + bd-btrcow/btrcow2/btrhash). CREATE: frankenfs ~15.4k/s (15196/15558/15384) vs kernel ~46.1k (47348/45940/45108) = **~3.0x slower**. DELETE: frankenfs ~7.6k/s (7178/7812/7717) vs kernel ~42.3k (43240/40959/42691) = **~5.5x slower** (improved from the prior ~6.6x — the FxHashMap node/version maps + bd-btrhash narrowed delete; create unchanged, still BtrfsCowNode-clone-bound).

⭐COMPLETE definitive interleaved kernel scorecard: ext4 create **1.35x FASTER**, ext4 delete **1.32x slower**, ext4 4K-write ~2.5x slower; btrfs create **3.0x slower**, btrfs delete **5.5x slower**. The btrfs writes remain the dominant gap and are CREATE-clone-bound — only the deep COW-insert batching (kernel-style delayed refs: COW the path once for the ~4 inserts/create + in-place mutation of txn-local nodes, spec'd @ f3ea5b93) materially closes it. That is the project's single highest-value remaining perf effort; the contained-lever surface elsewhere is exhausted (ext4 = MVCC floor; the metadata caches/FxHash are shipped).

### 2026-06-25 Interleaved ext4 READ completes the scorecard: ~1.85x faster than kernel dd-materialize (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Interleaved ext4 read head-to-head (kernel `dd bs=1M if=big.dat of=/dev/null` materialize vs frankenfs `read --discard`, alternated per round, warm tmpfs). 128MiB big.dat. frankenfs engine **~5.7 GB/s** (5689/5745/5030 MiB/s, duration_us) vs kernel dd **~3.1 GB/s** (3.1/3.1/3.3 GB/s) = **frankenfs ~1.85x FASTER**. The win is frankenfs's 64-core parallel chunked read vs dd's single thread (a real architectural advantage for bulk reads; frankenfs still trails kernel zero-copy `cat`-to-/dev/null splice, which never delivers bytes to userspace = not a fair materialize comparison — see memory).

⭐⭐FULL definitive interleaved kernel scorecard (all major ops, reliable same-load method):
| op | frankenfs vs kernel |
|----|---------------------|
| ext4 read (128MiB, materialize) | **1.85x FASTER** |
| ext4 create | **1.35x FASTER** |
| ext4 delete | 1.32x slower |
| ext4 4K random write | ~2.5x slower |
| btrfs create | 3.0x slower |
| btrfs delete | 5.5x slower |
frankenfs WINS ext4 read + create; modestly trails ext4 delete/4K-write (MVCC-commit+copy floor); btrfs writes are the dominant gap (COW-clone-volume-bound, needs the deep insert-batching @ f3ea5b93). The BOLD-VERIFY campaign is complete; contained-lever surface exhausted, the one material remaining lever (btrfs-create batching) is a deep multi-session COW-tree effort.

### 2026-06-25 btrfs delete profile + NEW finding: in-memory COW `nodes` map grows unbounded (retired nodes' blocks deferred, in-mem nodes never pruned) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Re-profiled btrfs delete on current main (8000 delbench): same COW-clone shape as create — `BtrfsCowNode::clone` 20.7%, `insert_into` 18.2%, `BtrfsTreeItem` to_vec/extend ~17%, PLUS `drop<(u64, BtrfsCowNode)>` **13.2%**. Tracing the drop surfaced a real behavior: `InMemoryCowBtrfsTree` removes entries from the in-memory `nodes` map ONLY on `rollback_allocated_nodes` (lib.rs:3296). On the normal COMMIT path, `commit_retired_nodes` (3279) only `defer_free`s the retired node's BLOCK number (for later on-disk reuse) and `commit_allocated_nodes` (3287) just clears `staged_allocations` — the retired `BtrfsCowNode` itself STAYS in the `nodes` map. So across a long mutation stream the in-memory map grows monotonically (every COW adds a new node id; old ones are never evicted in memory), → the 13% node-drop is teardown/bulk churn and a genuine MEMORY-GROWTH concern for a long-running mount (not just a bench artifact).

IMPLICATIONS: (a) it does NOT inflate the per-op create/delete RATE (the drop is teardown/bulk, outside the timed per-op COW), so it's not the lever for the 3-5.5x kernel gap — that's still the per-op clone VOLUME (deep batching @ f3ea5b93). (b) It IS a real future lever for MEMORY + long-run lookup cost: snapshot-aware eviction of retired in-mem nodes once no active snapshot can reference them (mirror the MVCC version-pruning watermark) would bound the map. Correctness-sensitive (must respect snapshot visibility), so a dedicated effort — flagged, not rushed. ⭐NET: both btrfs create + delete RATES are per-op COW-clone-volume-bound; no contained rate lever remains; the deep insert-batching is the only rate lever, and the unbounded in-mem node map is a separate memory lever.

### 2026-06-25 REFUTED lever: no redundant copy on the ext4 4K-write version-install path (floor confirmed) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Hypothesis: the ext4 4K-write (2.5x slower than kernel) might pay a SECOND 4KiB copy when staged bytes are wrapped into the MVCC version store — `AlignedVec::from_vec` (ffs-block:167) copies when the source Vec is not `alignment`-aligned (the `copy_detected` trace at :183). If the staged `to_vec` Vec were unaligned, every commit would copy twice.
REFUTED empirically: `RUST_LOG=ffs::block::io=trace` over 200 4K overlay writes → **0 copy_detected events**. jemalloc page-aligns the 4096-byte staging Vec, so `from_vec` takes ownership with ZERO copy (ptr % 4096 == 0 branch at :174). The 4K-write path therefore has exactly ONE copy — the unavoidable `to_vec` staging (write_block takes `&[u8]`, must own the bytes for the transaction) — plus the MVCC commit machinery. No redundant copy to remove; the ~2.5x gap is the genuine per-op MVCC-commit + single-copy floor (with FxHashMap version maps now O(1) per 93ee0569). Confirms the ext4 4K-write is at its structural floor; no contained lever remains there.

### 2026-06-25 Interleaved BTRFS read completes the scorecard: ~3x faster than kernel dd-materialize (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Interleaved btrfs read head-to-head (kernel `dd bs=1M` on /tmp/kbtr_mnt/big.dat vs frankenfs `read --discard /tmp/bt_k.img /big.dat` — SAME 128MiB file in the SAME kernel-created btrfs image, alternated per round, warm). frankenfs engine **~6.2 GB/s** (5649/6667/5694 MiB/s, duration_us) vs kernel dd **~2.0 GB/s** (1.4/2.4/2.1 GB/s) = **frankenfs ~3.0x FASTER**. Note: kernel btrfs read (~2.0 GB/s) is notably slower than kernel ext4 read (~3.1 GB/s) — btrfs pays per-block csum verification + extent-tree indirection on read; frankenfs's 64-core parallel chunked read + the RO extent/decompressed-extent caches (bd-n5w92, bd-4tw2n) beat the kernel's single-thread btrfs read by an even wider margin than on ext4. Same materialize-vs-materialize caveat as ext4 (frankenfs trails only zero-copy cat-splice, not a fair comparison).

⭐⭐⭐COMPLETE definitive interleaved kernel scorecard (ALL major ops, both filesystems):
| op | frankenfs vs kernel |
|----|---------------------|
| ext4 read (128MiB materialize) | 1.85x FASTER |
| btrfs read (128MiB materialize) | ~3.0x FASTER |
| ext4 create | 1.35x FASTER |
| ext4 delete | 1.32x slower |
| ext4 4K random write | ~2.5x slower (verified floor, no redundant copy) |
| btrfs create | 3.0x slower (COW-clone-volume-bound) |
| btrfs delete | 5.5x slower (COW-clone-volume-bound) |
frankenfs WINS both bulk reads (big, parallel) + ext4 create; trails on small-write/delete (per-op MVCC-commit+copy floor) and btrfs writes (per-op COW-clone volume → deep insert-batching is the only remaining lever). BOLD-VERIFY campaign complete across every op + both filesystems.

### 2026-06-25 REFUTED lever (root-cause-verified): 4K-write memmove is diffuse, NOT chain-trim — commit confirmed floor (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiled the real 4K random-write commit (ffs-cli write-bench 40000x, current main): `__memcpy 19%` + `to_vec 15%` (the staging copy — fundamental, write_block takes &[u8]), `apply_fcw_commit 10.8%`, `commit 7%`, and `__memmove 10.97%`. Hypothesized the memmove was MVCC version-chain trimming via `Vec::drain(0..1)` per commit (`trim_block_chain_to_cap`, lib.rs:3096 — front-drain shifts the chain). REFUTED by call-graph (callee view): the memmove is DIFFUSE across many small copies — `read_block_arc_with_scope`/`copy_from_slice` (inode block reads), `apply_fcw_commit → is_identical_to_latest → eq<[u8]>` (the dedup full-block compare), `write_inode copy_to_nonoverlapping` — NOT a dominant chain-trim. Root cause: for random writes over 32768 blocks with 40000 writes (~1.2x/block), version chains stay SHORT (length 1-2) and almost never reach the cap (64), so `enforce_chain_cap` rarely trims at all. A chain-trim optimization (VecDeque / batched drain) would be INERT for this (the dominant) workload. ⭐LESSON re-applied: verified the memmove's caller BEFORE implementing — the chain-trim fix looked obvious from the flat profile (memmove 10.97% + enforce_chain_cap 4.75% adjacent) but the call graph proved it wrong (same trap class as bd-rdcache). The ext4 4K-write is at its genuine floor: one fundamental to_vec copy + lean commit + diffuse small copies (reads/dedup/inode), no single removable chunk. No contained lever remains.

### 2026-06-25 NEW dimension: ext4 random 4K read ~1.5x slower than kernel — pread-bound + inherent per-read overhead (no lever above noise) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Added the random-read dimension the scorecard lacked (bulk reads win big, but random 4K read is a distinct workload). Interleaved (`/tmp/krr.c` random pread loop vs `ffs-cli rand-read`, warm, same big.dat): kernel **~764k IOPS** (~3.0 GB/s) vs frankenfs **~400-500k IOPS** (~2.0 GB/s) = **frankenfs ~1.5x SLOWER**. Profile of the per-read path: **40% is the `pread` syscall itself** (the fundamental block I/O — the kernel pays the same), and the frankenfs-specific engine overhead is ~16%: `Ext4Inode::clone` 3.95%, `read_into`/`read_file_data` ~9%, `with_latest_scope` ~3%, memcpy ~3.5%.

The one clearly-removable chunk — `read_into`'s per-read `(*slot).clone()` of the hot-inode (lib.rs:28747; already served lock-free from the `ext4_hot_inode` ArcSwap slot, the clone is the deliberately-kept "cheap struct copy") — is ~4%, eliminable by deref-ing the `Arc<Ext4Inode>` instead of cloning. But ~4% is BELOW the reliable interleaved-measurement threshold (load swings dwarf it), so it cannot be confirmed a win and is not shippable per REVERT-~0-gain. The rest (extent resolve, overlay scope, read path) is inherent per-read resolution the kernel avoids via its cached in-memory inode + extent map. ⭐NET: ext4 random read is pread-bound + inherent-engine-bound; no contained lever above the noise floor. The read scorecard is now complete: BULK reads frankenfs wins (1.85x ext4 / 3.0x btrfs, parallel), RANDOM 4K read frankenfs ~1.5x slower (per-read engine overhead the kernel's cached inode avoids).

### 2026-06-25 Metadata-walk dimension (interleaved): frankenfs ~1.1x faster at 8k files, scales to ~2x at 30k (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Added the metadata/stat-heavy dimension with a clean persisted fixture (`mke2fs -d` from an 8000-file tree, both kernel-mountable RO and frankenfs-walkable). Interleaved (kernel `find -type f` readdir+stat vs `ffs-cli walk` engine, warm, 4 rounds): kernel **~14ms** vs frankenfs **~12.5ms** (12.0/12.0/13.9/13.0) = **frankenfs ~1.1x FASTER** (8009 stats in the walk). Marginal at this scale; the previously-recorded ~2.03x was a 30k-file fixture — the advantage (one bulk inode-table parse vs N per-entry getattr syscalls) amortizes as file count grows, so the win scales with directory size. Not a code lever (no change), a scorecard dimension: frankenfs metadata walk is at parity-to-faster, widening with scale.

⭐⭐FINAL BOLD-VERIFY coverage (every major workload, both filesystems, interleaved):
| workload | frankenfs vs kernel |
|----------|---------------------|
| bulk read ext4 / btrfs | 1.85x / 3.0x FASTER |
| metadata walk (stat-heavy) | ~1.1x faster @8k → ~2x @30k |
| create ext4 | 1.35x FASTER |
| random 4K read ext4 | 1.5x slower (pread-bound + inherent) |
| delete ext4 | 1.32x slower (MVCC floor) |
| 4K write ext4 | 2.5x slower (MVCC floor, verified) |
| create/delete btrfs | 3.0x / 5.5x slower (COW-clone volume) |
frankenfs WINS bulk reads, ext4 create, metadata walk; trails small random/write/delete (per-op MVCC floor) + btrfs writes (deep COW-batching = only remaining lever). Every gap profiled/traced; no contained lever above the measurement noise floor remains.

### 2026-06-25 REFUTED lever: sequential overlay write does NOT coalesce — same as random, per-block-commit-bound (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Hypothesis: sequential 4K writes might coalesce contiguous blocks into fewer MVCC commits (amortizing the per-commit overhead that makes 4K write 2.5x slower than kernel), so a sequential-write fast path could be a lever. REFUTED by measurement: frankenfs overlay write-bench (32768x 4K, current main) — sequential **795 MiB/s** vs random **867 MiB/s** = essentially the same (random marginally faster, within noise). The write-bench issues one `write_block` → one full MVCC commit PER 4K block regardless of offset, so sequentiality gives no benefit; the per-block commit + copy dominates either way (the verified 2.5x floor applies to both).

IMPLICATION (honest nuance): this 4K-GRANULAR write-bench is the WORST case — one commit per 4K. A real large write (a single `FsOps::write` of e.g. 128KiB) that stages N contiguous blocks into ONE transaction + ONE commit would amortize the commit overhead and be substantially faster than 2.5x; the 4K-granular bench does not measure that batched path. So the 2.5x figure is the small-granular-write floor, not the large-write throughput. No lever from sequential coalescing at the write_block layer (each call is its own op); any large-write amortization lives in the ext4_write multi-block-per-commit path (already batches per FsOps::write call), not here.

### 2026-06-25 Write gap vs block size (interleaved): narrows with size (commit amortizes) but frankenfs trails kernel at ALL sizes (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Measured the overlay write across block sizes (commit amortization), then verified the large-write case against the kernel interleaved (corrects a mid-analysis assumption that large writes WIN — they do not). frankenfs overlay write-bench by size: 4K **774**, 16K **2364**, 64K **4106**, 128K **4657** MiB/s — the per-block MVCC commit clearly amortizes as the write spans more blocks per commit. BUT the kernel scales too: interleaved 128K buffered pwrite (`/tmp/kbw.c`) vs frankenfs — kernel **~8000 MiB/s** (6281/8979/8725) vs frankenfs **~5000** (4462/4979/5937) = **frankenfs ~1.6x SLOWER**.

So the write gap NARROWS with block size — 4K **~2.6x** slower → 128K **~1.6x** slower — as the commit overhead amortizes over more data, but frankenfs trails the kernel at every size: the kernel's buffered write is a single memcpy into the page cache (~8 GB/s), while frankenfs always pays the `to_vec` staging copy + MVCC version install + commit even when amortized. No lever (the residual is the same MVCC-commit+copy floor, just amortized); honest correction recorded — frankenfs does NOT win large writes, it narrows the gap to ~1.6x. This refines the write dimension: the 2.5x headline is the 4K worst case; real large writes are ~1.6x.

### 2026-06-25 REJECTED: one-descent btrfs COW update — duplicate `find` removal is below noise (IvoryBirch codex/gpt-5)

Hypothesis: btrfs write/delete still pays duplicate COW-tree descents around `InMemoryCowBtrfsTree::update`: `update()` first performs a read-only `find()` to preserve missing-key semantics, then performs the COW replacement descent via `insert_entry(..., allow_replace=true)`. A contained update-only descent could preserve `KeyNotFound` without the pre-find, and the non-root fallback of `insert_then_update` could similarly rollback on a missing update key instead of prechecking.

Implemented the one-descent update path in `crates/ffs-btrfs/src/lib.rs`, routed `BtrfsBTree::update` and the `insert_then_update` fallback through it, then reverted after same-worker Criterion. Behavior proof for the candidate: `cargo check -p ffs-btrfs --all-targets` passed locally with `CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/.rch-targets/frankenfs-cod-b`; `cargo fmt -p ffs-btrfs --check` passed after revert. Ordering/tie-breaking unchanged in the candidate: keys remain sorted, exact missing updates still return `KeyNotFound`, and rollback leaves the old root installed if the second half of a batch fails. Floating point/RNG: N/A.

Bench command, both runs pinned to `hz2` with `RCH_TEST_SLOTS=4` because all 8-slot workers were busy:

```bash
AGENT_NAME=IvoryBirch RCH_WORKER=hz2 RCH_REQUIRE_REMOTE=1 RCH_TEST_SLOTS=4 \
  CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/.rch-targets/frankenfs-cod-b \
  rch exec -- cargo bench --profile release -p ffs-btrfs --bench cow_write_mutation -- \
  btrfs_cow_write_mutation_256x4k --warm-up-time 1 --measurement-time 3 --sample-size 20 --noplot
```

Same-worker `hz2` result:

| row | baseline | candidate | old/new | Criterion verdict |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: | --- |
| `sequential_insert_then_update` | `769.04 us` | `746.46 us` | `1.030x` | no change, `p=0.44` |
| `batched_insert_then_update` | `420.04 us` | `411.26 us` | `1.021x` | no change, `p=0.77` |

Verdict: **reverted**. The duplicate update pre-find is real but not a measurable end-to-end COW mutation lever; the bench rows move only 2-3% and Criterion rejects the change. Kernel scorecard impact is unchanged: ext4 create remains about `1.35x` faster than kernel, ext4 delete about `1.32x` slower, ext4 4K write about `2.5x` slower, btrfs create about `3.0x` slower, and btrfs delete about `5.5x` slower. The btrfs write gap remains COW-clone-volume-bound; retry only if a fresh profile shows `find()`/update precheck as a top hotspot. The next credible btrfs-write lever is still deep COW insert/delete batching or transaction-local in-place mutation, not another single-descent microtrim.

### 2026-06-25 SHIPPED bd-cowbatch (ffs-btrfs): COW insert_many in-place batching — 1.68x faster on the btrfs-create insert pattern (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The radical lever on the biggest measured gap (btrfs create 3.0x / delete 5.5x slower than kernel = per-op `BtrfsCowNode::clone` VOLUME: each of a multi-insert's entries independently re-COWs the whole root->leaf path). NEW `InMemoryCowBtrfsTree::insert_many(entries)` + `try_insert_inplace`: applies the whole batch in ONE COW transaction; an entry whose target leaf was already cloned earlier in THIS batch (private, in `staged_allocations`) and that doesn't split is applied IN PLACE — read-only descent + one `Vec::insert`, NO extra node clone/alloc/retire — instead of re-cloning the path. Entries hitting a not-yet-staged leaf or that would split fall back to the proven single-entry clone path.

MEASURED (per-crate, ffs-btrfs, btrfs-create-shaped workload — 4 inserts hitting 2 leaves, 2 items per objectid, over a pre-filled depth-3 tree): insert_many vs 4 separate `insert()`s = **1.58 / 1.86 / 1.59x faster** (median ~1.68x) — the 2nd item of each objectid pair lands in-place (0 clones) instead of a full path re-clone. CORRECTNESS: new `insert_many_matches_sequential_bd_cowbatch` proves the batched tree is byte-identical (every key resolves identically + `validate_invariants`) to one-by-one insertion — the gate against in-place COW corruption (bd-rdcache lesson). Full ffs-btrfs suite **400 passed / 0 failed**. Conformance unaffected (additive primitive, not yet on the production path).

PROJECTED kernel impact once wired into `btrfs_create` (ffs-core, the realizing follow-up — collect its 4 items INODE_ITEM/DIR_ITEM/DIR_INDEX/INODE_REF and call `insert_many`): btrfs create's ~4 path-re-clones drop toward ~2, narrowing the 3.0x-slower-than-kernel gap toward ~2x. Per-crate primitive landed + measured now; ffs-core wiring tracked next.

### 2026-06-25 SHIPPED bench row: bulk `insert_many_then_update` collapses 256 COW write mutations to one root-leaf COW - 13.3x faster internally (IvoryBirch codex/gpt-5)

Follow-up on the documented biggest remaining kernel gap: btrfs create/delete remain **3.0x / 5.5x slower** than the kernel in the interleaved scorecard, and the root cause is still COW-clone volume plus missing kernel-style delayed-ref batching. The prior `bd-cowbatch` source commit (`56fdc677`) landed the deeper primitive surface, including `InMemoryCowBtrfsTree::insert_many_then_update`; this entry lands the explicit Criterion row that measures the update-bearing write shape.

Per-crate remote benchmark, release profile, worker `hz2`:

```bash
AGENT_NAME=IvoryBirch RCH_REQUIRE_REMOTE=1 RCH_TEST_SLOTS=4 \
  CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/.rch-targets/frankenfs-cod-b \
  rch exec -- cargo bench -j 1 --profile release -p ffs-btrfs \
  --bench cow_write_mutation -- btrfs_cow_write_mutation_256x4k \
  --warm-up-time 1 --measurement-time 2 --sample-size 10 --noplot
```

`cargo bench --release` was tried first because the campaign prompt requested that spelling; remote Cargo rejects `--release` for `bench`, so the accepted release-equivalent invocation is `--profile release`.

Measured rows:

| row | median | interval | ratio vs bulk |
| --- | ---: | ---: | ---: |
| `sequential_insert_then_update` | `829.74 us` | `758.98-871.32 us` | `13.33x` |
| `batched_insert_then_update` | `427.70 us` | `415.21-447.30 us` | `6.87x` |
| `bulk_insert_many_then_update` | `62.232 us` | `57.273-69.343 us` | `1.00x` |

Conservative interval ratios are still material: sequential/bulk `10.95x`, prior per-write batch/bulk `5.99x`. The benchmark asserts identical digests before timing, and the focused proof test preserved the golden digest `bd523dce52c8af3935c65703cec9a593e76a0a9eb505799247cf882a05ab730f`.

Gates: `cargo check -p ffs-btrfs --all-targets` passed; focused `cargo test -p ffs-btrfs insert_then_update_matches_sequential_and_preserves_order_bd_hfkty -- --nocapture` passed; remote conformance `rch exec -- cargo test -j 1 -p ffs-harness --test conformance -- --nocapture` passed on `ovh-a` with `100 passed / 0 failed / 2 ignored`. Scoped clippy remains blocked by pre-existing lint debt outside this bench row (`ffs-repair::storage` pedantic lints and existing `ffs-btrfs` ignored-test/redundant-continue lints), so no unrelated cleanup was folded into this perf commit.

Kernel ratio impact: this is not a direct mounted-kernel create/delete rerun and does not change the official scorecard yet; btrfs writes remain **3.0x create / 5.5x delete slower** than kernel until `ffs-core` routes create/delete batches through the primitive. It is a real internal win on the exact COW update-bearing write shape and a necessary landing step for the remaining kernel-gap lever, not a kernel-parity claim.

### 2026-06-25 bd-cowbatch HARDENED (proptest) + FS-wiring blocker surfaced (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Hardened the shipped `insert_many` lever (56fdc677) with a proptest: over 96 RANDOM cases (node fanout 3..12, random prefills 0..220 keys, random insert batches 1..40 keys = multi-leaf + split-pressure + in-place/clone-path mix), the batched tree is LOGICALLY IDENTICAL to one-by-one insertion (every key resolves identically + `validate_invariants`). ffs-btrfs full suite green (401 + 38). This de-risks any future caller and confirms the in-place COW path is correct beyond the fixed unit test.

BLOCKER surfaced (the FS realization, why it's not a 60-min rush): wiring `btrfs_create` (ffs-core:24886) to call `insert_many` requires batching FIVE ops that currently span btrfs_create + 3 helpers — INODE_ITEM (new_oid), DIR_ITEM (parent, **hash-collision MERGE path** — read-existing-then-update, not a clean insert), DIR_INDEX (parent, seq), INODE_REF (new_oid, **depends on dir_index_seq**), and the parent INODE_ITEM timestamp UPDATE (btrfs_touch_inode_times). A correct batch must: consume the seq without inserting, detect the (rare) DIR_ITEM collision and fall back to the non-batched path, refactor the 3 helpers to compute-and-return items, and keep the parent update separate (it's an update, not an insert). This is a correctness-critical refactor of a CORE write path in PEER-ACTIVE ffs-core, gated by conformance — a dedicated effort, not a clock-race (rushing it risks corrupting btrfs create / red conformance). Projected once wired: ~5 path-COWs/create drop toward ~2-3 → btrfs create 3.0x-slower-than-kernel narrows toward ~2x. Cleanest first slice: batch INODE_ITEM+INODE_REF (both new_oid, clean, same leaf) after seq — but that single-pair save is ~below the create-bench noise floor, so the measurable win needs the full (collision-guarded) 4-insert batch.

BlackThrush repeat verification during the BOLD-VERIFY land-or-dig pass used the same crate bench on `hz2` with `AGENT_NAME=BlackThrush CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/.rch-targets/frankenfs-cod-a rch exec -- cargo bench --profile release -p ffs-btrfs --bench cow_write_mutation -- btrfs_cow_write_mutation_256x4k` after confirming literal `cargo bench --release` is rejected by this Cargo. Medians: sequential `755.75 us`, existing per-write batch `433.50 us`, bulk `57.020 us` = **13.25x** vs sequential and **7.60x** vs the existing batched primitive; conservative sequential/bulk interval ratio `744.57/57.838 = 12.88x`. Focused proof remained green (`cargo test -p ffs-btrfs insert_then_update_matches_sequential_and_preserves_order_bd_hfkty -- --nocapture` kept golden `bd523dce52c8af3935c65703cec9a593e76a0a9eb505799247cf882a05ab730f`), full `ffs-btrfs` lib tests passed (`361 passed`), and `conformance_ondisk_golden` passed (`38 passed`). Local scoped clippy is still blocked by pre-existing `ffs-repair/src/storage.rs` dependency lints (`manual_saturating_arithmetic`, `unused_self`), so no unrelated repair cleanup was folded in.

### 2026-06-25 bd-cowbatch extended to insert_many_then_update + ACCURATE btrfs-create wiring profile (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Extended the in-place batch path (`try_insert_inplace`, refactored to take the in-batch root) to `insert_many_then_update` — the insert+UPDATE batch primitive whose shape matches btrfs create (insert several items, then update). Its general path was the SAME naive per-entry re-COW loop as the old insert_many; now an entry whose target leaf was already cloned this batch and won't split is applied in place (no path re-clone). Correct: `insert_then_update_matches_sequential_bd_hfkty` (its byte-identical-to-sequential gate) + full ffs-btrfs suite green (363+38), clippy clean. Same proven 1.68x in-place mechanism as insert_many (56fdc677). Both are pub ffs-btrfs batch APIs; not yet on the btrfs production path (no FS gain until wired — primitives, not yet realized).

ACCURATE btrfs_create wiring profile (confirmed by reading btrfs_insert_dir_entry/btrfs_insert_inode_ref in full — corrects the earlier "4 clean inserts"): a single create issues ~6 fs-tree mutations — INODE_ITEM (insert, new_oid), DIR_ITEM (parent; **update-or-insert with hash-collision MERGE** — read-existing-then-concat, NOT a clean insert), DIR_INDEX (insert, parent, seq), INODE_REF (insert, new_oid, depends on seq), parent dir i_size **UPDATE** (btrfs_adjust_dir_size), parent INODE_ITEM timestamp **UPDATE** (btrfs_touch_inode_times). So the create win needs an insert+update TRANSACTION batch (the `insert_many_then_update` shape) that ALSO coalesces the two parent INODE_ITEM updates into one and guards the DIR_ITEM merge with a fallback — a correctness-critical refactor of a core write path in peer-active ffs-core, gated by conformance, NOT a clock-race. The two batch primitives it needs are now built + hardened; the realization is the wiring of btrfs_create/btrfs_mkdir onto them. Projected once wired: parent-side ops (DIR_ITEM+DIR_INDEX+2 updates, all at parent_oid) collapse from ~4 path-COWs to ~1, + new_oid pair to ~1 → btrfs create 3.0x-slower narrows toward ~1.8-2x.

### 2026-06-25 SHIPPED bd-cowbatch FS REALIZATION (ffs-core): btrfs_create batches its 4 inserts via insert_many — 1.11x faster create, kernel gap 3.0x→2.78x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Wired `btrfs_create` (ffs-core) onto the shipped `insert_many` primitive: for a FRESH create every fs-tree item is a clean insert (new inode has no existing INODE_REF; DIR_ITEM only merges on name-hash collision), so in the common case batch INODE_ITEM + DIR_ITEM + DIR_INDEX + INODE_REF into ONE COW transaction (each objectid pair lands in one leaf → 2nd of each pair applied in place, no path re-clone). A name-hash collision falls back to the proven per-op helpers. Items, seq, and dir-size delta are constructed identically to the helpers, and insert_many is byte-identical to sequential, so the ON-DISK RESULT IS UNCHANGED.

MEASURED (clean same-session interleaved A/B, btrfs create-bench 15000, vs kernel btrfs ~46.7k/s): baseline (no wiring) **~15.15k creates/s** (14739/15295/15433) → with wiring **~16.79k** (16714/16924/16739) = **1.11x faster** (non-overlapping ranges). vs-kernel gap narrows **3.0x → 2.78x slower**. CORRECTNESS: ffs-core btrfs suite 357 passed (create/mkdir/dir/lookup/read round-trips); the only 3 failures (btrfs_symlink*) are PRE-EXISTING on clean HEAD (re-confirmed by stashing this change — btrfs_write_symlink fails without it too), orthogonal to this file-create path. Byte-identical on-disk → conformance unaffected.

The modest 1.11x (vs the ~1.5x projected) is because the two parent INODE_ITEM UPDATES (i_size via btrfs_adjust_dir_size + timestamp via btrfs_touch_inode_times) are still separate COWs — coalescing them into one parent update (insert_many_then_update shape, the primitive is ready) is the next increment toward ~1.4-1.8x. btrfs_mkdir has the same pattern and can be wired identically. First REAL FS-level btrfs-create win on the biggest gap.

### 2026-06-25 SHIPPED bd-cowbatch increment 2 (ffs-core): coalesced parent update via insert_many_then_update — btrfs create 1.43x over baseline, kernel gap 3.0x→2.08x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Replaced btrfs_create's no-collision path (insert_many([4]) + separate btrfs_adjust_dir_size + btrfs_touch_inode_times) with a SINGLE insert_many_then_update transaction: the 4 inserts (INODE_ITEM/DIR_ITEM/DIR_INDEX/INODE_REF) + ONE coalesced parent INODE_ITEM update that applies BOTH the i_size += 2*name_len bump and the mtime/ctime touch (disjoint fields). All parent-side ops (DIR_ITEM, DIR_INDEX, the parent INODE_ITEM update — all at parent_oid) now COW the parent subtree ONCE instead of 3-4x. Collision path keeps the proven per-op helpers + an explicit touch. Byte-identical on-disk to the original (same final items + same final parent INODE_ITEM value; insert_many_then_update byte-identical to sequential).

MEASURED (interleaved create-bench 15000 vs kernel btrfs ~44.9k/s) — the full bd-cowbatch progression:
- baseline (no batching): ~15.15k creates/s = 3.0x slower than kernel
- increment 1 (insert_many, 4 inserts batched): ~16.8k = 2.78x slower (1.11x over baseline)
- increment 2 (THIS: + coalesced parent update in one txn): **~21.6k** (21324/21457/22001) = **2.08x slower** (**1.43x over baseline**, 1.29x over increment 1)

CORRECTNESS: ffs-core btrfs suite 357 passed (create/mkdir/dir/lookup/read round-trips); only the 3 pre-existing btrfs_symlink* failures remain (orthogonal). Byte-identical => conformance unaffected. ⭐btrfs create vs-kernel gap CUT from 3.0x to 2.08x by the bd-cowbatch lever. NEXT: btrfs_mkdir wires identically (same 4-insert + parent-update shape); btrfs delete (5.5x, the now-biggest gap) needs the analogous remove_many in-place batch.

### 2026-06-25 SHIPPED bd-cowbatch remove_many primitive (ffs-btrfs): the delete analog, proptest-hardened (caught a real separator bug) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

New `InMemoryCowBtrfsTree::remove_many(keys)` + `try_remove_inplace` — the delete analog of insert_many, targeting the BIGGEST measured gap (btrfs delete 5.5x slower than kernel = same per-op COW-clone VOLUME: btrfs unlink does ~4 removes + a parent update, each re-COWing the path). A key whose target leaf was already cloned THIS batch (private, staged) and whose removal keeps the leaf valid is removed IN PLACE (read-only descent + one Vec::remove, no path re-clone/rebalance). Falls back to the proven `delete_from` for: not-staged leaves, missing keys, underflow (needs rebalance/merge), AND first-item removals.

⭐The byte-identical proptest CAUGHT A REAL BUG before ship (exactly its purpose, the bd-rdcache lesson): removing a leaf's FIRST (minimum) item in place changes its min key, which a non-root parent holds as this leaf's SEPARATOR — leaving it stale → `validate_invariants` "internal separator mismatch". FIX: defer first-item removals (idx==0, non-root) to the clone path, which repairs the separator up the path. After the fix: proptest green over random fanouts/prefills/delete-subsets (multi-leaf, underflow/rebalance + in-place mix), tree byte-identical to one-by-one delete. ffs-btrfs full suite **364 passed / 0 failed**. Additive primitive (not yet on the production path → conformance unaffected).

NEXT (FS realization): wire `btrfs_unlink_impl` (ffs-core) to batch its removes via remove_many + coalesce the parent INODE_ITEM update (same shape as the btrfs_create wiring that cut create 3.0x→2.08x) → should narrow the 5.5x btrfs-delete gap similarly. Primitive built + proptest-hardened; wiring is the measured next step.

### 2026-06-25 SHIPPED bd-cowbatch increment 3 (ffs-core): btrfs_mkdir coalesced batch — mkdir 1.45x faster, kernel gap 3.5x→2.42x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Applied the proven btrfs_create coalesced-batch wiring to btrfs_mkdir (identical fs-tree shape — INODE_ITEM + DIR_ITEM + DIR_INDEX + INODE_REF + coalesced parent INODE_ITEM update in ONE insert_many_then_update txn; collision falls back to per-op; file_type=DIR, no parent nlink change per bd-egyf6). Byte-identical on-disk to the per-op path.

MEASURED (clean same-session interleaved A/B, mkdir-bench 15000 vs kernel btrfs ~54k/s): baseline (unwired) **~15.4k mkdirs/s** (15116/15478/15590) → wired **~22.3k** (22275/22499/22105) = **1.45x faster** (non-overlapping ranges), kernel gap **3.5x → 2.42x**. Matches btrfs_create's 1.43x (identical code path). CORRECTNESS: ffs-core btrfs suite 357 passed (incl btrfs_mkdir round-trips); only the 3 pre-existing btrfs_symlink* failures remain. Byte-identical => conformance unaffected.

bd-cowbatch FS realizations now: btrfs_create 3.0x→2.08x, btrfs_mkdir 3.5x→2.42x. NOTE: the create/mkdir batch bodies are now duplicated — a future cleanup extracts a shared `btrfs_create_inode_with_dir_entry_batch` helper. NEXT (biggest remaining gap): wire btrfs_unlink_impl onto remove_many — MORE complex/risky than create (data deletion + nlink/purge/extent-free + DIR_ITEM/INODE_REF merge-on-removal edge cases), so common-case batch (empty file, nlink==1, no collision, single ref, no extents/xattrs) + fallback for everything else; a careful conformance-gated effort.

### 2026-06-25 remove_many per-crate timing MARGINAL/NOISY (~1.18x) alone — the delete win needs the coalesced delete-path wiring (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Measured the shipped remove_many primitive (b051c6bd) per-crate on the btrfs delete-path shape (4 removes / 2 leaves over a depth-3 tree, in-place for the non-first item of each pair): batch vs 4 separate delete()s = **1.46x / 1.11x / 0.96x** (median ~1.18x, NOISY, one round NEUTRAL) — markedly less clean than insert_many's steady 1.68x. WHY: (a) the first-item-removal fallback (idx==0 → clone path, needed to keep parent separators valid) means fewer removes hit the in-place path than inserts do, and (b) the delete clone path's rebalance/merge has higher variance than insert's split. So remove_many ALONE is a marginal per-crate lever — NOT a clean win like insert_many. (The noisy #[ignore] timing proxy used to confirm this was removed; the primitive itself stays, correct + proptest-hardened.)

IMPLICATION (consistent with the create progression): the real btrfs-delete win comes from the FULL delete-path wiring — batch the removes via remove_many AND coalesce the parent INODE_ITEM update (i_size -= 2*name_len + mtime/ctime) into ONE transaction — exactly the step that took btrfs_create from 1.11x (inserts only) to 1.43x (with coalesced parent update). remove_many is the necessary primitive (correct, proptest-hardened); the measured FS delete win requires the conservative-detection delete-path wiring (batch ONLY when the inode has exactly INODE_ITEM + one INODE_REF — no extents/xattrs, range-scan-verified — DIR_ITEM single entry, nlink<=1; fallback to per-op for every other case, incl the refcount-aware extent free in btrfs_collect_purge_plan). That is the careful, conformance-gated, deletion-risk next step on the biggest gap (delete 5.5x); not rushed under the clock. bd-cowbatch FS wins to date: btrfs create 3.0x→2.08x, mkdir 3.5x→2.42x.

### 2026-06-25 SHIPPED bd-cowbatch increment 4 (ffs-core): btrfs delete-path common-case batch — delete 1.44x faster, kernel gap 5.25x→3.65x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Wired btrfs_unlink_impl onto remove_many for the BIGGEST gap. When the whole delete reduces to exactly 4 clean key-removes + one parent update — a linked-once inode (nlink<=1) with NO other items (no extents/xattrs/extra refs, child objectid range-scan == exactly {INODE_ITEM, INODE_REF(parent)}) whose name does NOT hash-collide (stored DIR_ITEM bytes == this single entry's length) — batch DIR_ITEM+DIR_INDEX+INODE_REF+INODE_ITEM via remove_many + ONE coalesced parent INODE_ITEM update (i_size -= 2*name_len AND mtime/ctime). CONSERVATIVE — NO false positive => no data-loss risk: a collision makes the DIR_ITEM bytes longer; an extent/xattr/extra-ref makes the child count != 2; a multi-link makes child_will_be_purged false — every such case falls back to the proven per-op path (remove_dir_entry + remove_inode_ref + adjust_nlink + purge + touch). Byte-identical to it (same 4 keys removed, same final parent value; remove_many byte-identical to sequential delete; the skipped adjust_nlink write is overwritten by the INODE_ITEM removal anyway).

MEASURED (clean same-session interleaved A/B, delbench 12000 vs kernel btrfs ~38k/s): baseline (unwired) **~7.24k unlinks/s** (7221/7275/7209) → wired **~10.4k** (10606/10149/10528) = **1.44x faster** (non-overlapping ranges), kernel gap **5.25x → 3.65x** (matches create/mkdir's ~1.43x coalesced-batch step). CORRECTNESS: ffs-core btrfs suite 357 passed (incl delete/rmdir/unlink round-trips); only the 3 pre-existing btrfs_symlink* failures remain. Byte-identical => conformance unaffected.

⭐⭐bd-cowbatch FS realizations COMPLETE for the create/delete metadata triad: btrfs create 3.0x→2.08x, mkdir 3.5x→2.42x, delete 5.25x→3.65x — all via the insert_many/insert_many_then_update/remove_many in-place coalesced-batch primitives. Remaining btrfs-delete residual (still 3.65x) = the non-common cases (files with extents/xattrs, collisions, multi-link) still per-op + the inherent COW-clone for the 2 full-path removes (the in-place only saves the 2nd of each leaf pair). NEXT: rename (rename-bench, mixed remove+insert) is the last unwired metadata op; or extract the shared create/mkdir helper.

### 2026-06-25 MEASURED: btrfs rename is the NEW biggest metadata gap — ~4.4x slower than kernel (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

With the create/delete triad shipped, measured the last unwired metadata op. Interleaved (kernel `rename()` loop + syncfs via `/tmp/krename.c` vs `ffs-cli rename-bench`, 12000, same-dir rename): kernel **~24.4k renames/s** (24705/23965/24409) vs frankenfs **~5.5k** (5356/5625/5527) = **~4.4x SLOWER** — now the BIGGEST btrfs metadata gap (vs delete 3.65x, create 2.08x). frankenfs rename does, per op: remove old DIR_ITEM+DIR_INDEX+INODE_REF, insert new DIR_ITEM+DIR_INDEX+INODE_REF, + parent INODE_ITEM update(s) — each re-COWing the parent subtree (~6-8 path-COWs/rename), all per-op.

WIRING PLAN (the careful next step — rename is btrfs's MOST complex op = data movement): for the COMMON case (same parent: parent_oid==new_parent_oid; NO existing target; old DIR_ITEM single entry [stored bytes == single-entry length]; old INODE_REF single entry; new_name DIR_ITEM key absent = no collision), batch `remove_many([old DIR_ITEM, old DIR_INDEX, old INODE_REF])` + `insert_many([new DIR_ITEM, new DIR_INDEX, new INODE_REF])` + ONE coalesced parent update (i_size += 2*(new_len - old_len) + mtime/ctime). The child INODE_ITEM is NOT touched by rename (only parent timestamps) — simpler than delete's purge. Fallback to the proven per-op path for cross-parent / target-exists / multi-link / collision / old==new-hash. Conservative length-checks => no false positive => no data-movement risk; remove_many/insert_many byte-identical => same final tree. Projected ~4.4x → ~2.5-3x (the bd-cowbatch coalesced-batch step). Deferred as a dedicated effort (most-complex op, not rushed after a long session).

### 2026-06-25 SHIPPED bd-cowbatch increment 5 (ffs-core): btrfs rename common-case batch — rename 1.25x faster, kernel gap 4.9x→3.93x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Wired btrfs_rename (ffs-core:25878) per the plan above. For a same-dir rename with no target collision and single old DIR_ITEM/INODE_REF entries (no new-name collision), batch `remove_many([old DIR_ITEM, old DIR_INDEX, old INODE_REF])` + `insert_many_then_update([new DIR_ITEM, new DIR_INDEX, new INODE_REF], parent INODE_ITEM = i_size += 2*(new_len-old_len) + mtime/ctime)`. The INODE_REF key (child,INODE_REF,parent) is the same for old/new (same parent) — removed then re-inserted = value rewrite. CONSERVATIVE: cross-parent / target-exists / multi-entry old DIR_ITEM or INODE_REF (length check) / new-name collision (incl old==new hash) fall back to the proven per-op path. No false positive => no data-movement risk; byte-identical (same keys, fresh DIR_INDEX seq, same parent value).

MEASURED (clean same-session interleaved A/B, rename-bench 12000 vs kernel btrfs ~25k/s): baseline (unwired) **~5.11k renames/s** (5325/4987/5005) → wired **~6.36k** (6358/6307/6407) = **1.25x faster** (non-overlapping ranges), kernel gap **4.9x → 3.93x**. MODEST vs create/delete's 1.43x — the remove side's first-item-removal fallbacks (idx==0 -> clone path) + the old/new entries spanning 2 leaves dampen the in-place benefit (remove_many is inherently a weaker lever than insert_many, per the 2026-06-25 remove_many timing finding). CORRECTNESS: ffs-core btrfs suite 357 passed (incl all rename/rename2_exchange/hardlink round-trips); only the 3 pre-existing btrfs_symlink* failures remain. Byte-identical => conformance unaffected.

⭐⭐⭐bd-cowbatch ALL FOUR metadata ops now wired: btrfs create 3.0x→2.08x, mkdir 3.5x→2.42x, delete 5.25x→3.65x, rename 4.9x→3.93x — via insert_many/insert_many_then_update/remove_many in-place coalesced batches, every common case + conservative per-op fallback, all byte-identical (conformance-safe by construction). Residual gaps are the non-common cases (collisions, multi-link, extents/xattrs, cross-parent) + the inherent COW for the first full-path op of each leaf pair. NEXT: extract the shared create/mkdir helper (dedup, the 3 create-family fns); or deepen the in-place path to internal nodes (reuse staged internals across the 2 leaves) for a further step.

### 2026-06-25 bd-cowbatch campaign CONFORMANCE-VERIFIED end-to-end: all 4 metadata wirings 100/0/2 GREEN (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Formal correctness closure for the full bd-cowbatch campaign (all 4 btrfs metadata ops wired: create/mkdir/delete/rename). Ran the e2e conformance suite with every wiring live: `cargo test -p ffs-harness --test conformance` => **100 passed / 0 failed / 2 ignored**. This confirms end-to-end what the per-commit byte-identical reasoning + the 357 ffs-core btrfs round-trip tests asserted: each coalesced-batch common-case path produces byte-identical on-disk results to the per-op path, and every non-common case falls back. The campaign is complete and verified — btrfs create 3.0x→2.08x, mkdir 3.5x→2.42x, delete 5.25x→3.65x, rename 4.9x→3.93x (5 FS-realization commits 8b818c81/b5e22c17/d518312a/aee47f35/f90648f5 + 3 proptest-hardened primitives), all conformance-GREEN. Remaining levers (deeper, deferred): internal-node in-place reuse (deepen all 4) + the create-family dedup.

### 2026-06-25 MEASURED LOSS: btrfs metadata NEGATIVE-SCALES under parallelism — the parallel gap is the biggest (~4x at 4 threads), architectural (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The single-thread bd-cowbatch wins narrowed the SERIAL gaps; measured the PARALLEL dimension (create-bench --threads vs `/tmp/kpcreate.c` pthreads kernel harness, 16000 total, btrfs). frankenfs create NEGATIVE-scales (slower with more threads) while the kernel POSITIVE-scales:

| threads | kernel creates/s | frankenfs creates/s | gap |
|---------|------------------|---------------------|-----|
| 1  | 38089 | 20599 | 1.85x |
| 4  | 64025 | **16105** | **3.98x** |
| 8  | 52714 | 15198 | 3.47x |
| 16 | 46557 | 15060 | 3.09x |

frankenfs goes 20.6k (1t) → 16.1k (4t) → 15.1k (16t) — adding threads makes it SLOWER. ROOT CAUSE: every writer serializes on the global MVCC commit lock + the single shared `InMemoryCowBtrfsTree` (one `alloc_mutex.write()` per op holds the whole fs-tree), so parallel metadata has zero (negative) scaling; the kernel parallelizes across subdirs. So the PARALLEL metadata gap (~4x, widening with cores) now exceeds every serial gap.

LEVER (architectural, deep — NOT a contained single-turn change, distinct from the peer's single-thread internal-in-place): shard the MVCC commit lock + allow concurrent COW-tree mutation on disjoint subtrees (per-subvolume / per-objectid-range locking, lock-free snapshot registration — cf the earlier bd-snaplock attempt which was wall-neutral because a single Mutex just relocates the serialization point). This is the frankenfs parallel-write architecture work; surfaced as the highest-value remaining lever (it dominates at multi-core), to be a dedicated effort. Recorded as a measured loss per the BOLD-VERIFY ledger.

UNIVERSAL (confirmed ext4 too — the bottleneck is NOT btrfs-specific): ext4 create-bench --threads vs kernel ext4 parallel (kpcreate, 16000):

| threads | kernel ext4 creates/s | frankenfs ext4 creates/s | gap |
|---------|-----------------------|--------------------------|-----|
| 1 | 36270  | 47331 | frankenfs **1.3x FASTER** (serial) |
| 4 | 101467 | 27029 | 3.75x slower |
| 8 | 158890 | 26927 | **5.90x slower** |

frankenfs ext4 create WINS serial (47.3k vs 36.3k = 1.3x) but NEGATIVE-scales (47.3k→27k→26.9k) while the kernel scales ~4.4x (36k→159k) — so the ext4 parallel gap reaches **5.9x at 8 threads**, even larger than btrfs's 3.5x (the kernel's ext4 metadata parallelizes harder). This proves the negative-scaling is the FS-AGNOSTIC global-write-lock serialization (every metadata op takes one exclusive lock over the whole fs state + the MVCC commit lock), NOT a btrfs COW artifact. The single commit-lock-sharding / fine-grained-fs-lock architectural lever therefore lifts BOTH filesystems at multi-core — the dominant remaining frankenfs perf gap. The serial bd-cowbatch wins are real but are dwarfed by this parallel loss on any multi-core box.

PROFILE of the parallel btrfs create (4 threads, perf -g): the CPU self-time is dominated by `InMemoryCowBtrfsTree::insert_into` 45% + the key/item `extend` clone ~34% — the SAME COW-clone volume as the serial path — with NO prominent futex/park/lock-wait hotspot. Interpretation: the global lock SERIALIZES the COW work (only one thread mutates the fs-tree at a time; the others park off-CPU so they don't show in CPU self-time), and the drop BELOW the serial rate (47k→27k) is the lock-handoff + cache-line bouncing on the shared fs-tree/allocator. Two consequences: (1) reducing the per-op COW clone — the peer's single-thread internal-in-place lever — ALSO helps the parallel case (less serialized work per op), so it is doubly valuable; (2) closing the parallel gap to the kernel's positive scaling still requires fine-grained / disjoint-subtree locking so multiple threads COW concurrently (architectural, the btrfs COW-tree's locking model = the peer's lane). No contained single-turn parallel lever exists; the dominant remaining win is the architectural concurrent-mutation work.

PROFILE of the parallel EXT4 create (4 threads, perf -g) — a DIFFERENT bottleneck than btrfs: ~21% per-op dir-block work (`parse_dir_block` + `walk_dir_block_entries`, the `add_entry` slot-find — mostly necessary), ~15% `FxHashSet<Vec<u8>>` name-index build, ~9% memcpy, and crucially **~14% explicit lock contention** (`__sched_yield` 8.7% + parking_lot `lock_exclusive_slow` 5.2%). So ext4's parallel ceiling is the **MVCC commit lock** (`store.write()` per op), not a COW-clone serialization. (Verified the dir-name-index is NOT an O(N^2) rebuild: `OpenFs::create` updates both `names` AND `validation` incrementally at lib.rs:28695-28697, and the index is sharded by dir inode (DIR_NAME_INDEX_SHARDS) to avoid cross-thread thrash — so it stays current; ext4 create wins serial 1.3x, no contained per-op lever there.) NET: the two filesystems have DISTINCT parallel locks — btrfs = the single `alloc_mutex` over the in-mem COW fs-tree (peer's lane); ext4 = the MVCC commit lock (ffs-mvcc). Both need architectural sharding (concurrent disjoint-range commit + FCW conflict-detection that doesn't take one global lock; bd-snaplock was wall-neutral because a lone Mutex just moves the serialization point). This is the single dominant remaining frankenfs perf gap and is a dedicated architectural effort — no contained single-turn lever exists, on either FS.

REJECT (ruled-out quick lever): "bump the dir-name-index shard count to kill the ext4 parallel contention." Checked — `DIR_NAME_INDEX_SHARDS = 64` already (lib.rs:1175); for the 4-thread bench that is far more than enough, so the contended exclusive RwLock (`lock_exclusive_slow`→`park`) is NOT the index shard. By elimination (ext4 has no btrfs alloc_mutex; the index is 64-sharded) the contended lock is the global MVCC `store.write()` commit lock. So bumping shard counts is INERT for the ext4 parallel gap — the only lever is sharding the MVCC commit itself (architectural). Contained-lever surface is exhausted on both filesystems; the dominant remaining work (parallel commit/lock sharding) is architectural and multi-turn.

### 2026-06-26 REJECTED: staged internal-node reuse for btrfs COW insert batches did not improve the multi-leaf batch shape (IvoryBirch codex/gpt-5)

BOLD-VERIFY land-or-dig pass checked `.scratch`/worktree heads first; no unlanded measured worktree win remained that was not already represented by a production successor on `main`. The new lever tested the documented follow-up from the bd-cowbatch campaign: reuse an internal node allocated earlier in the same COW batch, updating its child pointer in place instead of cloning that staged internal again. This is the B-epsilon/write-buffering idea applied inside `InMemoryCowBtrfsTree::insert_into` for multi-leaf `insert_many_then_update` batches.

MEASURED on `hz2` via RCH, per-crate only:

```
AGENT_NAME=IvoryBirch \

  --bench cow_write_mutation -- btrfs_cow_staged_internal_multi_leaf \

Literal `cargo bench --release` was also probed through RCH and rejected by Cargo (`unexpected argument '--release'`), so the measured runs used the repository-compatible `--profile release` form. The worker cache was cold/noisy despite the requested target dir, but the Criterion comparison used the same worker and same benchmark row.

| row | baseline | staged-internal candidate | old/new |
|-----|----------|---------------------------|---------|

Criterion reported no statistically significant improvement (`p=0.46` for bulk) and the midpoint regressed. Candidate source and the temporary benchmark row were reverted. The direct btrfs metadata ratios remain the current ledger values: create `2.08x` slower than kernel, mkdir `2.42x`, delete `3.65x`, rename `3.93x`; ext4/btrfs parallel negative-scaling ratios remain unchanged. This reject says not to pursue staged internal-node insert reuse as the next btrfs COW micro-lever unless a different benchmark/profile shows a real hot path.

### 2026-06-26 REJECTED: MVCC FCW preflight/apply fused merge map did not improve request-scope commit (IvoryBirch codex/gpt-5)

BOLD-VERIFY land-or-dig pass rechecked the remaining non-ancestor `.scratch`/worktree heads first. The apparent tail-scan and ffs-block staging-skip wins already have measured production successors on `main` (`bd-xmh5g.405`, `bd-xmh5g.383/.410`), while the RaptorQ and DIR_INDEX scratch wins were already represented by later production source. No unlanded measured worktree win remained to land.

NEW LEVER TESTED: reduce the ext4 parallel metadata bottleneck's MVCC lock hold time by fusing FCW preflight with commit apply. Candidate changed `preflight_fcw` to return merged conflict bytes and made ordinary `commit()`/SSI consume that map instead of rescanning every staged block in `apply_fcw_commit` / `merged_writes_after_preflight`. Correctness argument: under `&mut MvccStore`, no transaction can commit between preflight and apply, so the preflight result is stable. The candidate source was reverted because the measured request-scope commit row was neutral-to-slower.

MEASURED on `hz2` via RCH, per-crate only:

```
AGENT_NAME=IvoryBirch \

  --bench mvcc_commit_batching -- request_scope_batched_commit \

| row | baseline | FCW fused-map candidate | old/new |
|-----|----------|-------------------------|---------|
| `mvcc_commit_batching_2000/request_scope_batched_commit` | `[5.8796, 5.9704, 6.1530] ms` | `[6.2761, 6.3608, 6.4414] ms` | midpoint `0.939x`; conservative `5.8796/6.4414 = 0.913x` |

Criterion reported `No change in performance detected` (`p=0.38`), and the midpoint regressed by ~6.5%.
