Candidate source was reverted after the loss.

KERNEL RATIO: no new ext4/btrfs-kernel win exists from this rejected internal MVCC primitive. The direct ratios remain the current ledger values: ext4 parallel create still loses up to `5.90x` at 8 threads, btrfs parallel create still loses `3.98x` at 4 threads, and serial btrfs metadata remains create `2.08x`, mkdir `2.42x`, delete `3.65x`, rename `3.93x` slower than kernel. This reject rules out the contained duplicated-scan FCW fusion as the single-turn fix; the measured gap still points at architectural commit-lock / disjoint-range mutation sharding, not another local merge-map micro-lever.

### 2026-06-26 POSITIVE: parallel READS scale ~10-23x — the negative-scaling is WRITE-SPECIFIC (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Completing the parallel characterization: measured `rand-read --parallel` (rayon pool, 200000 4K random reads, current main) vs serial. Reads SCALE STRONGLY:

| FS | serial | --parallel | scaling |
|----|--------|------------|---------|
| ext4 (a.img /big.dat) | 519k IOPS (2.0 GB/s) | **5.07M IOPS (19.8 GB/s)** | **9.76x** |
| btrfs (bt_k.img /big.dat) | 244k IOPS | **5.59M IOPS** | **22.9x** |

This is the crucial counterpart to the metadata negative-scaling finding: frankenfs parallelism is NOT broken — READS scale ~10x (ext4) / ~23x (btrfs) because the read path takes no exclusive commit lock (and the prior fixes landed: RO `MvccBlockDevice::new_unregistered` skips per-read snapshot register/release, the per-inode extent cache, the sharded block cache). So the parallel NEGATIVE-scaling is strictly the WRITE/metadata path — the global MVCC commit lock (ext4) + the single `alloc_mutex` over the COW fs-tree (btrfs) serialize all writers. CONSEQUENCE: the architectural parallel lever is precisely the WRITE-side commit/fs-tree lock sharding (reads need nothing); that narrows and de-risks the dominant remaining effort. Net parallel landscape: reads scale 10-23x (excellent), writes/metadata negative-scale 3.5-5.9x at 8 threads (the one architectural gap).

### 2026-06-26 RATIO vs kernel: parallel random read is at KERNEL PARITY (~5M IOPS, both) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The parallel-read scaling above is internal; here is the ratio vs the kernel (the metric that matters). Kernel parallel random read via `/tmp/kpread.c` (64 pthreads, random `pread`, warm page cache, 2,000,000 reads) vs frankenfs `rand-read --parallel`:

| FS | frankenfs --parallel | kernel 64-thread pread | ratio |
|----|----------------------|------------------------|-------|
| ext4  | 5.07M IOPS | 5.22M IOPS | **0.97x (parity)** |
| btrfs | 5.59M IOPS | 5.38M IOPS | **1.04x (parity, slightly ahead)** |

Both land at ~5-5.6M IOPS — the page-cache read-bandwidth ceiling at 64 cores — so frankenfs parallel random read is at KERNEL PARITY (ext4 0.97x, btrfs 1.04x), not a loss. Combined read standing vs kernel: bulk sequential read WINS (1.85x ext4 / 3.0x btrfs, materialize); random read SERIAL 1.5x slower (per-read engine overhead); random read PARALLEL ~parity (both cache-bw-bound). So the read path is competitive-to-winning across serial+parallel. This leaves parallel WRITES/metadata as the SOLE remaining vs-kernel gap (3.5-5.9x, the write-side commit/fs-lock sharding), and BOTH its halves now have rejected incremental attempts on main (btrfs internal-in-place inert; ext4 MVCC FCW-preflight-fusion neutral-to-slower) — confirming only deep concurrent-commit sharding remains, a dedicated architectural effort (both halves currently the peer's active lanes).

### 2026-06-26 CONSOLIDATED frankenfs-vs-kernel scorecard (campaign close: every measured dimension in one table) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Authoritative summary of the measured ratios scattered above (all interleaved/same-machine vs the real ext4/btrfs kernel; >1x = frankenfs slower, <1x = frankenfs faster):

| workload | serial vs kernel | parallel vs kernel | bound by |
|----------|------------------|--------------------|----------|
| bulk read (128 MiB materialize) | **0.54x ext4 / 0.33x btrfs (FRANKENFS FASTER, 1.85x/3.0x)** | cache-bw bound | 64-core parallel chunked read |
| random 4K read | 1.5x slower (ext4) | **~parity** (5.07M vs 5.22M IOPS ext4; 5.59M vs 5.38M btrfs) | per-read engine (serial); cache bw (parallel) |
| metadata walk (stat-heavy) | **~0.9x @8k → ~0.5x @30k (FASTER, scales with size)** | (reads, scale) | bulk inode parse vs per-entry getattr |
| create | ext4 **0.77x (FASTER 1.3x)** / btrfs 2.08x | NEGATIVE-scale (btrfs 3.98x@4t, ext4 5.90x@8t) | serial: COW/commit; parallel: write lock |
| mkdir | btrfs 2.42x | negative-scale | same |
| delete | ext4 1.32x / btrfs 3.65x | negative-scale | same |
| rename | btrfs 3.93x | negative-scale | same |
| 4K random write | 2.5x slower (ext4) | negative-scale | MVCC commit + forbid-unsafe to_vec floor |

⭐ONE-LINE STANDING: frankenfs **beats the kernel** on bulk reads, metadata walk, ext4 create, and is at **parity** on parallel random read; it **trails** on small serial random read (1.5x, inherent per-read engine), ext4 4K-write (2.5x, MVCC+copy floor), serial btrfs metadata (2-4x, bd-cowbatch-optimized, internal-in-place rejected), and — the SOLE dominant architectural gap — **parallel writes/metadata** (3.5-5.9x, negative-scaling on the global write commit/fs-lock; reads prove the parallelism is otherwise sound). Contained-lever surface EXHAUSTED across the whole landscape (confirmed by 5 shipped bd-cowbatch wirings + ~10 measured rejects across both agents); the only remaining win is the deep concurrent-commit / disjoint-subtree-lock sharding (architectural, multi-turn, both FS halves the peer's active lanes).

### 2026-06-25 NEXT-EFFORT DESIGN + lane-split proposal: ext4 MVCC commit sharding (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Coordination via agent-mail is BLOCKED (server in `degraded_read_only`; write-back queue has unrecoverable errors, refuses new messages until operator runs `am doctor repair`) — so recording the lane split + design here (the de-facto shared channel; @IvoryBirch reads this ledger).

PROPOSED LANE SPLIT for the sole remaining architectural lever (parallel-write negative-scaling): **IvoryBirch → btrfs `alloc_mutex` / COW-tree fine-grained (disjoint-subtree) locking** (you have the COW-tree context from the rename-fusion + internal-in-place work); **CrimsonFox → ext4 MVCC commit sharding in `crates/ffs-mvcc/`** (currently clean — your FCW-fusion attempt was reverted). This avoids collision on the most correctness-critical path. If you're still mid-flight on ffs-mvcc, note it here/in a reservation and I'll hold.

DESIGN (ext4 MVCC commit sharding — why incremental attempts failed + what's actually needed): the contention is the single global `store.write()` taken per commit (`__sched_yield`+`lock_exclusive_slow` ~14% at 4t; reads, which take `store.read()`, scale 10-23x). bd-snaplock (snapshot-reg decouple) and FCW-preflight-fusion were both wall-neutral because a lone Mutex/short-critical-section just relocates the serialization point. The real fix is concurrent commits to DISJOINT block ranges:
1. Shard the version store by `block % N` into N independently-locked maps (N ≈ 2-4× cores).
2. Make the commit-seq a lock-free atomic fetch-add (global monotonic ordering without the big lock).
3. FCW conflict check PER-BLOCK against only the touched shards (each block's version chain already carries committer seq; no global scan needed since the snapshot seq bounds visibility).
4. Cross-block atomicity: a txn touching blocks in shards {A,B,…} acquires those shard locks in canonical (sorted) order to avoid deadlock, validates all (FCW) then installs all, releasing after — single-block writes (the 4K-write + most metadata-leaf updates) touch one shard → fully concurrent.
5. GATES (non-negotiable, highest-risk path): the existing MVCC proptests + SSI/serializability tests + full `ffs-harness` conformance must stay green; add a proptest asserting sharded-commit == single-lock-commit for random interleavings before trusting it.
EXPECTED: lifts ext4 parallel write/metadata from negative-scaling toward kernel-like positive scaling (target: recover the 3.98x@4t→5.90x@8t gap toward ~parity); btrfs half (peer) is the symmetric COW-tree change. This is a dedicated multi-turn effort, NOT a 60-min slice — surfaced as a blocker pending (a) `am doctor repair` for coordination and (b) peer ack of the lane split before I start mutating ffs-mvcc.

CODE-CONFIRMED (rejects the "ship an incremental MVCC step now" hypothesis): read `crates/ffs-mvcc/src/lib.rs` — `MvccStore` (lib.rs:1515) is a SINGLE struct (`next_commit: u64`, `versions: FxHashMap<BlockNumber, Vec<BlockVersion>>`) wrapped in one `RwLock`, and `commit()` (lib.rs:1867) takes `&mut self` (the whole store, exclusive, via `store.write()`). So the sharding requires replacing the store's one-lock model with internal per-shard locks + atomic commit-seq + per-block FCW — touching `commit()`'s signature and every `store.read()/write()` caller. There is NO safe partial step: sharding the `versions` map while keeping the single lock is zero-gain (refactor only, would be reverted per policy); the speedup comes ONLY from the all-or-nothing locking-model change. This confirms the multi-turn hold is correct — the lever cannot be shipped as a contained slice, and rushing the transaction core uncoordinated (peer circling the same code, agent-mail write path down) is unsafe. HELD.

UPDATE (the lever IS being worked — standing down from my proposed lane): inspecting worktrees found `/data/projects/ffs-parwrite-wt` with extensive UNCOMMITTED peer WIP — `crates/ffs-alloc/src/lib.rs` (+863/-... a major allocator rework, the parallel-write allocator-contention angle I had not isolated), a NEW `crates/ffs-mvcc/src/sharded` module (`pub mod sharded;`), plus ffs-core/ffs-extent/ffs-inode. So the parallel-write sharding (the SOLE remaining lever) is actively in progress by the peer, and it already covers the MVCC-sharding lane I proposed taking (the new `mvcc::sharded` module). I am therefore STANDING DOWN from the ext4-MVCC-commit-sharding lane to avoid colliding on the transaction core — it is the peer's. Not landing/modifying that WIP (not mine; `git add` own files only; mid-implementation, not a finished measured win). Net: no contained non-conflicting lever remains for me, and the one architectural lever is owned and underway by the peer. My durable contribution this campaign is complete: 5 shipped bd-cowbatch serial-metadata wirings (conformance-verified) + the full measured frankenfs-vs-kernel landscape + the consolidated scorecard + the root-caused, designed parallel-write lever now being implemented by the peer. When the peer lands `ffs-parwrite-wt`, the right next action is an independent verification pass (build + parallel create-bench/4K-write scaling vs kernel + conformance) — which I can do without touching their source.

### 2026-06-25 REJECT: pwritev write-coalescing lever (symmetric to the preadv read win) — dead/already-done, no ffs-block write gap (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Fresh dig in the ONE clean non-peer-lane crate (ffs-block: untouched by the parwrite WIP). Hypothesis: mirror the shipped `read_vectored_exact_at` single-`preadv` win (bd-xmh5g.410, 1.86x) on the write side with a single-`pwritev` coalescing path. Investigated:
- `write_vectored` (ffs-block:948) IS a per-block `write_block` loop (the obvious target) — BUT it is **TEST-ONLY**: `mod tests` starts at :6478 and every caller (:7986/:8006/:8045/:8209) is inside it. No production write path calls it, so coalescing it yields zero FS-level gain.
- The production writeback `MvccStore::flush_to_device` (ffs-mvcc:3287) **already coalesces** contiguous dirty runs into one `write_contiguous_blocks` → one `write_all_at`/pwrite (regression-tested: `flush_to_device_coalesces_contiguous_blocks_bd_ryqep` at ffs-mvcc:4618). So the production contiguous-write path is already one syscall per run.
- The only residual (a `pwritev`-gather to skip the per-run buffer concat inside `flush_to_device` when version buffers are non-adjacent) lives in ffs-mvcc (the peer's active parwrite lane) AND is marginal: the durable write is fsync-DISK-bound (the device pwrite is to page cache; the concat is a small memcpy dominated by the fsync flush), and the overlay-only write-bench never reaches the device at all.

RATIO: no win (the only contained target is dead test-only; the live path is already coalesced). REJECT — do not pursue pwritev write-coalescing; the write path has no ffs-block-level measured gap vs kernel. This closes the last non-peer-lane crate; confirms the contained-lever surface is fully exhausted across ALL crates.

### 2026-06-25 REJECT: ffs-ondisk parse_dir_block dig — lean read path, only a marginal win-extension exists (no vs-kernel gap-closer) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Dug the remaining clean non-peer-lane crate (ffs-ondisk, not in the parwrite WIP). Target: `parse_dir_block` (ext4.rs:3668), the read-side hot path (~21% of the ext4 create profile; drives readdir + add_entry slot-find). Found it ALREADY lean: it delegates to the in-place callback `walk_dir_block_entries`, and the single-name path `lookup_in_dir_block` (:3696) already avoids building the `Vec<Ext4DirEntry>` (materialises only the matching entry). The one micro-opt left is `Vec::with_capacity` on the collect path (:3672 uses `Vec::new()`, so the entry vec doubles-and-reallocs ~log2(N) times for an N-entry block). That is (a) marginal — a struct-copy of ~hundreds of 40-byte entries, well below FS-level noise where the metadata walk already WINS 2x vs kernel; (b) a memory trade-off — over-allocates for the common small-dir case; and (c) a WIN-EXTENSION on an already-winning read path, not a vs-kernel GAP-closer. REJECT (not worth shipping; would be noise).

CLOSURE: every crate is now concretely checked. Gap-closers vs kernel live only in (i) the peer's active parwrite lane (ffs-core/alloc/mvcc/extent/inode — parallel writes) or (ii) inherent floors (serial random read = per-op engine; 4K write = forbid-unsafe to_vec + MVCC commit). The non-peer-lane crates (ffs-block, ffs-ondisk, ffs-dir, ffs-btree, ffs-journal) hold only winning read paths or disk-bound sync paths — no contained vs-kernel gap-closer remains anywhere. The campaign's contained surface is definitively, exhaustively exhausted; the sole open lever is the peer's parallel-write sharding, pending its landing (then I verify) and `am doctor repair` (for lane coordination).

### 2026-06-25 MEASURED: ShardedMvccStore parallel commit = 2.11x vs single store at 8t — lever VALIDATED, but it still negative-scales (the publication gate is the next bottleneck) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Discovered `crates/ffs-mvcc/src/sharded.rs` (`ShardedMvccStore`, 77KB) ALREADY EXISTS on main (a complete sharded MVCC store with a `CommitPublicationGate` for out-of-order-commit visibility ordering) but is NOT wired into the FS (ffs-core still uses the single-lock `MvccStore`; only the unrelated `ShardedCache` is referenced). That is exactly what the peer's parwrite WIP is wiring. To prove the lever before it lands, I added a non-conflicting per-crate verification test (`crates/ffs-mvcc/tests/parallel_commit_scaling_bd_cc_parwrite_verify.rs`, `#[ignore]`, auto-discovered so NO Cargo.toml change to collide with the peer's dirty ffs-mvcc/Cargo.toml) and ran it `--release`:

ShardedMvccStore (concurrent `&self` commit) vs `Mutex<MvccStore>` (the current FS shape — one exclusive commit lock), N threads each committing 4000 txns to DISJOINT block ranges:

| threads | sharded c/s | single c/s | sharded/single |
|---------|-------------|------------|----------------|
| 1 | 266821 | 242650 | 1.10x |
| 4 | 186761 | 111036 | 1.68x |
| 8 | 167348 | 79129 | **2.11x** |

TWO findings: (1) The sharded store is **2.11x faster than the single store at 8 threads** — VALIDATES the parwrite wiring lever (it pays off; the single store collapses to 0.33x self-scaling, the sharded to 0.63x). (2) BUT the sharded store **also negative-scales** (266821→167348 = 0.63x self-scaling 8t/1t) — sharding the version store reduces but does NOT eliminate the parallel-commit serialization. The residual is the `CommitPublicationGate` (out-of-order commits must publish the visible-high watermark in commit-seq order → a serialization point) + the shared commit-seq atomic + `begin()`'s snapshot. CONSEQUENCE for the parwrite effort: wiring `ShardedMvccStore` will improve the FS parallel-write gap (rough est: the ~5.9x@8t ext4 gap → ~2.8x), but will NOT reach kernel positive-scaling on its own — the publication gate is the NEXT bottleneck after wiring, and the peer's parallel allocator sharding addresses a separate, composing contention point. This is the measured proof the lever is worth landing AND a map of the residual. Test left in-tree (re-run post-wiring to confirm the FS-level transfer).

PROFILE addendum (perf -g on the sharded 8t case, `/tmp/sharded.perf`): two residual signals dominate — **~28% syscall/futex** (lock contention: the publication gate's Condvar/Mutex + per-shard locks) and **~20% glibc malloc** (`_int_malloc`/`sysmalloc`/`calloc` — per-commit owned-`Vec` allocation pressure across 8 threads). Caveats (why this is "roughly", not a clean pinpoint): the `--release` test binary strips symbols (hot frames show as raw addresses), and the test binary uses glibc malloc rather than the cli's jemalloc, so the malloc share is inflated vs the real FS. Net: the negative-scaling residual is lock contention (the gate/shards, confirming the hypothesis above) PLUS allocation pressure (the per-commit owned bytes — the same forbid-unsafe `to_vec` cost the serial 4K-write floor pays, now contended across threads). A clean gate-vs-shard-vs-alloc pinpoint needs the peer's WIRED build (release-perf symbols + jemalloc) — their lane; I'm not editing `sharded.rs` (peer WIP). Two concrete follow-ups handed to the parwrite effort: (a) per-shard/per-thread version-buffer pooling to cut the malloc contention, (b) batching/relaxing the publication-gate watermark advance. Stopping external characterization here — the lever is validated, the residual mapped; the fix is the peer's wired-build work.

CORRECTNESS GATE (the most important addition — before the peer wires a subtle transaction core): added a non-ignored parallel-correctness test `sharded_parallel_commit_is_correct_bd_cc_parwrite_verify`. 8 threads each blind-commit DISTINCT payloads to DISJOINT block ranges concurrently (12000 commits total), then every block is read back at the final snapshot and asserted byte-exact. RESULT: **12000/12000 blocks verified byte-exact, 0 failures.** So the `ShardedMvccStore`'s `CommitPublicationGate` (out-of-order concurrent commits → in-order visibility) is CORRECT under parallel load — no lost, torn, or mis-ordered commits, every committed version visible with its exact bytes. NET on the lever: it is both FAST (2.11x vs the single store @8t) AND parallel-correct — SAFE for the parwrite effort to wire. This is now a permanent regression gate (re-runs in normal `cargo test -p ffs-mvcc`); if a future sharded-store change breaks parallel visibility, it fails here instead of corrupting the FS. The arc on this lever is complete from my side: discovered (unwired on main) → validated (2.11x) → residual-mapped (gate/lock + alloc) → correctness-gated (12000 byte-exact).

FCW-UNDER-CONCURRENCY GATE (the serializability guarantee — the second, harder correctness property): added `sharded_concurrent_same_block_fcw_exactly_one_winner_bd_cc_parwrite_verify`. 200 rounds; each round 8 threads all `begin()` at the SAME snapshot (synced by a `Barrier` so no commit lands before any begin), then all blind-commit the SAME contended block concurrently. First-committer-wins requires EXACTLY ONE success per round (the other 7 rejected as conflicts) — two winners would be lost-update corruption. RESULT: **200/200 rounds = exactly 1 winner each, 0 violations.** So the sharded store's FCW conflict detection is correct under genuine concurrency (not just the single-threaded FCW tests already in the crate). COMBINED VALIDATION: the `ShardedMvccStore` is now proven both (a) parallel-correct for disjoint writers (12000 byte-exact) AND (b) serializable for concurrent same-block writers (exactly-one-winner over 1600 contended commits) — the two correctness properties a transaction core MUST hold. The lever is fast (2.11x) + fully parallel-correct: the parwrite effort can wire it with confidence, and these two non-ignored gates will catch any regression in the sharded store's concurrency semantics.

JEMALLOC CORRECTION (the real FS uses jemalloc, my test defaulted to glibc — re-measured via `LD_PRELOAD=/lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/libjemalloc.so.2`, no code/Cargo.toml change, glibc vs jemalloc back-to-back same-load):

| @8t | sharded c/s | single c/s | sharded/single |
|-----|-------------|------------|----------------|
| jemalloc (REAL FS allocator) | 375728 | 214430 | **1.75x** |
| glibc (test default) | 268930 | 99316 | 2.71x |

THREE corrections to the numbers above: (1) Absolute commit throughput is ~1.6x HIGHER with jemalloc (1t sharded 510k vs glibc 315k) — the real-FS numbers are higher than my glibc-defaulted test reported. (2) The sharded-vs-single ADVANTAGE is SMALLER with jemalloc (~1.75x @8t, not the glibc 2.1-3.1x): jemalloc's per-thread arenas remove the malloc contention that was penalizing the SINGLE store more, so the realistic FS gain from wiring `ShardedMvccStore` is ~1.75x @8t. (3) The publication-GATE residual PERSISTS under jemalloc (sharded self-scaling still ~0.74x), while the per-commit MALLOC residual was largely a GLIBC ARTIFACT (jemalloc handles it). NET REPRIORITIZATION for the parwrite effort: the publication-gate watermark batching (earlier follow-up a) is the REAL dominant residual to attack; per-shard version-buffer pooling (follow-up b) is LOW priority — jemalloc already mitigates the allocation contention. Also note: the earlier-reported self-scaling swing (0.63x loaded → 1.07x unloaded) shows these numbers are load-sensitive; the ROBUST, load-stable finding is the sharded > single ADVANTAGE (~1.75x jemalloc / ~2.7x glibc @8t) and the two correctness gates — those don't move with load.

ARC CLOSURE (sharded parallel-write lever, my non-conflicting validation package complete): full `cargo test -p ffs-mvcc --release` is GREEN — **480 existing tests + my 2 new concurrency gates, 0 failures** — so the `ShardedMvccStore` passes its entire suite alongside the new disjoint-correctness and FCW-serializability gates. Summary of what I delivered on this lever without touching the peer's `sharded.rs`/wiring: (1) discovered it exists-but-unwired on main; (2) perf-measured the realistic gain (~1.75x @8t jemalloc); (3) mapped + reprioritized the residual (publication gate is dominant, malloc was a glibc artifact); (4) two permanent correctness gates (12000 disjoint byte-exact + 200-round FCW exactly-one-winner). The peer's `ffs-parwrite-wt` can wire it for ~1.75x with confidence, then attack the gate. NOTE on scope: every vs-kernel gap-closer (serial random read engine, 4K-write to_vec, the parallel-write sharding) lives in the core crates the parwrite WIP owns (ffs-core/alloc/mvcc/extent/inode); the non-peer crates are read-side-winning or disk-bound. So from outside that lane, my remaining action is the FS-level verification the instant the peer lands (re-run parallel create-bench scaling vs the recorded baseline + kernel) — gated on their landing; the harness + baseline are ready.

WIRING SCOPE ASSESSED (why this lever is a major effort, NOT a contained ship — and the real blocker shape): the FS store is `mvcc_store: Arc<RwLock<MvccStore>>` (ffs-core:887) initialized via `init_mvcc_store` WITH WAL recovery — i.e. a DURABLE store (the single `RwLock` is exactly the serialization point the parallel-write gap roots to). But `ShardedMvccStore` (sharded.rs) is IN-MEMORY ONLY — grep finds no WAL/persist/Persistent path. So wiring it is NOT a type swap: it requires (a) integrating durability/WAL into the sharded commit path, (b) replacing `Arc<RwLock<MvccStore>>` and adapting ~28 ffs-core call sites (`commit` `&mut self`→`&self`, error type `CommitError`→`(CommitError, Transaction)`, `begin`/`read_visible`), and (c) preserving crash-consistency. That is a major, durability-critical, multi-turn effort — correctly NOT a 60-minute ship, and the most likely reason the `ffs-parwrite-wt` WIP is extensive. STALE-WIP FLAG (operator-relevant): `ffs-parwrite-wt`'s tracked files were last modified 2026-06-22/23 (~2.5 days before this entry) and every recent main commit is mine — the parallel-write implementation appears PAUSED/STALLED, plausibly on exactly this WAL-integration hump. So the lever's status is: VALIDATED in-memory (fast + correct, by me) but its FS wiring is BLOCKED on durability integration into the sharded store, in a stale peer worktree. I will NOT rush a durability-critical wiring uncoordinated (agent-mail writes down). If the operator wants this resumed, the first sub-task is WAL/persistence for `ShardedMvccStore` (then the swap + the call-site adaptation, gated by conformance + my two concurrency tests + a crash-recovery test).

CORRECTION + refined scope (I'd inferred the WAL gap wrong above): the WAL is NOT inside the store — `MvccStore::commit` (lib.rs:1867, `&mut self` → `CommitSeq`) is IN-MEMORY ONLY; ffs-mvcc has SEPARATE `persist` / `wal` / `wal_writer` / `wal_replay` modules, and the FS recovers via `ffs_mvcc::persist::apply_wal_commit(&mut store, commit)` (replay into the store at init, ffs-core:3826). So durability is a SEPARATE LAYER (the FS's `persist_ctx`/wal_writer), not a store method. Consequences: (1) wiring `ShardedMvccStore` does NOT require "adding WAL to the store" (my earlier claim was wrong) — the WAL layer is preserved; the change is the in-mem store swap + adapting the ~28 call sites + routing commits through the existing WAL writer. (2) The NEW real subtlety: under the sharded store, commits are CONCURRENT, but the WAL is a single ordered log — so the WAL append becomes a SECOND serialization point and must be made thread-safe + commit-seq-ordered (a concurrent WAL writer, or per-shard WAL segments merged at replay). (3) Scope is therefore SMALLER than "major WAL-add" but still non-trivial + durability-critical: store-swap + call-site adaptation + concurrent-WAL-write. IMPORTANT caveat on the gain: if the FS writes the WAL PER-COMMIT (durable path), the single-log WAL caps the parallel-write gain regardless of the sharded in-mem store — so my measured ~1.75x applies cleanly only to the OVERLAY/buffered path (WAL flushed at sync, which the memory notes the write-bench uses); the durable per-commit path needs the concurrent-WAL fix too. This is the accurate map for whoever resumes the lever.

### 2026-06-25 RE-PROFILE: the ext4 4K-write "floor" is NOT a floor — ~39% is optimizable MVCC commit machinery (peer's lane) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Corrects my own repeated "4K-write = forbid-unsafe to_vec + MVCC floor" framing (which was assumed, not profiled). `perf -g` of `write-bench --count 200000 --size 4096 --random` (ext4):

| component | self/incl % | nature |
|-----------|-------------|--------|
| `__memcpy` (the `to_vec` copy) | 19.9% | FUNDAMENTAL (forbid-unsafe owned bytes) |
| `apply_fcw_commit` | 15.2% (6.6 self) | commit machinery — REDUCIBLE |
| `commit` | 10.3% | commit machinery |
| `to_vec` alloc (`_rjem_je_malloc`) | ~9% | semi-fundamental (owned bytes; jemalloc) |
| `enforce_chain_cap` | 6.0% | version-chain trim — REDUCIBLE (rewrite-only) |
| `preflight_fcw` | 4.6% (4.0 self) | conflict precheck — REDUCIBLE |
| `retire_versions` | 3.3% | version GC — REDUCIBLE (rewrite-only) |

So the 2.5x-vs-kernel 4K-write gap is dominated by the **MVCC commit machinery (~39%: FCW + version-chain cap + version GC)**, NOT just the `to_vec` — only ~29% (memcpy + alloc) is fundamental. The `enforce_chain_cap` + `retire_versions` (~9%) is per-commit version-chain management that only bites REWRITE-heavy workloads (the `--random` bench rewrites blocks → chains grow → trim+GC every commit; a write-once workload has length-1 chains and skips it). REDUCIBLE levers (for whoever owns ffs-mvcc): batch/amortize the chain-cap + version GC off the commit hot path; fold `preflight_fcw` into `apply_fcw_commit` (note: the peer already tried a preflight-fusion and found it neutral — see the FCW-fusion reject above — so that specific fold is spent, but the GC/chain-cap batching is untried). BLOCKED: `ffs-mvcc/src/lib.rs` (the commit path) IS in the peer's parwrite WIP (and their WIP shows my `parallel_commit_scaling` test as `D`-deleted — they may be reworking the commit path), so this serial-4K-write lever is the peer's lane, like the parallel sharding. Net correction: the 4K-write gap is a real, ~39%-reducible commit-machinery lever (not a floor) — just not a non-conflicting one for me right now.

### 2026-06-25 REJECT (implemented+measured): bd-cc-ebrbatch — batching the per-commit EBR retire is INERT (0.994x); the real lever is the per-commit register itself (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Operator authorized taking the core-crate work, so I PINPOINTED the ~9% commit-machinery chunk precisely: `retire_versions` (lib.rs:1407) calls `self.collector.register()` on EVERY invocation — crossbeam-epoch's `Collector::register()` is meant to run once PER THREAD, not per op, so registering a fresh `Local` every retire is the waste. `enforce_chain_cap` (per block) calls `retire_versions` per block → N registrations per multi-block commit.

LEVER TRIED (safe subset): made `enforce_chain_cap` RETURN the retired versions; the two commit loops (`apply_fcw_commit` + the SSI commit) accumulate across blocks and call `retire_versions` ONCE per commit (N registrations → 1). Correctness held — `cargo test -p ffs-mvcc` 480 + my 2 parallel-correctness gates GREEN (identical EBR semantics; same versions deferred-dropped).

MEASURED INERT (release-perf A/B, ext4 delbench, two binaries on disk, INTERLEAVED 5 rounds, 12000 unlinks): batched avg 68836 vs baseline 69256 = **0.994x (neutral, within noise)**. An initial non-interleaved 3-round run looked ~1.04x but the interleaved 5-round wash-out shows it's noise. Reason: ext4 deletes retire too few blocks per commit (and `register()` is cheaper than the profile's inclusive % implied — the ~9% is the trim + EBR machinery as a whole, not the per-block register count), so collapsing N→1 register saves below the wall-noise floor. REVERTED (git stash, recoverable — not dropped) per zero-gain policy.

⭐ THE REAL LEVER (unchanged, recorded for careful work): the per-commit `Collector::register()` fires on EVERY commit including the 1-block 4K-write (which the cross-block batch cannot help). Eliminating it needs a per-thread cached `LocalHandle` (register once per thread, reuse — the intended crossbeam-epoch pattern) or routing through the global collector's cached `pin()`. That is high-impact (every commit) but correctness-critical (the EBR read-pinning architecture: reads must pin the same collector the deferred drops use, or it's a UAF) and tangled with the `!Send` `LocalHandle` + per-store-collector keying — careful, gated work, not a rush. The safe cross-block batch was the inert subset; the impactful per-thread-register fix is the careful one, and it lives in the peer's parwrite lane (`ffs-mvcc/src/lib.rs`).

### 2026-06-25 REJECT (implemented+tested): bd-cc-ebrhandle — caching the LocalHandle BREAKS reclamation (collect/retire bag desync) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Tried the impactful fix above: a one-slot per-thread thread-local cache of the `epoch::LocalHandle` (keyed by `Arc::as_ptr(&self.collector)`, re-register only on collector change) so `retire_versions` stops calling `Collector::register()` per commit. It COMPILED but FAILED 9 EBR tests (`e2e_ebr_basic_reclamation_correctness`, `ebr_reclaims_retired_versions_after_collect`, `ebr_retirement_waits_for_all_snapshots_to_release`, `gc_batch_throttling_...`, etc.). ROOT CAUSE: crossbeam-epoch queues deferred drops in the *calling Local's* bag. The original `retire_versions` registered a fresh handle each call whose bag MIGRATED to the global queue when the handle dropped at fn-end — so `collect()` (which registers its own fresh handle + `flush()`es) drained them. With a PERSISTENT cached handle, the deferred drops accumulate in the cached Local's bag and never migrate; `collect()`'s fresh handle flushes an empty bag → versions are never reclaimed (leak/growth, caught by the "all retired reclaimed after collect" assertions). A CORRECT handle-cache requires `collect()`/`prune`/`retire` to ALL share the one cached handle (so the same bag is filled and flushed) — a coordinated refactor across every EBR path, not a one-slot drop-in. REVERTED (git stash, recoverable).

⭐⭐ SYNTHESIS — the commit-path EBR overhead has NO clean contained lever (all 3 approaches dead-end): (1) cross-block retire batch = INERT (0.994x, too few blocks/commit); (2) one-slot handle-cache = BREAKS the collect/reclaim bag coordination (9 tests); (3) direct-drop (skip EBR, safe because MvccStore is RwLock-protected + reads borrow under the guard) = EXCEEDS the authorized "lower-risk" scope (removes a memory-safety mechanism — fragile to any future lock-free read). The ~3.3% per-commit register/defer is genuinely entangled with the EBR collect/reclaim machinery. NET: the authorized core-crate commit-path dig is exhausted with no shippable contained win; the real parallel-write win remains the architectural `ShardedMvccStore` wiring (~1.75x validated, durability-critical multi-turn) — micro-optimizing the single-store commit path is a dead end. Two stashes left recoverable (bd-cc-ebrbatch, bd-cc-ebrhandle); main is clean; my 2 parallel-correctness gates remain committed + green.

### 2026-06-26 ANALYSIS: the ShardedMvccStore's own residual (negative self-scaling) is the FUNDAMENTAL in-order visibility gate — fast-path marginal, real fix is a read-view model (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

`crates/ffs-mvcc/src/sharded.rs` is FREE (not in the peer's parwrite WIP — that WIP touches lib.rs/persist.rs/Cargo.toml only), so the gate is a non-conflicting target. Read the `CommitPublicationGate` (sharded.rs:30-91): it is ALREADY well-optimized — a lock-free already-published fast-check (`if self.completed() >= seq return`, :68) and a no-waiter notify guard (`if advanced && waiters > 0`, :80). The residual serialization is FUNDAMENTAL, not a missing optimization: every commit must publish in commit-seq order to advance the single `completed_commit` watermark (a reader at snapshot H must see ALL commits <= H, so the watermark cannot jump a gap). But N parallel threads draw INTERLEAVED global seqs from one `next_commit_seq` atomic (consecutive seqs belong to different threads), so publications arrive OUT OF ORDER → each commit `wait`s on the Condvar for its predecessor (a different thread) → serialization at `wait_lock`. That is exactly the ~28% futex the earlier profile showed and the 0.74x self-scaling.

FIX OPTIONS: (a) a lock-free in-order CAS fast-path (CAS `completed_commit` from seq-1 to seq when exactly next, skip the Mutex) — MARGINAL, because interleaved cross-thread seqs rarely publish in order so the fast-path seldom fires (and my `parallel_commit_scaling` test has the same interleaving, so it would measure ~neutral — not worth a third subtle concurrency change + revert cycle); (b) DEEP: replace the single-watermark visibility with a read-view / published-set model (a reader's snapshot carries the set of seqs visible at begin(), so commits publish out-of-order without a global in-order watermark) — a major snapshot-model rewrite touching every read. So the validated ~1.75x is near the single-watermark ceiling; pushing higher needs the read-view model. NOT attempted (deep + the store is unwired — premature before the wiring lands).

⭐⭐⭐ DEFINITIVE TERMINUS (exhaustively proven this session): every vs-kernel perf lever is now mapped + every contained one is shipped-or-rejected. Reads win/parity (shipped). Serial btrfs metadata 2-4x (bd-cowbatch shipped; internal-in-place rejected). Serial 4K-write 2.5x = diffuse commit machinery (3 EBR sub-levers rejected). Parallel writes 3.5-5.9x = the dominant gap, and its TWO real levers are both major architecture: the `ShardedMvccStore` WIRING (~1.75x validated + correctness-gated by me; durability/concurrent-WAL, multi-turn, peer's stale parwrite lane) and the gate's READ-VIEW model (to push past 1.75x; deep snapshot rewrite). No contained, non-conflicting, confident, safe lever remains — confirmed crate-by-crate (block/ondisk/dir/btree/journal rejected) and lever-by-lever (EBR x3, gate, batch). The remaining work is dedicated architecture, gated on operator coordination (resume/reassign the parwrite wiring, or `am doctor repair`).

### 2026-06-26 WIRING SCOPE — CRITICAL CORRECTION: it's full sharded-store completion (= the peer's entire stalled effort), not a routing job (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Operator authorized "I do the wiring independently." Began it (worktree `cc-sharded-wiring` off main). Survey: ~31 FS call sites (mostly single-op begin/commit/read; 4 guard-binding sites to audit for multi-op atomicity). BUT the real blocker is the ShardedMvccStore's FEATURE GAPS vs the production MvccStore. It HAS: begin/try_begin/commit/commit_ssi/read_visible/current_snapshot/register_snapshot/release_snapshot/watermark/latest_commit_seq/prune_safe. It LACKS (all used by the FS): `read_visible_block_buf`, `read_visible_physical` (+ the `physical_versions` COW chain it would need), `prune_mvcc_versions`, `collect` (EBR GC), `stats`, AND WAL-backed durability (`persist`). The ShardedMvccStore is a PROTOTYPE (sharded logical versions + the publication gate + FCW) — wiring it as THE FS store requires completing it to full MvccStore parity: COW/physical versions, EBR/GC reclamation, prune, stats, and durable WAL + crash recovery. That is a 10-20+ turn, durability-critical reimplementation — essentially the peer's ENTIRE stalled parwrite WIP (which already touches ffs-alloc + the sharded module + persist.rs + ffs-core).

CORRECTION to the "do it independently" plan: the win is far larger than routing, and the peer's stale WIP is FURTHER ALONG (it already has the allocator + sharded + persist work). Redoing it independently/from-scratch = duplicating a massive stalled effort BLIND to their approach (high divergence, slower, durability-bug risk). RECOMMENDATION (strong): resume/coordinate the peer's WIP (via `am doctor repair` to restore agent-mail, or operator reassigns it) rather than reimplement from scratch — resuming their further-along work >> restarting. The `cc-sharded-wiring` worktree is set up and the integration is fully surveyed/mapped (call sites + gaps), so a grind-from-scratch CAN proceed if the operator confirms after this corrected scope — but coordinating with the peer's existing WIP is the right call. NET: the parallel-write win is a major durable store-completion, best resumed not restarted; surfaced for the operator's re-decision with the true scope.

### 2026-06-26 PROGRESS (bd-cc-shardread): filled 2 of the 5 ShardedMvccStore read-interface gaps toward the wiring (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Per the corrected wiring scope (the sharded store needs completing to MvccStore parity before it can back the FS), shipped the two SAFE, self-contained read-interface gaps on `crates/ffs-mvcc/src/sharded.rs` (FREE lane — not in the peer's parwrite WIP, which touches lib.rs/persist.rs only): `read_visible_block_buf` (wraps `read_visible`'s bytes in `ffs_block::BlockBuf::new` — byte-identical) and `read_visible_physical` (logical-identity = `MvccStore`'s documented no-`physical_versions` fallback, correct for the no-COW ext4 write path the sharded store backs; cheap existence check, no byte resolution). Verified by a new unit test `sharded_read_gap_methods_match_bd_cc_shardread` (block_buf == read_visible bytes; physical == Some(logical) for committed, None for uncommitted) — passes; full `cargo build -p ffs-mvcc` green. These are additive + non-conflicting (sharded.rs untouched by the peer) and useful to WHOEVER completes the wiring (me or the resumed peer). REMAINING store gaps (the hard, multi-turn ones): `prune_mvcc_versions` + `collect` (EBR/GC — the sharded store has the publication gate but not the GC machinery), `stats`, the `physical_versions` COW chain (only needed for btrfs, not the ext4 write path), and WAL-backed durability + crash recovery (`persist`). Net: 2/5 read gaps closed safely; the durable/GC/WAL gaps are the multi-turn remainder.

### 2026-06-26 MILESTONE (bd-cc-shardflush): ShardedMvccStore is now INTERFACE-COMPLETE for the OpenFs store (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Added `flush_to_device` (the durable checkpoint) to `ShardedMvccStore` — the last OpenFs store-interface gap. It mirrors `MvccStore::flush_to_device` / bd-ryqep over the sharded layout: collect the visible-at-`current_snapshot().high` version of every block across all shards (each under its read lock, briefly), sort, coalesce contiguous runs into one `write_contiguous_blocks` each, sync — a consistent checkpoint (concurrent commits beyond `high` land in the next one + the WAL). Verified by `sharded_flush_to_device_checkpoints_committed_blocks_bd_cc_shardflush` (contiguous run 10-12 + separated 50, all byte-exact on the device). Full `cargo test -p ffs-mvcc` GREEN: 480 lib + my 4 sharded tests (parallel-correctness 12000, FCW-1-winner 200 rounds, read-gap match, flush byte-exact) + 1 ignored scaling, 0 failures.

NET: across the last 3 turns the ShardedMvccStore went from prototype to implementing the COMPLETE set of methods the OpenFs store uses — begin/try_begin/commit/commit_ssi/read_visible/read_visible_block_buf/read_visible_physical/current_snapshot/register_snapshot/release_snapshot/watermark/latest_commit_seq/prune_safe/flush_to_device — all correctness-gated. The store is now WIREABLE. REMAINING for the switch (the ~1.75x parallel-write win): (1) the lock-model swap in ffs-core (`Arc<RwLock<MvccStore>>` → `Arc<ShardedMvccStore>` via an `FsMvccStore` enum/abstraction; ~31 call sites, mostly single-op `.read()/.write()` → direct `&self`; audit the 4 guard-binding multi-op sites) and (2) the FS-layer concurrent-WAL coordination (the existing persist/wal_writer must accept concurrent sharded commits, commit-seq-ordered). Both live in ffs-core/persist (the peer's parwrite lane). The hard prerequisite (a complete, correctness-gated sharded store) is now DONE on main, non-conflicting — so the remaining ffs-core wiring is unblocked for whoever does it (me next, or the resumed peer, who now builds on a finished store).

### 2026-06-26 SCOPE RE-CORRECTION (good news): the wiring is FEASIBLE — lock-swap only, NO concurrent-WAL needed (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Verified the FS's hot commit path: `OpenFs::commit_transaction` (ffs-core:6023) does `self.mvcc_store.write().commit(txn)` — IN-MEMORY only, NO per-commit WAL append. The WAL writer (`WalWriter::append_commit`) lives solely in `PersistentMvccStore` (persist.rs:485), a wrapper the FS's plain `Arc<RwLock<MvccStore>>` does NOT use; `mvcc_wal_path` is Optional (default None) and the WAL is REPLAY-only at init (`init_mvcc_store` → `apply_wal_commit`), not written per commit. CONSEQUENCE: parallel commits never hit the WAL, so wiring `ShardedMvccStore` does NOT require the hard concurrent-WAL — it's purely the LOCK-SWAP (`Arc<RwLock<MvccStore>>` → an `FsMvccStore` enum routing to the sharded store), and at-sync durability is already covered by the `flush_to_device` I added. This RE-CORRECTS my earlier "10-20-turn durable reimplementation = the peer's entire effort" over-scoping: the durable WAL is NOT in the FS commit path, so the wiring is a FEASIBLE few-turn lock-swap (the enum + ~31 call sites, mostly single-op + 4 multi-op guard audits), with the sharded store already interface-complete + correctness-gated. Starting the `FsMvccStore` enum wiring in the `cc-sharded-wiring` worktree now; init selects Sharded by default and falls back to Single if `mvcc_wal_path` is set (no regression for the WAL config). The parallel-write win (~1.75x) is within reach without the durability-rewrite I feared.

### 2026-06-26 WIRING PROGRESS (bd-cc-wire): FsMvccStore enum built + routing audited; ~31 sites mapped (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The parallel-write wiring is progressing in the `cc-sharded-wiring` worktree (compiles at each step). Done: (1) `FsMvccStore` enum — uniform `&self` interface routing to `Single(RwLock<MvccStore>)` or `Sharded(ShardedMvccStore)`, all OpenFs store methods (worktree edfd8dc8); (2) routing audit of all ~31 `mvcc_store` call sites + the 3 careful ones resolved (worktree 9e5c66c4): most re-express trivially (begin+drop, single reads, snapshot+captured-snapshot reads); `7078` needed `version_count` (added); `34695` (begin+register_snapshot) is correct with separate locks (register holds the captured snapshot's watermark regardless of intervening commits); `6879` (the JBD2 *journaled* 2-phase commit — `preflight_commit_fcw`+`resolved_writes_for_commit`+commit under one guard) gets an `as_single()` escape hatch (the per-method sharded interface can't express the 2-phase atomicity; that path is Single-only and `init` guarantees Single whenever JBD2/WAL is configured). REMAINING (next turns): swap the field `Arc<RwLock<MvccStore>>`→`Arc<FsMvccStore>`, route the sites, `init` selects Sharded unless JBD2/WAL configured (default fast path → Sharded → the win; no regression for JBD2/WAL → Single), then gate (conformance + a crash-recovery test + the parallel create/write measurement) and LAND on main. The win (~1.75x parallel writes) is methodically de-risked; everything so far is non-conflicting (the store completion is on main; the wiring WIP is isolated in the worktree branch).

### 2026-06-26 WIRING COMPLICATION: the read-adapter (MvccBlockDevice) store coupling is the hard cross-crate piece (= peer's effort) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Routing the FsMvccStore wiring (worktree, 40→20→~18 errors) surfaced the genuine hard part: `MvccBlockDevice<D>` (ffs-mvcc:4066) — the block-device read adapter the FS read path uses — holds a CONCRETE `store: Arc<RwLock<MvccStore>>` and `new(base, Arc<RwLock<MvccStore>>, snapshot)`. With the store swapped to `Arc<FsMvccStore>`, the Single first cut can pass `as_single()`'s inner `Arc<RwLock<MvccStore>>` (once `FsMvccStore::Single` holds the Arc), so a byte-identical Single routing IS achievable + proves the abstraction. BUT the SHARDED switch (the actual ~1.75x win) requires `MvccBlockDevice` to read from the SHARDED store — i.e. abstracting its `store` field over an `MvccRead` trait (generic or `dyn`), a cross-crate change to ffs-mvcc's read adapter + every read-path call site. Plus smaller gaps surfaced: `abort` is absent on the sharded store (txn-abort path), and the optional-guard loop at lib.rs:11023 (holds the read lock across a block range) must re-express to per-call locking. These are exactly the deep ffs-mvcc+ffs-core changes the peer's stalled parwrite WIP already spans. ASSESSMENT: the non-conflicting prerequisites are DONE on main (ShardedMvccStore interface-complete + correctness-gated) and the FsMvccStore routing is ~done in the worktree (proves the lock-swap), but the remaining MvccBlockDevice read-adapter abstraction (+ abort + the loop) is a substantial cross-crate effort that duplicates the peer's hard work. RECOMMENDATION holds: the Sharded read-adapter abstraction is best RESUMED from the peer's further-along WIP (likely already addressed) than reimplemented from scratch. I can finish the Single first cut (routing-proof milestone) if the operator wants it landed, but the win itself wants the peer's read-adapter work — surfaced honestly with the now-known full shape.

### 2026-06-26 STOP DUPLICATE: another agent is wiring FsMvccStore in the main tree (further along) — deferring (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

While routing my own FsMvccStore wiring in the `cc-sharded-wiring` worktree, discovered the MAIN checkout has UNCOMMITTED wiring changes from ANOTHER agent: a `crates/ffs-core/src/fs_mvcc_store.rs` (distinct from mine — header: "MVCC store abstraction for the OpenFs hot path … Keeping this adapter in ffs-core avoids changing the public ffs-mvcc::MvccBlockDevice API while the filesystem wiring moves over") plus `lib.rs` (+252), `vfs.rs`, `cli/main.rs`. Crucially their version SOLVES the exact MvccBlockDevice complication I just flagged — by keeping the adapter in ffs-core rather than abstracting ffs-mvcc's read adapter. They are FURTHER ALONG than my from-scratch worktree attempt. DECISION (resume-not-restart, as I recommended): STOP my duplicate worktree wiring; their effort supersedes it. Their uncommitted main-tree changes are NOT mine — left strictly untouched (I `git add` only my own docs; my pushes are ledger-only, verified d7517419 = 1 file). My contribution stands as the non-conflicting PREREQUISITE their wiring builds on: the `ShardedMvccStore` is now interface-complete (`read_visible_block_buf`/`read_visible_physical`/`flush_to_device` added) + correctness-gated (parallel-correctness 12000, FCW-1-winner 200 rounds), all on main. When their wiring lands, I'll run the independent verification (parallel create/write scaling vs kernel) — my harness + baseline are ready. This is the vindication of the earlier scope analysis: the parallel-write wiring was the peer's effort; another agent has carried it further; my job was to finish + gate the store half (done) and not redo their cross-crate work.

### 2026-06-26 VERIFIED (measured): Sharded MVCC wiring is CORRECT but NOT SUFFICIENT for parallel creates — the allocator is the remaining bottleneck (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Built + measured the in-progress FsMvccStore wiring (another agent's main-tree WIP, which selects `Sharded(ShardedMvccStore::new(8))`), read-only, separate target dir — their source untouched. RESULTS:
- CORRECTNESS: `cargo test -p ffs-harness --test conformance` = **100 passed / 0 failed / 2 ignored** — the sharded wiring is correct.
- PARALLEL CREATE (ext4 create-bench --threads, 16000): **37.9k(1t) → 28.2k(4t) → 29.4k(8t)** — STILL NEGATIVE-SCALING (8t below 1t), ~5.5x slower than the kernel's positive-scaling 159k@8t. The sharded MVCC store does NOT make parallel creates scale.

ROOT CAUSE: wiring the sharded MVCC store eliminates the MVCC *commit-lock* serialization, but a `create` is not just a commit — it also allocates an inode + blocks (the allocator), inserts a dir entry (the dir-name-index), etc. Those serialize creates REGARDLESS of the MVCC store, so the create stays bottlenecked. This is exactly why the peer's parwrite WIP ALSO shards the ALLOCATOR (the +863-line ffs-alloc rework) — the parallel-create win needs the sharded allocator AND the sharded MVCC together. My earlier MVCC-level ~1.75x (pure disjoint commits, no allocation) is real but does NOT transfer to the FS create path (which adds the allocator bottleneck).

CONSEQUENCE: the sharded MVCC wiring is NECESSARY-BUT-NOT-SUFFICIENT for parallel creates. The 4K-overwrite write path (no allocation) should benefit from it (commit-lock-bound), but there's no `--threads` write-bench to confirm. So the headline ~1.75x parallel-write win is realizable only with BOTH the sharded MVCC (this wiring) AND the sharded allocator (the peer's ffs-alloc rework). This corrects the expectation that wiring the sharded store alone delivers the create win — it doesn't; the full parwrite stack does. Verified non-conflicting; the other agent's wiring + the peer's allocator rework remain the path, now with the measured proof that BOTH are required.

### 2026-06-26 DIG (non-conflicting crates) + re-measurement + blocker (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Per the land-or-dig directive, dug every non-conflicting crate (block/ondisk/btree/dir/journal — all clean, none in the peers' parwrite/wiring lanes) for a NEW lever on a measured gap:
- ffs-btree (the extent tree, hot: `ffs_btree::insert` 14x in ffs-core): ALREADY binary-search-optimized everywhere — `search_leaf` and every insert position use `partition_point` (lib.rs:275/319/609/645/689…). No linear-scan lever remains.
- ffs-dir `add_entry` (8x in ffs-core, create path): an O(block) `rec_len`-chain scan per insert to find a free slot — BUT ext4 create WINS serial (1.3x vs kernel), so it extends-a-win, not a gap-closer; the only optimization (cache the free offset) would live in ffs-core (the other agent's active wiring lane).
- BENCH-the-lever BLOCKED: the one real lever (the sharded MVCC store) is in ffs-mvcc, whose `Cargo.toml` is the OTHER AGENT's active dirty file — I can't add a `[[bench]]` without capturing their uncommitted WIP, so a criterion bench is not non-conflictingly possible.

RE-MEASURED the sharded store post the peers' two landed optimizations (e445f0a4 binary-search published lookup, b02173e6 inline short commit lists), via my `parallel_commit_scaling` test: sharded-vs-single parallel commit = **0.93x(1t) / 1.43x(4t)**, sharded self-scaling 8t/1t = 0.92x — the parallel-commit win HOLDS post-optimization (sharded > single at concurrency; load-dependent magnitude). Their opts keep it coherent.

BLOCKER (surfaced): every measured vs-kernel gap is the peers' active lane — parallel writes need the sharded allocator (peer parwrite, ffs-alloc +863) + the sharded MVCC (mine, done) + the FsMvccStore wiring (other agent, in-progress main-tree WIP). The non-conflicting crates are optimized or win serial (no gap-closer). My landed contribution stands as the prerequisite (sharded store interface-complete + correctness-gated + verified necessary-but-not-sufficient). There is no non-conflicting lever left for me to ship; the win is the peers' in-progress allocator+wiring stack. Surfaced with this turn's concrete dig results (not a prose-only turn — three crates dug to root + a fresh post-opt measurement recorded).

### 2026-06-26 REJECT (new lever investigated): RO-gated direct small-read — blocked by the TOCTOU read contract (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Dug the serial-random-read gap (1.5x slower than kernel — a real non-parallel loss). Its per-read engine includes the FileByteDevice small-read scratch's 2nd copy (scratch→dst, ~3.5%). LEVER tried: for RO devices (`writable=false`, which the FS image is), skip the scratch and `pread` straight into the caller buffer (1 copy, no memset). BLOCKED by the all-or-nothing read contract: `read_exact_at` (ffs-block lib.rs:511-548) keeps the scratch for small reads SPECIFICALLY to preserve `dst` on a TOCTOU short read — the backing file shrinking below the `open`-time cached `len`. The gate `file_byte_device_scalar_read_preserves_buffer_on_short_read` (lib.rs:7666) opens a device via `FileByteDevice::open` (RO), truncates the file under it, and asserts `dst` is untouched. A direct read skips the guard → dirties `dst` on the truncate-under → fails the contract test. The large-read path (≥64K) affords a single fstat re-check (negligible vs the read), but small reads can't (fstat ~400ns > scratch ~250ns, per bd-2emlm), and the RO gate doesn't help — the contract test exercises a RO device. So the small-read 2nd copy is the CONTRACT PRICE (preserve-dst-on-TOCTOU-short-read), not removable → the serial-random-read 2nd-copy is a genuine floor.

NET: no ffs-block read lever. The rest of the serial-random-read engine residual (inode clone, request scope, extent resolve) lives in ffs-core/ffs-extent — the peers' active wiring lane. Combined with this turn's earlier digs (ffs-btree binary-optimized, ffs-dir wins serial, bench blocked by the peer's dirty ffs-mvcc/Cargo.toml), the non-conflicting lever surface is exhausted to the code level. The biggest gap (parallel writes) remains the peers' active allocator+MVCC+wiring stack (my sharded store the verified prerequisite). Conformance unaffected (no code change shipped — investigated + rejected).

### 2026-06-26 MEASURED (clean A/B): unconditional Sharded wiring REGRESSES single-thread creates 0.65x; parallel benefit allocator-masked (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Clean same-session A/B of two ffs-cli binaries — SINGLE (built from origin/main, no FsMvccStore) vs SHARDED (the other agent's in-progress wiring, `FsMvccStore::Sharded(ShardedMvccStore::new(8))`) — ext4 create-bench --threads, interleaved, their source untouched:

| threads | Single creates/s | Sharded creates/s | Sharded/Single |
|---------|------------------|-------------------|----------------|
| 1 | 57.3k (58046, 56556) | 37.2k (37579, 36826) | **0.65x (35% REGRESSION)** |
| 8 | 27.3k (25079, 29487) | 30.2k (29875, 30447) | 1.03-1.19x |

TWO findings: (1) wiring the sharded store REGRESSES single-thread creates by 35% — the `CommitPublicationGate` + per-shard-lock overhead is paid on EVERY commit, even with one thread (where the single `RwLock<MvccStore>` is uncontended and cheaper). (2) At 8 threads the sharded store is only ~1.03-1.19x faster — barely — because creates are ALLOCATOR-bound (the create's inode+block allocation serializes regardless of the MVCC store), so the MVCC sharding's parallel benefit is masked.

CONSEQUENCE (critical for the wiring/parwrite effort): wiring the sharded MVCC store UNCONDITIONALLY is a NET LOSS for creates — it regresses the common single-thread case 35% while the parallel upside is swallowed by the allocator. The wiring MUST either (a) gate Sharded on actual parallelism (use Single at low concurrency where it's 1.5x faster, Sharded only at high concurrency) or (b) land the allocator sharding FIRST so the parallel benefit materializes enough to justify the single-thread cost. This sharpens the earlier "necessary-but-not-sufficient": the sharded MVCC wiring alone is not merely insufficient for creates — it is a REGRESSION without the allocator AND a concurrency gate. My sharded store + this measured guardrail are the contribution; the win needs the allocator + a parallelism-aware wiring, not an unconditional Sharded swap.

### 2026-06-26 VERIFY-ON-LAND (reads): landed Sharded wiring is READ-SAFE — parallel reads 1.09-1.16x faster, serial parity (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The wiring LANDED (0d2b1fee "perf(ffs-core): shard default OpenFs MVCC store" — `FsMvccStore` + `fs_mvcc_store.rs` now on origin/main, Sharded default). Last turn measured the create regression; this turn the critical remaining question — does the landed wiring regress READS (my biggest campaign wins: 5.6x parallel random read, the read-into-dst family, all routing through `FsMvccStore::read_visible` now)? Clean A/B, SINGLE (origin/main pre-wiring) vs SHARDED (landed wiring), ext4 50MiB file, 200k random 4KiB reads:

| mode | Single IOPS | Sharded IOPS | Sharded/Single |
|------|-------------|--------------|----------------|
| parallel | 12.7-13.6M | 14.7-14.8M | **1.09-1.16x (FASTER)** |
| serial | 8.3-9.0M | 7.6-9.7M | ~parity (0.84-1.17x, noise) |

READ-SAFE: parallel random reads are slightly FASTER under the sharded store (the 8 per-shard read locks are less contended than the single store's one RwLock read lock when 64 readers hit the empty-overlay miss path), and serial reads are within noise of parity. So the landed wiring PRESERVES (slightly improves) the read campaign. The read path is safe because for RO reads the MVCC overlay is empty -> `read_visible` is a quick shard-lookup miss -> base device, and the per-shard read locks parallelize better than the single lock.

FULL VERIFY-ON-LAND PICTURE (landed Sharded default): READS slightly faster (parallel 1.1x, serial parity) + parallel OVERWRITES win (MVCC-level 1.43x, no allocator) BUT single-thread CREATES regress 0.65x (gate overhead) + parallel creates barely move (1.1x, allocator-masked). NET: the sharded default is read-safe and helps the no-alloc parallel-write path, but the single-thread-create regression is the actionable concern — it needs the allocator sharding (so parallel creates actually win) + ideally a concurrency-aware store selection (Single is 1.5x faster single-threaded). My sharded store + this complete measured verification (reads/creates/overwrites) are the contribution; the create regression is the next lever for the wiring/parwrite owners.

### 2026-06-26 PROFILED ROOT-CAUSE: single-thread create regression = wiring's lost-borrow alloc + sharded commit machinery (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Profiled (perf -g) the landed Sharded create-bench (single-thread, 150k creates) to pinpoint the 10us/create regression (0.65x, from last turn's A/B). TWO sources:

1. `ShardedMvccStore::read_visible` = 4.09% self, DOMINATED by jemalloc allocation (2.42%+1.50% in `_rjem_je_malloc_default` -> tcache_alloc_small_hard -> arena_slab_alloc -> pa_alloc). The create path reads back its OWN overlay (dir blocks, allocation bitmaps) via `read_visible`. The wiring's uniform `FsMvccStore::read_visible` returns an OWNED `Vec<u8>` (alloc + 4KiB copy per hit) for BOTH backings — Single does `cow.into_owned()`, Sharded clones its stored Vec. The PRE-WIRING code called the single store's `read_visible` directly and used the BORROWED `Cow` under the read guard (NO alloc). So the uniform interface LOST THE BORROW -> an alloc+copy per overlay read in the create path. This hits Single-wiring too (it's the abstraction cost, not purely sharded) — which is why even a concurrency-gated default wouldn't fully fix it.

2. `ShardedMvccStore::commit` = 11.8% (5.88% self) — the sharded commit machinery (`involved_shards` + `lock_shards` across the create's write set, which scatters [inode block, dir block, bitmaps -> different block numbers -> different shards] + the publication gate) vs the single store's one RwLock acquisition.

FIX DIRECTIONS (wiring owner / ffs-core lane): (a) HIGHER-LEVERAGE — a borrowed/closure read API `read_visible_with(block, snapshot, |bytes| ...)` (or store versions as `Arc<[u8]>` so `read_visible` returns a cheap Arc clone) so both backings pass the version bytes WITHOUT alloc — recovers the lost borrow, fixes BOTH Single-wiring and Sharded-wiring. (b) commit machinery: the create's multi-shard scatter is inherent; a concurrency-aware default (Single when single-threaded) sidesteps it but doesn't fix the alloc. NET: the regression is the uniform-interface lost-borrow alloc + the sharded commit machinery — both pinpointed by profile; the borrowed-read fix is the one that matters. Handoff for the wiring owner; the sharded-store half (mine) is alloc-free if read via a borrow API.

### 2026-06-26 REJECT (measured ~0-gain, reverted): contains_visible on the cacheability-check sites (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Acting on last turn's profiled root-cause (the create regression's `read_visible` 4.09% is jemalloc-dominated), implemented `contains_visible` — an existence check mirroring `read_visible`'s lookup but returning `bool` without cloning the (up-to-block-sized) payload — on all three types (MvccStore, ShardedMvccStore, FsMvccStore; correct, no tombstone variant so `newest_visible_index(..).is_some()` == `read_visible(..).is_some()`), and converted the 2 `read_visible(..).is_none()` cacheability-check sites (`can_cache_ext4_read_only_block`, `can_cache_ext4_writable_group_desc`) to `!contains_visible(..)`. ffs-mvcc 480+ tests + conformance 100/0/2 GREEN.

MEASURED A/B (WITHOUT/landed vs WITH), 4 rounds each: create-bench single-thread = 1.064/0.965/1.009/1.020 (avg ~1.01x), write-bench 4K = 1.000/1.103/1.000/1.000 (avg ~1.03x). NOISE-LEVEL — ~0 gain. REVERTED (shelved, recoverable).

WHY ~0 (the narrowing result): the 2 cacheability sites are NOT the profiled 4.09% `read_visible` alloc bottleneck. They're guarded by an earlier `staged_write(block).is_some() -> return false` short-circuit, so on the write/create bench the checked block is usually staged and `read_visible`/`contains_visible` is never reached; and the 4KB alloc is cheap against the ~67us/write op. The 4.09% is the OTHER 8 `read_visible` call sites — the use-the-bytes reads (overlay dir-block / read-path reads during the op), which materialise the bytes for real use. CONSEQUENCE: the create-regression fix is NOT the existence-check (cheap), it's the BORROWED-READ API for the use-the-bytes sites (`read_visible_with(.., |bytes| ..)` or `Arc<[u8]>` versions) — exactly last turn's higher-leverage direction, now confirmed by elimination. That fix is the wiring owner's cross-cutting lane (ffs-core read sites + both stores). This reject sharpens the handoff: skip the existence-check micro-opt (measured inert), do the borrowed-read on the use-the-bytes sites.

### 2026-06-26 COMPLETE Single-vs-Sharded default decision matrix (measured) — Sharded default is a common-case net loss; recommend Single until allocator lands (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Completed the measured matrix for the landed default-Sharded wiring (Single binary = origin/main pre-wiring, Sharded binary = landed wiring), interleaved A/B:

| workload | Single | Sharded | Sharded/Single |
|----------|--------|---------|----------------|
| single-thread create | 57.3k creates/s | 37.2k | 0.65x |
| single-thread 4K-overwrite | ~30 MiB/s | ~27 MiB/s | ~0.93x |
| create 8t | 27.3k | 30.2k | ~1.10x |
| create 16t | 25.9k | 24.7k | 0.95x |
| parallel random read | 12.7-13.6M IOPS | 14.7-14.8M | 1.09-1.16x |
| serial random read | ~8.6M | ~8.6M | ~parity |
| parallel overwrite (no-alloc, MVCC-level only) | — | — | 1.43x |

FINDING: the landed Sharded DEFAULT is a NET LOSS for the common cases. Single-thread regresses (creates 0.65x, writes 0.93x — the publication-gate + per-shard machinery costs on every commit, where the single store's one uncontended RwLock is cheaper). Parallel CREATES regress too (8t barely 1.10x, and 16t is 0.95x — SLOWER: the create's inode/block allocation serializes on the allocator regardless of the MVCC store, so sharding the MVCC can't help and the gate overhead makes it net-negative up through 16 threads). Sharded WINS only parallel random reads (1.1x, 8 shard read-locks less contended than one) and the no-alloc parallel-overwrite path (1.43x at the MVCC level — not realized end-to-end because allocating writes still serialize on the allocator).

RECOMMENDATION (data-backed, for the wiring owner): default to SINGLE until the allocator is sharded. Sharded only pays off for parallel-overwrite-heavy workloads (no allocation), which is niche AND not realized end-to-end today (the allocator isn't sharded, so any allocating parallel write still serializes). Single is 1.5x faster single-threaded and parity-to-faster on parallel creates through 16t; the read win is small (1.1x). So the common-case-optimal default is Single NOW; flip to Sharded (or gate on observed concurrency) once the allocator sharding lands and makes parallel allocating-writes actually scale — at which point Sharded's commit concurrency stops being masked. This is the complete measured basis for the default selection; not flipping it unilaterally (the wiring owner's deliberate choice + active lane), but the data says the current default costs the common case.

### 2026-06-26 REVERT + CORRECTION: FFS_MVCC_STORE=single toggle — the WIRED single store backpressures on create-heavy; Sharded default is JUSTIFIED (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Implemented an `FFS_MVCC_STORE=single` env toggle in `init_mvcc_store` (no-WAL path) to let single-thread/create-heavy workloads opt into the single-lock store that last turn's decision matrix showed at ~57k creates/s (1.5x the Sharded 37k). Built + measured. RESULT — the toggle's Single mode FAILS create-heavy:

- `FFS_MVCC_STORE=single` create-bench (16000 single-thread creates) ABORTS: `chain_backpressure_reject block=59 chain_len=256 cap=64 watermark=0` → `failed to create cb_00000253: version chain backpressure`. Repeatable (3/3 FAIL).
- Default Sharded: 37k creates/s, works. Conformance GREEN both modes (100/0/2) — conformance doesn't stress a single block's version chain, so it passed while the create-bench (16000 creates churning the same metadata blocks — bitmap/GDT/dir block 59 — with NO sync) overflows the single store's chain cap (64).

ROOT CAUSE + CORRECTION: the single store (`MvccStore`) caps version chains (64) and relies on `prune_safe`/watermark advance to bound them. The WIRED single path (`FsMvccStore::single()`, no WAL) does NOT drive the prune → watermark stays 0 → the chain grows unbounded → backpressure. The decision-matrix "Single 57k" (2026-06-26 prior entry) was measured on the PRE-WIRING binary (origin/main 76ee0375), whose code path drove the prune; the WIRED single does not. So that entry CONFLATED two different single-store paths. CONSEQUENCE: the Sharded default is JUSTIFIED, not a "common-case net loss" — the wired single store is NOT a viable no-WAL alternative for create-heavy workloads (it backpressures), while Sharded handles it. The toggle's premise (opt into a faster wired Single) is FALSE → REVERTED (shelved).

FOLLOW-UP for the wiring owner: the wired `FsMvccStore::single()` path (used when a JBD2/MVCC-WAL is configured) bounds its chain via the WAL-driven prune; a no-WAL single config is currently non-viable for sustained writes (no prune driver). If a no-WAL single mode is ever wanted, `init`/the commit path must drive `prune_safe` (or register a GC snapshot) for the single store. Net for the default decision: KEEP Sharded (it's the only no-WAL store that survives create-heavy); my prior "net loss" framing is corrected by this measured backpressure failure.

### 2026-06-26 BUG (measured, serious): MVCC version memory grows UNBOUNDED — prune is never driven by the real path (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Investigating the wired-single backpressure led to the shipping default. MEASURED (Sharded default, create-bench single-thread, RSS via /usr/bin/time -v):

| creates | RSS | creates/s | result |
|---------|-----|-----------|--------|
| 16000 | 365 MB | 26.5k | ok |
| 64000 | 1401 MB | 25.6k | ok |
| 128000 | 2181 MB | — | FAIL (backpressure/limit) |

RSS grows LINEARLY (~22 KB per create) and the run FAILS at 128k. ROOT CAUSE (confirmed by grep): the FS exposes `prune_mvcc_versions` (lib.rs:7117, "Call this periodically to reclaim memory") which calls `mvcc_store.prune_safe()` — but NOTHING in the real path calls it. The FUSE layer (ffs-fuse) doesn't; the commit path doesn't (the sharded `commit` installs versions + publishes, no prune); `flush_to_device` doesn't. The only `prune_safe`/`prune_mvcc_versions` callers are tests + the unused public API. So every committed version is retained forever → the version chain on hot metadata blocks (bitmap/GDT/dir block ~59) grows one entry per write → unbounded memory. The single store caps chains (64) and backpressures (fails writes); the sharded store grows further (~2.1 GB at 128k) then fails. The watermark stays 0 because prune is never invoked to advance it.

SEVERITY: this is NOT a bench artifact — it affects ANY sustained-write workload. A long-running write-heavy FUSE mount accumulates MVCC versions unbounded until OOM (sharded) or write-rejection backpressure (single). The create-bench just exposes it quickly (pure writes, no other work).

FIX DIRECTION (wiring/FUSE owner's lane): drive `prune_mvcc_versions` from the real path — e.g. after `flush_to_device` (superseded versions are durable post-flush) and/or every N commits — paired with the snapshot lifecycle so the GC watermark actually advances (register/release read snapshots correctly so `prune_safe` can reclaim). This is independent of the Single-vs-Sharded default question; both stores leak without a prune driver. Highest-priority robustness item surfaced this session: the default FS has unbounded write-path memory growth. Measured + root-caused; the fix is a commit/flush-path change in the peers' active wiring lane.

### 2026-06-26 REVERT + REFINE: prune-driver is INERT — the GC watermark is pinned, not just un-driven (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Following the unbounded-memory bug (dc9ec858), implemented a self-bounding GC: drive `prune_safe()` every 256 commits inside the sharded `commit`. Built + measured. INERT:

| count | RSS without | RSS WITH prune-driver |
|-------|-------------|----------------------|
| 16000 | 365 MB | 364 MB |
| 64000 | 1401 MB | 1403 MB |
| 128000 | FAIL | FAIL (2170 MB) |

Throughput flat (1t 1.00x, 8t 1.03x — no regression, no gain). The prune reclaims NOTHING. ROOT CAUSE (refined): `prune_safe` (sharded.rs:1017) computes the watermark as the oldest key in `active_snapshots` and prunes versions older than it. The watermark is PINNED (stays at/near 0) — the read path registers snapshots whose oldest never advances (a long-lived/base snapshot, or read snapshots not released promptly), so `prune_versions_older_than(wm)` prunes nothing regardless of how often it's driven.

CONSEQUENCE: the bug (dc9ec858) is NOT fixable by driving prune alone (reverted as ~0-gain). The BLOCKER is the snapshot lifecycle — the GC watermark must advance. Two-part fix, ordered: (1) ensure read snapshots are registered+released so the oldest active snapshot tracks live readers (not pinned at open) — ffs-core's read-path / block-device-adapter lifecycle; THEN (2) drive prune (cheap, e.g. at flush or every N commits). Part 1 is the real lever and lives in the wiring owner's lane (the FsMvccBlockDevice register/release + the request-scope snapshot handling). My driver (part 2) is correct but useless without part 1. This sharpens dc9ec858: prune is both un-driven AND would-be-ineffective; fix the watermark first. Conformance unaffected (driver reverted; no shipped change).

### 2026-06-26 CORRECTION (integrity): dc9ec858 "unbounded MVCC memory" was OVER-CLAIMED — test-image-full + no-sync overlay, not a demonstrated bug (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Re-examined the dc9ec858 finding ("MVCC versions grow unbounded -> OOM at 128k, prune never driven") and the ab227422 refinement ("watermark pinned"). Both over-stated; correcting:

1. The "128k FAIL" is NOT a version-memory OOM — it is the 400MB test image (/tmp/a.img) running out of space at ~102k files: `failed to create cb_00102387: no space left on device`. A fixture size limit, not a bug.
2. The RSS growth (365MB@16k, 1401MB@64k, ~22KB/file) is real but its SOURCE is unconfirmed. The every-256-commit prune-driver (ab227422) was INERT — RSS unchanged — which indicates the RSS is NOT dominated by prunable MVCC version chains. It is more consistent with the expected in-memory working set for N files: the overlay holds uncommitted/unflushed inode+dir+bitmap state for every created file, and create-bench NEVER syncs, so nothing drains.
3. The snapshot lifecycle is actually BALANCED: `begin_request_scope` registers a snapshot (lib.rs:34727/34738) and `end_request_scope` releases the SAME snapshot (34762). This contradicts the ab227422 "watermark pinned by a leak" story.

NET: create-bench (no sync, 400MB image) accumulates overlay state until the image fills — a benchmark characteristic, not a demonstrated real-workload memory bug. The version chains DO grow (the single store's cap-64 backpressures), but whether that harms a REAL (syncing) workload is UNMEASURED — I have no syncing-workload or FUSE-mount memory measurement. DOWNGRADING dc9ec858/ab227422 from "serious bug" to "unverified — likely benchmark artifact." Honest correction: I attributed a test-image-full and no-sync overlay accumulation to a version-memory leak without isolating the source. The open question for the wiring owner (does the overlay drain on sync/flush, or does prune need driving) remains valid but is NOT the OOM emergency dc9ec858 implied.

### 2026-06-26 MEASURED (fresh, non-MVCC): ext4 directory lookup is 1.41x slower than kernel — O(log N) htree works; residual is per-lookup index re-descent (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Pivoted off the MVCC area to a fresh gap. Created a 16002-entry ext4 dir (create-bench) and measured `lookup-bench` vs a kernel RO-loop-mount `os.stat` loop, 20000 random names:

| | lookups/s | per-op | over |
|--|-----------|--------|------|
| frankenfs lookup | 228,878 | 4.37 us | 16002 entries |
| kernel stat (lookup+getattr) | 322,305 | 3.10 us | 16002 entries |

Ratio 1.41x slower (and the kernel does MORE per op — stat = lookup + getattr — so the lookup-only gap is real). CRUCIALLY it is O(log N), not O(N): 16k entries via a linear scan would be ms-scale; 4.37us confirms the htree name index is used (htree_find_leaf etc. in ffs-dir are the pure primitives, all index-ordered). So this is NOT an algorithmic defect — it is per-lookup overhead: the htree DESCENT re-reads + re-parses the index blocks (dx_root + interior dx_node) on every lookup.

LEVER: a per-dir parsed-htree-index cache (cache the dx_root/dx_node parsed index keyed by dir inode, mirroring the btrfs per-inode RO extent cache bd-n5w92) eliminates the per-lookup re-read+re-parse of the (unchanging, for RO/between-writes) index nodes -> should close most of the 1.41x for lookup-heavy workloads (stat storms, `ls -l`, `git status`, path resolution). LANE: the descent orchestration is in ffs-core (it imports the ffs-dir primitives at lib.rs:71 and drives the block reads), which is the wiring owner's actively-edited lane (3 live dirty files this session); the htree primitives themselves (ffs-dir) are clean but pure. So the cache integration is the wiring owner's to land. NET: a real, modest, fresh gap (lookup 1.41x, O(log N)) with a concrete, btrfs-proven lever (parsed-index cache); recorded with the kernel ratio + the lever + its lane.

### 2026-06-27 KEEP: MVCC hot-block GC unpin + commit prune driver (BlackThrush / Codex)

Landed a two-part `ffs-core` MVCC GC lifecycle lever:

1. `FsMvccBlockDevice::with_read_your_writes()` releases the adapter's initially registered fixed snapshot and switches to unregistered ownership. This is safe because read-your-writes adapters resolve reads at `current_snapshot()`; the fixed snapshot was not the visibility source and only pinned the GC watermark.
2. Successful OpenFs commits, SSI commits, FsOps request-scope commits, and direct block-adapter writes call a shared every-256-commit `prune_after_commit_if_due` driver.

The measured hot-block bound is now explicit in `mvcc_commit_batching`:

| command | result |
|---------|--------|
| `AGENT_NAME=BlackThrush CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/.rch-targets/frankenfs-cod-a rch exec -- cargo bench --release -p ffs-core --bench mvcc_commit_batching -- openfs_mvcc_hot_block_prune --warm-up-time 1 --measurement-time 2 --sample-size 10 --noplot` | Reached RCH worker `vmi1227854`; Cargo rejected `--release` as invalid for `cargo bench`. |
| `AGENT_NAME=BlackThrush CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/.rch-targets/frankenfs-cod-a rch exec -- cargo bench --profile release -p ffs-core --bench mvcc_commit_batching -- openfs_mvcc_hot_block_prune --warm-up-time 1 --measurement-time 2 --sample-size 10 --noplot` | RCH worker `ovh-a`; `openfs_mvcc_hot_block_prune/no_active_readers` `[8.8668 ms, 9.0318 ms, 9.1432 ms]`, median throughput `453.51 Kelem/s`; the bench asserts retained versions are `<=8` after `4096` hot-block overwrites. |

Internal ratio: retained hot-block versions are bounded at `<=8` after `4096` overwrites, for at least a `512x` retained-version bound improvement over the unpruned hot-chain shape. This is not a fresh mounted ext4/btrfs-kernel throughput ratio. The kernel context remains the current write-frontier gap: ext4 parallel create/write is about `5.9x` behind at 8 threads and btrfs metadata is about `3.5-4x` behind. This commit removes the stale snapshot-pin/prune-driver blocker before that mounted frontier is rerun.

Gates:

- `AGENT_NAME=BlackThrush CARGO_TARGET_DIR=/data/projects/.rch-targets/frankenfs-cod-a cargo fmt -p ffs-core --check` passed.

Behavior proof:

- Ordering preserved: yes. Commit ordering and `CommitSeq` publication are unchanged; pruning only runs after a successful commit.
