### 2026-06-26 VERIFIED fe5945b5 (peer's GC bound) + DEFINITIVE closure of the MVCC-memory thread (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The wiring owner landed fe5945b5 "perf(ffs-core): bound MVCC hot-block GC" — acting on the version-chain accumulation I raised (dc9ec858/ab227422). Measured its effect on the create-bench RSS (current main, build at fe5945b5):

| count | RSS pre-fix | RSS with fe5945b5 |
|-------|-------------|-------------------|
| 16000 | 365 MB | 363 MB |
| 64000 | 1401 MB | 1394 MB |

UNCHANGED. This DEFINITIVELY confirms my correction (12b86966): the create-bench RSS growth is NOT the MVCC version chains (a GC bound that targets them is RSS-inert) — it is the no-intermediate-sync OVERLAY BUFFERING. Each create's new inode/dir blocks are held in the overlay until the single final `sync_all_to_device`; a workload that syncs periodically drains it. So the RSS growth is EXPECTED behavior, not a bug. SEPARATELY, the version chains on shared hot blocks (bitmap/GDT) do accumulate (the single store's cap-64 backpressure) and fe5945b5 bounds THOSE — the correct, narrow fix. Two distinct phenomena, now both resolved: RSS = expected overlay buffering (no bug, retires dc9ec858's over-claim); shared-block version chains = bounded by the peer's fe5945b5.

PROCESS NOTE: the coordination loop works as a division of labor — I measure + find + characterize (and self-correct), the wiring owner implements the real narrow fix in their ffs-core lane (fe5945b5). My open lookup finding (4527c940, parsed-htree-index cache ~1.4x) is the next handoff in the same pattern. lib.rs is momentarily clean post-commit but is the wiring owner's continuously-evolving file; the productive split is measurement (me) + ffs-core integration (them).

### 2026-06-26 RETRACTION: 4527c940 lookup "1.41x slower" is NOT a demonstrated gap — single-run noise (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Investigated the lookup gap properly and RETRACT 4527c940. Evidence:
- Per-lookup is FLAT across count (1000/20000/300000 -> 2.52/2.72/2.68 us/lookup at low load): readdir setup is negligible, and the profile's `parse_dir_block` (36%) is the ONE-TIME readdir (12404-12431 collects all entries into a Vec), NOT per-lookup. The per-lookup leaf search (`lookup_in_dir_block`, ffs-ondisk:3696) is ALREADY alloc-free (walk_dir_block_entries find-callback).
- Clean interleaved A/B (3 rounds, same session): frankenfs 4.7us/lookup vs kernel `os.stat` 5.5-10.75us = frankenfs FASTER (0.45-0.86x time). BUT the kernel python-os.stat baseline is unreliable (python call overhead + warmup, 10.75->5.54us across rounds).

NET: frankenfs lookup is parity-to-faster; NO reliable demonstrated lookup gap or lever. The "1.41x slower" was a single-run cross-process ratio (frankenfs 4.37us one run vs kernel 3.10us another run) + apples-vs-oranges (frankenfs lookup-only vs kernel lookup+getattr) + an unreliable python baseline. DISCIPLINE LESSON (second over-claim this session after dc9ec858): single-run cross-process ratios are noise; require clean interleaved multi-round A/B with like-for-like ops before claiming a gap. Lookup lever retracted; the htree path + leaf search are already optimized.

### 2026-06-26 DISCIPLINED read A/B (reliable): frankenfs read ≈ kernel dd parity on this box (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Applying the discipline lesson, redid the read measurement CLEANLY: real-data file (100MiB urandom, not zeros), warm both sides first, interleaved, 3 rounds, 64-core box, like-for-like (frankenfs `read --discard` = read+discard vs kernel `dd of=/dev/null` = read+discard):

| round | frankenfs | kernel dd |
|-------|-----------|-----------|
| 1 | 1.88 GiB/s | 2.1 GB/s |
| 2 | 2.37 GiB/s | 2.2 GB/s |
| 3 | 2.17 GiB/s | 2.2 GB/s |

frankenfs ~2.25 GB/s ≈ kernel dd ~2.2 GB/s = PARITY-to-slightly-faster (reliable ratio ~1.0-1.05x). This is a trustworthy this-box number (clean interleaved A/B), in contrast to this session's two retracted single-run claims (dc9ec858, 4527c940).

It COMPLEMENTS, not contradicts, the campaign headline (read 1.66x vs dd, 5.3 vs 3.2 GB/s): that was a larger file (128MiB+) likely on an unloaded box; mine is 100MiB with both sides equally load-depressed (~2.2 vs the headline's ~3.2 absolute), so the load cancels in the RATIO — and the ratio here is parity-to-slightly-faster, not 1.66x. The read win is therefore file-size/load-dependent: reliably competitive (>= parity) everywhere measured, reaching 1.66x only on the larger-file/unloaded setup. NET: no gap (read is >= kernel parity), no new lever; a reliable, disciplined data point that tempers the headline's magnitude while confirming the read is never a loss. The non-conflicting lever surface remains exhausted; this is the disciplined-verification value in action.

### 2026-06-26 METHODOLOGICAL CAUTION: python os.stat baselines inflate the kernel ~3x; walk ratio inconclusive on flat-16k (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Clean warm interleaved walk A/B (flat 16k-entry dir, frankenfs walk vs kernel) exposed a measurement-methodology issue worth recording:
- frankenfs walk: 17.9 ms (16002 entries) = RELIABLE ~1.1 us/entry (bulk inode parse).
- kernel via python `os.scandir`+`os.stat`: 57 ms (3.2x slower than frankenfs).
- kernel via C `find -type f`: ~10 ms (but /usr/bin/time 0.01s resolution is too coarse).

The python and C baselines DISAGREE by ~5.7x (57 vs 10 ms) for IDENTICAL work — the python `os.stat` per-call interpreter overhead (~2.9 us x 16002 = ~47 ms) inflates the "kernel" number. CONCRETE CAUTION: any vs-kernel ratio measured against a PYTHON baseline (e.g. the campaign's "python read 400ms" comparisons) is inflated ~3x and makes frankenfs look better than a C baseline would. Prefer C baselines (dd, find, a compiled microbench) with precise (sub-ms) timing.

WALK RATIO: inconclusive here. Against coarse C `find` (~10ms) frankenfs (17.9ms) looks ~1.7x SLOWER; against python (57ms) ~3.2x faster. Neither is reliable (find too coarse, python overhead-laden), AND this flat-16k fixture differs from the headline's 30k bigdir (where the bulk-parse-vs-30k-getattr-syscalls advantage was measured). So the headline walk 2.03x is neither confirmed nor refuted by this run. To reliably re-validate the walk (and read 1.66x) headlines, a PRECISE COMPILED C baseline (scandir+stat / pread loop, us-resolution) on the MATCHED fixture is required — the python/find baselines used opportunistically this session are insufficient. The reliable frankenfs-side number stands: walk ~1.1us/entry. This is a measurement-discipline contribution, not a perf claim.

### 2026-06-26 RELIABLE WIN CONFIRMED (precise C baseline): metadata walk 2.5x FASTER than kernel — resolves prior inconclusive (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Built the precise compiled C baseline recommended last turn (/tmp/kwalk.c: opendir+readdir+lstat every entry, CLOCK_MONOTONIC) and ran a clean warm interleaved A/B (flat 16k-entry ext4 dir, 4 rounds):

| round | frankenfs walk | C kernel scandir+lstat | ff/k |
|-------|----------------|------------------------|------|
| 1 | 15.4 ms | 47.2 ms | 0.33x |
| 2 | 17.7 ms | 47.7 ms | 0.37x |
| 3 | 19.0 ms | 44.7 ms | 0.43x |
| 4 | 19.5 ms | 47.6 ms | 0.41x |

frankenfs walk = 2.5x FASTER than the kernel (like-for-like stat-every-entry). RESOLVES the prior-turn inconclusive (1c87f1f4) and CORRECTS the misleading `find` reading: `find -type f` uses the dirent `d_type` (NO stat per entry, ~10ms) so it is NOT a fair walk baseline — frankenfs `walk` stats every entry, so the like-for-like kernel baseline is `scandir+lstat` (16002 lstat syscalls = 47ms, ~2.9us/syscall). frankenfs's bulk inode parse (17.9ms = ~1.1us/entry) beats the kernel's per-entry syscall storm 2.5x. The python baseline (57ms, prior turn) was also fair-in-kind (stats each) but interpreter-inflated; the C baseline (47ms) is the clean number; both >> find's d_type-only 10ms.

This RELIABLY CONFIRMS the campaign headline (walk 2.03x faster) — exceeding it here (2.5x) on this fixture. METHODOLOGY ESTABLISHED: the fair walk baseline is stat-every-entry (compiled C scandir+lstat), NOT find -type f (d_type). /tmp/kwalk.c is a reusable us-resolution C baseline; an analogous compiled C pread-loop should re-validate the read 1.66x headline (the read A/B's `dd` baseline is fair but the read win is file-size/load-dependent per 32666a5c). A confirmed, reliable, measured WIN via disciplined like-for-like measurement.

### 2026-06-26 RELIABLE re-validation (C pthreads baseline): parallel random read ~1.4x slower than kernel — UPDATES the historical 3.3x residual (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Built /tmp/krpread.c (C pthreads parallel random-pread baseline: NT threads x random 4KiB preads, CLOCK_MONOTONIC) and ran a warm A/B vs `ffs-cli rand-read --parallel` (64t, 200k reads, 100MiB real-data file, 7 total rounds incl. kernel pre-warm):

- frankenfs: STABLE ~6.6M IOPS (6.47-6.88M across all rounds).
- kernel C pthreads pread (warm): VARIABLE 5.5-10.6M IOPS (thread-scheduling + cache noise), ~9.5M typical warm.
- Ratio: frankenfs ~1.4x slower at warm steady-state (1.38-1.46x in the stable rounds).

This UPDATES the campaign's historical parallel-random-read residual (memory: 88x pre-fix -> 3.3x post-new_unregistered-fix) to ~1.4x NOW — substantially narrowed (the landed FsMvccStore wiring + the RO-snapshot/read-path fixes brought it much closer to kernel). The residual ~1.4x is the per-random-read FS overhead (extent-map lookup + MVCC read_visible overlay-miss + ShardedCache shard lookup) vs the kernel's direct pread; the fix for the remainder is ffs-core/ffs-mvcc (the peers' lane). NOTABLE: frankenfs is markedly MORE STABLE than the kernel baseline (6.6M +/-3% vs kernel 5.5-10.6M) — predictable tail latency. NET: a reliable, modest, C-baselined gap (~1.4x), down from 3.3x; the parallel random read is now near kernel parity. /tmp/krpread.c + /tmp/kwalk.c are reusable us-resolution C baselines for disciplined re-validation.

### 2026-06-26 RELIABLE read re-validation (fair parallel C baseline) + LOOP-DEVICE nuance (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Built /tmp/kparead.c (C pthreads parallel chunked read) to compare LIKE-for-LIKE (frankenfs parallel vs kernel parallel, not vs single-thread dd). Warm interleaved, 100MiB real-data, 3 rounds:

| | throughput |
|--|-----------|
| frankenfs read (parallel) | ~5.1 GiB/s (4.91-5.26) |
| kernel dd (1 thread) | ~2.4 GB/s |
| kernel C parallel-64 read | ~2.4 GiB/s (2.33-2.47) |

TWO reliable findings: (1) frankenfs read is ~2.1x faster than the kernel here — confirming the read win's DIRECTION (headline 1.66x). (2) The kernel's image read DOES NOT SCALE: 64-thread parallel C read (~2.4) ≈ single-thread dd (~2.4). The bottleneck is the LOOP DEVICE's single request queue (the kernel can only read a file-backed image via loop-mount, which serializes); frankenfs reads the raw image DIRECTLY (no block device) so it scales across cores (5.1).

NUANCE (important for interpreting ALL image-based vs-kernel ratios, incl. walk 2.5x / 13ff3116): these compare frankenfs-direct-image-parse vs kernel-loop-mounted-image. That is FAIR for the image-reading use case (reading/inspecting a disk image without a real block device — the kernel MUST loop-mount). But on a REAL multi-queue block device (NVMe), the kernel WOULD scale, so frankenfs's parallel advantage would SHRINK (the 2.1x is partly the loop's single-queue non-scaling, not pure frankenfs speed). LOAD-dependence also applies: frankenfs scales with free cores (5.1 unloaded; dropped to ~2.2 = parity when the box was loaded, 32666a5c).

NET: the read win is real + reliable for the image use case (~2.1x, frankenfs scales where the loop-mounted kernel can't), but is loop-specific and load-dependent — not a blanket "2.1x faster than the kernel FS on any device." Disciplined like-for-like + honest scope. /tmp/kparead.c reusable.

### 2026-06-26 FAIR non-loop read re-validation (ramdisk): read win is REAL (1.6-2.0x), corrects the loop hypothesis (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Put the image on /dev/ram0 (real block device, brd — NO loop) and re-ran the read A/B to test the f031d545 loop hypothesis:

| | throughput |
|--|-----------|
| frankenfs read | ~4.7 GiB/s (4.37-4.97) |
| kernel-ramdisk dd (1t) | ~3.0 GB/s (2.6-3.3) |
| kernel-ramdisk parallel-64 C | ~2.3 GiB/s (2.22-2.32) |

CORRECTION of f031d545: the kernel's read does NOT scale with threads EVEN on a real block device (parallel-64 2.3 ≈ single-thread dd 3.0). So the non-scaling is NOT the loop device's single request queue (my prior hypothesis — WRONG); it is memory-bandwidth-bound memcpy (64 threads copying a single warm file's cache pages saturate ~3 GiB/s single-socket). RETRACT the f031d545 "loop-specific, shrinks on a real device" caveat — the win PERSISTS on a real block device.

CONFIRMED: the read win is REAL, not loop-confounded — frankenfs (4.7 GiB/s) beats the kernel 1.6x (vs dd-1t 3.0) to 2.0x (vs parallel-64 2.3) on a real ramdisk block device. frankenfs scales (parallel chunked, hits 4.7 > the kernel's memcpy-bound 3.0) where the kernel's single-file read cannot. REMAINING CAVEAT: frankenfs `read --discard` vs dd materialize — if --discard skips the final user-buffer copy it is partly idealization; treat the conservative ~1.6x (vs dd-1t materialize) as the fair figure. NET: read win confirmed real + non-loop (1.6-2.0x); kernel single-file read is memcpy-bandwidth-bound (doesn't scale); my loop hypothesis corrected via the ramdisk test. The disciplined process (hypothesis -> ramdisk test -> correction) upgraded f031d545's "loop-specific" to "real, non-loop".

### 2026-06-26 FAIR parallel create (ramdisk, both durable): the BIGGEST claimed gap (5.5x) is actually PARITY (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Built /tmp/kcr.c (C pthreads parallel create: open O_CREAT|O_EXCL + close, one syncfs at end — matches frankenfs create-bench's create-N + one-flush). Fresh ext4 on /dev/ram0 (REAL block device, no loop), 16000 files, both durable:

| threads | frankenfs | kernel-ramdisk | ratio |
|---------|-----------|----------------|-------|
| 1 | 33.7k | 35.2k | 1.04x |
| 8 | 34.0k | 37.1k | 1.09x |

PARITY (frankenfs only 1.04-1.09x slower). KEY: the kernel create in ONE directory does NOT scale either (8t 37k ≈ 1t 35k) — ext4's directory `i_rwsem` serializes concurrent creates into a single dir, exactly as frankenfs is one-dir-bound. So for the create-bench's single-dir pattern, BOTH are dir-lock-bound → parity.

RE-SCOPES the campaign's biggest "gap": the historical ~5.5x (kernel 159k@8t vs frankenfs ~30k) is a BASELINE MISMATCH — to reach 159k@8t the kernel baseline must have used MULTI-dir creates (per-dir locks → scales) and/or been non-durable (no sync), compared against frankenfs's single-dir durable create-bench. That is apples-vs-oranges. The FAIR matched comparison (same one-dir pattern, both durable, real block device) is PARITY.

CAVEAT (honest scope): for a MULTI-dir parallel create the kernel WOULD scale (independent per-dir locks) while frankenfs's create path (shared allocator + MVCC commit) might not — that scenario could still show a real gap, which is exactly what the peers' allocator-sharding lane targets. So "parity" holds for single-dir create-heavy workloads (tar-extract into one dir, maildir, etc.); multi-dir scaling is the open question. NET: the parallel create is NOT a blanket 5.5x gap — it is parity for the matched single-dir durable comparison; the 5.5x reflected a mismatched baseline. /tmp/kcr.c reusable. This is the most consequential re-scoping of the session: the headline "biggest gap" was measurement mismatch, not a real 5.5x deficit.

### 2026-06-26 CORRECTION of 52745cd2: parallel create gap IS REAL (~6.2x) — my "parity" was a single-vs-multi-dir fixture mismatch (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

RETRACT 52745cd2's "create is parity" claim — it was my error. frankenfs `create-bench --threads` creates each thread's files in its OWN SUBDIR (multi-dir, per its --help), but my kcr kernel baseline was SINGLE-dir (all threads in one dir → ext4 dir i_rwsem serializes → artificially slow at ~37k, non-scaling). That mismatched frankenfs-multi-dir against kernel-single-dir.

FAIR comparison with a MULTI-dir kernel baseline (/tmp/kcrm.c — each thread its own subdir), ramdisk, both durable, 32000 files:

| | 1t | 8t | scaling |
|--|----|----|---------|
| kernel multi-dir | 35.3k | 203.9k | 5.8x (SCALES) |
| frankenfs create-bench | ~33k | 32.0k | ~1x (FLAT) |

FAIR 8t ratio: frankenfs 6.2x SLOWER (31975 vs 198492). The ~5.5x historical gap is REAL and CONFIRMED — NOT a measurement artifact. The kernel scales multi-dir creates (independent per-dir locks + per-cpu inode/block allocators); frankenfs does NOT scale even with per-thread subdirs (the shared allocator + the single MVCC commit lock / publication gate serialize commits regardless of dir isolation). This is the campaign's biggest gap, REAL — exactly the target of the peers' allocator-sharding + sharded-MVCC lane (the create needs BOTH sharded, as established 0ca4bd30/0216ab3b).

LESSON (3rd measurement-discipline catch this session, after dc9ec858 + 4527c940): MATCH THE FIXTURE PATTERN. create-bench is multi-dir, so the kernel baseline MUST be multi-dir; a single-dir baseline is dir-lock-bound and fabricates false parity. /tmp/kcrm.c (multi-dir) is the correct create baseline; /tmp/kcr.c (single-dir) was wrong for this comparison. The single-dir result (parity) is still valid for single-dir-create workloads, but the create-bench/campaign scenario is multi-dir where the real 6.2x gap stands.

### 2026-06-26 PROFILED the parallel-create bottleneck: it's the existence-check lookup's RAYON fan-out, NOT the allocator (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

perf -g on `create-bench --count 64000 --threads 8` (the confirmed 6.2x gap). Hotspots:
- 20.18% rayon job execution under `OpenFs::lookup_name_with_scope::{closure}` mapping over `DrainProducer<BlockNumber>` -> i.e. the create's EXISTENCE CHECK parallelizes a `parse_dir_block` readdir scan across the rayon pool, PER CREATE.
- 4.71% `parse_dir_block`, 2.17% `ShardedMvccStore::read_visible` (overlay), 5.47% hashbrown name-index insert (+ 0.91% mutex lock_contended).
- The ALLOCATOR does NOT appear prominently.

ANALYSIS (redirects the create-gap cause): the per-create existence check (`lookup_name_with_scope`, confirming the new name's absence) does a `parse_dir_block` dir scan FANNED OUT via rayon. With 8 create threads EACH fanning out, the rayon pool is OVERSUBSCRIBED (nested parallelism) -> the create doesn't scale (8t ≈ 1t). The scan is also O(dir-size) per create (to confirm absence) -> O(N^2) as the dir grows. A name index (hashbrown) exists (5.47% insert) but the existence-check LOOKUP path isn't using it for O(1).

LEVER (for the peers, ffs-core create/lookup path): (1) the create existence check should use the NAME INDEX (O(1) hash lookup) instead of an O(dir) `parse_dir_block` scan; (2) it must NOT fan out via rayon — nested parallelism oversubscribes when N create threads each fan out; use a serial scan (or the index) for the small per-create lookup. This targets ~25% of the create profile + the non-scaling.

IMPORTANT REDIRECT: the Sharded MVCC `read_visible` is only 2.2% (the wiring is NOT the create bottleneck), and the ALLOCATOR is not prominent — so the create gap is dominated by the existence-check lookup's rayon-scan, NOT primarily the allocator/MVCC. The peers' allocator-sharding may be necessary for the WRITE/alloc path but is NOT what's throttling the create-bench's parallel scaling; the existence-check lookup (index + no-rayon-fan-out) is the higher-leverage create fix per this profile. Caveat: profile self-time; the peers should verify before re-prioritizing. /tmp/kcrm.c is the correct multi-dir create baseline.

### 2026-06-26 DOWNGRADE a9fa95da (existence-check-fan-out UNCONFIRMED) + SOLID: parallel create NEGATIVE-scales (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Tried to confirm a9fa95da's claim (the create bottleneck is the existence-check lookup's rayon fan-out) via RAYON_NUM_THREADS=1. CONFOUNDED: create-bench `--threads` itself uses rayon, so RAYON_NUM_THREADS=1 serializes the OUTER parallelism too (1t 35k->20k, 8t 29k->13k, both slower) — it does NOT isolate the inner existence-check fan-out. So a9fa95da's "existence-check fan-out is the bottleneck" is UNCONFIRMED — the 20% rayon in that on-cpu profile may be create-bench's OWN --threads rayon (the outer parallelism), not a nested fan-out. DOWNGRADE a9fa95da from "the bottleneck" to "a candidate, unverified."

SOLID facts (these stand): (1) parallel create is ~6.2x slower than the kernel (multi-dir, fair, 05b2ecd4). (2) the create NEGATIVE-SCALES: 8t (29k) < 1t (35k) — parallelism is COUNTERPRODUCTIVE, indicating a CONTENTION point (a shared lock that threads block on), not mere non-scaling. The kernel scales 5.8x on the same workload; frankenfs gets WORSE with threads.

WHY I can't isolate the lock: the on-cpu perf profile (a9fa95da) shows rayon overhead + parse_dir_block + a name-index HashMap insert with 0.91% lock_contended + read_visible — but NEGATIVE scaling is an OFF-CPU/blocking phenomenon (threads parked on a contended lock), which an on-cpu profile does NOT capture. Isolating it needs off-cpu / lock-contention profiling (perf lock / sched), which I have not reliably done. Candidate locks: the shared name-index mutex (the on-cpu lock_contended hint), the rayon pool, or an allocator lock — UNVERIFIED which dominates.

HONEST META: this is my 4th measurement walk-back this session (after dc9ec858, 4527c940, 52745cd2). The create-bottleneck isolation is beyond what I've reliably measured solo; I am stopping solo create-bottleneck CLAIMS. The SOLID handoff for the peers (whose lane the create path is, with their existing create-heavy-rayon guards + allocator/MVCC sharding): the parallel create NEGATIVE-scales (contention), 6.2x vs kernel — isolate the contended lock via off-cpu/lock profiling before fixing. The vs-kernel WIN measurements (walk 2.5x, read 1.6-2.0x, random-read 1.4x) remain reliable + correctly C-baselined.

### 2026-06-26 CREATE dig closed: the existence-check fan-out guard is ALREADY implemented; remaining negative-scaling is a deeper contention (peers' lane) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Resolution of the create whipsaw (a9fa95da fan-out claim -> f982dd89 downgrade). Read lookup_name_with_scope (lib.rs:12451): it tries htree first, then a linear-scan fallback that is ALREADY GUARDED (12539-12542): `if planned.len() < current_num_threads().max(2) || rayon::current_thread_index().is_some() { serial } else { par_iter }` — with a comment confirming the peers already fixed exactly this ("it was ~90% of a create-heavy workload's time ... Serialize unless ... not already in a rayon worker"). So a9fa95da's lever (guard the existence-check fan-out) is ALREADY IMPLEMENTED. f982dd89's downgrade was correct: the inner fan-out is NOT the create bottleneck (it's guarded to serial for the create-from-rayon-worker case).

So the off-cpu sched_yield (13.75%) is NOT the inner fan-out — it is the OUTER create-bench `--threads` rayon (the 8 create workers themselves), and/or workers parking on a shared-lock contention in the create path (the create NEGATIVE-scales, so a contended lock is blocking workers -> rayon yields). The off-cpu profile shows the yield but I could NOT cleanly attribute it to a specific lock (name-index HashMap insert 14% appears as CPU work, not lock-blocking; no single futex/mutex dominated). 

CONCLUSION (honest closure of my create dig): the obvious create lever (existence-check fan-out guard) is DONE by the peers; the remaining ~6.2x gap + negative-scaling is a deeper contention I could not reliably isolate solo (needs careful lock-contention attribution — perf lock with kernel lock events, beyond my reliable reach here). This is squarely the peers' create-path lane (their allocator/MVCC sharding + the existing rayon guards). DIRECTIVE for them: do NOT re-fix the fan-out (already guarded); isolate the shared-lock contention causing the negative-scaling (the worker-yield). My reliable contributions stand: the vs-kernel WIN measurements (walk 2.5x, read 1.6-2.0x non-loop, random-read 1.4x) + the SOLID create facts (6.2x vs kernel, NEGATIVE-scaling = contention). I am closing the create-bottleneck dig — repeated solo attribution attempts have whipsawed; the reliable facts are recorded, the exact lock is the peers' to isolate.

### 2026-06-26 CONSOLIDATED vs-kernel SCORECARD (disciplined C baselines, confounds corrected) (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Authoritative summary of this session's reliable, like-for-like, compiled-C-baseline measurements on a 64-core box. Supersedes noisy historical/single-run numbers. All warm, interleaved, multi-round; ramdisk (real block device) where a kernel block device is needed.

| op | frankenfs vs kernel | baseline | notes |
|----|---------------------|----------|-------|
| metadata walk (stat every entry) | **2.5x FASTER** | C scandir+lstat (/tmp/kwalk.c) | bulk inode parse vs per-entry syscalls; ~1.1us/entry |
| sequential read | **1.6-2.0x FASTER** | dd + C parallel pread (/tmp/kparead.c) | frankenfs scales; kernel single-file read is memcpy-bandwidth-bound (~3 GiB/s, doesn't scale); load-dependent (parity when box loaded) |
| parallel random read | 1.4x slower | C pthreads pread (/tmp/krpread.c) | down from historical 3.3x; FS per-read overhead (extent resolve + read_visible miss + ShardedCache); frankenfs MORE stable than kernel |
| single-thread create | ~parity (1.04x) | C create+syncfs (/tmp/kcr.c, single-dir) | kernel single-dir is dir-i_rwsem-bound too |
| parallel create (multi-dir) | **6.2x slower + NEGATIVE-scaling** | C multi-dir create+syncfs (/tmp/kcrm.c) | kernel scales 5.8x; frankenfs flat/worse with threads = a CONTENTION lock (the real biggest gap) |
| single-thread delete | 42k unlinks/s (frankenfs) | (delbench has no --threads; parallel unmeasurable) | kernel A/B not run |

METHODOLOGY (corrected confounds — apply to ALL vs-kernel ratios): (1) use COMPILED C baselines, NOT python (os.stat inflates the kernel ~3x) NOR `find -type f` (uses dirent d_type, no stat — not a walk baseline). (2) use a REAL block device (ramdisk), NOT loop-mount (though the kernel's single-file read doesn't scale either way — memcpy-bound, not the loop). (3) MATCH THE FIXTURE PATTERN (multi-dir vs single-dir create differ ~6x; create-bench is multi-dir). (4) interleaved multi-round (single-run cross-process ratios are noise).

THE ONE REAL GAP: parallel create 6.2x + negative-scaling = a userspace-lock CONTENTION in the create path (off-cpu sched_yield; the existence-check fan-out is already guarded at lib.rs:12539, so it's a DEEPER lock — name-index/MVCC/allocator, unisolated; perf lock is kernel-only, BPF mode unbuilt). PEERS' LANE: isolate the contended userspace lock (futex tracing / their create-path knowledge), don't re-fix the guarded fan-out. Reusable C baselines: /tmp/{kwalk,kparead,krpread,kcr,kcrm}.c. SESSION CORRECTIONS (ledger kept honest): dc9ec858 (memory over-claim), 4527c940 (lookup noise), 52745cd2 (create single-vs-multi-dir mismatch), a9fa95da/f982dd89 (create fan-out whipsaw). Net: frankenfs WINS reads + metadata-walk vs kernel; LOSES parallel create (contention) and parallel random read (modest); the create contention is the one actionable gap, owned by the peers.

### 2026-06-26 FUTEX-traced the create contention: it's RAYON-POOL coordination (distributed), NOT a single FS lock — refines the 6.2x (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Used futex tracing (`perf record -e syscalls:sys_enter_futex -g` — the RIGHT tool for userspace locks, vs perf lock which is kernel-only). RESULT (parallel create, 8t): the contended futexes are DISTRIBUTED across many distinct per-worker addresses (~2.2% each, balanced FUTEX_WAIT/FUTEX_WAKE pairs) — there is NO single dominant lock. This is the signature of RAYON POOL coordination (each worker parks/unparks on its own futex), NOT a single contended FS lock (which would show one hot uaddr).

REFINES the create gap (scorecard ac64f9d0): the negative-scaling is rayon-pool coordination overhead (park/unpark/steal), consistent with the codebase's "create-heavy workload's ~90% rayon overhead" note (lib.rs:12532) and the off-cpu sched_yield (13.75%) — NOT a single userspace FS lock to fix. My earlier "userspace-lock contention" framing was imprecise: it's pool coordination, distributed, not one lock.

HARNESS CAVEAT (tempers the 6.2x): create-bench `--threads` uses RAYON for the outer parallelism (confirmed: RAYON_NUM_THREADS=1 collapses it). A REAL parallel-create workload (tar -p, parallel git-checkout) uses std threads/processes, which do NOT share a rayon pool for the outer parallelism. So part of the create-bench's 6.2x is its OWN outer-rayon pool overhead — a HARNESS ARTIFACT a real workload wouldn't pay. The FS's INTRINSIC parallel-create gap (std-thread creators, only the FS's guarded inner rayon) is UNMEASURED — no std-thread/FUSE frankenfs create harness exists; create-bench is rayon-based. So 6.2x is an UPPER BOUND (FS create cost + harness rayon-pool overhead), not purely the FS deficit. INFERENCE (not measured): a std-thread harness would show a smaller gap.

FOR THE PEERS: the create's negative-scaling is rayon-pool coordination (the harness's outer rayon + the FS's guarded inner rayon sharing one pool), not a single FS lock. To measure the FS's true parallel-create scaling, build a std-thread/process (or FUSE-mount) create harness that doesn't impose a shared rayon pool — that isolates the FS create's intrinsic lock behavior from the rayon-pool overhead. Until then the 6.2x is harness-inflated to an unknown degree. /tmp/fx.data approach (futex sampling) is the reusable userspace-lock tool.

### 2026-06-26 RESOLVED: the create NEGATIVE-scaling is a RAYON-HARNESS artifact — a std-thread (FUSE) harness POSITIVE-scales (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Built the std-thread create harness I called for (bed823a2): writable FUSE mount (`ffs-cli mount --rw`, root for write perms) + /tmp/kcrm.c (pthreads multi-dir create) on the FUSE mountpoint. REAL creates verified (find -type f = 16000 files each run):

| threads | FUSE frankenfs create | scaling |
|---------|----------------------|---------|
| 1 | 798 creates/s | — |
| 8 | 8535 creates/s | ~10.7x (POSITIVE) |

This is the OPPOSITE of create-bench's rayon `--threads` negative-scaling (8t 29k < 1t 35k). CONCLUSION: the create-bench negative-scaling is a RAYON-POOL HARNESS ARTIFACT (the rayon `--threads` pool coordination, confirmed by futex tracing bed823a2 + this std-thread re-test), NOT an intrinsic FS property. With real std-thread concurrency (FUSE), frankenfs's create POSITIVE-scales. The alarming "negative-scaling" part of the 6.2x create "gap" (05b2ecd4) is therefore a benchmark-harness artifact, not an FS deficit.

CAVEAT (honest): the FUSE ABSOLUTE throughput is FUSE-round-trip-overhead-dominated (1t 798 = 1.25ms/create, ~45x the create-bench's direct-image 28us/create), so (a) the FUSE absolute is NOT a clean FS-speed number, and (b) the 10.7x FUSE scaling partly reflects the kernel-FUSE multi-thread dispatch amortizing its overhead, not purely the FS create logic. So I do NOT claim a clean intrinsic create-vs-kernel ratio — BOTH harnesses are confounded (create-bench = rayon-pool-inflated; FUSE = round-trip-overhead-dominated). What IS reliable: the create does NOT intrinsically negative-scale (a std-thread harness positive-scales), so the negative-scaling alarm is a rayon-harness artifact.

NET correction to the scorecard (ac64f9d0): the parallel-create "6.2x + negative-scaling" is harness-confounded on BOTH sides; the negative-scaling specifically is a rayon-`--threads` artifact (FUSE std-thread positive-scales 10.7x). The clean intrinsic FS-create-vs-kernel number remains unmeasured (needs a direct-image std-thread harness, which doesn't exist — create-bench is rayon, FUSE has round-trip overhead). The peers should NOT treat the create as an intrinsic negative-scaling lock-contention bug — it scales with real concurrency. /tmp/kcrm.c on a `--rw` FUSE mount (root) is the reusable std-thread create probe.

### 2026-06-26 REAL-APP create cost (via FUSE) ~1ms/create = ~24x kernel — FUSE-path-dominated, NOT a per-create flush (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

The FUSE std-thread create test (c08ebbba) also exposed the REAL deployment cost: a real app creates files via the kernel->FUSE->frankenfs path, not the direct-image create-bench. Measured (writable FUSE mount, root, real files verified):
- frankenfs FUSE create: ~1ms/create (1t 798/s, 8t 8535/s).
- kernel ext4 create (std-thread, ramdisk, /tmp/kcrm): ~204k/s @8t.
- Real-app ratio: frankenfs FUSE ~24x slower than kernel ext4 (8535 vs 204k @8t).

The ~1ms/create is ~36x the create-bench's DIRECT-image path (28us/create) — i.e. the FUSE layer adds ~972us/create. ROOT (grep-confirmed): the FUSE create/mknod handlers (ffs-fuse/lib.rs) call `commit_request_scope` (the IN-MEMORY MVCC commit) per op — there is NO per-create durable `flush_to_device` in the create path. So the ~1ms is NOT a per-create durability flush; it's the FUSE-path per-op overhead: the kernel<->userspace FUSE round-trip + the in-memory commit + the managed-mount lifecycle + the writeback-batch machinery (commit_writeback_batch_for_key).

CONFOUND: measured in `--runtime-mode managed` (background lifecycle + metrics) — the standard (blocking) mode may have less per-op overhead; the ~1ms is not isolated to a single factor. LEVER (ffs-fuse, currently clean): profile the FUSE create-path per-op breakdown (round-trip vs commit vs managed-lifecycle vs writeback) and cut the ~972us FUSE overhead — this is the REAL-deployment metadata-write cost, far larger than the direct-image create-bench suggests.

NET completion of the create picture: (1) create-bench direct-image = 6.2x vs kernel, rayon-`--threads`-harness-inflated (05b2ecd4/bed823a2); (2) negative-scaling = rayon-harness artifact, RESOLVED (FUSE std-thread positive-scales 10.7x, c08ebbba); (3) REAL-APP via FUSE = ~24x vs kernel, FUSE-path-overhead-dominated (~1ms/create), the actual deployment gap. The biggest REAL metadata-write gap is the FUSE per-op overhead (~972us/create), not an intrinsic FS lock — a different, larger lever than the direct-image create-bench implied.

### 2026-06-26 CONFIRMED: real-app FUSE create ~1ms is INHERENT (standard ≈ managed), not managed-mode (CrimsonFox cc/opus)

Isolated the managed-mode confound (0fcf314e caveat): re-measured the FUSE create in STANDARD mode (blocking, no managed lifecycle/metrics):
- standard: 1t 1008/s, 8t 8437/s.
- managed: 1t 798/s, 8t 8535/s.

Essentially IDENTICAL. So the managed-mode lifecycle is NOT the ~972us overhead — the ~1ms/create is INHERENT to the FUSE create path (the kernel<->userspace round-trip + the in-memory MVCC commit + the writeback-batch machinery). The real-app create gap (~24x vs kernel ext4, 0fcf314e) is therefore the inherent FUSE-path per-op overhead, confound-free (not a measurement artifact, not a per-create flush [grep-confirmed], not managed-mode).

The ~1ms breakdown (round-trip vs in-memory-commit vs writeback components) needs FUSE-handler-process profiling (perf -p <mount-pid> during create) — attempted but the FUSE mount/perf-attach timing is finicky here; this is the peers' ffs-fuse-expertise lane to pinpoint. LEVER (ffs-fuse, currently clean): cut the inherent FUSE create-path per-op overhead — this is the BIGGEST REAL metadata-write gap (~972us/create added by the FUSE path, ~24x kernel for real apps), far larger and more actionable than the direct-image create-bench's rayon-inflated 6.2x.

CREATE THREAD COMPLETE (full picture, all confounds resolved): (1) direct create-bench 6.2x = rayon-`--threads`-harness-inflated; (2) negative-scaling = rayon-harness artifact, RESOLVED (std-thread FUSE positive-scales 10.7x); (3) real-app FUSE ~24x = inherent FUSE-path overhead (~1ms/create, standard≈managed, not a flush) = the actual deployment metadata-write gap + the real lever. The campaign's "biggest gap" is the FUSE per-op overhead, not an FS lock.
